Title: Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022
Date: 2024-05-20
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2022/32

## Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022

      B e it enacted  by the Queen’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the
advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this
present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Protection of the police etc

#### Police covenant report

##### Police covenant report

1

1.1

The Secretary of State must in each financial year—

1.1.a

prepare a police covenant report, and

1.1.b

lay a copy of the report before Parliament.

1.2

A police covenant report is a report about—

1.2.a

the health and well-being of members and former members of the police
workforce,

1.2.b

the physical protection of such persons,

1.2.c

the support required by members of their families, and

1.2.d

any other matter in relation to members or former members of the police
workforce, or a particular description of such persons, that the Secretary of
State considers appropriate,

so far as these matters relate to the fact that the persons concerned are
members or former members of the police workforce.

1.3

In preparing a police covenant report the Secretary of State must have regard
in particular to—

1.3.a

the obligations of and sacrifices made by members of the police workforce, and

1.3.b

the principle that it is desirable to remove any disadvantage for members or
former members of the police workforce arising from their membership or former
membership.

1.4

In preparing a police covenant report the Secretary of State must ensure that
the views of—

1.4.a

any relevant government department, and

1.4.b

anyone else the Secretary of State considers appropriate,

are sought in relation to the matters to be covered by the report.

1.5

A police covenant report must set out in full or summarise any views obtained
under subsection (4).

1.6

The Secretary of State may not include in a police covenant report a summary
under subsection (5) unless the person whose views are summarised has approved
the summary.

1.7

A police covenant report must state whether, in the Secretary of State’s
opinion, in respect of any matter covered by the report, members or former
members of the police workforce, or a particular description of such persons,
are at a disadvantage when compared with other persons or such descriptions of
other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

1.8

Where the Secretary of State’s opinion is that there is any such disadvantage
as mentioned in subsection  (7) , the report must set out the Secretary of
State’s response to that.

1.9

In this section—

“ financial year ” means— the period which begins with the day on which this
section comes into force and ends with the following 31 March, and each
successive period of 12 months; “ members of the police workforce ” means—
members of police forces in England and Wales, special constables appointed
under section 27 of the Police Act 1996, staff appointed by the chief officer
of police of a police force in England and Wales, persons designated as
community support volunteers or policing support volunteers under section 38
of the Police Reform Act 2002, staff appointed by a local policing body if, or
to the extent that, they are employed to assist a police force in England and
Wales, persons providing services, in pursuance of contractual arrangements
(but without being employed by the chief officer of a police force in England
and Wales or a local policing body), to assist a police force in England and
Wales in relation to the discharge of its chief officer’s functions,
constables of the British Transport Police Force, special constables of the
British Transport Police Force appointed under section 25 of the Railways and
Transport Safety Act 2003, employees of the British Transport Police Authority
appointed under section 27 of that Act and under the direction and control of
the chief constable of the British Transport Police Force, persons designated
as community support volunteers or policing support volunteers under section
38 of the Police Reform Act 2002 as applied by section 28 of the Railways and
Transport Safety Act 2003, members of the Civil Nuclear Constabulary,
employees of the Civil Nuclear Police Authority employed under paragraph 6 of
Schedule 10 to the Energy Act 2004 if, or to the extent that, they are
employed to assist the Civil Nuclear Constabulary, members of the Ministry of
Defence Police and other persons under the direction and control of the Chief
Constable of the Ministry of Defence Police, and National Crime Agency
officers; “ former members of the police workforce ” means persons who have
ceased to be members of the police workforce; “ relevant government department
”, in relation to a matter to be covered by a police covenant report, means a
department of the Government of the United Kingdom (apart from the Home
Office) which the Secretary of State considers has functions relevant to that
matter.

1.10

The reference in subsection (2) to members of the families of members and
former members of the police workforce is a reference to such descriptions of
persons connected with members or former members of the police workforce as
the Secretary of State considers should be covered by a police covenant
report.

#### Offences against emergency workers

##### Increase in penalty for assault on emergency worker

2

2.1

In section 1 of the Assaults on Emergency Workers (Offences) Act 2018 (offence
of common assault, or battery, committed against emergency worker), in
subsection (2)(b) (penalty for conviction on indictment), for “12 months”
substitute  “2 years” .

2.2

Subsection  (1)  applies only in relation to offences committed on or after
the day on which this section comes into force.

##### Required life sentence for manslaughter of emergency worker

3

3.1

The Sentencing Code is amended in accordance with subsections  (2)  to  (15) .

3.2

In section 177 (youth rehabilitation orders), in subsection (3)(b)(i), after
“258” insert  “or 258A” .

3.3

In section 221 (overview of Part 10), in subsection (2)(b), for “section 258”
substitute  “sections 258 and 258A” .

3.4

In section 249 (sentence of detention under section 250), in subsection
(2)(a), for “section 258” substitute  “sections 258 and 258A” .

3.5

In section 255 (extended sentence of detention), in subsection (1)(d), after
“258(2)” insert  “or 258A(2)” .

3.6

After section 258 insert—

########### Required sentence of detention for life for manslaughter of emergency worker

3.6.258A

3.6.258A.1

This section applies where—

3.6.258A.1.a

a person aged under 18 is convicted of a relevant offence,

3.6.258A.1.b

the offence was committed—

3.6.258A.1.b.i

when the person was aged 16 or over, and

3.6.258A.1.b.ii

on or after the relevant commencement date, and

3.6.258A.1.c

the offence was committed against an emergency worker acting in the exercise
of functions as such a worker.

3.6.258A.2

The court must impose a sentence of detention for life under section 250
unless the court is of the opinion that there are exceptional circumstances
which—

3.6.258A.2.a

relate to the offence or the offender, and

3.6.258A.2.b

justify not doing so.

3.6.258A.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(c)  the circumstances in which an offence
is to be taken as committed against a person acting in the exercise of
functions as an emergency worker include circumstances where the offence takes
place at a time when the person is not at work but is carrying out functions
which, if done in work time, would have been in the exercise of functions as
an emergency worker.

3.6.258A.4

In this section “ relevant offence ” means the offence of manslaughter, but
does not include—

3.6.258A.4.a

manslaughter by gross negligence, or

3.6.258A.4.b

manslaughter mentioned in section 2(3) or 4(1) of the Homicide Act 1957 or
section 54(7) of the Coroners and Justice Act 2009 (partial defences to
murder).

3.6.258A.5

In this section—

“ emergency worker ” has the meaning given by section 68; “ relevant
commencement date ” means the date on which section 3 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (required life sentence for manslaughter of
emergency worker) comes into force.

3.6.258A.6

An offence the sentence for which is imposed under this section is not to be
regarded as an offence the sentence for which is fixed by law.

3.6.258A.7

Where an offence is found to have been committed over a period of 2 or more
days, or at some time during a period of 2 or more days, it must be taken for
the purposes of subsection  (1)(b)  to have been committed on the last of
those days.

3.7

In section 267 (extended sentence of detention in a young offender
institution), in subsection (1)(d), for “or 274” substitute  “, 274 or 274A” .

3.8

In section 272 (offences other than murder), in subsection (2)(b), for “or
274” substitute  “, 274 or 274A” .

3.9

After section 274 insert—

########### Required sentence of custody for life for manslaughter of emergency worker

3.9.274A

3.9.274A.1

This section applies where—

3.9.274A.1.a

a person aged 18 or over but under 21 is convicted of a relevant offence,

3.9.274A.1.b

the offence was committed—

3.9.274A.1.b.i

when the person was aged 16 or over, and

3.9.274A.1.b.ii

on or after the relevant commencement date, and

3.9.274A.1.c

the offence was committed against an emergency worker acting in the exercise
of functions as such a worker.

3.9.274A.2

The court must impose a sentence of custody for life under section 272 unless
the court is of the opinion that there are exceptional circumstances which—

3.9.274A.2.a

relate to the offence or the offender, and

3.9.274A.2.b

justify not doing so.

3.9.274A.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(c)  the circumstances in which an offence
is to be taken as committed against a person acting in the exercise of
functions as an emergency worker include circumstances where the offence takes
place at a time when the person is not at work but is carrying out functions
which, if done in work time, would have been in the exercise of functions as
an emergency worker.

3.9.274A.4

In this section “ relevant offence ” means the offence of manslaughter, but
does not include—

3.9.274A.4.a

manslaughter by gross negligence, or

3.9.274A.4.b

manslaughter mentioned in section 2(3) or 4(1) of the Homicide Act 1957 or
section 54(7) of the Coroners and Justice Act 2009 (partial defences to
murder).

3.9.274A.5

In this section—

“ emergency worker ” has the meaning given by section 68; “ relevant
commencement date ” means the date on which section 3 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (required life sentence for manslaughter of
emergency worker) comes into force.

3.9.274A.6

An offence the sentence for which is imposed under this section is not to be
regarded as an offence the sentence for which is fixed by law.

3.9.274A.7

Where an offence is found to have been committed over a period of 2 or more
days, or at some time during a period of 2 or more days, it must be taken for
the purposes of subsection  (1)(b)  to have been committed on the last of
those days.

3.10

In section 280 (extended sentence of imprisonment), in subsection (1)(d), for
“or 285” substitute  “, 285 or 285A” .

3.11

After section 285 insert—

########### Required life sentence for manslaughter of emergency worker

3.11.285A

3.11.285A.1

This section applies where—

3.11.285A.1.a

a person aged 21 or over is convicted of a relevant offence,

3.11.285A.1.b

the offence was committed—

3.11.285A.1.b.i

when the person was aged 16 or over, and

3.11.285A.1.b.ii

on or after the relevant commencement date, and

3.11.285A.1.c

the offence was committed against an emergency worker acting in the exercise
of functions as such a worker.

3.11.285A.2

The court must impose a sentence of imprisonment for life unless the court is
of the opinion that there are exceptional circumstances which—

3.11.285A.2.a

relate to the offence or the offender, and

3.11.285A.2.b

justify not doing so.

3.11.285A.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1)(c)  the circumstances in which an offence
is to be taken as committed against a person acting in the exercise of
functions as an emergency worker include circumstances where the offence takes
place at a time when the person is not at work but is carrying out functions
which, if done in work time, would have been in the exercise of functions as
an emergency worker.

3.11.285A.4

In this section “ relevant offence ” means the offence of manslaughter, but
does not include—

3.11.285A.4.a

manslaughter by gross negligence, or

3.11.285A.4.b

manslaughter mentioned in section 2(3) or 4(1) of the Homicide Act 1957 or
section 54(7) of the Coroners and Justice Act 2009 (partial defences to
murder).

3.11.285A.5

In this section—

“ emergency worker ” has the meaning given by section 68; “ relevant
commencement date ” means the date on which section 3 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (required life sentence for manslaughter of
emergency worker) comes into force.

3.11.285A.6

An offence the sentence for which is imposed under this section is not to be
regarded as an offence the sentence for which is fixed by law.

3.11.285A.7

Where an offence is found to have been committed over a period of 2 or more
days, or at some time during a period of 2 or more days, it must be taken for
the purposes of subsection  (1)(b)  to have been committed on the last of
those days.

3.12

In section 329 (conversion of sentence of detention to sentence of
imprisonment), in subsection (7)(a), after “258” insert  “or 258A” .

3.13

In section 399 (mandatory sentences), in paragraph (b)(i)—

3.13.a

for “258, 274 or 285” substitute  “258, 258A, 274, 274A, 285 or 285A” ;

3.13.b

omit “dangerous”.

3.14

In section 417 (commencement of Schedule 22), in subsection (3)(d), for “and
274” substitute  “, 274 and 274A” .

3.15

In Schedule 22 (amendments of the Sentencing Code etc)—

3.15.a

after paragraph 59 insert—

3.15.a.59A

In section  285A  (required life sentence for manslaughter of emergency
worker), in subsection (1)(a), for “21” substitute  “18” .

;

3.15.b

in paragraph 73(a)(ii), after “274” insert  “, 274A” ;

3.15.c

3.16.a

3.16.a.i

after “258,” insert  “258A,” ;

in subsection (1B)—

3.16.b.i

#### Special constables and Police Federations

##### Special constables and Police Federations: amendments to the Police Act 1996

4

4.1

The Police Act 1996 is amended as follows.

4.2

In section 51 (regulations for special constables), in subsection (2), after
paragraph (c) insert—

4.2.ca

the treatment as occasions of police duty of attendance at meetings of the
Police Federations and of any body recognised by the Secretary of State for
the purposes of section 64;

.

4.3

Section 59 (Police Federations) is amended as set out in subsections  (4)  to
(7) .

4.4

For subsection (1) substitute—

4.4.1

There shall continue to be a Police Federation for England and Wales for the
purpose of representing members of the police forces in England and Wales, and
special constables appointed for a police area in England and Wales, in all
matters affecting their welfare and efficiency, except for—

4.4.1.a

questions of promotion affecting individuals, and

4.4.1.b

(subject to subsection  (2) ) questions of discipline affecting individuals.

4.5

After subsection (1A) insert—

4.5.1B

There shall continue to be a Police Federation for Scotland for the purpose of
representing constables of the Police Service of Scotland in all matters
affecting their welfare and efficiency, except for—

4.5.1B.a

questions of promotion affecting individuals, and

4.5.1B.b

(subject to subsection  (2A) ) questions of discipline affecting individuals.

4.6

For subsection (2) substitute—

4.6.2

The Police Federation for England and Wales may—

4.6.2.a

represent a member of a police force at any proceedings brought under
regulations made in accordance with section 50(3) above, or on an appeal from
any such proceedings;

4.6.2.b

represent a special constable at any proceedings brought under regulations
made in accordance with section 51(2A) above, or on an appeal from any such
proceedings.

4.6.2A

The Police Federation for Scotland may represent a constable of the Police
Service of Scotland at any proceedings brought under regulations made in
accordance with section 48 of the Police and Fire Reform (Scotland) Act  2012
(asp 8)  in so far as relating to the matters described in section 52 of that
Act, or on an appeal from any such proceedings.

4.7

For subsection (3) substitute—

4.7.3

Except on an appeal to a police appeals tribunal or as provided in regulations
made in accordance with section 84—

4.7.3.a

a member of a police force in England and Wales may only be represented under
subsection  (2)(a)  by another member of a police force or a special
constable;

4.7.3.b

a special constable appointed for a police area in England and Wales may only
be represented under subsection  (2)(b)  by another special constable or a
member of a police force;

4.7.3.c

a constable of the Police Service of Scotland may only be represented under
subsection  (2A)  by another constable of the Police Service of Scotland.

4.8

In section 60 (regulations for Police Federations), in subsection (2), in
paragraph (e), for the words from the beginning to “requiring” substitute
“about the pay, pension or allowances and other conditions of service for any
member of a police force or special constable who is the secretary or officer
of a Police Federation (including provision which applies existing regulations
with modifications), and may require” .

#### Police driving standards

##### Meaning of dangerous driving: constables etc

5

5.1

Section 2A of the Road Traffic Act 1988 (meaning of dangerous driving) is
amended in accordance with subsections  (2)  to  (4) .

5.2

In subsection (1), after paragraph (b) insert  “But this subsection does not
apply where subsection (1B) applies.”

5.3

After subsection (1) insert—

5.3.1A

Subsection (1B) applies where a designated person—

5.3.1A.a

is driving for police purposes (subject to subsections (1E) and (1F)), and

5.3.1A.b

has undertaken prescribed training.

5.3.1B

For the purposes of sections 1, 1A and 2 above, the designated person is to be
regarded as driving dangerously if (and, subject to subsection (2) below, only
if)—

5.3.1B.a

the way the person drives falls far below what would be expected of a
competent and careful constable who has undertaken the same prescribed
training, and

5.3.1B.b

it would be obvious to such a competent and careful constable that driving in
that way would be dangerous.

5.3.1C

In subsections (1A) and (1B) “ designated person ” means—

5.3.1C.a

a constable,

5.3.1C.b

a member of staff appointed by the chief officer of police of a police force
in England and Wales,

5.3.1C.c

a member of staff appointed by a local policing body and employed to assist a
police force in England and Wales,

5.3.1C.d

a member of staff appointed by the Scottish Police Authority under section
26(1) of the Police and Fire Reform (Scotland) Act  2012 (asp 8) ,

5.3.1C.e

an employee of the British Transport Police Authority appointed under section
27 of the Railways and Transport Safety Act 2003,

5.3.1C.f

a person employed or engaged by—

5.3.1C.f.i

a chief officer of police,

5.3.1C.f.ii

the British Transport Police Authority,

5.3.1C.f.iii

the Civil Nuclear Police Authority,

5.3.1C.f.iv

the chief constable for the Ministry of Defence Police, or

5.3.1C.f.v

the Scottish Police Authority,

to train a person within any of paragraphs (a) to (e) to drive for police
purposes,

5.3.1C.g

a person employed or engaged by a person within paragraph (f)(i) to (v) to
train another person to carry out training of the kind mentioned in that
paragraph,

5.3.1C.h

a National Crime Agency officer, or

5.3.1C.i

a person engaged by the National Crime Agency—

5.3.1C.i.i

to train a National Crime Agency officer to drive for law enforcement
purposes, or

5.3.1C.i.ii

to train another person to carry out training of the kind mentioned in sub-
paragraph (i).

5.3.1D

In subsection (1C)(a) “ constable ” does not include a port constable within
the meaning of section 7 of the Marine Navigation Act 2013 or a person
appointed to act as a constable under provision made by virtue of section 16
of the Harbours Act 1964.

5.3.1E

In the case of a National Crime Agency officer, the reference in subsection
(1A)(a) to driving for police purposes is to be read as a reference to driving
for law enforcement purposes.

5.3.1F

In the case of a person within paragraph (i) of subsection (1C), the reference
in subsection (1A)(a) to driving for police purposes is to be read as a
reference to driving for the purpose of the training mentioned in that
paragraph.

5.4

In subsection (3)—

5.4.a

after “(1)” insert  “, (1B)” , and

5.4.b

after “driver” insert  “or constable (as the case may be)” .

5.5

The amendments made by this section have effect only in relation to driving
occurring after this section comes into force.

##### Meaning of careless driving: constables etc

6

6.1

Section 3ZA of the Road Traffic Act 1988 (meaning of careless driving) is
amended in accordance with subsections  (2)  to  (4) .

6.2

In subsection (2), after “driver.” insert  “But this subsection does not apply
where subsection (2B) applies.”

6.3

After subsection (2) insert—

6.3.2A

Subsection (2B) applies where a designated person—

6.3.2A.a

is driving for police purposes (subject to subsections (2E) and (2F)), and

6.3.2A.b

has undertaken prescribed training.

6.3.2B

The designated person is to be regarded as driving without due care and
attention if (and only if) the way the person drives falls below what would be
expected of a competent and careful constable who has undertaken the same
prescribed training.

6.3.2C

In subsections (2A) and (2B) “ designated person ” means—

6.3.2C.a

a constable,

6.3.2C.b

a member of staff appointed by the chief officer of police of a police force
in England and Wales,

6.3.2C.c

a member of staff appointed by a local policing body and employed to assist a
police force in England and Wales,

6.3.2C.d

a member of staff appointed by the Scottish Police Authority under section
26(1) of the Police and Fire Reform (Scotland) Act  2012 (asp 8) ,

6.3.2C.e

an employee of the British Transport Police Authority appointed under section
27 of the Railways and Transport Safety Act 2003,

6.3.2C.f

a person employed or engaged by—

6.3.2C.f.i

a chief officer of police,

6.3.2C.f.ii

the British Transport Police Authority,

6.3.2C.f.iii

the Civil Nuclear Police Authority,

6.3.2C.f.iv

the chief constable for the Ministry of Defence Police, or

6.3.2C.f.v

the Scottish Police Authority,

to train a person within any of paragraphs (a) to (e) to drive for police
purposes,

6.3.2C.g

a person employed or engaged by a person within paragraph (f)(i) to (v) to
train another person to carry out training of the kind mentioned in that
paragraph,

6.3.2C.h

a National Crime Agency officer, or

6.3.2C.i

a person engaged by the National Crime Agency—

6.3.2C.i.i

to train a National Crime Agency officer to drive for law enforcement
purposes, or

6.3.2C.i.ii

to train another person to carry out training of the kind mentioned in sub-
paragraph (i).

6.3.2D

In subsection (2C)(a) “ constable ” does not include a port constable within
the meaning of section 7 of the Marine Navigation Act 2013 or a person
appointed to act as a constable under provision made by virtue of section 16
of the Harbours Act 1964.

6.3.2E

In the case of a National Crime Agency officer, the reference in subsection
(2A)(a) to driving for police purposes is to be read as a reference to driving
for law enforcement purposes.

6.3.2F

In the case of a person within paragraph (i) of subsection (2C), the reference
in subsection (2A)(a) to driving for police purposes is to be read as a
reference to driving for the purpose of the training mentioned in that
paragraph.

6.4

In subsection (3)—

6.4.a

after “(2)” insert  “or (2B)” , and

6.4.b

after “driver” insert  “or constable (as the case may be)” .

6.5

The amendments made by this section have effect only in relation to driving
occurring after this section comes into force.

##### Regulations relating to sections 5 and 6

7

In section 195 of the Road Traffic Act 1988 (provisions as to regulations),
after subsection (6) insert—

7.7

Regulations prescribing training for the purposes of section 2A(1A)(b) or
3ZA(2A)(b) may make different provision for different persons or areas.

### Prevention, investigation and prosecution of crime

#### Functions relating to serious violence

##### Functions relating to serious violence

###### Duties to collaborate and plan to prevent and reduce serious violence

8

8.1

The specified authorities for a local government area must collaborate with
each other to prevent and reduce serious violence in the area.

8.2

The duty imposed on the specified authorities for a local government area by
subsection  (1)  includes a duty to plan together to exercise their functions
so as to prevent and reduce serious violence in the area.

8.3

In particular, the specified authorities for a local government area must—

8.3.a

identify the kinds of serious violence that occur in the area,

8.3.b

identify the causes of serious violence in the area, so far as it is possible
to do so, and

8.3.c

prepare and implement a strategy for exercising their functions to prevent and
reduce serious violence in the area.

8.4

In preparing a strategy under this section for a local government area, the
specified authorities for the area must ensure that the following are
consulted—

8.4.a

each educational authority for the area;

8.4.b

each prison authority for the area;

8.4.c

each youth custody authority for the area.

8.5

A strategy under this section for a local government area may specify an
action to be carried out by—

8.5.a

an educational authority for the area,

8.5.b

a prison authority for the area, or

8.5.c

a youth custody authority for the area.

See section 15 for further provision about the duties of such authorities in
relation to such actions.

8.6

In preparing a strategy under this section for a local government area, the
specified authorities for the area may invite participation from—

8.6.a

in the case of a strategy for a local government area in England, a person of
a description for the time being prescribed by order of the Secretary of State
under section 5(3) of the Crime and Disorder Act 1998;

8.6.b

in the case of a strategy for a local government area in Wales, a person of a
description for the time being prescribed by order of the Welsh Ministers
under section 5(3) of that Act.

8.7

Once a strategy has been prepared under this section for a local government
area, the specified authorities for the area must—

8.7.a

publish the strategy,

8.7.b

keep the strategy under review, and

8.7.c

from time to time prepare and implement a revised strategy.

8.8

A strategy under this section must not include any material that the specified
authorities consider—

8.8.a

might jeopardise the safety of any person,

8.8.b

might prejudice the prevention or detection of crime or the investigation or
prosecution of an offence, or

8.8.c

might compromise the security of, or good order or discipline within, an
institution of a kind mentioned in the first column of a table in Schedule 2.

8.9

A strategy under this section may cover an area that is wider than a local
government area if it is also prepared in the exercise of the powers in
section 9.

8.10

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision for or in
connection with the publication and dissemination of a strategy under this
section.

8.11

References in subsections  (4)  to  (10)  to a strategy under this section
include a revised strategy.

8.12

This section does not affect any power of a specified authority to collaborate
or plan apart from this section.

8.13

For provisions about the interpretation of this section, see—

8.13.a

section 11 and Schedule 1 (specified authorities and local government areas);

8.13.b

section 12 and Schedule 2 (educational, prison and youth custody authorities);

8.13.c

section 13 (preventing and reducing serious violence).

###### Powers to collaborate and plan to prevent and reduce serious violence

9

9.1

Two or more specified authorities may collaborate with each other to prevent
and reduce serious violence in a relevant area.

9.2

The power conferred on specified authorities by subsection  (1)  includes a
power to plan together to exercise their functions so as to prevent and reduce
serious violence in a relevant area.

9.3

In particular, the specified authorities may—

9.3.a

identify the kinds of serious violence that occur in a relevant area,

9.3.b

identify the causes of serious violence in the area, and

9.3.c

prepare and implement a strategy for exercising their functions to prevent and
reduce serious violence in the area.

9.4

In preparing a strategy under this section for a relevant area, the specified
authorities preparing the strategy must ensure that the following are
consulted—

9.4.a

every other specified authority for the area;

9.4.b

each educational authority for the area;

9.4.c

each prison authority for the area;

9.4.d

each youth custody authority for the area.

9.5

A strategy under this section for a relevant area may specify actions to be
carried out by—

9.5.a

an educational authority for the area,

9.5.b

a prison authority for the area, or

9.5.c

a youth custody authority for the area.

See section 15 for further provision about the duties of such authorities in
relation to such actions.

9.6

In preparing a strategy under this section for a relevant area, the specified
authorities for the area may invite participation from—

9.6.a

in the case of a strategy for a relevant area in England, an eligible person
for the time being prescribed by order of the Secretary of State under section
5(3) of the Crime and Disorder Act 1998;

9.6.b

in the case of a strategy for a relevant area in Wales, an eligible person for
the time being prescribed by order of the Welsh Ministers under section 5(3)
of that Act;

9.6.c

in the case of a strategy for a relevant area partly in England and partly in
Wales, an eligible person for the time being prescribed by order of the
Secretary of State or the Welsh Ministers under section 5(3) of that Act.

9.7

For the purposes of subsection  (6) , an eligible person is—

9.7.a

where a person is prescribed in terms of a description which includes a
connection to a local government area, a person of that description with such
a connection to a local government area all or part of which coincides with or
falls within the relevant area, or

9.7.b

a person prescribed in terms that do not refer to a connection with a local
government area.

In this subsection “ local government area ” has the same meaning as in
section 5 of the Crime and Disorder Act 1998 (see subsection (4) of that
section).

9.8

Once a strategy has been prepared under this section for a relevant area, the
specified authorities for the area—

9.8.a

must publish the strategy,

9.8.b

may keep the strategy under review, and

9.8.c

may from time to time prepare and implement a revised strategy.

9.9

A strategy under this section must not include any material that the specified
authorities consider—

9.9.a

might jeopardise the safety of any person,

9.9.b

might prejudice the prevention or detection of crime or the investigation or
prosecution of an offence, or

9.9.c

might compromise the security of, or good order or discipline within, an
institution of a kind mentioned in the first column of a table in Schedule 2.

9.10

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision for or in
connection with the publication and dissemination of a strategy under this
section.

9.11

References in subsections  (4)  to  (10)  to a strategy under this section
include a revised strategy.

9.12

This section does not affect any power of a specified authority to collaborate
or plan apart from this section.

9.13

In this Chapter “ relevant area ”, in relation to a specified authority,
educational authority, prison authority or youth custody authority means an
area made up of—

9.13.a

all or part of a local government area for which it is a specified authority,
educational authority, prison authority or youth custody authority, and

9.13.b

all or part of one or more other local government areas (regardless of
whether, in the case of a specified authority or educational authority, it is
also a specified authority or educational authority for the other area or
areas).

9.14

For further provisions about the interpretation of this section, see—

9.14.a

section 11 and Schedule 1 (specified authorities and local government areas);

9.14.b

section 12 and Schedule 2 (educational, prison and youth custody authorities);

9.14.c

section 13 (preventing and reducing serious violence).

###### Power to authorise collaboration etc. with other persons

10

10.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

10.1.a

confer powers on a specified authority to collaborate with a prescribed person
to prevent and reduce serious violence in a prescribed area;

10.1.b

confer powers on a prescribed person to collaborate with a specified authority
to prevent and reduce serious violence in a prescribed area.

10.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations authorise the disclosure of
information—

10.2.a

by a prescribed person to any person listed in subsection  (3)  for the
purposes of preventing and reducing serious violence in a prescribed area;

10.2.b

by any person listed in subsection  (3)  to a prescribed person for such
purposes.

10.3

Those persons are—

10.3.a

a specified authority;

10.3.b

a local policing body;

10.3.c

an educational authority;

10.3.d

a prison authority;

10.3.e

a youth custody authority.

10.4

Regulations under subsection  (2)  may provide that a disclosure under the
regulations does not breach—

10.4.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

10.4.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

10.5

But if regulations under subsection  (2)  contain provision under subsection
(4)(b) , they must provide that they do not authorise a disclosure of
information that—

10.5.a

would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, any power conferred by the regulations is to be taken
into account), or

10.5.b

is prohibited by any of Parts 1 to 7 or Chapter 1 of Part 9 of the
Investigatory Powers Act 2016.

10.6

Regulations under subsection (2) must not authorise—

10.6.a

the disclosure of patient information, or

10.6.b

the disclosure of personal information by a specified authority which is a
health or social care authority.

10.7

This section does not affect any power to collaborate or to disclose
information apart from regulations under this section.

10.8

In this section, “ prescribed ” means prescribed, or of a description
prescribed, in regulations under this section.

10.9

Regulations under this section may, in particular, prescribe persons by
reference to the fact that they have been invited under section 8 (6)  or 9
(6)  to participate in the preparation of a strategy under section 8 or 9.

10.10

In this Chapter—

      “ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);           “ health or social
care authority ” means a specified authority which is listed in the first
column of the table headed “Health and social care” in Schedule 1;           “
patient information ” means personal information (however recorded) which
relates to—         the physical or mental health or condition of an
individual,           the diagnosis of an individual’s condition, or
an individual’s care or treatment,         or is (to any extent) derived
directly or indirectly from information relating to any of those matters;
“ personal information ” means information which is in a form that identifies
any individual or enables any individual to be identified (either by itself or
in combination with other information).

###### Specified authorities and local government areas

11

11.1

In this Chapter “ specified authority ” means a person listed in the first
column of a table in Schedule 1.

11.2

Subsection  (3)  applies to a specified authority listed in Schedule 1 in
terms that refer to the exercise of particular functions or to a particular
capacity that it has.

11.3

References in this Chapter to the authority’s functions are to those functions
or its functions when acting in that capacity.

11.4

In this Chapter “ local government area ” means—

11.4.a

in relation to England, a district, a London borough, the City of London or
the Isles of Scilly;

11.4.b

in relation to Wales, a county or county borough.

11.5

For the purposes of this Chapter the Inner Temple and the Middle Temple form
part of the City of London.

11.6

For the purposes of this Chapter a specified authority listed in a table in
Schedule 1 is an authority for the local government area or (as the case may
be) each local government area listed in the corresponding entry in the second
column of the table.

11.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Schedule 1 by adding,
modifying or removing a reference to a specified authority or a local
government area.

###### Educational, prison and youth custody authorities

12

12.1

In this Chapter—

      “ educational authority ” means a person listed in the first column of
the first table in Schedule 2;           “ prison authority ” means a person
listed in the first column of the second table in Schedule 2;           “
youth custody authority ” means a person listed in the first column of the
third table in Schedule 2.

12.2

For the purposes of this Chapter an educational authority, prison authority or
a youth custody authority listed in a table in Schedule 2 is an authority for
the local government area or (as the case may be) each local government area
listed in the corresponding entry in the second column of the table.

12.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Schedule 2 by adding,
modifying or removing an entry in a table in that Schedule.

###### Preventing and reducing serious violence

13

13.1

In this Chapter—

13.1.a

references to preventing serious violence in an area are to preventing people
from becoming involved in serious violence in the area, and

13.1.b

references to reducing serious violence in an area are to reducing instances
of serious violence in the area.

13.2

The reference in subsection  (1)(a)  to becoming involved in serious violence
includes becoming a victim of serious violence.

13.3

In this Chapter “violence”—

13.3.a

includes, in particular—

13.3.a.i

domestic abuse within the meaning of the Domestic Abuse Act 2021 (see section
1 of that Act),

13.3.a.ii

sexual offences,

13.3.a.iii

violence against property, and

13.3.a.iv

threats of violence;

13.3.b

does not include terrorism (within the meaning of the Terrorism Act 2000 (see
section 1(1) to (4) of that Act)).

13.4

In subsection (3)(a)(ii), “ sexual offence ” means an offence under the law of
England and Wales which is for the time being specified in Schedule 3 to the
Sexual Offences Act 2003, other than the offence specified in paragraph 14 of
that Schedule (fraudulent evasion of excise duty).

13.5

In determining for the purposes of subsection  (4)  whether an offence is
specified in Schedule 3 to the Sexual Offences Act 2003, any limitation in
that Schedule referring to the circumstances of a particular case (including
the sentence imposed) is to be disregarded.

13.6

In considering whether violence in an area amounts to serious violence for the
purposes of this Chapter, account must be taken in particular of the following
factors—

13.6.a

the maximum penalty which could be imposed for the offence (if any) involved
in the violence,

13.6.b

the impact of the violence on any victim,

13.6.c

the prevalence of the violence in the area, and

13.6.d

the impact of the violence on the community in the area.

##### Exercise of functions

###### Involvement of local policing bodies

14

14.1

A local policing body for a police area may assist a specified authority in
the exercise of—

14.1.a

the authority’s functions under or in accordance with section 8 in relation to
a local government area which coincides with or falls within the police area,
or

14.1.b

the authority’s functions under or in accordance with section 9 in relation to
a relevant area which, or any part of which, coincides with or falls within
the police area.

14.2

A local policing body for a police area may—

14.2.a

monitor the exercise by specified authorities of their functions under or in
accordance with section 8 in relation to a local government area which
coincides with or falls within the police area, or

14.2.b

monitor the exercise by specified authorities of their functions under or in
accordance with section 9 in relation to a relevant area which, or any part of
which, coincides with or falls within the police area.

14.3

A local policing body may report its findings under subsection  (2)  to the
Secretary of State.

14.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision conferring functions
on a local policing body for a police area for the purposes of subsection  (1)
.

14.5

Provision under subsection  (4)  may include provision—

14.5.a

for a local policing body to provide funding to a specified authority,

14.5.b

for a local policing body to arrange for meetings to be held for the purpose
of assisting the exercise by specified authorities of their functions under or
in accordance with section 8 or 9,

14.5.c

for the local policing body or a representative of the body to chair the
meetings, and

14.5.d

for such descriptions and numbers of persons as the local policing body may
specify to be required to attend the meetings.

14.6

If a local policing body acts under subsection  (1)  or  (2) , or under
regulations under subsection  (4) , in relation to the exercise by a specified
authority of its functions under or in accordance with section 8 or 9, the
authority must co-operate with the body.

14.7

References in this Chapter (however expressed) to a specified authority
exercising functions in accordance with section 8 or 9 are to the authority
exercising functions conferred on it apart from this Chapter in accordance
with the section in question.

###### Involvement of educational, prison and youth custody authorities

15

15.1

An educational, prison or youth custody authority (a “relevant authority”) for
a local government area and a specified authority for that area may
collaborate with each other to prevent and reduce serious violence in that
area.

15.2

A relevant authority for a relevant area and a specified authority for that
area may collaborate with each other to prevent and reduce serious violence in
that area.

15.3

A relevant authority and a specified authority must collaborate with each
other as mentioned in subsection  (1)  or  (2)  if either the relevant
authority or the specified authority requests the other to do so.

15.4

A relevant authority must carry out any actions which are specified under
section 8 (5)  or 9 (5)  as actions to be carried out by the authority.

15.5

A relevant authority for a local government area—

15.5.a

may collaborate with another relevant authority for that area to prevent and
reduce serious violence in that area, and

15.5.b

must collaborate with another relevant authority for that area for those
purposes if requested by that other relevant authority to do so.

15.6

A relevant authority (“RA1”) may collaborate with another relevant authority
(“RA2”) to prevent and reduce serious violence in an area which is made up of—

15.6.a

all or part of the local government area for which RA1 is a relevant
authority, and

15.6.b

all or part of the local government area for which RA2 is a relevant
authority.

15.7

A relevant authority is not subject to a duty in subsection  (3) ,  (4)  or
(5) (b), and a specified authority is not subject to a duty in subsection  (3)
, if or to the extent that compliance with the duty—

15.7.a

would be incompatible with any other duty of the authority imposed by an
enactment (other than subsection  (5) (b)),

15.7.b

would otherwise have an adverse effect on the exercise of the authority’s
functions,

15.7.c

would be disproportionate to the need to prevent and reduce serious violence
in the area to which the duty relates, or

15.7.d

would mean that the authority incurred unreasonable costs.

15.8

In determining whether subsection  (7)  applies to an authority, the
cumulative effect of complying with duties under this section must be taken
into account.

15.9

Subsection  (7)  or  (8)  does not apply in relation to the duty of a relevant
authority to collaborate with a specified authority under subsection  (3)  to
the extent that it relates to—

15.9.a

the exercise by the specified authority of its function under subsection  (3)
(a) or (b) of section 8 of identifying the kinds or causes of serious violence
in an area or its function of preparing a strategy under subsection  (3) (c)
of that section, or

15.9.b

the exercise by the specified authority of its function under subsection  (3)
(a) or (b) of section 9 of identifying the kinds or causes of serious violence
in an area or its function of preparing a strategy under subsection  (3) (c)
of that section.

15.10

This section does not affect any power to collaborate apart from this section.

15.11

In this section “ enactment ” includes—

15.11.a

an enactment comprised in subordinate legislation within the meaning of the
Interpretation Act 1978, and

15.11.b

an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, a Measure or Act of
Senedd Cymru.

###### Disclosure of information

16

16.1

A person listed in subsection  (2)  may disclose information that it holds for
the purposes of its functions to another person listed in that subsection for
the purposes of the exercise by the other person of its functions under or in
accordance with this Chapter.

16.2

Those persons are—

16.2.a

a specified authority;

16.2.b

a local policing body;

16.2.c

an educational authority;

16.2.d

a prison authority;

16.2.e

a youth custody authority.

16.3

A disclosure of information authorised by this section does not breach—

16.3.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

16.3.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

16.4

But this section does not authorise—

16.4.a

the disclosure of patient information,

16.4.b

the disclosure of personal information by a specified authority which is a
health or social care authority,

16.4.c

a disclosure of information that would contravene the data protection
legislation (but in determining whether a disclosure would do so, the power
conferred by this section is to be taken into account), or

16.4.d

a disclosure of information that is prohibited by any of Parts 1 to 7 or
Chapter 1 of Part 9 of the Investigatory Powers Act 2016.

16.5

Subsection  (6)  applies if—

16.5.a

a disclosure of information under this section is also permitted by
regulations under section 6(2) of the Crime and Disorder Act 1998 or by
section 115 of that Act (but is not also a disclosure under section 17A of
that Act), and

16.5.b

a condition or limitation applies to a disclosure under those regulations or
section 115 of that Act by virtue of such regulations.

16.6

The condition or limitation does not apply to the disclosure of information
under this section.

16.7

This section does not otherwise affect any power to disclose information apart
from this section.

###### Supply of information to local policing bodies

17

17.1

A local policing body may, for the purposes of enabling or assisting it to
exercise its functions under section 14 in relation to an area, request any
person listed in subsection  (2)  to supply it with such information as may be
specified in the request.

17.2

Those persons are—

17.2.a

a specified authority for that area;

17.2.b

an educational authority for that area;

17.2.c

a prison authority for that area;

17.2.d

a youth custody authority for that area.

17.3

Information requested under subsection  (1)  must be information that is held
by the person to whom the request is made and that relates to—

17.3.a

the person to whom the request was made,

17.3.b

a function of the person to whom the request was made, or

17.3.c

a person in respect of whom a function is exercisable by the person requested
to supply the information.

17.4

Subject to subsection  (6) , a person who is requested to supply information
under subsection  (1)  must comply with the request.

17.5

A disclosure of information required by subsection  (4)  does not breach—

17.5.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

17.5.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

17.6

But subsection  (4)  does not require—

17.6.a

the disclosure of patient information,

17.6.b

the disclosure of personal information by a specified authority which is a
health or social care authority,

17.6.c

a disclosure of information that would contravene the data protection
legislation (but in determining whether a disclosure would do so, the duty
imposed by that subsection is to be taken into account), or

17.6.d

a disclosure of information that is prohibited by any of Parts 1 to 7 or
Chapter 1 of Part 9 of the Investigatory Powers Act 2016.

17.7

Information supplied to a local policing body under this section may be used
by the body only for the purpose of enabling or assisting it to exercise its
functions under section 14.

###### Directions

18

18.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if the Secretary of State is satisfied that—

18.1.a

a specified authority has failed to discharge a duty imposed on it by section
8, 14 (6) , 15 (3)  or 17 (4) , or

18.1.b

an educational authority, prison authority or youth custody authority has
failed to discharge a duty imposed on it by section 15 (3) ,  (4)  or  (5) (b)
or 17 (4) .

18.2

The Secretary of State may give directions to the authority for the purpose of
securing compliance with the duty.

18.3

A direction under subsection  (2)  may be enforced, on an application made on
behalf of the Secretary of State, by a mandatory order.

18.4

The Secretary of State must obtain the consent of the Welsh Ministers before
giving a direction under this section to a devolved Welsh authority within the
meaning of the Government of Wales Act 2006 (see section 157A of that Act).

18.5

This section does not apply in relation to—

18.5.a

a provider of probation services if that provider is the Secretary of State,

18.5.b

the governor of a prison, young offender institution or secure training
centre, or

18.5.c

the principal of a directly managed secure college as defined in paragraph 27
of Schedule 10 to the Criminal Justice and Courts Act 2015.

###### Guidance

19

19.1

A person listed in subsection  (2)  must have regard to guidance issued by the
Secretary of State—

19.1.a

in exercising any function conferred by or by virtue of this Chapter, or

19.1.b

in exercising any function in accordance with this Chapter.

19.2

Those persons are—

19.2.a

a specified authority;

19.2.b

a person prescribed in regulations under section 10;

19.2.c

a local policing body;

19.2.d

an educational authority;

19.2.e

a prison authority;

19.2.f

a youth custody authority.

19.3

The Secretary of State must consult the Welsh Ministers before issuing
guidance relating to the exercise of functions as mentioned in subsection  (1)
by a devolved Welsh authority within the meaning of the Government of Wales
Act 2006 (see section 157A of that Act).

19.4

After issuing guidance under this section, the Secretary of State must lay a
copy of the guidance before Parliament.

##### Amendments to the Crime and Disorder Act 1998 etc

###### Amendments to the Crime and Disorder Act 1998

20

20.1

The Crime and Disorder Act 1998 is amended as follows.

20.2

In section 5A (combination agreements: further provision)—

20.2.a

in subsection (2), after paragraph (c) insert—

20.2.a.d

preventing people from becoming involved in serious violence;

20.2.a.e

reducing instances of serious violence.

, and

20.2.b

after subsection (9) insert—

20.2.b.10

References in this section to serious violence and to becoming involved in
serious violence are to be construed in accordance with section 18.

20.3

Section 6 (formulation and implementation of strategies) is amended in
accordance with subsections  (4)  to  (7) .

20.4

In subsection (1), at the end of paragraph (c) insert

; and

20.4.d

a strategy for—

20.4.d.i

preventing people from becoming involved in serious violence in the area, and

20.4.d.ii

reducing instances of serious violence in the area.

20.5

In subsection (6)—

20.5.a

omit the “or” at the end of paragraph (a), and

20.5.b

after paragraph (b) insert—

20.5.b.c

the prevention of people becoming involved in serious violence of a particular
description; or

20.5.b.d

the reduction of instances of serious violence of a particular description.

20.6

In subsection (9), at the end of paragraph (a) insert  “and strategies for
preventing people from becoming involved in and reducing instances of serious
violence in areas in Wales” .

20.7

After subsection (9) insert—

20.7.10

The Secretary of State must consult the Welsh Ministers before making
regulations under this section if and to extent that the regulations—

20.7.10.a

relate to a strategy within subsection (1)(d), and

20.7.10.b

make provision that applies in relation to a devolved Welsh authority within
the meaning of the Government of Wales Act 2006 (see section 157A of that
Act).

20.7.11

References in this section to serious violence and to becoming involved in
serious violence are to be construed in accordance with section 18.

20.8

Section 17 (duty to consider crime and disorder implications) is amended in
accordance with subsections  (9)  to  (11) .

20.9

In subsection (1), at the end of paragraph (c) insert

; and

20.9.d

serious violence in its area.

20.10

After subsection (1) insert—

20.10.1A

The duty imposed on an authority by subsection (1) to do all it reasonably can
to prevent serious violence in its area is a duty on the authority to do all
it reasonably can to—

20.10.1A.a

prevent people from becoming involved in serious violence in its area, and

20.10.1A.b

reduce instances of serious violence in its area.

20.11

After subsection (5) insert—

20.11.6

References in this section to serious violence and to becoming involved in
serious violence are to be construed in accordance with section 18.

20.12

In section 18 (interpretation of Chapter 1)—

20.12.a

in subsection (1), at the appropriate place insert—

      “violence”—         includes, in particular—         domestic abuse
within the meaning of the Domestic Abuse Act 2021 (see section 1 of that Act),
sexual offences,           violence against property, and           threats of
violence;                 does not include terrorism (within the meaning of
the Terrorism Act 2000 (see section 1(1) to (4) of that Act)).

, and

20.12.b

after that subsection insert—

20.12.b.1A

In the definition of “violence” in subsection (1) “ sexual offence ” means an
offence under the law of England and Wales which is for the time being
specified in Schedule 3 to the Sexual Offences Act 2003, other than the
offence specified in paragraph 14 of that Schedule (fraudulent evasion of
excise duty).

20.12.b.1B

In determining for the purposes of subsection (1A) whether an offence is
specified in Schedule 3 to the Sexual Offences Act 2003, any limitation in
that Schedule referring to the circumstances of a particular case (including
the sentence imposed) is to be disregarded.

20.12.b.1C

References in this Chapter to becoming involved in serious violence include
becoming a victim of serious violence.

20.12.b.1D

In considering whether violence in an area amounts to serious violence for the
purposes of this Chapter account must be taken in particular of the following
factors—

20.12.b.1D.a

the maximum penalty which could be imposed for the offence (if any) involved
in the violence,

20.12.b.1D.b

the impact of the violence on any victim,

20.12.b.1D.c

the prevalence of the violence in the area, and

20.12.b.1D.d

the impact of the violence on the community in the area.

###### Amendment to the Police and Justice Act 2006

21

In section 19(11) of the Police and Justice Act 2006 (local authority scrutiny
of crime and disorder matters: interpretation), in the definition of “local
crime and disorder matter”—

21.a

omit the “or” at the end of paragraph (a), and

21.b

at the end of paragraph (b) insert

or

      serious violence (within the meaning of Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the Crime
and Disorder Act 1998),

.

##### General

###### Regulations

22

22.1

Regulations under this Chapter are to be made by statutory instrument.

22.2

Regulations under this Chapter—

22.2.a

may make different provision for different purposes or areas;

22.2.b

may make consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or
saving provision.

22.3

The Secretary of State must consult the Welsh Ministers before making
regulations under this Chapter if and to extent that the regulations make
provision that applies in relation to a devolved Welsh authority within the
meaning of the Government of Wales Act 2006 (see section 157A of that Act).

22.4

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this Chapter may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

22.5

Subsection  (4)  does not apply to a statutory instrument containing only one
or more of the following—

22.5.a

regulations under section 8 (10) ;

22.5.b

regulations under section 9 (10) ;

22.5.c

regulations under section 11 (7)  which make provision for the removal of an
entry in Schedule 1 where the authority concerned has ceased to exist;

22.5.d

regulations under section 11 (7)  which make provision for the modification of
an entry in Schedule 1 in consequence of a change of name or transfer of
functions;

22.5.e

regulations under section 12 (3)  which make provision for the removal of an
entry in Schedule 2 where the authority concerned has ceased to exist;

22.5.f

regulations under section 12 (3)  which make provision for the modification of
an entry in Schedule 2 in consequence of a change of name or transfer of
functions;

22.5.g

regulations under section 14 (4) .

22.6

A statutory instrument within subsection  (5)  is subject to annulment in
pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.
