#### Offensive weapons homicide reviews

##### Duty to arrange a review

24

24.1

Where a review partner considers that—

24.1.a

the death of a person was, or is likely to have been, a qualifying homicide,

24.1.b

the death occurred, or is likely to have occurred, in England or Wales,

24.1.c

such other conditions as the Secretary of State may specify by regulations are
satisfied, including, for example, conditions relating to—

24.1.c.i

the circumstances of or relating to the death,

24.1.c.ii

the circumstances or history of the person who died, or

24.1.c.iii

the circumstances or history of other persons with a connection to the death,
and

24.1.d

the review partner is one of the relevant review partners in respect of the
death (see section 25),

the review partner must join with the other relevant review partners in
respect of the death in arranging for there to be a review under this section
of the person’s death.

24.2

Subsection  (1)  is subject to subsections  (3)  to  (5)  and section 26.

24.3

If the review partner considers, on further information, that any of the
conditions mentioned in subsection  (1) (a)  to  (c)  is not satisfied in the
case of the person’s death, the review partner ceases to be under a duty to
arrange for there to be a review under this section of the death (and a review
may accordingly be discontinued).

24.4

If the review partner considers, on further information, that the condition
mentioned in subsection  (1) (d)  is not satisfied in the case of the person’s
death, the review partner ceases to be under a duty to arrange for there to be
a review under this section of the death, except where such a review of the
death has already started to take place under arrangements made by the review
partner and other review partners.

24.5

Subsection  (1)  does not require a review partner to arrange for there to be
a review under this section of a person’s death if such a review of the death
has already taken place, or started to take place, under arrangements made by
other review partners.

24.6

For the purposes of this section, the homicide of a person is a qualifying
homicide if—

24.6.a

the person was aged 18 or over, and

24.6.b

the death, or the events surrounding it, involved the use of an offensive
weapon.

24.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

24.7.a

amend this section so as to alter the meaning of “qualifying homicide”, and

24.7.b

make such consequential amendments of this Chapter as appear to the Secretary
of State to be appropriate.

24.8

In this section “ offensive weapon ” has the same meaning as in section 1 of
the Prevention of Crime Act 1953.

##### Relevant review partners

25

25.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for identifying which
review partners are to be the relevant review partners in respect of a
person’s death.

25.2

The regulations may provide that the relevant review partners in respect of a
person’s death are—

25.2.a

a chief officer of police for a police area in England or Wales of a
description specified in the regulations,

25.2.b

a local authority of a description specified in the regulations or, in a case
of a description specified in the regulations, a county council and a district
council of a description specified in the regulations, and

25.2.c

an integrated care board   or a local health board of a description specified
in the regulations.

25.3

The regulations may, in particular, provide that, in a case of a description
specified in the regulations, the relevant review partners in respect of a
person’s death are—

25.3.a

the chief officer of police for the police area in England or Wales in which
the death occurred or is likely to have occurred,

25.3.b

the local authority in whose area the death occurred or is likely to have
occurred or, if the death occurred or is likely to have occurred within the
area of a district council whose area is within the area of a county council,
both of those local authorities, and

25.3.c

the   integrated care board   or the local health board in whose area the
death occurred or is likely to have occurred.

25.4

The regulations may include provision for identifying the relevant review
partners in respect of a person’s death by reference to other matters,
including—

25.4.a

the last known place of residence of the person who died;

25.4.b

an earlier place of residence of the person who died;

25.4.c

the place of residence of the person who caused or is likely to have caused,
or of any of the persons who caused or are likely to have caused, the person’s
death;

25.4.d

the police area in England or Wales of the police force that is investigating
or has investigated the person’s death.

25.5

The regulations may—

25.5.a

provide for a group of review partners to agree with another group of review
partners to be the relevant review partners in respect of a person’s death
instead of that other group;

25.5.b

provide for review partners of a description specified in the regulations to
agree between them which of them is a relevant review partner in respect of a
person’s death;

25.5.c

provide for the Secretary of State to give a direction specifying which review
partners are the relevant review partners in respect of a person’s death.

##### Relationship with other review requirements

26

26.1

The duty in section 24 (1)  does not apply in relation to a death if—

26.1.a

a child death review must or may be arranged in relation to the death (see
section 16M(1) and (2) of the Children Act 2004),

26.1.b

the death may be the subject of a domestic homicide review (see section 9 of
the Domestic Violence, Crime and Victims Act 2004), or

26.1.c

a safeguarding adults review must or may be established in relation to the
death (see section 44(1) and (4) of the Care Act 2014).

26.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the duty in
section 24 (1)  not applying in the case of a death which may or must be
investigated under arrangements made by NHS bodies with respect to deaths
caused by persons who are receiving or have received any health services
relating to mental health.

26.3

The duty in section 24 (1)  does not apply in relation to a death if
regulations under section 135(4)(a) of the  Social Services and Well-being
(Wales) Act 2014 (anaw 4)  require a Safeguarding Board to undertake a review
of the death.

26.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the duty in
section 24 (1)  not applying in the case of a death, caused by a person who is
receiving or has received any health services relating to mental health, where
there may be a review of, or investigation into, the provision of that health
care under section 70 of the Health and Social Care (Community Health and
Standards) Act 2003.

##### Notification of Secretary of State

27

27.1

If a review partner becomes aware of qualifying circumstances in relation to a
person’s death, the review partner must notify the Secretary of State before
the end of the notification period of one of the following—

27.1.a

that the review partner is under a duty to arrange for there to be a review
under section 24 of the person’s death,

27.1.b

that the review partner is not under that duty in respect of the death, or

27.1.c

that the review partner has not been able to take a decision on the matter.

27.2

Subsection  (1)  does not apply if, when the review partner becomes aware of
qualifying circumstances in relation to a person’s death, the review partner
is also aware that no duty in section 24(1) arises in respect of the death
because of section 24(5) or 26.

27.3

If a review partner gives a notification under subsection  (1) (c) , the
review partner must notify the Secretary of State of the review partner’s
decision on the matter once it has been taken.

27.4

Where a review partner—

27.4.a

notifies the Secretary of State that the review partner is under a duty to
arrange a review under section 24 of a death, but

27.4.b

before the review starts to take place, decides that the review partner is not
under that duty in respect of that death (see section 24(3) and (4)),

the review partner must notify the Secretary of State of that decision.

27.5

Where a review under section 24 of a death is discontinued because the review
partner considers that a condition mentioned in section 24(1)(a) to (c) is not
satisfied in relation to the death (see section 24(3)), the review partner
must notify the Secretary of State.

27.6

Where a review partner—

27.6.a

notifies the Secretary of State that the review partner is not under a duty to
arrange a review under section 24 of a death, but

27.6.b

afterwards decides that the review partner is under that duty in respect of
that death,

the review partner must notify the Secretary of State of that decision.

27.7

For the purposes of this section, a review partner becomes aware of qualifying
circumstances in relation to a person’s death if the review partner becomes
aware of such facts as make it likely that—

27.7.a

the conditions mentioned in section 24(1)(a) and (b) are satisfied in relation
to the death, and

27.7.b

the review partner is one of the relevant review partners in respect of the
death.

27.8

In this section “ the notification period ”, in relation to notification by a
review partner, means the period of one month beginning with the day on which
the review partner becomes aware of qualifying circumstances in relation to
the death in question.

##### Conduct of review

28

28.1

Where a review under section 24 of a person’s death takes place, the review
partners that arranged it must co-operate in and contribute to the carrying
out of the review.

28.2

The purposes of a review under section 24 are—

28.2.a

to identify the lessons to be learnt from the death, and

28.2.b

to consider whether it would be appropriate for anyone to take action in
respect of those lessons learned.

28.3

Where the review partners consider that it would be appropriate for a person
to take action as mentioned in subsection  (2) (b) , they must inform that
person.

28.4

The review partners must prepare a report on the review and send it to the
Secretary of State.

28.5

The report must include—

28.5.a

the findings of the review,

28.5.b

any conclusions drawn by the review partners, and

28.5.c

recommendations made in light of those findings and conclusions (including
those referred to in subsection  (3) ).

28.6

The review partners must not include in the report sent to the Secretary of
State material that they consider—

28.6.a

might jeopardise the safety of any person, or

28.6.b

might prejudice the investigation or prosecution of an offence.

28.7

The Secretary of State must publish, or make arrangements for the publication
of, the report, unless the Secretary of State considers it inappropriate for
the report to be published.

28.8

If the Secretary of State considers it inappropriate for the report to be
published, the Secretary of State must publish, or make arrangements for the
publication of, so much of the contents of the report as the Secretary of
State considers appropriate to be published.

##### Information

29

29.1

A review partner may request a person to provide information specified in the
request to the review partner or another review partner.

29.2

A review partner may make a request to a person under this section only if the
conditions in subsections  (3)  and  (4)  are satisfied.

29.3

The condition in this subsection is that the request is made for the purpose
of enabling or assisting the performance of functions conferred on a review
partner by sections 24 to 28.

29.4

The condition in this subsection is that the request is made to a person whose
functions or activities are considered by the review partner to be such that
the person is likely to have information that would enable or assist the
performance of functions conferred on a review partner by sections 24 to 28.

29.5

The person to whom a request under this section is made must comply with the
request.

29.6

The review partner that made the request may enforce the duty under subsection
(5)  against the person by making an application to the High Court or the
county court for an injunction.

29.7

A review partner may provide information to another review partner for the
purpose of enabling or assisting the performance of functions under sections
24 to 28.

##### Information: supplementary

30

30.1

A person may not be required under section 29 to disclose information that the
person could not be compelled to disclose in proceedings before the High
Court.

30.2

A disclosure of information required or authorised by sections 27 to 29 does
not breach—

30.2.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

30.2.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

30.3

But sections 27 to 29 do not require or authorise a disclosure of information
that—

30.3.a

would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, the duty imposed or power conferred by the section in
question is to be taken into account), or

30.3.b

is prohibited by any of Parts 1 to 7 or Chapter 1 of Part 9 of the
Investigatory Powers Act 2016.

30.4

Sections 27 to 29 do not affect any duty or power to disclose information
apart from those sections.

30.5

In this section “ data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the
Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3(9) of that Act).

##### Delegating functions

31

31.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision enabling the relevant
review partners in respect of a person’s death to act jointly to appoint—

31.1.a

one of themselves, or

31.1.b

another person,

to carry out on their behalf, in relation to the person’s death, one or more
of the functions specified in the regulations.

31.2

Regulations under subsection  (1)  may specify some or all of the functions of
a review partner under section 28 or 29 relating to a review under section 24
or a report on the review.

31.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision enabling—

31.3.a

a county council, and

31.3.b

a district council for an area that is within the area of the county council,

to agree that one of them carry out on behalf of the other one or more of the
functions specified in the regulations.

31.4

Regulations under subsection  (3)  may specify some or all of the functions of
a review partner under sections 24 to 29.

##### Guidance

32

32.1

Review partners must have regard to any guidance issued by the Secretary of
State in connection with functions conferred on them under sections 24 to 31.

32.2

Before issuing guidance under this section, the Secretary of State must
consult—

32.2.a

persons appearing to the Secretary of State to represent review partners,

32.2.b

the Welsh Ministers, so far as the proposed guidance relates to a devolved
Welsh authority, and

32.2.c

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

32.3

After issuing guidance under this section, the Secretary of State must lay a
copy of the guidance before Parliament.

##### Power to pay grant: local health boards

33

Section 31(2) to (5) of the Local Government Act 2003 (power of the Secretary
of State to pay grant to local authorities in Wales) applies in relation to
local health boards in Wales and expenditure incurred or to be incurred by
those local health boards in the exercise of their functions under this
Chapter as it applies in relation to local authorities in Wales and
expenditure incurred or to be incurred by those local authorities.

##### Piloting

34

34.1

The Secretary of State may exercise the power in section 208(1) so as to bring
sections 24 to 30, 32 and 33 into force—

34.1.a

for all purposes, and

34.1.b

in relation to the whole of England and Wales,

only if the conditions in subsections  (2)  and  (3)  are met.

34.2

The condition in this subsection is that regulations under section 208(1) have
brought some or all of sections 24 to 30, 32 and 33 into force only—

34.2.a

for one or more specified purposes, or

34.2.b

in relation to one or more specified areas.

34.3

The condition in this subsection is that the Secretary of State has laid
before Parliament a report on the operation of some or all of the provisions
of sections 24 to 31—

34.3.a

for one or more of those purposes, or

34.3.b

in relation to one or more of those areas.

34.4

Regulations under section 208(1) which bring any provision of sections 24 to
30, 32 and 33 into force only for a specified purpose or in relation to a
specified area may—

34.4.a

provide for that provision to be in force for that purpose or in relation to
that area for a specified period;

34.4.b

make transitional or saving provision in connection with that provision
ceasing to be in force at the end of the specified period.

34.5

Regulations containing provision by virtue of subsection  (4) (a)  may be
amended by subsequent regulations under section 208(1) so as to continue any
provision of sections 24 to 30, 32 and 33 in force—

34.5.a

for the specified purpose, or

34.5.b

in relation to the specified area,

for a further specified period.

34.6

In this section “ specified ” means specified in regulations under section
208(1).

##### Regulations

35

35.1

Regulations under this Chapter are to be made by statutory instrument.

35.2

Regulations under this Chapter—

35.2.a

may make different provision for different purposes and different provision
for different areas;

35.2.b

may make consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or
saving provision.

35.3

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this Chapter may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

35.4

Subsection  (3)  does not apply to a statutory instrument containing only
regulations under section 26 (2)  or  (4) .

35.5

A statutory instrument within subsection  (4)  is subject to annulment in
pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

##### Interpretation

36

36.1

In this Chapter—

... “ devolved Welsh authority ” has the meaning given in section 157A of the
Government of Wales Act 2006;   “ integrated care board ” means a body
established under section 14Z25 of the National Health Service Act 2006;   “
local authority ” means— in relation to England— a county council, a district
council, a London borough council, the Common Council of the City of London in
its capacity as a local authority, or the Council of the Isles of Scilly; in
relation to Wales— a county council, or a county borough council; “ local
health board ” means a local health board established under section 11 of the
National Health Service (Wales) Act 2006; “ NHS body ” has the same meaning as
in the National Health Service Act 2006 (see section 275 of that Act); “
review partner ” means— a chief officer of police for a police area in England
or Wales, a local authority,   an integrated care board, or   a local health
board; “ relevant review partner ” has the meaning given by section 25.

36.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

36.2.a

amend the definition of “review partner”, and

36.2.b

make such consequential amendments of this Chapter as appear to the Secretary
of State to be appropriate.

36.3

Before making regulations under subsection  (2) , the Secretary of State must
consult—

36.3.a

such persons as appear to the Secretary of State to represent review partners,

36.3.b

the Welsh Ministers, so far as the proposed regulations relate to a devolved
Welsh authority, and

36.3.c

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

#### Extraction of information from electronic devices

##### Extraction of information from electronic devices: investigations of crime etc

37

37.1

An authorised person may extract information stored on an electronic device
from that device if—

37.1.a

a user of the device has voluntarily provided the device to an authorised
person, and

37.1.b

that user has agreed to the extraction of information from the device by an
authorised person.

37.2

The power in subsection  (1)  may be exercised only for the purposes of—

37.2.a

preventing, detecting, investigating or prosecuting crime,

37.2.b

helping to locate a missing person, or

37.2.c

protecting a child or an at-risk adult from neglect or physical, mental or
emotional harm.

37.3

The reference in subsection  (2)  to crime is a reference to—

37.3.a

conduct which constitutes one or more criminal offences in any part of the
United Kingdom, or

37.3.b

conduct which, if it took place in any part of the United Kingdom, would
constitute one or more criminal offences.

37.4

For the purposes of subsection  (2)  an adult is an at-risk adult if the
authorised person reasonably believes that the adult—

37.4.a

is experiencing, or at risk of, neglect or physical, mental or emotional harm,
and

37.4.b

is unable to protect themselves against the neglect or harm or the risk of it.

37.5

An authorised person may exercise the power in subsection  (1)  only if—

37.5.a

in a case where the authorised person proposes to exercise the power for a
purpose within subsection  (2)(a) , the authorised person reasonably believes
that information stored on the electronic device is relevant to a reasonable
line of enquiry which is being, or is to be, pursued by an authorised person,

37.5.b

in a case where the authorised person proposes to exercise the power for a
purpose within subsection  (2)(b)  or  (c) , the authorised person reasonably
believes that information stored on the electronic device is relevant to that
purpose, and

37.5.c

in any case, the authorised person is satisfied that exercise of the power is
necessary and proportionate to achieve the purpose within subsection  (2)  for
which the person proposes to exercise the power.

37.6

Subsection  (7)  applies if the authorised person thinks that, in exercising
the power, there is a risk of obtaining information other than—

37.6.a

information necessary for a purpose within subsection  (2)  for which the
authorised person may exercise the power, or

37.6.b

information necessary for a purpose within subsection  (2)  of section 41
(investigations of death) for which the authorised person may exercise the
power in subsection  (1)  of that section.

37.7

The authorised person must, to be satisfied that the exercise of the power in
subsection  (1)  is proportionate, be satisfied that—

37.7.a

there are no other means of obtaining the information sought by the authorised
person which avoid that risk, or

37.7.b

there are such other means, but it is not reasonably practicable to use them.

37.8

Subsection  (9)  applies if the authorised person thinks that, in exercising
the power in subsection (1), there is a risk of obtaining confidential
information.

37.9

The authorised person must, to be satisfied that the exercise of the power is
proportionate—

37.9.a

have regard to the matters in subsection  (10) , and

37.9.b

be satisfied that—

37.9.b.i

there are no other means of obtaining the information sought by the authorised
person which avoid that risk, or

37.9.b.ii

there are such other means, but it is not reasonably practicable to use them.

37.10

The matters referred to in subsection  (9)(a)  are—

37.10.a

the amount of confidential information likely to be stored on the device, and

37.10.b

the potential relevance of the confidential information to—

37.10.b.i

a purpose within subsection (2) for which the authorised person may exercise
the power, or

37.10.b.ii

a purpose within subsection (2) of section 41 for which the authorised person
may exercise the power in subsection (1) of that section.

37.11

An authorised person must have regard to the code of practice for the time
being in force under section 42 in exercising, or deciding whether to
exercise, the power in subsection  (1) .

37.12

This section does not affect any power relating to the extraction or
production of information, or any power to seize any item or obtain any
information, conferred by an enactment or rule of law.

37.13

In this Chapter—

      “ adult ” means a person aged 18 or over;           “ authorised person
” has the meaning given by subsection  (1)  of section 44 (subject to
subsections  (2)  and  (3)  of that section);           “ child ” means a
person aged under 18;           “ confidential information ” has the meaning
given by section 43;           “ criminal offence ” includes—         a
service offence within the meaning of the Armed Forces Act 2006, and
an SDA offence within the meaning of the Armed Forces Act 2006 (Transitional
Provisions etc) Order 2009 ( S.I. 2009/1059 );                 “ electronic
device ” means any device on which information is capable of being stored
electronically and includes any component of such a device;           “
enactment ” includes—         an enactment contained in subordinate
legislation within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978,           an
enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish
Parliament,           an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made
under, an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru, and           an enactment contained
in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland legislation;
“ information ” includes moving or still images and sounds;           “ user
”, in relation to an electronic device, means a person who ordinarily uses the
device.

37.14

References in this Chapter to the extraction of information include its
reproduction in any form.

37.15

This section is subject to sections 38 (children, and adults without
capacity), 39 (requirements for voluntary provision and agreement) and 40
(persons who have died etc).

##### Application of section 37 to children and adults without capacity

38

38.1

A child is not to be treated for the purposes of section 37 (1)  as being
capable of—

38.1.a

voluntarily providing an electronic device to an authorised person for those
purposes, or

38.1.b

agreeing for those purposes to the extraction of information from the device
by an authorised person.

38.2

If a child is a user of an electronic device, a person who is not a user of
the device but is listed in subsection  (3)  may—

38.2.a

voluntarily provide the device to an authorised person for the purposes of
section 37 (1) , and

38.2.b

agree for those purposes to the extraction of information from the device by
an authorised person.

38.3

The persons mentioned in subsection  (2)  are—

38.3.a

a parent or guardian of the child or, if the child is in the care of a
relevant authority or voluntary organisation, a person representing that
authority or organisation, or

38.3.b

if no person within paragraph  (a)  is available, any responsible person who
is aged 18 or over other than a relevant authorised person.

38.4

Before exercising the power under section 37 (1)  by virtue of subsection  (2)
, an authorised person must, so far as it is reasonably practicable to do so—

38.4.a

ascertain the views of the child, and

38.4.b

have regard to any views so ascertained, taking account of the child’s age and
maturity.

38.5

If an authorised person (“ A ”) exercises the power under section 37 (1)  as a
result of action taken under subsection  (2)  by a person within subsection
(3) (b), A must, unless A considers that it is not appropriate to do so,
inform a person within subsection  (3) (a) that A has exercised the power.

38.6

An adult without capacity is not to be treated for the purposes of section 37
(1)  as being capable of—

38.6.a

voluntarily providing an electronic device to an authorised person for those
purposes, or

38.6.b

agreeing for those purposes to the extraction of information from the device
by an authorised person.

38.7

If a user of an electronic device is an adult without capacity, a person who
is not a user of the device but is listed in subsection  (8)  may—

38.7.a

voluntarily provide the device to an authorised person for the purposes of
section 37 (1) , and

38.7.b

agree for those purposes to the extraction of information from the device by
an authorised person.

38.8

The persons mentioned in subsection  (7)  are—

38.8.a

a parent or guardian of the adult without capacity or, if the adult without
capacity is in the care of a relevant authority or voluntary organisation, a
person representing that authority or organisation,

38.8.b

a registered social worker,

38.8.c

a person who, under a power of attorney, may make decisions for the purposes
of subsection  (7) (a) and (b) on behalf of the adult without capacity,

38.8.d

a deputy appointed under section 16 of the Mental Capacity Act 2005 or section
113 of the Mental Capacity Act (Northern Ireland) 2016 who may make decisions
for the purposes of subsection  (7) (a) and (b) on behalf of the adult without
capacity by virtue of that appointment,

38.8.e

a person authorised under an intervention order under section 53 of the Adults
with Incapacity (Scotland) Act  2000 (asp 4)  who may make decisions for the
purposes of subsection  (7) (a) and (b) on behalf of the adult without
capacity by virtue of that authorisation, or

38.8.f

if no person within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (e)  is available, any
responsible person who is aged 18 or over other than a relevant authorised
person.

38.9

Nothing in this section prevents any other user of an electronic device who is
not a child or an adult without capacity from—

38.9.a

voluntarily providing the device to an authorised person for the purposes of
section 37 (1) , or

38.9.b

agreeing for those purposes to the extraction of information from the device
by an authorised person.

38.10

For the purposes of this Chapter a person is an adult without capacity if—

38.10.a

in relation to England and Wales, the person is an adult who, within the
meaning of the Mental Capacity Act 2005, lacks capacity to do the things
mentioned in section 37 (1) (a) and (b);

38.10.b

in relation to Scotland, the person is an adult (within the meaning of this
Chapter) who is incapable within the meaning of the Adults with Incapacity
(Scotland) Act 2000 in relation to the matters mentioned in section 37 (1) (a)
and (b);

38.10.c

in relation to Northern Ireland, the person is an adult who, within the
meaning of the Mental Capacity Act (Northern Ireland) 2016, lacks capacity to
do the things mentioned in section 37 (1) (a) and (b).

38.11

In this Chapter—

      “local authority”—         in relation to England, means a county
council, a district council for an area for which there is no county council,
a London borough council or the Common Council of the City of London in its
capacity as a local authority;           in relation to Wales, means a county
council or a county borough council;           in relation to Scotland, means
a council constituted under section 2 of the Local Government etc (Scotland)
Act 1994;                 “ registered social worker ” means a person
registered as a social worker in a register maintained by—         Social Work
England,           the Care Council for Wales,           the Scottish Social
Services Council, or           the Northern Ireland Social Care Council;
“ relevant authorised person ”, in relation to the extraction of information
from an electronic device for a particular purpose, means an authorised person
who may extract the information from the device for that purpose;
“relevant authority”—         in relation to England and Wales and Scotland,
means a local authority;           in relation to Northern Ireland, means an
authority within the meaning of the Children (Northern Ireland) Order 1995 (
S.I. 1995/755 (N.I. 2) );                 “voluntary organisation”—         in
relation to England and Wales, has the same meaning as in the Children Act
1989;           in relation to Scotland, has the same meaning as in Part 2 of
the Children (Scotland) Act 1995;           in relation to Northern Ireland,
has the same meaning as in the Children (Northern Ireland) Order 1995.

38.12

This section is subject to section 39 (requirements for voluntary provision
and agreement).

##### Requirements for voluntary provision and agreement

39

39.1

A person (“ P ”) is to be treated for the purposes of section 37 or 38 as
having—

39.1.a

voluntarily provided an electronic device to an authorised person, and

39.1.b

agreed to the extraction of information from the device by an authorised
person,

only if the requirements of this section have been met.

39.2

An authorised person must not have placed undue pressure on P to provide the
device or agree to the extraction of information from it.

39.3

An authorised person must have given P notice in writing—

39.3.a

specifying or describing the information that is sought,

39.3.b

specifying the reason why the information is sought,

39.3.c

specifying how the information will be dealt with once it has been extracted,

39.3.d

stating that P may refuse to provide the device or agree to the extraction of
information from it, and

39.3.e

stating that the investigation or enquiry for the purposes of which the
information is sought will not be brought to an end merely because P refuses
to provide the device or agree to the extraction of information from it.

39.4

Subject to subsection  (5) , P must have confirmed in writing that P has—

39.4.a

voluntarily provided the device to an authorised person, and

39.4.b

agreed to the extraction of information from the device by an authorised
person.

39.5

If P was unable to provide that confirmation in writing as a result of P’s
physical impairment or lack of literacy skills—

39.5.a

P must have given that confirmation orally, and

39.5.b

an authorised person must have recorded P’s confirmation in writing.

39.6

If P’s confirmation was given in writing and in hard copy form, the authorised
person must have given P a copy of that confirmation (in hard copy or
electronic form).

39.7

If P’s confirmation was given orally, the authorised person must have given P
a copy of the record of that confirmation (in hard copy or electronic form).

##### Application of section 37 where user has died etc

40

40.1

If any of conditions A to C is met, an authorised person may exercise the
power in section 37 (1)  to extract information stored on an electronic device
from that device even though—

40.1.a

the device has not been voluntarily provided to an authorised person by a user
of the device, or

40.1.b

no user of the device has agreed to the extraction of information from the
device by an authorised person.

40.2

Condition A is that—

40.2.a

a person who was a user of the electronic device has died, and

40.2.b

the person was a user of the device immediately before their death.

40.3

Condition B is that—

40.3.a

a user of the electronic device is a child or an adult without capacity, and

40.3.b

an authorised person reasonably believes that the user’s life is at risk or
there is a risk of serious harm to the user.

40.4

Condition C is that—

40.4.a

a person who was a user of the electronic device is missing,

40.4.b

the person was a user of the device immediately before they went missing, and

40.4.c

an authorised person reasonably believes that the person’s life is at risk or
there is a risk of serious harm to the person.

40.5

The exercise of the power in subsection  (1)  of section 37 by virtue of this
section is subject to that section.

##### Extraction of information from electronic devices: investigations of death

41

41.1

An authorised person may extract information stored on an electronic device
from that device if—

41.1.a

a person who was a user of the electronic device has died, and

41.1.b

the person was a user of the device immediately before their death.

41.2

The power in subsection  (1)  may be exercised only for the purposes of—

41.2.a

an investigation into the person’s death under Chapter 1 of Part 1 of the
Coroners and Justice Act 2009,

41.2.b

an inquest into the person’s death under the Coroners Act (Northern Ireland)
1959, or

41.2.c

an investigation into the person’s death by the Lord Advocate.

41.3

References in subsection  (2)  to the exercise of the power in subsection (1)
for the purposes of an investigation or inquest include references to the
exercise of that power for the purposes of determining whether an
investigation should be conducted or an inquest should be held.

41.4

An authorised person may exercise the power in subsection  (1)  only if—

41.4.a

the authorised person reasonably believes that information stored on the
electronic device is relevant to a purpose within subsection  (2) , and

41.4.b

the authorised person is satisfied that exercise of the power is necessary and
proportionate to achieve that purpose.

41.5

Subsection  (6)  applies if the authorised person thinks that, in exercising
the power, there is a risk of obtaining information other than—

41.5.a

information necessary for a purpose within subsection  (2) , or

41.5.b

information necessary for a purpose within section 37 (2) .

41.6

The authorised person must, to be satisfied that the exercise of the power is
proportionate, be satisfied that—

41.6.a

there are no other means of obtaining the information sought by the authorised
person which avoid that risk, or

41.6.b

there are such other means, but it is not reasonably practicable to use them.

41.7

Subsection  (8)  applies if the authorised person thinks that, in exercising
the power in subsection (1), there is a risk of obtaining confidential
information.

41.8

The authorised person must, to be satisfied that the exercise of the power is
proportionate—

41.8.a

have regard to the matters in subsection  (9) , and

41.8.b

be satisfied that—

41.8.b.i

there are no other means of obtaining the information sought by the authorised
person which avoid that risk, or

41.8.b.ii

there are such other means, but it is not reasonably practicable to use them.

41.9

The matters referred to in subsection  (8)(a)  are—

41.9.a

the amount of confidential information likely to be stored on the device, and

41.9.b

the potential relevance of the confidential information to a purpose within
subsection (2) or section 37(2).

41.10

An authorised person must have regard to the code of practice for the time
being in force under section 42 in exercising, or deciding whether to
exercise, the power in subsection  (1) .

41.11

This section does not affect any power relating to the extraction or
production of information, or any power to seize any item or obtain any
information, conferred by an enactment or rule of law.

##### Code of practice about the extraction of information

42

42.1

The Secretary of State must prepare a code of practice containing guidance
about the exercise of the powers in sections 37(1) and 41(1).

42.2

The code may make different provision for different purposes or areas.

42.3

In preparing the code, the Secretary of State must consult—

42.3.a

the Information Commissioner,

42.3.b

the Scottish Ministers,

42.3.c

the Department of Justice in Northern Ireland,

42.3.d

the Commissioner for Victims and Witnesses,

42.3.e

the Domestic Abuse Commissioner,

42.3.f

the Commission for Victims and Survivors for Northern Ireland, and

42.3.g

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

42.4

Subsection  (3)(f)  does not apply on or after the day appointed under Article
4(4) of the Victims and Survivors (Northern Ireland) Order 2006 ( S.I.
2006/2953 (N.I. 17) ) (power to revoke Article 4).

42.5

After preparing the code, the Secretary of State must lay it before Parliament
and publish it.

42.6

The code is to be brought into force by regulations made by statutory
instrument.

42.7

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (6)  is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

42.8

After the code has come into force the Secretary of State may from time to
time revise it.

42.9

A failure on the part of an authorised person to act in accordance with the
code does not of itself render the person liable to any criminal or civil
proceedings.

42.10

But the code is admissible in evidence in criminal or civil proceedings and a
court may take into account a failure to act in accordance with it in
determining a question in the proceedings.

42.11

References in subsections  (2)  to  (10)  to the code include a revised code,
subject to subsection  (12) .

42.12

The duty to consult in subsection  (3)  does not apply in relation to the
preparation of a revised code if the Secretary of State considers that the
proposed revisions are insubstantial.

##### Confidential information

43

43.1

In this Chapter “ confidential information ” means information which
constitutes or may constitute—

43.1.a

confidential journalistic material within the meaning of the Investigatory
Powers Act 2016 (see section 264(6) and (7) of that Act), or

43.1.b

protected material.

43.2

In subsection  (1) (b) “protected material”—

43.2.a

in relation to England and Wales means—

43.2.a.i

items subject to legal privilege, within the meaning of the Police and
Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (see section 10 of that Act),

43.2.a.ii

material falling within section 11(1)(a) of that Act (certain personal records
held in confidence), or

43.2.a.iii

material to which section 14(2) of that Act applies (other material acquired
in the course of a trade etc that is held in confidence);

43.2.b

in relation to Scotland means—

43.2.b.i

items in respect of which a claim to confidentiality of communications could
be maintained in legal proceedings, or

43.2.b.ii

other material of a kind mentioned in paragraph (a)(ii) or (iii) of this
subsection;

43.2.c

in relation to Northern Ireland, means—

43.2.c.i

items subject to legal privilege, within the meaning of the Police and
Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I. 12) )
(see Article 12 of that Order),

43.2.c.ii

material falling with Article 13(1)(a) of that Order (certain personal records
held in confidence), or

43.2.c.iii

material to which Article 16(2) of that Order applies (other material acquired
in the course of a trade etc that is held in confidence).

##### Authorised persons

44

44.1

Subject to subsections  (2)  and  (3) , in this Chapter “ authorised person ”
means a person listed in Schedule 3.

44.2

The power in subsection  (1)  of section 37 may be exercised for a purpose
mentioned in subsection  (2) (b)  or  (c)  of that section only by a person
listed in Part 1 or 2 of Schedule 3.

44.3

The power in section 41 (1)  may be exercised only by a person listed in Part
1 of Schedule 3.

44.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument amend
Schedule 3—

44.4.a

so as to add a reference to a person;

44.4.b

so as to remove a reference to a person;

44.4.c

so as to modify a description of a person mentioned in that Schedule.

44.5

Regulations under subsection  (4)  may contain transitional, transitory or
saving provision.

44.6

The Secretary of State must consult the Scottish Ministers before making
regulations under subsection  (4)  if and so far as the regulations make
provision that would be within the legislative competence of the Scottish
Parliament if it were contained in an Act of that Parliament.

44.7

The Secretary of State must consult the Department of Justice in Northern
Ireland before making regulations under subsection  (4)  if and so far as the
regulations make provision that, if it were contained in an Act of the
Northern Ireland Assembly—

44.7.a

would be within the legislative competence of that Assembly, and

44.7.b

would not require the consent of the Secretary of State.

44.8

Subject to subsection  (9) , a statutory instrument containing regulations
under subsection  (4) (a)  (whether alone or with other provision) may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

44.9

Subsection  (8)  does not apply to a statutory instrument containing
regulations which—

44.9.a

remove a reference to a person from Part 1 of Schedule 3 and add a reference
to that person to Part 2 or 3 of that Schedule, or

44.9.b

remove a reference to a person from Part 2 of that Schedule and add a
reference to that person to Part 3 of that Schedule.

44.10

A statutory instrument containing—

44.10.a

regulations under subsection  (4) (a)  to which subsection  (9)  applies, or

44.10.b

regulations under subsection  (4) (b)  or  (c) ,

and which is not a statutory instrument to which subsection  (8)  applies is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

#### Other provisions

##### Pre-charge bail

###### Pre-charge bail

45

45.1

Schedule 4 contains amendments relating to pre-charge bail.

45.2

In that Schedule—

45.2.a

Part 1 makes provision relating to the grant of pre-charge bail,

45.2.b

Part 2 makes provision about the factors to be taken into account in
determining whether to grant pre-charge bail,

45.2.c

Part 3 makes provision requiring the views of alleged victims to be sought in
relation to the grant or variation of pre-charge bail subject to conditions,

45.2.d

Part 4 makes provision relating to limits on periods of pre-charge bail,

45.2.e

Part 5 makes provision about the determination of a period of police detention
following a person’s arrest for breach of pre-charge bail, and

45.2.f

Part 6 makes provision for guidance about pre-charge bail.

45.3

An amendment made by Schedule 4—

45.3.a

applies in relation to a person arrested for an offence only if the person was
arrested for the offence after the coming into force of that amendment,

45.3.b

applies in relation to a person arrested under section 46A of the Police and
Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (failure to answer to police bail etc) only if the
person was arrested after the coming into force of that amendment for the
offence for which the person was originally released on bail, and

45.3.c

applies in relation to a person arrested under section 24A of the Criminal
Justice Act 2003 (failure to comply with conditional caution) only if the
person was arrested after the coming into force of that amendment for the
offence in respect of which the caution was given.

###### Positions of trust

47

47.1

The Sexual Offences Act 2003 is amended as follows.

47.2

After section 22 insert—

############ Further positions of trust

47.2.22A

47.2.22A.1

For the purposes of sections 16 to 19, a person (A) is in a position of trust
in relation to another person (B) if—

47.2.22A.1.a

A coaches, teaches, trains, supervises or instructs B, on a regular basis, in
a sport or a religion, and

47.2.22A.1.b

A knows that they coach, teach, train, supervise or instruct B, on a regular
basis, in that sport or religion.

47.2.22A.2

In subsection (1)—

“ sport ” includes— any game in which physical skill is the predominant
factor, and any form of physical recreation which is also engaged in for
purposes of competition or display; “ religion ” includes— a religion which
involves belief in more than one god, and a religion which does not involve
belief in a god.

47.2.22A.3

This section does not apply where a person (A) is in a position of trust in
relation to another person (B) by virtue of circumstances within section 21.

47.2.22A.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend subsections (1) and (2) to add
or remove an activity in which a person may be coached, taught, trained,
supervised or instructed.

47.3

In section 138(2) (orders and regulations) after “section 21,” insert  “22A,”
.

###### Voyeurism: breast-feeding

48

48.1

Section 67A of the Sexual Offences Act 2003 (voyeurism: additional offences)
is amended as follows.

48.2

After subsection (2) insert—

48.2.2A

A person (A) commits an offence if—

48.2.2A.a

A operates equipment,

48.2.2A.b

A does so with the intention of enabling A or another person (C), for a
purpose mentioned in subsection (3), to observe another (B) while B is breast-
feeding a child, and

48.2.2A.c

A does so—

48.2.2A.c.i

without B’s consent, and

48.2.2A.c.ii

without reasonably believing that B consents.

48.2.2B

A person (A) commits an offence if—

48.2.2B.a

A records an image of another (B) while B is breast-feeding a child,

48.2.2B.b

A does so with the intention that A or another person (C) will look at the
image for a purpose mentioned in subsection (3), and

48.2.2B.c

A does so—

48.2.2B.c.i

without B’s consent, and

48.2.2B.c.ii

without reasonably believing that B consents.

48.3

In subsection (3), for “and (2)” substitute  “to (2B)” .

48.4

After subsection (3) insert—

48.4.3A

In this section a reference to B breast-feeding a child includes B re-
arranging B’s clothing—

48.4.3A.a

in the course of preparing to breast-feed the child, or

48.4.3A.b

having just finished breast-feeding the child.

48.4.3B

It is irrelevant for the purposes of subsections (2A) and (2B)—

48.4.3B.a

whether or not B is in a public place while B is breast-feeding the child,

48.4.3B.b

whether or not B’s breasts are exposed while B is breast-feeding the child,
and

48.4.3B.c

what part of B’s body—

48.4.3B.c.i

is, or is intended by A to be, visible in the recorded image, or

48.4.3B.c.ii

is intended by A to be observed.

##### Domestic abuse

###### Time limit for prosecution of common assault or battery in domestic abuse cases

49

After section 39 of the Criminal Justice Act 1988 insert—

########## Time limit for prosecution of common assault or battery in domestic abuse cases

49.39A

49.39A.1

This section applies to proceedings for an offence of common assault or
battery where—

49.39A.1.a

the alleged behaviour of the accused amounts to domestic abuse, and

49.39A.1.b

the condition in subsection (2) or (3) is met.

49.39A.2

The condition in this subsection is that—

49.39A.2.a

the complainant has made a witness statement with a view to its possible
admission as evidence in the proceedings, and

49.39A.2.b

the complainant has provided the statement to—

49.39A.2.b.i

a constable of a police force, or

49.39A.2.b.ii

a person authorised by a constable of a police force to receive the statement.

49.39A.3

The condition in this subsection is that—

49.39A.3.a

the complainant has been interviewed by—

49.39A.3.a.i

a constable of a police force, or

49.39A.3.a.ii

a person authorised by a constable of a police force to interview the
complainant, and

49.39A.3.b

a video recording of the interview has been made with a view to its possible
admission as the complainant’s evidence in chief in the proceedings.

49.39A.4

Proceedings to which this section applies may be commenced at any time which
is both—

49.39A.4.a

within two years from the date of the offence to which the proceedings relate,
and

49.39A.4.b

within six months from the first date on which either of the conditions in
subsection (2) or (3) was met.

49.39A.5

This section has effect despite section 127(1) of the Magistrates’ Court Act
1980 (limitation of time).

49.39A.6

In this section—

“ domestic abuse ” has the meaning given by section 1 of the Domestic Abuse
Act 2021; “ police force ” has the meaning given by section 3(3) of the
Prosecution of Offences Act 1985; “ video recording ” has the meaning given by
section 63(1) of the Youth Justice and Criminal Evidence Act 1999; “ witness
statement ” means a written statement that satisfies the conditions in section
9(2)(a) and (b) of the Criminal Justice Act 1967.

49.39A.7

This section does not apply in relation to an offence committed before the
coming into force of section 49 of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts
Act 2022.

##### Criminal damage to memorials

###### Criminal damage to memorials: mode of trial

50

50.1

In Schedule 2 to the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980 (offences for which the
value involved is relevant to the mode of trial), in paragraph 1 (offences
under section 1 of the Criminal Damage Act 1971), in the first column, for the
words from “any offence” to the end substitute

— any offence committed by destroying or damaging property by fire, and any
offence committed by destroying or damaging a memorial (see section 22 (11A)
to  (11D) ).

50.2

In section 22 of that Act, after subsection (11) insert—

50.2.11A

In paragraph 1 of Schedule 2 “ memorial ” means—

50.2.11A.a

a building or other structure, or any other thing, erected or installed on
land (or in or on any building or other structure on land), or

50.2.11A.b

a garden or any other thing planted or grown on land,

which has a commemorative purpose.

50.2.11B

For the purposes of that paragraph, any moveable thing (such as a bunch of
flowers) which—

50.2.11B.a

is left in, on or at a memorial within the meaning of subsection (11A), and

50.2.11B.b

has (or can reasonably be assumed to have) a commemorative purpose,

is also to be regarded as a memorial.

50.2.11C

For the purposes of subsections  (11A)  and  (11B) —

50.2.11C.a

references to a building or a structure include a reference to part of a
building or part of a structure (as the case may be), and

50.2.11C.b

something has a commemorative purpose if at least one of its purposes is to
commemorate—

50.2.11C.b.i

one or more individuals or animals (or a particular description of individuals
or animals), or

50.2.11C.b.ii

an event or a series of events (such as an armed conflict).

50.2.11D

It is immaterial for the purposes of subsection  (11C)(b)(i)  whether or not
any individuals or animals concerned are or were (at any material time)—

50.2.11D.a

living or deceased, or

50.2.11D.b

capable of being identified.

50.3

The amendments made by this section do not apply in relation to offences
committed before it comes into force.

##### Overseas production orders

###### Overseas production orders

51

Schedule 5 contains amendments to the Crime (Overseas Production Orders) Act
2019.

##### Amendments to the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 etc

###### Power to photograph certain persons at a police station

52

52.1

The Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 is amended as follows.

52.2

In section 64A (photographing of suspects etc.), after subsection (1B) insert—

52.2.1C

A person to whom subsection (1) or (1A) does not apply may be photographed at
a police station without the appropriate consent if that person falls within
subsection  (1D) ,  (1F)  or  (1H) .

52.2.1D

A person falls within this subsection if (before or after the coming into
force of this subsection) that person has been—

52.2.1D.a

arrested for a recordable offence and released,

52.2.1D.b

charged with a recordable offence, or

52.2.1D.c

informed that they will be reported for such an offence,

and either of the conditions in subsection  (1E)  is met in relation to that
person.

52.2.1E

The conditions referred to in subsection  (1D)  are—

52.2.1E.a

that the person has not been photographed in the course of the investigation
of the offence by the police, or

52.2.1E.b

that the person has been so photographed but—

52.2.1E.b.i

any photograph taken on such a previous occasion is unavailable or inadequate,
and

52.2.1E.b.ii

a constable considers that taking a further photograph is necessary to assist
in the prevention or detection of crime.

52.2.1F

A person falls within this subsection if (before or after the coming into
force of this subsection) that person has been—

52.2.1F.a

convicted of a recordable offence, or

52.2.1F.b

given a caution in respect of a recordable offence which, at the time of the
caution they have admitted,

and either of the conditions in subsection  (1G)  is met in relation to that
person.

52.2.1G

The conditions referred to in subsection  (1F)  are—

52.2.1G.a

that the person has not been photographed since being convicted or cautioned,
or

52.2.1G.b

that the person has been so photographed but—

52.2.1G.b.i

any photograph taken on such a previous occasion is unavailable or inadequate,
and

52.2.1G.b.ii

a constable considers that taking a further photograph is necessary to assist
in the prevention or detection of crime.

52.2.1H

A person falls within this subsection if—

52.2.1H.a

under the law in force in a country or territory outside England and Wales the
person has been convicted of an offence under that law (whether before or
after the coming into force of this subsection and whether or not they have
been punished for it),

52.2.1H.b

the act constituting the offence would constitute a qualifying offence if done
in England and Wales (whether or not it constituted such an offence when the
person was convicted), and

52.2.1H.c

either of the conditions in subsection  (1I)  is met in relation to that
person.

52.2.1I

The conditions referred to in subsection  (1H)  are—

52.2.1I.a

that the person has not been photographed on a previous occasion by virtue of
being a person falling within subsection (1H), or

52.2.1I.b

that the person has been so photographed but—

52.2.1I.b.i

any photograph taken on such a previous occasion is unavailable or inadequate,
and

52.2.1I.b.ii

a constable considers that taking a further photograph is necessary to assist
in the prevention or detection of crime.

52.2.1J

A person who falls within subsection  (1F)  or  (1H)  may be photographed
under subsection (1C) only with the authorisation of an officer of at least
the rank of inspector.

52.2.1K

An officer may only give an authorisation under subsection (1J) if the officer
is satisfied that taking the photograph is necessary to assist in the
prevention or detection of crime.

52.2.1L

In subsections (1E), (1G) and (1I)—

52.2.1L.a

references to a photograph being unavailable include references to a
photograph being lost or destroyed, and

52.2.1L.b

references to a photograph being inadequate include references to a photograph
being—

52.2.1L.b.i

unclear,

52.2.1L.b.ii

an incomplete photograph of the subject, or

52.2.1L.b.iii

no longer an accurate representation of the subject’s appearance.

52.2.1M

In subsections (1E), (1G), (1I) and (1K) references to crime include
references to any conduct which—

52.2.1M.a

constitutes one or more criminal offences (whether under the law of a part of
the United Kingdom or of a country or territory outside the United Kingdom),
or

52.2.1M.b

is, or corresponds to, any conduct which, if it all took place in any one part
of the United Kingdom, would constitute one or more criminal offences.

52.3

Schedule 2A (fingerprinting and samples: power to require attendance at police
station) is amended in accordance with subsections (4) to (8).

52.4

In the heading of the Schedule, for “and samples” substitute  “, samples and
photographs” .

52.5

After Part 3 insert—

############ Photographs

############# Persons arrested and released

52.5.14A

52.5.14A.1

A constable may require a person who falls within section 64A(1D)(a) to attend
a police station to be photographed under section 64A(1C).

52.5.14A.2

The power under sub-paragraph (1) may not be exercised in a case where section
64A(1E)(b) applies (photograph taken on a previous occasion unavailable or
inadequate) after the end of the period of six months beginning with the day
on which the appropriate officer was informed that section 64(1E)(b)(i)
applied.

52.5.14A.3

In sub-paragraph (2) the “ appropriate officer ” means the officer
investigating the offence for which the person was arrested.

############# Persons charged etc.

52.5.14B

52.5.14B.1

A constable may require a person who falls within section 64A(1D)(b) or (c) to
attend a police station to be photographed under section 64A(1C).

52.5.14B.2

The power under sub-paragraph (1) may not be exercised after the end of the
period of six months beginning with—

52.5.14B.2.a

in a case where section 64A(1E)(a) applies (photograph not previously taken),
the day on which the person was charged or informed that they would be
reported, or

52.5.14B.2.b

in a case where section 64A(1E)(b) applies (photograph taken on a previous
occasion unavailable or inadequate), the day on which the appropriate officer
was informed that section 64A(1E)(b)(i) applied.

52.5.14B.3

In sub-paragraph (2)(b) the “ appropriate officer ” means the officer
investigating the offence for which the person was charged or informed that
they would be reported.

############# Persons convicted of an offence etc. in England and Wales

52.5.14C

52.5.14C.1

A constable may require a person who falls within section 64A(1F) to attend a
police station to be photographed under section 64A(1C).

52.5.14C.2

Where section 64A(1G)(a) applies (photographs not previously taken), the power
under sub-paragraph (1) may not be exercised after the end of the period of
two years beginning with—

52.5.14C.2.a

the day on which the person was convicted or cautioned, or

52.5.14C.2.b

if later, the day on which this Part comes into force.

52.5.14C.3

Where section 64A(1G)(b) applies (photograph taken on previous occasion
unavailable or inadequate), the power under sub-paragraph (1) may not be
exercised after the end of the period of two years beginning with—

52.5.14C.3.a

the day on which an appropriate officer was informed that section
64A(1G)(b)(i) applied, or

52.5.14C.3.b

if later, the day on which this Part comes into force.

52.5.14C.4

In sub-paragraph (3)(a), “ appropriate officer ” means an officer of the
police force which investigated the offence in question.

52.5.14C.5

Sub-paragraphs (2) and (3) do not apply where the offence is a qualifying
offence (whether or not it was such an offence at the time of the conviction
or caution).

############# Persons convicted of an offence etc. outside England and Wales

52.5.14D

A constable may require a person falling within section 64A(1H) to attend at a
police station to be photographed under section 64A(1C).

############# Multiple exercise of power

52.5.14E

52.5.14E.1

Where a photograph is taken of a person under section 64A on two occasions in
relation to any offence, the person may not under this Schedule be required to
attend a police station to be photographed under that section in relation to
that offence on a subsequent occasion without the authorisation of an officer
of at least the rank of inspector.

52.5.14E.2

Where an authorisation is given under sub-paragraph (1)—

52.5.14E.2.a

the fact of the authorisation, and

52.5.14E.2.b

the reasons for giving it,

must be recorded as soon as practicable after it has been given.

52.6

In the italic heading before paragraph 15 (requirement to have power to take
fingerprints or sample), for “or sample” substitute  “, sample or photograph”
.

52.7

In paragraph 15—

52.7.a

for “or a sample” substitute  “, a sample or a photograph” , and

52.7.b

for “or sample”, in both places it occurs, substitute  “, sample or
photograph” .

52.8

In paragraph 16(2) (date and time of attendance), for “or sample” substitute
“, sample or photograph” .

###### Power to specify date of attendance at police station for fingerprinting etc

53

53.1

Paragraph 16 of Schedule 2A to the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984
(attendance at police station for fingerprinting and taking of samples: date
and time of attendance) is amended as follows.

53.2

For sub-paragraph (1) substitute—

53.2.1

A requirement under this Schedule—

53.2.1.a

must direct the person to attend the police station on a specified date, and

53.2.1.b

may either direct the person to attend the police station at a specified time
on that date or direct the person to attend the police station between
specified times on that date.

53.3

In sub-paragraph (2), for “period or time or times of day” substitute  “date,
time or times” .

53.4

Omit sub-paragraphs (3) and (4).

53.5

In sub-paragraph (5), for “any period within which, or date or time at which,”
substitute  “any date, time at which or times between which” .

53.6

The amendments made by this section apply only in relation to a requirement to
attend a police station given under Schedule 2A to the Police and Criminal
Evidence Act 1984 after the coming into force of this section.

###### PACE etc powers for food crime officers

54

54.1

In the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984, after section 114B insert—

############ Power to apply Act to food crime officers

54.1.114C

54.1.114C.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations apply any provision of this Act
which relates to investigations of offences conducted by police officers to
investigations of offences conducted by food crime officers.

54.1.114C.2

The regulations may apply provisions of this Act with any modifications
specified in the regulations.

54.1.114C.3

In this section “ food crime officer ” means an officer of the Food Standards
Agency who—

54.1.114C.3.a

is acting for the purposes of the performance by the Food Standards Agency of
its functions under the Food Standards Act 1999 or any other enactment
(including functions relating to the investigation of offences), and

54.1.114C.3.b

is authorised (whether generally or specifically) by the Secretary of State
for the purposes of this section.

54.1.114C.4

The investigations for the purposes of which provisions of this Act may be
applied by regulations under this section include investigations of offences
committed, or suspected of having been committed, before the coming into force
of the regulations or of this section.

54.1.114C.5

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

54.1.114C.6

Regulations under this section may make—

54.1.114C.6.a

different provision for different purposes;

54.1.114C.6.b

provision which applies generally or for particular purposes;

54.1.114C.6.c

incidental, supplementary, consequential, transitional or transitory provision
or savings.

54.1.114C.7

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this section is subject to
annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

54.1.114C.8

In this section “ enactment ” includes—

54.1.114C.8.a

an enactment comprised in subordinate legislation within the meaning of the
Interpretation Act 1978, and

54.1.114C.8.b

an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, a Measure or Act of
Senedd Cymru.

54.2

In the Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994, after section 39 insert—

############ Power to apply sections 36 and 37 in relation to food crime officers

54.2.39A

54.2.39A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for any provision of section
36 or 37 that applies in relation to a constable to apply in relation to a
food crime officer.

54.2.39A.2

Regulations under subsection  (1)  may apply any provision of section 36 or 37
with any modifications specified in the regulations.

54.2.39A.3

Regulations under subsection  (1)  may not apply a provision of section 36 or
37 in relation to a failure or refusal which occurred before the regulations
come into force.

54.2.39A.4

Regulations under subsection  (1)  are to be made by statutory instrument.

54.2.39A.5

Regulations under subsection  (1)  may make—

54.2.39A.5.a

different provision for different purposes;

54.2.39A.5.b

provision which applies generally or for particular purposes;

54.2.39A.5.c

incidental, supplementary, consequential, transitional or transitory provision
or savings.

54.2.39A.6

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (1)  is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

54.2.39A.7

In this section “ food crime officer ” has the meaning given by section  114C
of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (PACE powers for food crime
officers).

54.3

In the Food Standards Act 1999, after section 25 insert—

############ Obstruction of food crime officers

54.3.25A

54.3.25A.1

A person commits an offence if the person—

54.3.25A.1.a

intentionally obstructs a food crime officer who is acting in the exercise of
functions conferred on the officer by virtue of section  114C  of the Police
and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (PACE powers for food crime officers),

54.3.25A.1.b

fails without reasonable excuse to comply with any requirement made of the
person by such a food crime officer who is so acting, or

54.3.25A.1.c

in purported compliance with such a requirement provides information which the
person knows to be false or misleading in any material particular or
recklessly provides information which is false or misleading in any material
particular.

54.3.25A.2

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 3 months or to a fine, or
to both.

54.3.25A.3

In this section “ food crime officer ” has the meaning given by section  114C
of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (PACE powers for food crime
officers).

54.4

In the Police Reform Act 2002—

54.4.a

in section 10 (general functions of the Director General)—

54.4.a.i

in subsection (1), at the end of paragraph (ga) insert

; and

54.4.a.i.gb

to carry out such corresponding functions in relation to officers of the Food
Standards Agency acting in the exercise of functions conferred on them by
virtue of—

54.4.a.i.gb.i

section  114C  of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (PACE powers for
food crime officers), or

54.4.a.i.gb.ii

section 39A of the Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994 (powers for food
crime officers: inferences from silence).

, and

54.4.a.ii

in subsection (3), after paragraph (bd) insert—

54.4.a.ii.be

any regulations under section  26E  of this Act (food crime officers);

, and

54.4.b

after section 26D insert—

############## Food crime officers

54.4.b.26E

54.4.b.26E.1

The Secretary of State may make regulations conferring functions on the
Director General in relation to officers of the Food Standards Agency (the
“Agency”) acting in the exercise of functions conferred on them by virtue of—

54.4.b.26E.1.a

section  114C  of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (PACE powers for
food crime officers), or

54.4.b.26E.1.b

section 39A of the Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994 (powers for food
crime officers: inferences from silence).

54.4.b.26E.2

Regulations under this section may, in particular—

54.4.b.26E.2.a

apply (with or without modifications), or make provision similar to, any
provision of or made under this Part;

54.4.b.26E.2.b

make provision for payment by the Agency to, or in respect of, the Office or
in respect of the Director General.

54.4.b.26E.3

The Director General and the Parliamentary Commissioner for Administration may
jointly investigate a matter in relation to which—

54.4.b.26E.3.a

the Director General has functions by virtue of this section, and

54.4.b.26E.3.b

the Parliamentary Commissioner for Administration has functions by virtue of
the Parliamentary Commissioner Act 1967.

54.4.b.26E.4

An officer of the Agency may disclose information to the Director General or
to a person acting on the Director General’s behalf, for the purposes of the
exercise by the Director General or by any person acting on the Director
General’s behalf, of an Agency complaints function.

54.4.b.26E.5

The Director General and the Parliamentary Commissioner for Administration may
disclose information to each other for the purposes of the exercise of a
function—

54.4.b.26E.5.a

by virtue of this section, or

54.4.b.26E.5.b

under the Parliamentary Commissioner Act 1967.

54.4.b.26E.6

Regulations under this section may, in particular, make—

54.4.b.26E.6.a

further provision about the disclosure of information under subsection  (4)
or  (5) ;

54.4.b.26E.6.b

provision about the further disclosure of information that has been so
disclosed.

54.4.b.26E.7

A disclosure of information authorised by this section does not breach—

54.4.b.26E.7.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

54.4.b.26E.7.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

54.4.b.26E.8

But this section does not authorise a disclosure of information that—

54.4.b.26E.8.a

would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a
disclosure would do so, the power conferred by this section is to be taken
into account), or

54.4.b.26E.8.b

is prohibited by any of Parts 1 to 7 or Chapter 1 of Part 9 of the
Investigatory Powers Act 2016.

54.4.b.26E.9

In this section—

“ Agency complaints function ” means a function in relation to the exercise of
functions by officers of the Agency; “ data protection legislation ” has the
same meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act).

54.5

The amendments made by subsections  (1)  to  (3)  and any regulations made
under provision inserted by subsections  (1)  and  (2)  bind the Crown.

54.6

No contravention by the Crown of section  25A  of the Food Standards Act 1999
(as inserted by subsection  (3) ) makes the Crown criminally liable; but the
High Court may declare unlawful any act or omission of the Crown which
constitutes such a contravention.

54.7

That section applies to persons in the public service of the Crown as it
applies to other persons.

54.8

If the Secretary of State certifies that it appears requisite or expedient in
the interests of national security that any powers of entry conferred by
regulations made under provision inserted by subsection  (1)  should not be
exercisable in relation to any Crown premises specified in the certificate,
those powers shall not be exercisable in relation to those premises.

54.9

In this section “ Crown premises ” means premises held or used by or on behalf
of the Crown.

54.10

Nothing in this section affects Her Majesty in her private capacity; and this
subsection is to be interpreted as if section 38(3) of the Crown Proceedings
Act 1947 (references to Her Majesty in her private capacity) were contained in
this Act.

##### Search for material relating to human remains

###### Entry and search of premises for human remains or material relating to human remains

55

55.1

On an application made by a constable, a justice of the peace may issue a
warrant authorising a constable to enter and search premises if the justice of
the peace is satisfied that the following conditions are met.

55.2

The first condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that
there is material on the premises mentioned in subsection  (5)  that consists
of, or may relate to the location of, relevant human remains.

55.3

The second condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that
the material does not consist of or include—

55.3.a

items subject to legal privilege,

55.3.b

excluded material, or

55.3.c

special procedure material.

55.4

The third condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing, in
relation to each set of premises specified in the application—

55.4.a

that it is not practicable to communicate with any person entitled to grant
entry to the premises,

55.4.b

that it is practicable to communicate with a person entitled to grant entry to
the premises but it is not practicable to communicate with any person entitled
to grant access to the material,

55.4.c

that entry to the premises will not be granted unless a warrant is produced,
or

55.4.d

that the purpose of a search may be frustrated or seriously prejudiced unless
a constable arriving at the premises can secure immediate entry to them.

55.5

The premises referred to in subsection  (2)  are—

55.5.a

one or more sets of premises specified in the application (in which case the
application is for a “specific premises warrant”), or

55.5.b

any premises occupied or controlled by a person specified in the application,
including such sets of premises as are so specified (in which case the
application is for an “all premises warrant”).

55.6

If the application is for an all premises warrant, the justice of the peace
must also be satisfied—

55.6.a

that there are reasonable grounds for believing that it is necessary to search
premises occupied or controlled by the person in question which are not
specified in the application in order to find the material referred to in
subsection  (2) , and

55.6.b

that it is not reasonably practicable to specify in the application all the
premises which the person occupies or controls and which might need to be
searched.

55.7

The warrant may authorise entry to and search of premises on more than one
occasion if, on the application, the justice of the peace is satisfied that it
is necessary to authorise multiple entries in order to achieve the purpose for
which the justice of the peace issues the warrant.

55.8

If the warrant authorises multiple entries, the number of entries authorised
may be unlimited, or limited to a maximum.

55.9

A constable may—

55.9.a

seize and retain anything for which a search has been authorised under
subsection  (1) , and

55.9.b

if necessary, use reasonable force in the exercise of a power conferred by a
warrant issued under this section.

55.10

The power to issue a warrant conferred by this section is in addition to any
such power otherwise conferred.

55.11

In this section, section 56 and Schedule 6 “ relevant human remains ” means
the body or any other human remains of—

55.11.a

a person who the constable making the application reasonably believes to have
died in England and Wales but whose death has not been registered under
section 15 of the Births and Deaths Registration Act 1953,

55.11.b

a person whose death has been registered under that Act following an
investigation under section 1(5) of the Coroners and Justice Act 2009, or

55.11.c

a person in respect of whom a declaration has been made under section 2 of the
Presumption of Death Act 2013.

55.12

In this section, section 56 and Schedule 6 the following expressions have the
same meaning as in the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984—

55.12.a

“ items subject to legal privilege ” (see section 10 of that Act);

55.12.b

“ excluded material ” (see section 11 of that Act);

55.12.c

“ special procedure material ” (see section 14 of that Act);

55.12.d

“ premises ” (see section 23 of that Act).

###### Special procedure for access to material relating to human remains

56

56.1

Schedule 6 makes provision for a constable to obtain access to excluded
material or special procedure material that consists of, or relates to the
location of, relevant human remains.

56.2

Section 4 of the Summary Jurisdiction (Process) Act 1881 (which includes
provision for the execution of process of English and Welsh courts in
Scotland) and section 29 of the Petty Sessions (Ireland) Act 1851 (which makes
equivalent provision for execution in Northern Ireland) apply to any process
issued by a judge under Schedule 6 to this Act as they apply to process issued
by a magistrates’ court under the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980.
