57

In Part 1 of Schedule 1 to the Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001 (powers of
seizure to which section 50 of that Act applies), at the end insert—

########## Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022

57.73U

Each of the powers of seizure conferred by section 55 (9)(a)  of, and
paragraph  11(a)  of Schedule 6 to, the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts
Act 2022 (seizure in connection with human remains or material relating to
human remains).

##### Prisoner custody officers

###### Functions of prisoner custody officers in relation to live link hearings

58

58.1

The Criminal Justice Act 1991 is amended as follows.

58.2

Section 80 (arrangements for the provision of prisoner escorts) is amended in
accordance with subsections  (3)  to  (5) .

58.3

In subsection (1), after paragraph (b) insert—

58.3.ba

the custody of prisoners at a police station for any purpose connected with
their participation in a preliminary, sentencing or enforcement hearing
through a live audio link or live video link;

.

58.4

After subsection (1A) insert—

58.4.1B

Subsection (1)(ba) applies in relation to prisoners whether the hearing is yet
to take place, is taking place or has taken place.

58.5

In subsection (4), at the appropriate place insert—

“enforcement hearing”, “live audio link”, “live video link”, “preliminary
hearing” and “sentencing hearing” each has the meaning given in section 56(1)
of the Criminal Justice Act 2003;

.

58.6

Section 82 (powers and duties of prisoner custody officers) is amended in
accordance with subsections  (7)  and  (8) .

58.7

After subsection (4) insert—

58.7.4A

Subsections (4B) and (4C) apply if a prisoner custody officer acting in
pursuance of prisoner escort arrangements is at a police station for the
purposes of exercising functions under section 80(1)(ba) (custody of prisoners
in relation to live link proceedings) in relation to a prisoner.

58.7.4B

It is the prisoner custody officer’s duty to give effect to—

58.7.4B.a

any order of the Crown Court under section 142 of the Powers of Criminal
Courts (Sentencing) Act 2000 in relation to the prisoner, or

58.7.4B.b

any order of a magistrates’ court under section 80 of the 1980 Act in relation
to the prisoner.

58.7.4C

The fact that the prisoner custody officer is exercising, or may exercise,
functions under section 80(1)(ba) in relation to the prisoner does not prevent
a constable from exercising any powers in relation to the prisoner that are
otherwise available to the constable.

58.8

In subsection (5) for “and (4)” substitute  “, (4) and (4B)” .

##### Proceeds of crime

###### Proceeds of crime: account freezing orders

59

59.1

omit subsections (5A) and (5B), and

59.2

In section 316(1) of that Act (general interpretation), in the definition of

59.3

In section 48 of the Financial Services Act 2021 (extent)—

59.3.a

in subsection (1), for “subsections (2) and (3)” substitute  “subsection (2)”
, and

59.3.b

omit subsection (3).

59.4

In paragraph 14 of Schedule 12 to that Act (forfeiture of money: electronic
money institutions and payment institutions) omit sub-paragraphs (3) and (4).

##### Non-criminal hate incidents

###### Code of practice relating to non-criminal hate incidents

60

60.1

The Secretary of State may issue a code of practice about the processing by a
relevant person of personal data relating to a hate incident.

60.2

In this section “ hate incident ” means an incident or alleged incident which
involves or is alleged to involve an act by a person (“the alleged
perpetrator”) which is perceived by a person other than the alleged
perpetrator to be motivated (wholly or partly) by hostility or prejudice
towards persons with a particular characteristic.

60.3

The provision that may be made by a code of practice under this section
includes, in particular, provision about—

60.3.a

whether and how personal data relating to a hate incident should be recorded;

60.3.b

the persons who are to process such personal data;

60.3.c

the circumstances in which a data subject should be notified of the processing
of such personal data;

60.3.d

the retention of such personal data, including the period for which it should
be retained and the circumstances in which and the procedures by which that
period might be changed;

60.3.e

the consideration by a relevant person of requests by the data subject
relating to such personal data.

60.4

But a code of practice under this section must not make provision about—

60.4.a

the processing of personal data for the purposes of a criminal investigation,
or

60.4.b

the processing of personal data relating to the alleged perpetrator of a hate
incident at any time after they have been charged with an offence relating to
the hate incident.

60.5

A code of practice under this section may make different provision for
different purposes.

60.6

A relevant person must have regard to the code of practice that is for the
time being in force under this section in processing personal data relating to
a hate incident.

60.7

In this section—

“ data subject ” has the meaning given by section 3(5) of the Data Protection
Act 2018; “ personal data ” has the meaning given by section 3(2) of that Act;
“ processing ” has the meaning given by section 3(4) of that Act.

60.8

In this section “ relevant person ” means—

60.8.a

a member of a police force in England and Wales,

60.8.b

a special constable appointed under section 27 of the Police Act 1996,

60.8.c

a member of staff appointed by the chief officer of police of a police force
in England and Wales,

60.8.d

a person designated as a community support volunteer or a policing support
volunteer under section 38 of the Police Reform Act 2002,

60.8.e

an employee of the Common Council of the City of London who is under the
direction and control of a chief officer of police,

60.8.f

a constable of the British Transport Police Force,

60.8.g

a special constable of the British Transport Police Force appointed under
section 25 of the Railways and Transport Safety Act 2003,

60.8.h

an employee of the British Transport Police Authority appointed under section
27 of that Act,

60.8.i

a person designated as a community support volunteer or a policing support
volunteer under section 38 of the Police Reform Act 2002 as applied by section
28 of the Railways and Transport Safety Act 2003, or

60.8.j

a National Crime Agency officer.

###### Further provision about a code of practice under section 60

61

61.1

The Secretary of State may not issue a code of practice under section 60
unless a draft of the code has been laid before and approved by a resolution
of each House of Parliament.

61.2

The Secretary of State may from time to time revise and reissue a code of
practice under section 60.

61.3

Before reissuing a code of practice the Secretary of State must lay a draft of
the code as proposed to be reissued before Parliament.

61.4

If, within the 40-day period, either House of Parliament resolves not to
approve the code of practice laid under subsection  (3) —

61.4.a

the code is not to be reissued, and

61.4.b

the Secretary of State may prepare another code.

61.5

If no such resolution is passed within the 40-day period, the Secretary of
State may reissue the code of practice.

61.6

In this section “ the 40-day period ” means—

61.6.a

the period of 40 days beginning with the day on which the draft is laid before
Parliament, or

61.6.b

if the draft is not laid before each House on the same day, the period of 40
days beginning with the later of the days on which it is laid before
Parliament.

61.7

In calculating the 40-day period no account is to be taken of any period
during which Parliament is dissolved or prorogued or during which both Houses
of Parliament are adjourned for more than 4 days.

##### Offences relating to hares etc

###### Increase in penalty for offences related to game etc

62

62.1

Section 1 of the Night Poaching Act 1828 (taking or destroying game or rabbits
by night or entering land for that purpose) is amended in accordance with
subsections  (2)  to  (4) .

62.2

The existing text becomes subsection (1).

62.3

In that subsection—

62.3.a

after “conviction” insert  “to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 51
weeks,” , and

62.3.b

for “not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale” substitute  “or to both” .

62.4

After that subsection insert—

62.4.2

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of section
281(5) of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (alteration of penalties for certain
summary offences: England and Wales), the reference in subsection (1) to 51
weeks is to be read as a reference to 6 months.

62.5

Section 30 of the Game Act 1831 (trespass in daytime in search of game etc) is
amended in accordance with subsections  (6)  to  (8) .

62.6

The existing text becomes subsection (1).

62.7

In that subsection—

62.7.a

for the words from “conviction”, in the first place it occurs, to “seem meet”,
in the second place it occurs, substitute  “summary conviction, be liable to
imprisonment for a term not exceeding 51 weeks, to a fine or to both” , and

62.7.b

for “each of the two offences” substitute  “the offence” .

62.8

After that subsection insert—

62.8.2

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of section
281(5) of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (alteration of penalties for certain
summary offences: England and Wales), the reference in subsection (1) to 51
weeks is to be read as a reference to 6 months.

62.9

In section 4A of the Game Laws (Amendment) Act 1960 (forfeiture of vehicles),
in subsection (1), omit “as one of five or more persons liable under that
section”.

62.10

The amendments made by this section have effect only in relation to offences
committed on or after the day on which this section comes into force.

###### Trespass with intent to search for or to pursue hares with dogs etc

63

63.1

A person commits an offence if they trespass on land with the intention of—

63.1.a

using a dog to search for or to pursue a hare,

63.1.b

facilitating or encouraging the use of a dog to search for or to pursue a
hare, or

63.1.c

enabling another person to observe the use of a dog to search for or to pursue
a hare.

63.2

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (1)  to
prove that they had a reasonable excuse for the trespass mentioned in that
subsection.

63.3

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (1)  is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 51 weeks, to a fine or to
both.

63.4

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of section
281(5) of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (alteration of penalties for certain
summary offences: England and Wales), the reference in subsection  (3)  to 51
weeks is to be read as a reference to 6 months.

###### Being equipped for searching for or pursuing hares with dogs etc

64

64.1

A person commits an offence if they have an article with them in a place other
than a dwelling with the intention that it will be used in the course of or in
connection with the commission by any person of an offence under section 63
(trespass with intent to search for or to pursue hares with dogs etc).

64.2

Where a person is charged with an offence under subsection  (1) , proof that
the person had with them any article made or adapted for use in committing an
offence under section 63 is evidence that the person had it with them with the
intention that it would be used in the course of or in connection with the
commission by any person of an offence under that section.

64.3

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (1)  is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 51 weeks, to a fine or to
both.

64.4

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of section
281(5) of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (alteration of penalties for certain
summary offences: England and Wales), the reference in subsection  (3)  to 51
weeks is to be read as a reference to 6 months.

64.5

In this section—

“ article ” includes a vehicle and, except in subsection  (2) , an animal; “
dwelling ” means— a building or structure which is used as a dwelling, or a
part of a building or structure, if the part is used as a dwelling, and
includes any yard, garden, garage or outhouse belonging to and used with a
dwelling.

###### Recovery order on conviction for certain offences involving dogs

65

65.1

This section applies where—

65.1.a

a person is convicted of an offence within subsection  (5)  which was
committed on or after the day on which this section comes into force,

65.1.b

a dog was used in or was present at the commission of the offence, and

65.1.c

the dog was lawfully seized and detained in connection with the offence.

65.2

The court may make an order (a “recovery order”) requiring the offender to pay
all the expenses incurred by reason of the dog’s seizure and detention.

65.3

Any sum required to be paid under subsection  (2)  is to be treated for the
purposes of enforcement as if it were a fine imposed on conviction.

65.4

Where a recovery order is available for an offence, the court may make such an
order whether or not it deals with the offender in any other way for the
offence.

65.5

The following offences are within this subsection—

65.5.a

an offence under section 1 of the Night Poaching Act 1828 (taking or
destroying game or rabbits by night or entering land for that purpose);

65.5.b

an offence under section 30 of the Game Act 1831 (trespass in daytime in
search of game etc);

65.5.c

an offence under section 63 (trespass with intent to search for or to pursue
hares with dogs etc);

65.5.d

an offence under section 64 (being equipped for searching for or pursuing
hares with dogs etc).

###### Disqualification order on conviction for certain offences involving dogs

66

66.1

This section applies where—

66.1.a

a person is convicted of an offence within subsection  (9)  which was
committed on or after the day on which this section comes into force, and

66.1.b

a dog was used in or was present at the commission of the offence.

66.2

The court may make an order (a “disqualification order”) disqualifying the
offender, for such period as the court thinks fit, from—

66.2.a

owning dogs,

66.2.b

keeping dogs, or

66.2.c

both.

66.3

The disqualification order may specify a period during which the offender may
not make an application under section 68 to terminate the order.

66.4

The court may, where it appears to the court that the offender owns or keeps a
dog, suspend the operation of the disqualification order for such period as it
thinks necessary for enabling alternative arrangements to be made in respect
of the dog.

66.5

Where a court makes a disqualification order, it must—

66.5.a

give its reasons for making the order in open court, and

66.5.b

cause them to be entered in the register of its proceedings.

66.6

A person who breaches a disqualification order commits an offence.

66.7

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (6)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.

66.8

Where a disqualification order is available for an offence, the court may make
such an order whether or not it deals with the offender in any other way for
the offence.

66.9

The following offences are within this subsection—

66.9.a

an offence under section 1 of the Night Poaching Act 1828 (taking or
destroying game or rabbits by night or entering land for that purpose);

66.9.b

an offence under section 30 of the Game Act 1831 (trespass in daytime in
search of game etc);

66.9.c

an offence under section 63 (trespass with intent to search for or to pursue
hares with dogs etc);

66.9.d

an offence under section 64 (being equipped for searching for or pursuing
hares with dogs etc).

66.10

In section 171 of the Sentencing Code (offences relating to animals), after
subsection (2) insert—

66.10.3

See section 66 of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022
(disqualification order on conviction for certain offences involving dogs) for
orders relating to disqualification in the case of offences involving dogs
under that Act, the Night Poaching Act 1828 and the Game Act 1831.

###### Seizure and disposal of dogs in connection with disqualification order

67

67.1

Where, on a court making a disqualification order, it appears to the court
that the person to whom the order applies owns or keeps a dog contrary to the
order, the court may order that the dog be taken into possession.

67.2

Where a person is convicted of an offence under section 66 (6)  by reason of
owning or keeping a dog in breach of a disqualification order, the court by
which the person is convicted may order that all dogs owned or kept in breach
of the order be taken into possession.

67.3

An order under subsection  (1)  or  (2) , so far as relating to any dog owned
by the person to whom the disqualification order applies, must make provision
for disposal of the dog.

67.4

Any dog taken into possession in pursuance of an order under subsection  (1)
or  (2)  that is not owned by the person subject to the disqualification order
is to be dealt with in such manner as an appropriate court may order.

67.5

But an order under subsection  (4)  may not provide for the dog to be—

67.5.a

destroyed, or

67.5.b

disposed of for the purposes of vivisection.

67.6

A court may not make an order for disposal of the dog under subsection  (4)
unless—

67.6.a

it has given the owner of the dog an opportunity to be heard, or

67.6.b

it is satisfied that it is not reasonably practicable to communicate with the
owner.

67.7

Where a court makes an order under subsection  (4)  for the disposal of the
dog, the owner of the dog may appeal against the order to the Crown Court.

67.8

In this section—

“ appropriate court ” means— the magistrates’ court which made the order under
subsection  (1)  or  (2) , or another magistrates’ court acting for the same
local justice area as that court; “ disqualification order ” has the same
meaning as in section 66.

67.9

In this section references to disposing of a dog do not include—

67.9.a

destroying it, or

67.9.b

disposing of it for the purposes of vivisection.

###### Termination of disqualification order

68

68.1

A person who is subject to a disqualification order may apply to an
appropriate court for the order to be terminated.

68.2

No application under subsection  (1)  may be made—

68.2.a

before the end of the period of one year beginning with the date on which the
disqualification order was made,

68.2.b

where a previous application under that subsection has been made in relation
to the same order, before the end of the period of one year beginning with the
date on which the previous application was determined, or

68.2.c

before the end of any period specified under section 66 (3) , or subsection
(5) , in relation to the order.

68.3

On an application under subsection  (1) , the court may—

68.3.a

terminate the disqualification order,

68.3.b

vary the order so as to make it less onerous, or

68.3.c

refuse the application.

68.4

When determining an application under subsection  (1) , the court is to have
regard to—

68.4.a

the character of the applicant,

68.4.b

the applicant’s conduct since the disqualification order was made, and

68.4.c

any other relevant circumstances.

68.5

Where the court refuses an application under subsection  (1)  or varies a
disqualification order on such an application, it may specify a period during
which the applicant may not make a further application under that subsection
in relation to the order concerned.

68.6

The court may order an applicant to pay all or part of the costs of an
application.

68.7

In this section—

“ appropriate court ” means— the magistrates’ court which made the
disqualification order, or another magistrates’ court acting for the same
local justice area as that court; “ disqualification order ” has the same
meaning as in section 66.

###### Section 67: supplementary

69

69.1

The court by which an order under section 67 is made may—

69.1.a

appoint a person to carry out, or arrange for the carrying out of, the order;

69.1.b

require any person who has possession of a dog to which the order applies to
deliver it up to enable the order to be carried out;

69.1.c

give directions with respect to the carrying out of the order;

69.1.d

confer additional powers (including power to enter premises where a dog to
which the order applies is being kept) for the purpose of, or in connection
with, the carrying out of the order;

69.1.e

order the person who committed the offence in relation to which the order was
made, or another person, to reimburse the expenses of carrying out the order.

69.2

A person who fails to comply with a requirement imposed under subsection
(1)(b)  commits an offence.

69.3

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (2)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.

69.4

Directions under subsection  (1)(c)  may—

69.4.a

specify the manner in which a dog is to be disposed of, or

69.4.b

delegate the decision about the manner in which a dog is to be disposed of to
a person appointed under subsection  (1)(a) .

69.5

In determining how to exercise its powers under section 67 and this section
the court is to have regard (amongst other things) to—

69.5.a

the desirability of protecting the value of any dog to which the order under
section 67 applies, and

69.5.b

the desirability of avoiding increasing any expenses which a person may be
ordered to reimburse.

69.6

In determining how to exercise a power delegated under subsection  (4)(b) , a
person is to have regard, amongst other things, to the things mentioned in
subsection  (5)(a)  and  (b) .

69.7

If the owner of a dog ordered to be disposed of under section 67 is subject to
a liability by virtue of subsection  (1)(e) , any amount to which the owner is
entitled as a result of sale of the dog may be reduced by an amount equal to
that liability.

69.8

Any sum ordered to be paid under subsection  (1)(e)  is to be treated for the
purposes of enforcement as if it were a fine imposed on conviction.

69.9

In this section references to disposing of a dog do not include—

69.9.a

destroying it, or

69.9.b

disposing of it for the purposes of vivisection.

###### Disqualification orders: appeals

70

70.1

Nothing may be done under an order under section 66 or 67 with respect to a
dog unless—

70.1.a

the period for giving notice of appeal against the order has expired,

70.1.b

the period for giving notice of appeal against the conviction on which the
order was made has expired, and

70.1.c

if the order or conviction is the subject of an appeal, the appeal has been
determined or withdrawn.

70.2

Where the effect of an order is suspended under subsection  (1) —

70.2.a

no requirement imposed or directions given in connection with the order have
effect, but

70.2.b

the court may give directions about how any dog to which the order applies is
to be dealt with during the suspension.

70.3

Directions under subsection  (2)(b)  may, in particular—

70.3.a

authorise the dog to be taken into possession;

70.3.b

authorise the dog to be cared for either on the premises where it was being
kept when it was taken into possession or at some other place;

70.3.c

appoint a person to carry out, or arrange for the carrying out of, the
directions;

70.3.d

require any person who has possession of the dog to deliver it up for the
purposes of the directions;

70.3.e

confer additional powers (including power to enter premises where the dog is
being kept) for the purpose of, or in connection with, the carrying out of the
directions;

70.3.f

provide for the recovery of any expenses in relation to the removal or care of
the dog which are incurred in carrying out the directions.

70.4

A person who fails to comply with a requirement imposed under subsection
(3)(d)  commits an offence.

70.5

A person guilty an offence under subsection  (4)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.

70.6

Any sum directed to be paid under subsection  (3)(f)  is to be treated for the
purposes of enforcement as if it were a fine imposed on conviction.

##### Administering a substance with intent to cause harm

###### Administering a substance with intent to cause harm

71

71.1

The Secretary of State must, before the end of the relevant period—

71.1.a

prepare and publish a report—

71.1.a.i

about the nature and prevalence of the conduct described in subsection (2),
and

71.1.a.ii

setting out any steps Her Majesty’s Government has taken or intends to take in
relation to the matters referred to in sub-paragraph (i), and

71.1.b

lay the report before Parliament.

71.2

The conduct referred to in subsection (1)(a)(i) is a person intentionally
administering a substance to, or causing a substance to be taken by, another
person—

71.2.a

without the consent of that other person, and

71.2.b

with the intention of causing harm (whether or not amounting to an offence) to
that other person.

71.3

In subsection (1), the “ relevant period ” means the period of 12 months
beginning with the day on which this Act is passed.

##### Offences motivated by hostility based on sex or gender

###### Response to Law Commission report on hate crime laws

72

72.1

The Secretary of State must, before the end of the period of 12 months
beginning with the day on which this Act is passed—

72.1.a

prepare and publish a response to Recommendation 8 of the Law Commission
report on hate crime (adding sex or gender as a protected characteristic for
the purposes of aggravated offences and enhanced sentencing), and

72.1.b

lay the response before Parliament.

72.2

In this section “ the Law Commission report on hate crime ” means the Law
Commission report “Hate Crime Laws” that was published on 7 December 2021.

### Public order

#### Public processions and public assemblies

##### Imposing conditions on public processions

73

73.1

Section 12 of the Public Order Act 1986 (imposing conditions on public
processions) is amended as follows.

73.2

In subsection (1)—

73.2.a

for the “or” at the end of paragraph (a) substitute—

73.2.a.aa

in the case of a procession in England and Wales, the noise generated by
persons taking part in the procession may result in serious disruption to the
activities of an organisation which are carried on in the vicinity of the
procession,

73.2.a.ab

in the case of a procession in England and Wales—

73.2.a.ab.i

the noise generated by persons taking part in the procession may have a
relevant impact on persons in the vicinity of the procession, and

73.2.a.ab.ii

that impact may be significant, or

, and

73.2.b

in the words following paragraph (b), after “disruption” insert  “, impact” .

73.3

After subsection (2) insert—

73.3.2A

For the purposes of subsection (1)(a), the cases in which a public procession
in England and Wales may result in serious disruption to the life of the
community include, in particular, where—

73.3.2A.a

it may result in a significant delay to the delivery of a time-sensitive
product to consumers of that product, or

73.3.2A.b

it may result in a prolonged disruption of access to any essential goods or
any essential service, including, in particular, access to—

73.3.2A.b.i

the supply of money, food, water, energy or fuel,

73.3.2A.b.ii

a system of communication,

73.3.2A.b.iii

a place of worship,

73.3.2A.b.iv

a transport facility,

73.3.2A.b.v

an educational institution, or

73.3.2A.b.vi

a service relating to health.

73.3.2B

In subsection  (2A)(a)  “ time-sensitive product ” means a product whose value
or use to its consumers may be significantly reduced by a delay in the supply
of the product to them.

73.3.2C

For the purposes of subsection (1)(aa), the cases in which the noise generated
by persons taking part in a public procession may result in serious disruption
to the activities of an organisation which are carried on in the vicinity of
the procession include, in particular, where it may result in persons
connected with the organisation not being reasonably able, for a prolonged
period of time, to carry on in that vicinity the activities or any one of
them.

73.3.2D

For the purposes of subsection (1)(ab)(i), the noise generated by persons
taking part in a public procession may have a relevant impact on persons in
the vicinity of the procession if—

73.3.2D.a

it may result in the intimidation or harassment of persons of reasonable
firmness with the characteristics of persons likely to be in the vicinity, or

73.3.2D.b

it may cause such persons to suffer alarm or distress.

73.3.2E

In considering for the purposes of subsection (1)(ab)(ii) whether the noise
generated by persons taking part in a public procession may have a significant
impact on persons in the vicinity of the procession, the senior police officer
must have regard to—

73.3.2E.a

the likely number of persons of the kind mentioned in paragraph (a) of
subsection  (2D)  who may experience an impact of the kind mentioned in
paragraph (a) or (b) of that subsection,

73.3.2E.b

the likely duration of that impact on such persons, and

73.3.2E.c

the likely intensity of that impact on such persons.

73.4

After subsection (11) insert—

73.4.12

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend any of subsections (2A) to
(2C) for the purposes of making provision about the meaning for the purposes
of this section of—

73.4.12.a

serious disruption to the activities of an organisation which are carried on
in the vicinity of a public procession, or

73.4.12.b

serious disruption to the life of the community.

73.4.13

Regulations under subsection (12) may, in particular, amend any of those
subsections for the purposes of—

73.4.13.a

defining any aspect of an expression mentioned in subsection (12)(a) or (b)
for the purposes of this section;

73.4.13.b

giving examples of cases in which a public procession is or is not to be
treated as resulting in—

73.4.13.b.i

serious disruption to the activities of an organisation which are carried on
in the vicinity of the procession, or

73.4.13.b.ii

serious disruption to the life of the community.

73.4.14

Regulations under subsection (12)—

73.4.14.a

are to be made by statutory instrument;

73.4.14.b

may apply only in relation to public processions in England and Wales;

73.4.14.c

may make incidental, supplementary, consequential, transitional, transitory or
saving provision, including provision which makes consequential amendments to
this Part.

73.4.15

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection (12) may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

73.5

The Secretary of State must, before the end of the period of 2 years beginning
with the day on which this section comes into force—

73.5.a

prepare and publish a report on the operation of the amendments to section 12
of the Public Order Act 1986 made by this section, and

73.5.b

lay the report before Parliament.

##### Imposing conditions on public assemblies

74

74.1

Section 14 of the Public Order Act 1986 (imposing conditions on public
assemblies) is amended as follows.

74.2

In subsection (1)—

74.2.a

for “If” substitute  “Subsection (1A) applies if” ,

74.2.b

for the “or” at the end of paragraph (a) substitute—

74.2.b.aa

in the case of an assembly in England and Wales, the noise generated by
persons taking part in the assembly may result in serious disruption to the
activities of an organisation which are carried on in the vicinity of the
assembly,

74.2.b.ab

in the case of an assembly in England and Wales—

74.2.b.ab.i

the noise generated by persons taking part in the assembly may have a relevant
impact on persons in the vicinity of the assembly, and

74.2.b.ab.ii

that impact may be significant, or

, and

74.2.c

omit the words after paragraph (b).

74.3

After subsection (1) insert—

74.3.1A

The senior police officer may give directions imposing on the persons
organising or taking part in the assembly—

74.3.1A.a

in the case of an assembly in England and Wales, such conditions as appear to
the officer necessary to prevent the disorder, damage, disruption, impact or
intimidation mentioned in subsection (1);

74.3.1A.b

in the case of an assembly in Scotland, such conditions as to the place at
which the assembly may be (or continue to be) held, its maximum duration, or
the maximum number of persons who may constitute it, as appear to the officer
necessary to prevent the disorder, damage, disruption or intimidation
mentioned in subsection (1)(a) or (b).

74.4

In subsection (2), for “subsection (1)” substitute  “this section” .

74.5

After subsection (2) insert—

74.5.2A

For the purposes of subsection (1)(a), the cases in which a public assembly in
England and Wales may result in serious disruption to the life of the
community include, in particular, where—

74.5.2A.a

it may result in a significant delay to the supply of a time-sensitive product
to consumers of that product, or

74.5.2A.b

it may result in a prolonged disruption of access to any essential goods or
any essential service, including, in particular, access to—

74.5.2A.b.i

the supply of money, food, water, energy or fuel,

74.5.2A.b.ii

a system of communication,

74.5.2A.b.iii

a place of worship,

74.5.2A.b.iv

a transport facility,

74.5.2A.b.v

an educational institution, or

74.5.2A.b.vi

a service relating to health.

74.5.2B

In subsection  (2A)(a)  “ time-sensitive product ” means a product whose value
or use to its consumers may be significantly reduced by a delay in the supply
of the product to them.

74.5.2C

For the purposes of subsection (1)(aa), the cases in which the noise generated
by persons taking part in a public assembly may result in serious disruption
to the activities of an organisation which are carried on in the vicinity of
the assembly include, in particular, where it may result in persons connected
with the organisation not being reasonably able, for a prolonged period of
time, to carry on in that vicinity the activities or any one of them.

74.5.2D

For the purposes of subsection (1)(ab)(i), the noise generated by persons
taking part in an assembly may have a relevant impact on persons in the
vicinity of the assembly if—

74.5.2D.a

it may result in the intimidation or harassment of persons of reasonable
firmness with the characteristics of persons likely to be in the vicinity, or

74.5.2D.b

it may cause such persons to suffer alarm or distress.

74.5.2E

In considering for the purposes of subsection (1)(ab)(ii) whether the noise
generated by persons taking part in an assembly may have a significant impact
on persons in the vicinity of the assembly, the senior police officer must
have regard to—

74.5.2E.a

the likely number of persons of the kind mentioned in paragraph (a) of
subsection (2D) who may experience an impact of the kind mentioned in
paragraph (a) or (b) of that subsection,

74.5.2E.b

the likely duration of that impact on such persons, and

74.5.2E.c

the likely intensity of that impact on such persons.

74.6

After subsection (10A) (as inserted by section 75 (11) ) insert—

74.6.11

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend any of subsections (2A) to
(2C) for the purposes of making provision about the meaning for the purposes
of this section of—

74.6.11.a

serious disruption to the activities of an organisation which are carried on
in the vicinity of a public assembly, or

74.6.11.b

serious disruption to the life of the community.

74.6.12

Regulations under subsection (11) may, in particular, amend any of those
subsections for the purposes of—

74.6.12.a

defining any aspect of an expression mentioned in subsection (11)(a) or (b)
for the purposes of this section;

74.6.12.b

giving examples of cases in which a public assembly is or is not to be treated
as resulting in—

74.6.12.b.i

serious disruption to the activities of an organisation which are carried on
in the vicinity of the assembly, or

74.6.12.b.ii

serious disruption to the life of the community.

74.6.13

Regulations under subsection (11)—

74.6.13.a

are to be made by statutory instrument;

74.6.13.b

may apply only in relation to public assemblies in England and Wales;

74.6.13.c

may make incidental, supplementary, consequential, transitional, transitory or
saving provision, including provision which makes consequential amendments to
this Part.

74.6.14

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection (11) may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

74.7

The Secretary of State must, before the end of the period of 2 years beginning
with the day on which this section comes into force—

74.7.a

prepare and publish a report on the operation of the amendments to section 14
of the Public Order Act 1986 made by this section, and

74.7.b

lay the report before Parliament.

##### Power to specify other areas as controlled areas

77

After section 149 of the Police Reform and Social Responsibility Act 2011
insert—

######### Power to specify other areas as controlled areas

77.149A

77.149A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for any provision of
sections 143 to 148 and 149(3) to apply, with or without modifications, in
relation to an area specified in the regulations.

77.149A.2

An area may be specified in regulations under subsection (1) by description,
by reference to a map or plan or in any other way.

77.149A.3

Regulations under subsection (1) may be made only if—

77.149A.3.a

either House of Parliament is, or is proposed to be, located somewhere other
than the Palace of Westminster as a result of the Parliamentary building works
or for any other reason, and

77.149A.3.b

as a result of that relocation, or proposed relocation, the Secretary of State
considers that it is reasonably necessary for activities which are prohibited
in relation to the controlled area of Parliament Square or the Palace of
Westminster controlled area to be prohibited in relation to the area specified
in the regulations.

77.149A.4

In subsection (3)(a) “ the Parliamentary building works ” has the meaning
given by section 1(1) of the Parliamentary Buildings (Restoration and Renewal)
Act 2019.

77.149A.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for any other
enactment, or any instrument made under an enactment, to have effect with
modifications in consequence of regulations under subsection (1).

#### Public nuisance

##### Intentionally or recklessly causing public nuisance

78

78.1

A person commits an offence if—

78.1.a

the person—

78.1.a.i

does an act, or

78.1.a.ii

omits to do an act that they are required to do by any enactment or rule of
law,

78.1.b

the person’s act or omission—

78.1.b.i

creates a risk of, or causes, serious harm to the public or a section of the
public, or

78.1.b.ii

obstructs the public or a section of the public in the exercise or enjoyment
of a right that may be exercised or enjoyed by the public at large, and

78.1.c

the person intends that their act or omission will have a consequence
mentioned in paragraph  (b)  or is reckless as to whether it will have such a
consequence.

78.2

In subsection  (1)(b)(i)  “ serious harm ” means—

78.2.a

death, personal injury or disease,

78.2.b

loss of, or damage to, property, or

78.2.c

serious distress, serious annoyance, serious inconvenience or serious loss of
amenity.

78.3

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (1)  to
prove that they had a reasonable excuse for the act or omission mentioned in
paragraph (a) of that subsection.

78.4

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (1)  is liable—

78.4.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding   the general
limit in a magistrates’ court , to a fine or to both;

78.4.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 10
years, to a fine or to both.

78.5

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of paragraph
24(2) of Schedule 22 to the Sentencing Act 2020 (increase in magistrates’
court power to impose imprisonment) the reference in subsection  (4) (a)  to
the general limit in a magistrates’ court   is to be read as a reference to 6
months.

78.6

The common law offence of public nuisance is abolished.

78.7

Subsections  (1)  to  (6)  do not apply in relation to—

78.7.a

any act or omission which occurred before the coming into force of those
subsections, or

78.7.b

any act or omission which began before the coming into force of those
subsections and continues after their coming into force.

78.8

This section does not affect—

78.8.a

the liability of any person for an offence other than the common law offence
of public nuisance,

78.8.b

the civil liability of any person for the tort of public nuisance, or

78.8.c

the ability to take any action under any enactment against a person for any
act or omission within subsection (1).

78.9

In this section “ enactment ” includes an enactment comprised in subordinate
legislation within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978.

#### One-person protests

##### Imposing conditions on one-person protests

79

79.1

After section 14 of the Public Order Act 1986 insert—

########### Imposing conditions on one-person protests

79.1.14ZA

79.1.14ZA.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if the senior police officer, having regard to the
time or place at which and the circumstances in which any one-person protest
in England and Wales is being carried on or is intended to be carried on,
reasonably believes—

79.1.14ZA.1.a

that the noise generated by the person carrying on the protest may result in
serious disruption to the activities of an organisation which are carried on
in the vicinity of the protest, or

79.1.14ZA.1.b

that—

79.1.14ZA.1.b.i

the noise generated by the person carrying on the protest may have a relevant
impact on persons in the vicinity of the protest, and

79.1.14ZA.1.b.ii

that impact may be significant.

79.1.14ZA.2

The senior police officer may give directions imposing on the person
organising or carrying on the protest such conditions as appear to the officer
necessary to prevent such disruption or impact.

79.1.14ZA.3

Where the one-person protest is moving, or is intended to move, from place to
place—

79.1.14ZA.3.a

the senior police officer must also have regard under subsection  (1)  to its
route or proposed route, and

79.1.14ZA.3.b

the conditions which may be imposed under subsection  (2)  include conditions
as to the route of the protest or prohibiting the person carrying on the
protest from entering any public place specified in the direction while the
person is carrying it on.

79.1.14ZA.4

In this section “ one-person protest ” means a protest which, at any one time,
is carried on by one person in a public place.

79.1.14ZA.5

In this section “ the senior police officer ” means—

79.1.14ZA.5.a

in relation to a one-person protest being held or to a one-person protest
intended to be held in a case where a person is in a place with a view to
carrying on such a protest, the most senior in rank of the police officers
present at the scene, and

79.1.14ZA.5.b

in relation to a one-person protest intended to be held in a case where
paragraph (a) does not apply, the chief officer of police.

79.1.14ZA.6

For the purposes of subsection (1)(a), the cases in which the noise generated
by a person taking part in a one-person protest may result in serious
disruption to the activities of an organisation which are carried on in the
vicinity of the protest include, in particular, where it may result in persons
connected with the organisation not being reasonably able, for a prolonged
period of time, to carry on in that vicinity the activities or any one of
them.

79.1.14ZA.7

For the purposes of subsection  (1) (b)(i), the noise generated by a person
carrying on a one-person protest may have a relevant impact on persons in the
vicinity of the protest if—

79.1.14ZA.7.a

it may result in the intimidation or harassment of persons of reasonable
firmness with the characteristics of persons likely to be in the vicinity, or

79.1.14ZA.7.b

it may cause such persons to suffer alarm or distress.

79.1.14ZA.8

In considering for the purposes of subsection  (1) (b)(ii) whether the noise
generated by a person carrying on a one-person protest may have a significant
impact on persons in the vicinity of the protest, the senior police officer
must have regard to—

79.1.14ZA.8.a

the likely number of persons of the kind mentioned in paragraph (a) of
subsection  (7)  who may experience an impact of the kind mentioned in
paragraph (a) or (b) of that subsection,

79.1.14ZA.8.b

the likely duration of that impact on such persons, and

79.1.14ZA.8.c

the likely intensity of that impact on such persons.

79.1.14ZA.9

A direction given by a chief officer of police by virtue of subsection  (5)
(b) must be given in writing.

79.1.14ZA.10

A person (“ P ”) is guilty of an offence if—

79.1.14ZA.10.a

P organises or carries on a one-person protest,

79.1.14ZA.10.b

P fails to comply with a condition imposed under this section, and

79.1.14ZA.10.c

at the time P fails to comply with the condition, P knows or ought to know
that the condition has been imposed.

79.1.14ZA.11

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (10)
to prove that the failure arose from circumstances beyond the person’s
control.

79.1.14ZA.12

A person who incites another to commit an offence under subsection  (10)  is
guilty of an offence.

79.1.14ZA.13

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (10)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 4 on the standard scale.

79.1.14ZA.14

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (12)  is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 51 weeks or a fine not
exceeding level 4 on the standard scale or both.

79.1.14ZA.15

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of section
281(5) of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (alteration of penalties for certain
summary offences: England and Wales), the reference in subsection  (14)  to 51
weeks is to be read as a reference to 6 months.

79.1.14ZA.16

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend subsection (6) for the
purposes of making provision about the meaning for the purposes of this
section of serious disruption to the activities of an organisation which are
carried on in the vicinity of a one-person protest.

79.1.14ZA.17

Regulations under subsection  (16)  may, in particular, amend that subsection
for the purposes of—

79.1.14ZA.17.a

defining any aspect of that expression for the purposes of this section;

79.1.14ZA.17.b

giving examples of cases in which a one-person protest is or is not to be
treated as resulting in serious disruption to the activities of an
organisation which are carried on in the vicinity of the protest.

79.1.14ZA.18

Regulations under subsection  (16) —

79.1.14ZA.18.a

are to be made by statutory instrument;

79.1.14ZA.18.b

may make incidental, supplementary, consequential, transitional, transitory or
saving provision, including provision which makes consequential amendments to
this Part.

79.1.14ZA.19

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (16)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

79.2

The Secretary of State must, before the end of the period of 2 years beginning
with the day on which this section comes into force—

79.2.a

prepare and publish a report on the operation of section 14ZA of the Public
Order Act 1986, and

79.2.b

lay the report before Parliament.

80.3.1A

in paragraph 7(4), omit “or (3)”, and

81.6.a.iv

in paragraph 7(7)(a), omit “or (3)”, and

81.6.b

in Schedule 5 (powers exercisable by accredited persons), omit paragraph
2(3)(aa).

81.7

In the Sentencing Code—

81.7.a

in section 20(1) (committal in certain cases where offender committed in
respect of another offence)—

81.7.a.i

at the end of paragraph (e), insert  “or” , and

81.7.a.ii

omit paragraph (g) (and the “or” immediately before it), and

81.7.b

omit section 24(1)(f) (further powers to commit offender to the Crown Court to
be dealt with).

81.8

The amendments and repeals made by this section do not apply in relation to an
offence committed before this section comes into force.

#### Expedited public spaces protection orders

##### Expedited public spaces protection orders

82

82.1

The Anti-social Behaviour, Crime and Policing Act 2014 is amended as follows.

82.2

After section 59 insert—

########### Power to make expedited public spaces protection orders

82.2.59A

82.2.59A.1

A local authority may make an expedited public spaces protection order (an
“expedited order”) in relation to a public place within the local authority’s
area if satisfied on reasonable grounds that three conditions are met.

82.2.59A.2

The first condition is that the public place is in the vicinity of—

82.2.59A.2.a

a school in the local authority’s area, or

82.2.59A.2.b

a site in the local authority’s area where, or from which—

82.2.59A.2.b.i

vaccines are provided to members of the public by, or pursuant to arrangements
with, an NHS body, or

82.2.59A.2.b.ii

test and trace services are provided.

The reference in paragraph (b)(i) to arrangements includes arrangements made
by the NHS body in the exercise of functions of another person by virtue of
any provision of the National Health Service Act 2006.

82.2.59A.3

The second condition is that activities carried on, or likely to be carried
on, in the public place by one or more individuals in the course of a protest
or demonstration have had, or are likely to have, the effect of—

82.2.59A.3.a

harassing or intimidating members of staff or volunteers at the school or
site,

82.2.59A.3.b

harassing or intimidating persons using the services of the school or site,

82.2.59A.3.c

impeding the provision of services by staff or volunteers at the school or
site, or

82.2.59A.3.d

impeding access by persons seeking to use the services of the school or site.

82.2.59A.4

The third condition is that the effect or likely effect mentioned in
subsection  (3) —

82.2.59A.4.a

is, or is likely to be, of a persistent or continuing nature,

82.2.59A.4.b

is, or is likely to be, such as to make the activities unreasonable, and

82.2.59A.4.c

justifies the restrictions imposed by the order.

82.2.59A.5

An expedited order is an order that identifies the public place referred to in
subsection  (1)  (“the restricted area”) and—

82.2.59A.5.a

prohibits specified things being done in the restricted area,

82.2.59A.5.b

requires specified things to be done by persons carrying on specified
activities in that area, or

82.2.59A.5.c

does both of those things.

82.2.59A.6

The only prohibitions or requirements that may be imposed are ones that are
reasonable to impose in order—

82.2.59A.6.a

to prevent the harassment, intimidation or impediment referred to in
subsection  (3)  from continuing, occurring or recurring, or

82.2.59A.6.b

to reduce that harassment, intimidation or impediment or to reduce the risk of
its continuance, occurrence or recurrence.

82.2.59A.7

A prohibition or requirement may be framed—

82.2.59A.7.a

so as to apply to all persons, or only to persons in specified categories, or
to all persons except those in specified categories;

82.2.59A.7.b

so as to apply at all times, or only at specified times, or at all times
except those specified;

82.2.59A.7.c

so as to apply in all circumstances, or only in specified circumstances, or in
all circumstances except those specified.

82.2.59A.8

An expedited order must—

82.2.59A.8.a

identify the activities referred to in subsection (3);

82.2.59A.8.b

explain the effect of section 63 (where it applies) and section 67;

82.2.59A.8.c

specify the period for which the order has effect.

82.2.59A.9

An expedited order may not be made in relation to a public place if that place
(or any part of it) is or has been the subject of an expedited order (“ the
earlier order ”), unless the period specified in subsection  (11)  has
expired.

82.2.59A.10

In subsection  (9)  the second reference to “an expedited order” is to be read
as including a reference to a public spaces protection order (made after the
day on which this section comes into force) which neither prohibited nor
required anything that could not have been prohibited or required by an
expedited order.

82.2.59A.11

The period specified in this subsection is the period of a year beginning with
the day on which the earlier order ceased to have effect.

82.2.59A.12

An expedited order must be published in accordance with regulations made by
the Secretary of State.

82.2.59A.13

For the purposes of subsection  (2) , a public place that is coextensive with,
includes, or is wholly or partly within, a school or site is regarded as being
“in the vicinity of” that school or site.

82.2.59A.14

In this section references to a “school” are to be read as including a 16 to
19 Academy.

82.2.59A.15

In this section “ test and trace services ” means—

82.2.59A.15.a

in relation to England, services of the programme known as NHS Test and Trace;

82.2.59A.15.b

in relation to Wales, services of the programme known as Test, Trace, Protect.

82.3

After section 60 insert—

########### Duration of expedited orders

82.3.60A

82.3.60A.1

An expedited order may not have effect for a period of more than 6 months.

82.3.60A.2

Subject to subsection  (1) , the local authority that made an expedited order
may, before the time when the order is due to expire, extend the period for
which the order has effect if satisfied on reasonable grounds that doing so is
necessary to prevent—

82.3.60A.2.a

occurrence or recurrence after that time of the activities identified in the
order, or

82.3.60A.2.b

an increase in the frequency or seriousness of those activities after that
time.

82.3.60A.3

Where a local authority has made an expedited order, the authority may, at any
time before the order is due to expire, reduce the period for which the order
is to have effect if satisfied on reasonable grounds that the reduced period
will be sufficient having regard to the degree of risk of an occurrence,
recurrence or increase such as is mentioned in subsection  (2)(a)  or (b).

82.3.60A.4

An extension or reduction under this section of the period for which an order
has effect must be published in accordance with regulations made by the
Secretary of State.

82.3.60A.5

An expedited order may be extended or reduced under this section more than
once.

82.4

After section 72 insert—

########### Expedited orders: Convention rights and consents

82.4.72A

82.4.72A.1

A local authority, in deciding—

82.4.72A.1.a

whether to make an expedited order (under section 59A) and if so what it
should include,

82.4.72A.1.b

whether to extend or reduce the period for which an expedited order has effect
(under section 60A) and if so by how much,

82.4.72A.1.c

whether to vary an expedited order (under section 61) and if so how, or

82.4.72A.1.d

whether to discharge an expedited order (under section 61),

must have particular regard to the rights of freedom of expression and freedom
of assembly set out in articles 10 and 11 of the Convention.

82.4.72A.2

In subsection (1) “ Convention ” has the meaning given by section 21(1) of the
Human Rights Act 1998.

82.4.72A.3

A local authority must obtain the necessary consents before—

82.4.72A.3.a

making an expedited order,

82.4.72A.3.b

extending or reducing the period for which an expedited order has effect, or

82.4.72A.3.c

varying or discharging an expedited order.

82.4.72A.4

If the order referred to in subsection (3) was made, or is proposed to be
made, in reliance on section 59A (2)(a) , “ the necessary consents ” means the
consent of—

82.4.72A.4.a

the chief officer of police for the police area that includes the restricted
area, and

82.4.72A.4.b

a person authorised (whether in specific or general terms) by the appropriate
authority for the school or 16 to 19 Academy.

82.4.72A.5

If the order referred to in subsection (3) was made, or is proposed to be
made, in reliance on section 59A (2)(b) , “ the necessary consents ” means the
consent of—

82.4.72A.5.a

the chief officer of police for the police area that includes the restricted
area, and

82.4.72A.5.b

a person authorised by the appropriate NHS authority.

82.4.72A.6

In this section—

“ appropriate authority ” means— in relation to a school maintained by a local
authority, the governing body; in relation to any other school or a 16 to 19
Academy, the proprietor; “ appropriate NHS authority ” means— if the order was
made, or is proposed to be made, in reliance on sub-paragraph (i) of section
59A (2)(b) , the NHS body mentioned in that sub-paragraph; if the order was
made, or is proposed to be made, in reliance on sub-paragraph (ii) of section
59A (2)(b)  and the site is in England, the UK Health Security Agency; if the
order was made, or is proposed to be made, in reliance on that sub-paragraph
and the site is in Wales, the Local Health Board for the area in which the
site is located.

82.4.72A.7

In this section “ proprietor ”, in relation to a school or a 16 to 19 Academy,
has the meaning given in section 579(1) of the Education Act 1996.

########### Consultation and notifications after making expedited order

82.4.72B

82.4.72B.1

A local authority must carry out the necessary consultation as soon as
reasonably practicable after making an expedited order.

82.4.72B.2

In subsection (1) “ necessary consultation ” means consulting with the
following about the terms and effects of the order—

82.4.72B.2.a

the chief officer of police, and the local policing body, for the police area
that includes the restricted area;

82.4.72B.2.b

whatever community representatives the local authority thinks it appropriate
to consult;

82.4.72B.2.c

the owner or occupier of land within the restricted area.

82.4.72B.3

A local authority must carry out the necessary notification (if any) as soon
as reasonably practicable after—

82.4.72B.3.a

making an expedited order,

82.4.72B.3.b

extending or reducing the period for which an expedited order has effect, or

82.4.72B.3.c

varying or discharging an expedited order.

82.4.72B.4

In subsection  (3)  “ necessary notification ” means notifying the following
of the extension, reduction, variation or discharge—

82.4.72B.4.a

the parish council or community council (if any) for the area that includes
the restricted area;

82.4.72B.4.b

in the case of an expedited order made by a district council in England, the
county council (if any) for the area that includes the restricted area;

82.4.72B.4.c

the owner or occupier of land within the restricted area.

82.4.72B.5

The requirement to notify the owner or occupier of land within the restricted
area—

82.4.72B.5.a

does not apply to land that is owned or occupied by the local authority;

82.4.72B.5.b

applies only if, and to the extent that, it is reasonably practicable to
notify the owner or occupier of the land.

82.5

Schedule 7 contains amendments relating to subsections  (1)  to  (4) .

### Unauthorised encampments

#### Offence relating to residing on land without consent in or with a vehicle

83

83.1

At the beginning of Part 5 of the Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994,
before the italic heading before section 61, insert—

########## Residing on land without consent in or with a vehicle

########### Offence relating to residing on land without consent in or with a vehicle

83.1.60C

83.1.60C.1

Subsection  (2)  applies where—

83.1.60C.1.a

a person aged 18 or over (“ P ”) is residing, or intending to reside, on land
without the consent of the occupier of the land,

83.1.60C.1.b

P has, or intends to have, at least one vehicle with them on the land,

83.1.60C.1.c

one or more of the conditions mentioned in subsection  (4)  is satisfied, and

83.1.60C.1.d

the occupier, a representative of the occupier or a constable requests P to do
either or both of the following—

83.1.60C.1.d.i

leave the land;

83.1.60C.1.d.ii

remove from the land property that is in P’s possession or under P’s control.

83.1.60C.2

P commits an offence if—

83.1.60C.2.a

P fails to comply with the request as soon as reasonably practicable, or

83.1.60C.2.b

P—

83.1.60C.2.b.i

enters (or having left, re-enters) the land within the prohibited period with
the intention of residing there without the consent of the occupier of the
land, and

83.1.60C.2.b.ii

has, or intends to have, at least one vehicle with them on the land.

83.1.60C.3

The prohibited period is the period of 12 months beginning with the day on
which the request was made.

83.1.60C.4

The conditions are—

83.1.60C.4.a

in a case where P is residing on the land, significant damage or significant
disruption has been caused or is likely to be caused as a result of P’s
residence;

83.1.60C.4.b

in a case where P is not yet residing on the land, it is likely that
significant damage or significant disruption would be caused as a result of
P’s residence if P were to reside on the land;

83.1.60C.c

that significant damage or significant disruption has been caused or is likely
to be caused as a result of conduct carried on, or likely to be carried on, by
P while P is on the land;

83.1.60C.d

that significant distress has been caused or is likely to be caused as a
result of offensive conduct carried on, or likely to be carried on, by P while
P is on the land.

83.1.60C.5

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding three months or a fine not
exceeding level 4 on the standard scale, or both.

83.1.60C.6

In proceedings for an offence under this section it is a defence for the
accused to show that the accused had a reasonable excuse for—

83.1.60C.6.a

failing to comply as soon as reasonably practicable with the request mentioned
in subsection  (1)(d) , or

83.1.60C.6.b

after receiving such a request, entering (or re-entering) the land with the
intention of residing there without the consent of the occupier of the land.

83.1.60C.7

In its application to common land, this section has effect—

83.1.60C.7.a

in a case where the common land is land to which the public has access and the
occupier cannot be identified, as if references to the occupier were
references to the local authority in relation to the common land;

83.1.60C.7.b

in a case where P’s residence or intended residence without the consent of the
occupier is, or would be, an infringement of the commoners’ rights and—

83.1.60C.7.b.i

the occupier is aware of P’s residence or intended residence and had an
opportunity to consent to it, or

83.1.60C.7.b.ii

if sub-paragraph  (i)  does not apply, any one or more of the commoners took
reasonable steps to try to inform the occupier of P’s residence or intended
residence and provide an opportunity to consent to it,

as if in subsection  (1)(d)  after “a constable” there were inserted  “or the
commoners or any of them or their representative” .

83.1.60C.8

In this section--

“ common land ” and “ commoner ” have the same meaning as in section 61; “
damage ” includes— damage to the land; damage to any property on the land not
belonging to P; damage to the environment (including excessive noise, smells,
litter or deposits of waste); “ disruption ” includes interference with— a
person’s ability to access any services or facilities located on the land or
otherwise make lawful use of the land, or a supply of water, energy or fuel; “
land ” does not include buildings other than— agricultural buildings within
the meaning of paragraphs 3 to 8 of Schedule 5 to the Local Government Finance
Act 1988, or scheduled monuments within the meaning of the Ancient Monuments
and Archaeological Areas Act 1979; “ the local authority ”, in relation to
common land, has the same meaning as in section 61; “ occupier ” means the
person entitled to possession of the land by virtue of an estate or interest
held by the person; “ offensive conduct ” means— the use of threatening,
abusive or insulting words or behaviour, or disorderly behaviour, or the
display of any writing, sign, or other visible representation that is
threatening, abusive or insulting; “ vehicle ” includes— any vehicle, whether
or not it is in a fit state for use on roads, and includes any chassis or
body, with or without wheels, appearing to have formed part of such a vehicle,
and any load carried by, and anything attached to, such a vehicle, and a
caravan as defined in section 29(1) of the Caravan Sites and Control of
Development Act 1960.

83.1.60C.9

For the purposes of this section a person is to be considered as residing or
having the intention to reside in a place even if that residence or intended
residence is temporary, and a person may be regarded as residing or having an
intention to reside in a place notwithstanding that the person has a home
elsewhere.

########### Offence under section 60C: seizure of property etc

83.1.60D

83.1.60D.1

If a constable reasonably suspects that an offence has been committed under
section 60C, the constable may seize and remove any relevant property that
appears to the constable—

83.1.60D.1.a

to belong to the person who the constable suspects has committed the offence
(“ P ”);

83.1.60D.1.b

to be in P’s possession; or

83.1.60D.1.c

to be under P’s control.

83.1.60D.2

“ Relevant property ” means—

83.1.60D.2.a

a vehicle (wherever located) which, for the purposes of section 60C (1)(b)
(in the case of an offence under section 60C (2)(a) ) or for the purposes of
section 60C (2)(b)(ii)  (in the case of an offence under section 60C (2)(b) ),
the constable suspects P had or intended to have with them, or

83.1.60D.2.b

any other property that is on the relevant land.

83.1.60D.3

The “relevant land” is the land in respect of which a request under section
60C (1)(d)  is made.

83.1.60D.4

The relevant chief officer of police may retain any property that has been
seized under subsection  (1)  until the end of the period of three months
beginning with the day of the seizure (“ the relevant period ”).

83.1.60D.5

But the relevant chief officer of police ceases to be entitled to retain the
property if before the end of the relevant period a custody officer gives
written notice to P that P is not to be prosecuted for the offence under
section 60C in relation to which the property was seized.

(And see subsection  (10) ).

83.1.60D.6

Subsection  (7)  applies where before the end of the relevant period
proceedings for an offence under section 60C are commenced against P.

83.1.60D.7

Where this subsection applies the relevant chief officer of police may retain
the property seized until the conclusion of proceedings relating to the
offence (including any appeal) (but see subsection  (10) ).

83.1.60D.8

Where a chief officer of police ceases to be entitled to retain property under
this section the chief officer must, subject to any order for forfeiture under
section 60E, return it to the person whom the chief officer believes to be its
owner.

83.1.60D.9

If a chief officer of police cannot after reasonable inquiry identify a person
for the purposes of subsection  (8) —

83.1.60D.9.a

the chief officer must apply to a magistrates’ court for directions, and

83.1.60D.9.b

the court must make an order about the treatment of the property.

83.1.60D.10

If at any time a person other than P satisfies a chief officer of police that
property that is retained by the chief officer under this section—

83.1.60D.10.a

belongs to the person at that time, and

83.1.60D.10.b

belonged to them at the time of the suspected offence under section 60C,

the chief officer must return the property to the person.

83.1.60D.11

Subsection  (10)  does not apply in relation to a vehicle belonging to a
person other than P if the chief officer of police reasonably believes that
the vehicle was, with the consent of the other person, in P’s possession or
under P’s control at the time of the suspected offence under section 60C.

83.1.60D.12

For the purposes of subsection  (6) , proceedings are commenced when—

83.1.60D.12.a

a written charge is issued under section 29(1) of the Criminal Justice Act
2003,

83.1.60D.12.b

a person is charged under Part 4 of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984,
or

83.1.60D.12.c

an information is laid under section 1 of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980.

83.1.60D.13

For the purposes of this section—

83.1.60D.13.a

the relevant chief officer of police is the chief officer of the police force
for the area in which the property was seized, and

83.1.60D.13.b

“ vehicle ” has the same meaning as in section 60C.

########### Offence under section 60C: forfeiture

83.1.60E

83.1.60E.1

A court that convicts a person of an offence under section 60C may order any
property to which subsection  (2)  applies to be forfeited and dealt with in a
manner specified in the order.

83.1.60E.2

This subsection applies to any property that—

83.1.60E.2.a

was seized under section 60D(1), and

83.1.60E.2.b

is retained by a chief officer of police under that section.

83.1.60E.3

Before making an order for the forfeiture of property the court must—

83.1.60E.3.a

permit anyone who claims to be its owner or to have an interest in it to make
representations, and

83.1.60E.3.b

consider its value and the likely consequences of forfeiture.

83.2

In the heading to Part 5 of the Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994,
after “Order:” insert  “Unauthorised encampments and ” .

subsections  (3)  to  (7) .

84.3.a.i

in the case of persons trespassing on land in England and Wales, has caused

84.3.a.ii

in the case of persons trespassing on land in Scotland,

, and

84.3.b

at the beginning of paragraph (b) insert  “in either case,” .

84.5.4ZA

84.7.10

For the purposes of subsection (1)(a)(i)—

“ damage ” includes— damage to the land; damage to any property on the land
not belonging to the persons trespassing; damage to the environment (including
excessive noise, smells, litter or deposits of waste); “ disruption ” includes
an interference with— a person’s ability to access any services or facilities

in the case of a person trespassing on land in England and Wales, the period
of twelve months beginning with the day on which the direction was given;

84.8.b.1A.a

in the case of a person trespassing on land in Scotland, the period of three

84.11.a

a highway unless it is a footpath, bridleway or byway open to all traffic
within the meaning of Part 3 of the Wildlife and Countryside Act 1981, is a
restricted byway within the meaning of Part 2 of the Countryside and Rights of
Way Act 2000 or is a cycle track under the Highways Act 1980 or the Cycle

84.11.aa

within the definitions in section 151(2)(a)(ii) or (b) (footpaths and cycle

.

#### Guidance on exercise of police powers in respect of trespassers on land etc

85

After section 62E of the Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994 insert—

######## Guidance

85.62F

85.62F.1

The Secretary of State must issue guidance relating to the exercise of—

85.62F.1.a

the functions of police officers in England and Wales, and

85.62F.1.b

the functions of constables in England and Wales,

under the provisions mentioned in subsection  (2) .

85.62F.2

Those provisions are—

85.62F.2.a

sections 60C to 62E, and

85.62F.2.b

regulations under section 67 relating to vehicles seized under section 62(1)
or section 62C(3).

85.62F.3

Police officers in England and Wales and constables in England and Wales must
have regard to the guidance when exercising any of those functions conferred
on them.

85.62F.4

The Secretary of State may from time to time revise the guidance.

85.62F.5

The Secretary of State must arrange for the guidance and any revised guidance
issued under this section to be published in such manner as the Secretary of
State considers appropriate.

85.62F.6

The Secretary of State must lay before Parliament a copy of any guidance or
revised guidance published under subsection (5).

##### Causing serious injury by careless, or inconsiderate, driving

87

87.1

In the Road Traffic Act 1988, after section 2B (causing death by careless, or
inconsiderate, driving) insert—

########### Causing serious injury by careless, or inconsiderate, driving

87.1.2C

87.1.2C.1

A person who causes serious injury to another person by driving a mechanically
propelled vehicle on a road or other public place without due care and
attention, or without reasonable consideration for other persons using the
road or place, is guilty of an offence.

87.1.2C.2

In this section “ serious injury ” means—

87.1.2C.2.a

in England and Wales, physical harm which amounts to grievous bodily harm for
the purposes of the Offences against the Person Act 1861, and

87.1.2C.2.b

in Scotland, severe physical injury.

87.2

In section 3ZA of that Act (meaning of careless, or inconsiderate, driving),
in subsection (1), after “sections 2B” insert  “, 2C” .

87.3

In Part 1 of Schedule 2 to the Road Traffic Offenders Act 1988 (prosecution
and punishment of offences: offences under the Traffic Acts), after the entry
relating to section 2B of the Road Traffic Act 1988 insert—

RTA section 2C Causing serious injury by careless, or inconsiderate, driving
(a) Summarily (a) On conviction in England and Wales: 12 months or a fine or
both Obligatory Obligatory 3-11 On conviction in Scotland: 12 months or the
statutory maximum or both (b) On indictment (b) 2 years or a fine or both

87.4

In the entries in Part 1 of Schedule 2 to the Road Traffic Offenders Act 1988
relating to an offence under section 2C of the Road Traffic Act 1988 (causing
serious injury by careless, or inconsiderate, driving), in relation to an
offence committed before paragraph 24(2) of Schedule 22 to the Sentencing Act
2020 comes into force, the reference in column (4) (punishment) to 12 months
on summary conviction in England and Wales is to be read as a reference to 6
months.
