#### Courses offered as an alternative to prosecution

##### Courses offered as alternative to prosecution: fees etc

89

89.1

After section 90F of the Road Traffic Offenders Act 1988 insert—

########### Courses offered as alternative to prosecution

############ Power to charge fees: England and Wales

89.1.90G

89.1.90G.1

A policing body may charge a fee for enrolment on an approved course offered
as an alternative to prosecution in England and Wales for a specified fixed
penalty offence.

89.1.90G.2

A fee may be set at a level that exceeds the cost of an approved course and
related administrative expenses, but any excess must be used for the purpose
of promoting road safety.

89.1.90G.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about—

89.1.90G.3.a

how fees, or components of fees, are to be calculated;

89.1.90G.3.b

the level of fees or components of fees;

89.1.90G.3.c

the use of fee income.

89.1.90G.4

The regulations may include provision as to the amount, or maximum amount, of
a fee or component of a fee.

89.1.90G.5

In this section—

“ approved course ” means a course approved (whether before or after this
section comes into force) by a body specified in regulations under subsection
(6) ; “ fixed penalty offence ” means an offence that is a fixed penalty
offence for the purposes of Part 3 (see section 51); “ policing body ” means—
a local policing body, or the British Transport Police Authority; “ promoting
road safety ” includes the prevention, detection or enforcement of offences
relating to vehicles; “ prosecution ”, in relation to an offence, includes any
alternative way of being dealt with for the offence (other than attending an
approved course); “ specified fixed penalty offence ” means an offence
specified under subsection  (6) .

89.1.90G.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

89.1.90G.6.a

specify fixed penalty offences for the purposes of this section;

89.1.90G.6.b

specify a body to approve courses for the purposes of this section.

89.1.90G.7

Nothing in this section limits any power to charge fees apart from this
section.

############ Power to prevent courses being offered for repeat offences: England and Wales

89.1.90H

89.1.90H.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations prohibit a chief officer from
offering an approved course to a person as an alternative to prosecution in
England and Wales for a specified fixed penalty offence where—

89.1.90H.1.a

there is a course fee, and

89.1.90H.1.b

the person has, within a period specified in the regulations, satisfactorily
completed a similar approved course in respect of an earlier specified fixed
penalty offence.

89.1.90H.2

The regulations must include provision for the purpose of identifying what
counts as a “similar” course; and that provision may, in particular, confer
power on a person to determine what courses count as similar.

89.1.90H.3

In this section “ chief officer ” means—

89.1.90H.3.a

a chief officer of police of a police force in England and Wales, or

89.1.90H.3.b

the Chief Constable of the British Transport Police Force.

89.1.90H.4

In this section the following terms have the meaning given by section  90G (5)
—

“approved course”; “prosecution”; “specified fixed penalty offence”.

############ Further provision about regulations under this Part

89.1.90I

89.1.90I.1

A power to make regulations under this Part is exercisable by statutory
instrument.

89.1.90I.2

A statutory instrument containing regulations made by the Secretary of State
under this Part is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either
House of Parliament.

89.1.90I.3

Regulations under this Part may include—

89.1.90I.3.a

incidental or supplementary provision;

89.1.90I.3.b

different provision for different purposes.

89.2

After Article 91F of the Road Traffic Offenders (Northern Ireland) Order 1996
( S.I. 1996/1320 (N.I. 10) ) insert—

########### Courses offered as alternative to prosecution

############ Power to charge fees

89.2.91G

89.2.91G.1

The Chief Constable may charge a fee for enrolment on an approved course
offered as an alternative to prosecution for a specified fixed penalty
offence.

89.2.91G.2

A fee may be set at a level that exceeds the cost of an approved course and
related administrative expenses, but any excess must be used for the purpose
of promoting road safety.

89.2.91G.3

The power in paragraph  (1)  may be exercised only with the approval in
writing of the Policing Board.

Such approval may be given—

89.2.91G.3.a

generally or specifically, and

89.2.91G.3.b

subject to conditions.

89.2.91G.4

The Department of Justice may by regulations make further provision about—

89.2.91G.4.a

how fees, or components of fees, are to be calculated;

89.2.91G.4.b

the level of fees or components of fees;

89.2.91G.4.c

the use of fee income.

89.2.91G.5

The regulations may include provision as to the amount, or maximum amount, of
a fee or component of a fee.

89.2.91G.6

In this Article—

“ approved course ” means a course approved (whether before or after this
Article comes into operation) by a body specified in regulations under
paragraph  (7) ; “ fixed penalty offence ” means an offence that is a fixed
penalty offence for the purposes of Part 4 (see Article 57); “ promoting road
safety ” includes the prevention, detection or enforcement of offences
relating to vehicles; “ prosecution ”, in relation to an offence, includes any
alternative way of being dealt with for the offence (other than attending an
approved course); “ specified fixed penalty offence ” means an offence
specified under paragraph  (7) .

89.2.91G.7

The Department of Justice may by regulations—

89.2.91G.7.a

specify fixed penalty offences for the purposes of this Article;

89.2.91G.7.b

specify a body to approve courses for the purposes of this Article.

89.2.91G.8

Nothing in this Article limits any power to charge fees apart from this
Article.

############ Power to prevent courses being offered for repeat offences

89.2.91H

89.2.91H.1

The Department of Justice may by regulations prohibit the Chief Constable from
offering an approved course to a person as an alternative to prosecution for a
specified fixed penalty offence where—

89.2.91H.1.a

there is a course fee, and

89.2.91H.1.b

the person has, within a period specified in the regulations, satisfactorily
completed a similar approved course in respect of an earlier specified fixed
penalty offence.

89.2.91H.2

The regulations must include provision for the purpose of identifying what
counts as a “similar” course; and that provision may, in particular, confer
power on a person to determine what courses count as similar.

89.2.91H.3

In this Article the following terms have the meaning given by Article  91G (6)
—

“approved course”; “prosecution”; “specified fixed penalty offence”.

############ Further provision about regulations under this Part

89.2.91I

89.2.91I.1

Regulations under this Part are subject to negative resolution.

89.2.91I.2

Regulations under Article 91G (4)  may be made only with the consent of the
Department of Finance.

89.2.91I.3

Regulations under this Part may include such incidental or supplementary
provision as appears to the Department of Justice to be necessary or
expedient.

89.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Part 3B of the Road Traffic
Offenders Act 1988 for the purpose of making provision corresponding or
similar to section  90G  or  90H  of that Act in relation to courses offered
as an alternative to prosecution in Scotland for a fixed penalty offence.

89.4

In subsection  (3)  “ fixed penalty offence ” means an offence that is a fixed
penalty offence for the purposes of Part 3 of the Road Traffic Offenders Act
1988 (see section 51 of that Act).

89.5

The Secretary of State must consult the Lord Advocate before making
regulations under subsection  (3) .

89.6

The power to make regulations under subsection  (3)  is exercisable by
statutory instrument.

89.7

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (3)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

########### Surrender of licence to Secretary of State where disqualified

92.1.37A

92.1.37A.1

92.1.37A.1.b

92.1.37A.3.c

92.1.37A.4

### Cautions

#### Introductory

##### Diversionary and community cautions

98

98.1

This Part makes provision for cautions known as—

98.1.a

diversionary cautions, and

98.1.b

community cautions.

98.2

A diversionary caution may, in accordance with this Part, be given by an
authorised person to a person aged 18 or over in respect of an offence.

98.3

A community caution may, in accordance with this Part, be given by an
authorised person to a person aged 18 or over in respect of an offence other
than an excluded offence.

98.4

Diversionary and community cautions must have one or more conditions attached
to them.

98.5

Breach of a condition may, in accordance with this Part, result in—

98.5.a

prosecution for the offence, in the case of a diversionary caution, or

98.5.b

a financial penalty, in the case of a community caution.

98.6

In this Part “ excluded offence ” means—

98.6.a

an indictable-only offence;

98.6.b

an offence triable either way which is prescribed in regulations, or

98.6.c

a summary offence which is prescribed in regulations.

98.7

In this Part “ authorised person ”, in relation to a diversionary or community
caution, means—

98.7.a

a constable,

98.7.b

an investigating officer, or

98.7.c

a person authorised by a prosecution authority for purposes relating to
cautions of that kind.

#### Diversionary cautions

##### Giving a diversionary caution

99

99.1

An authorised person may give a diversionary caution to a person aged 18 or
over (“the offender”) in respect of an offence if the following requirements
are met.

99.2

The requirements are that—

99.2.a

an authorised person or a prosecution authority decides—

99.2.a.i

that there is sufficient evidence to charge the offender with the offence, and

99.2.a.ii

that a diversionary caution should be given to the offender in respect of the
offence;

99.2.b

the offender admits having committed the offence;

99.2.c

the offender consents to being given the caution;

99.2.d

an authorised person—

99.2.d.i

explains the effect of the caution to the offender, and

99.2.d.ii

in particular, warns the offender that failure to comply with any of the
conditions attached to the caution may result in prosecution for the offence;

99.2.e

the offender signs a document which contains—

99.2.e.i

details of the offence,

99.2.e.ii

the offender’s admission to having committed the offence,

99.2.e.iii

the offender’s consent to being given the caution, and

99.2.e.iv

the conditions attached to the caution.

99.3

But if the offence is an indictable-only offence, the authorised person may
not give a diversionary caution to the offender except—

99.3.a

in exceptional circumstances relating to the person or the offence, and

99.3.b

with the consent of the Director of Public Prosecutions.

99.4

A diversionary caution may not be given in respect of an offence committed
before the coming into force of this section.

99.5

The power to give a diversionary caution under subsection  (1)  is also
subject to regulations under section 117 (restrictions on multiple use of
cautions).

##### Deciding on the conditions

100

100.1

The conditions attached to a diversionary caution are to be decided upon by—

100.1.a

an authorised person, or

100.1.b

in a case where a prosecution authority has taken the decision that the
caution should be given, the prosecution authority.

100.2

The conditions which may be attached to a diversionary caution are those
authorised by—

100.2.a

section 101 (rehabilitation and reparation conditions),

100.2.b

section 102 (financial penalty conditions), and

100.2.c

section 103 (conditions relating to certain foreign offenders).

100.3

When deciding what conditions to attach to a diversionary caution the
authorised person or prosecution authority must—

100.3.a

make reasonable efforts, or ensure that reasonable efforts are or have been
made, to obtain the views of any victim or victims of the offence, and

100.3.b

take those views into account.

100.4

The views referred to in subsection  (3)  include in particular views as to
whether the offender should carry out any of the actions listed in the
community remedy document.

100.5

Where it is the view of the victim or all the victims that the offender should
carry out a particular action listed in the community remedy document, the
authorised person or prosecution authority must attach that as a condition
unless it seems to the authorised person or prosecution authority—

100.5.a

the action is not one that can be attached as a condition to a diversionary
caution, or

100.5.b

it would be inappropriate to do so.

##### Rehabilitation and reparation conditions

101

101.1

Conditions with one or both of the objects in subsection  (2)  may be attached
to a diversionary caution.

101.2

The objects are—

101.2.a

facilitating the rehabilitation of the offender;

101.2.b

ensuring that the offender makes reparation for the offence.

101.3

The conditions which may be attached to a diversionary caution for the objects
referred to in subsection  (2)  include—

101.3.a

restrictive conditions,

101.3.b

unpaid work conditions, and

101.3.c

attendance conditions.

101.4

A restrictive condition is a condition requiring the offender—

101.4.a

not to meet or communicate with specified individuals;

101.4.b

not to be in, or go to, specified addresses, places or areas in the United
Kingdom;

101.4.c

not to carry out or participate in specified activities;

101.4.d

not to engage in specified conduct (which may include conduct constituting a
criminal offence).

101.5

An unpaid work condition is a condition requiring the offender to carry out
unpaid work of a specified description for a specified number of hours, which
may not exceed 20.

101.6

An attendance condition is a condition requiring the offender to attend a
specified place—

101.6.a

for a specified purpose, and

101.6.b

for a specified number of hours, which may not exceed 20 where the condition
only has the object referred to in subsection  (2)(b) .

101.7

Where an attendance condition requires the offender to attend somewhere for
the purpose of participating in any education or training, or receiving any
other service, the attendance condition may also require the offender to pay
for the reasonable cost of the provision of the education, training or service
to the offender.

101.8

Regulations may amend subsection  (5)  or  (6)(b)  (or both) so as to
substitute a different number of hours.

101.9

A condition authorised by this section may—

101.9.a

contain further details as to how it must be complied with (including the
times at or between which something must or must not be done);

101.9.b

provide for those details to be supplied, after the giving of the caution, by
a specified person or a person of a specified description.

101.10

A condition authorised by this section may not require a person to remain at
their own or anyone else’s residence for any period of time.

101.11

In this section “ specified ” means specified in the caution.

##### Financial penalty conditions

102

102.1

A condition requiring the offender to pay a financial penalty may be attached
to a diversionary caution with the object of punishing the offender.

102.2

The condition must specify—

102.2.a

the amount of the financial penalty,

102.2.b

the person to whom the financial penalty must be paid,

102.2.c

how it must or may be paid, and

102.2.d

the date on or before which it must be paid.

102.3

The amount specified under subsection  (2)(a)  must not exceed an amount
prescribed in regulations.

102.4

Where the person specified under subsection  (2)(b)  is not the designated
officer for a magistrates’ court, once the penalty is paid to that person they
must give it to such an officer.

102.5

The date specified under subsection  (2)(d)  must be the last day of the
period of 28 days beginning with the day on which the caution is given.

##### Foreign offenders’ conditions

103

103.1

Where a diversionary caution is given to a relevant foreign offender, a
condition with one or both of the objects in subsection  (2)  may be attached
to it.

103.2

The objects are—

103.2.a

bringing about the departure of the relevant foreign offender from the United
Kingdom;

103.2.b

ensuring that the relevant foreign offender does not return to the United
Kingdom for a period of time.

103.3

If a diversionary caution has a condition with the object referred to in
subsection  (2)(b) , the expiry of the period does not of itself give rise to
any right on the part of the offender to return to the United Kingdom.

103.4

In this section “ relevant foreign offender ” means—

103.4.a

an offender directions for whose removal from the United Kingdom have been, or
may be, given under Schedule 2 to the Immigration Act 1971 or section 10 of
the Immigration and Asylum Act 1999, or

103.4.b

an offender against whom a deportation order under section 5 of the
Immigration Act 1971 is in force.

##### Variation of conditions

104

An authorised person or prosecution authority may, with the consent of the
offender, vary the conditions attached to a diversionary caution by—

104.a

varying or omitting any of the conditions;

104.b

adding a condition.

##### Effect of diversionary caution

105

105.1

Where a diversionary caution is given, criminal proceedings may be instituted
against the offender for the offence in respect of which the caution was given
if, but only if, the offender fails without reasonable excuse to comply with
any of the conditions attached to the caution.

105.2

The document mentioned in section 99 (2)(e)  is admissible in such
proceedings.

105.3

Where such proceedings are instituted, the diversionary caution ceases to have
effect.

##### Arrest for failure to comply

106

106.1

If a constable has reasonable grounds for believing that the offender has
failed without reasonable excuse to comply with any of the conditions attached
to a diversionary caution, the constable may arrest the offender without
warrant.

106.2

A person arrested under this section must be—

106.2.a

charged with the offence in question, or

106.2.b

released without charge.

106.3

A person released without charge under subsection  (2)(b)  must be—

106.3.a

released on bail if—

106.3.a.i

the release is to enable a decision to be made as to whether the offender
should be charged with the offence, and

106.3.a.ii

the pre-conditions for bail are satisfied, or

106.3.b

in any other case, released without bail (with or without any variation in the
conditions attached to the caution).

106.4

Subsection  (2)  also applies in the case of—

106.4.a

a person who, having been released on bail under subsection  (3)(a) , returns
to a police station to answer bail or is otherwise in police detention at a
police station;

106.4.b

a person who, having been released on bail under section 30A of the 1984 Act
(bail elsewhere than at police station) as applied by section 107 below,
attends at a police station to answer bail or is otherwise in police detention
at a police station;

106.4.c

a person who is arrested under section 30D or 46A of the 1984 Act (power of
arrest for failure to answer to police bail) as applied by section 107 below.

106.5

Where a person is released on bail under subsection  (3)(a) , the custody
officer must inform the person that the release is to enable a decision to be
made as to whether the person should be charged with the offence in question.

106.6

A person arrested under this section, or any other person in whose case
subsection  (2)  applies, may be kept in police detention—

106.6.a

to enable the person to be dealt with in accordance with that subsection, or

106.6.b

where applicable, to enable the power under section 47(4A) of the 1984 Act
(power of custody officer to appoint a different or additional time for
answering to police bail), as applied by section 107 below, to be exercised.

If the person is not in a fit state to be dealt with in that way, or to enable
that power to be exercised, they may be kept in police detention until they
are.

106.7

The power under subsection  (6)(a)  includes power to keep the person in
police detention if it is necessary to do so for the purpose of investigating
whether the person has failed, without reasonable excuse, to comply with any
of the conditions attached to the diversionary caution.

106.8

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  must be complied with as soon as practicable after
the person arrested arrives at the police station or, in the case of a person
arrested at the police station, as soon as practicable after the arrest.

106.9

Subsection  (2)  does not require a person who—

106.9.a

falls within subsection  (4)(a)  or  (b) , and

106.9.b

is in police detention in relation to a matter other than the diversionary
caution,

to be released if the person is liable to be kept in detention in relation to
that other matter.

106.10

In subsection  (3)(a)(ii) , the reference to the pre-conditions for bail is to
be read in accordance with section 50A of the 1984 Act.

##### Application of Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984

107

107.1

In the case of a person arrested under section 106, the provisions of the 1984
Act specified in subsection  (2)  apply, with the modifications specified in
subsection  (3)  and with such further modifications as are necessary, as they
apply in the case of a person arrested for an offence.

107.2

The provisions are—

107.2.a

section 30 (arrest elsewhere than at police station);

107.2.b

sections 30A to 30D (bail elsewhere than at police station);

107.2.c

section 31 (arrest for further offence);

107.2.d

section 34(1) to (5E) (limitations on police detention);

107.2.e

section 36 (custody officers at police stations);

107.2.f

section 37(4) to (6C) (record of grounds for detention);

107.2.g

section 38 (duties of custody officer after charge);

107.2.h

section 39 (responsibilities in relation to persons detained);

107.2.i

section 55A (x-rays and ultrasound scans).

107.3

The modifications are—

107.3.a

in section 30CA, omit subsections (4A) to (4D);

107.3.b

in section 30CA, in subsection (5), in paragraph (a) of the definition of
“relevant officer”, for the reference to being involved in the investigation
of the relevant offence substitute a reference to being involved—

107.3.b.i

in the investigation of the offence in respect of which the person was given
the diversionary caution, or

107.3.b.ii

in investigating whether the person has failed, without reasonable excuse, to
comply with any of the conditions attached to the diversionary caution;

107.3.c

in section 36(5) and (7), for the references to being involved in the
investigation of an offence for which the person is in police detention
substitute references to being involved—

107.3.c.i

in the investigation of the offence in respect of which the person was given
the diversionary caution, or

107.3.c.ii

in investigating whether the person has failed, without reasonable excuse, to
comply with any of the conditions attached to the diversionary caution;

107.3.d

in section 38(1)(a)(iii) and (iv), for “arrested for” substitute  “charged
with” ;

107.3.e

in section 39(2) and (3), for the references to an offence substitute
references to a failure to comply with conditions attached to the diversionary
caution.

107.4

Section 40 of the 1984 Act (review of police detention) applies to a person in
police detention by virtue of section 106 above as it applies to a person in
police detention in connection with the investigation of an offence, but with
the following modifications—

107.4.a

omit subsections (8) and (8A);

107.4.b

in subsection (9), for the reference to section 37(9) or 37D(5) substitute a
reference to the second sentence of section 106(6) above.

107.5

The following provisions of the 1984 Act apply to a person released on bail
under section 106(3)(a) above as they apply to a person released on bail under
section 37 of that Act—

107.5.a

section 46A (power of arrest for failure to answer to police bail);

107.5.b

section 47 (bail after arrest), except subsections (4D) and (4E).

107.6

Section 54 of the 1984 Act (searches of detained persons) applies in the case
of a person who falls within section 106(4) above and is detained in a police
station under that section as it applies in the case of a person who falls
within section 34(7) of that Act and is detained at a police station under
section 37.

107.7

Section 54A of the 1984 Act (searches and examination to ascertain identity)
applies with the following modifications in the case of a person who is
detained in a police station under section 106 above—

107.7.a

in subsections (1)(a) and (12), after “as a person involved in the commission
of an offence” insert  “or as having failed to comply with any of the
conditions attached to the person’s diversionary caution” ;

107.7.b

in subsection (9)(a), after “the investigation of an offence” insert  “, the
investigation of whether the person in question has failed to comply with any
of the conditions attached to the person’s diversionary caution” .

#### Community cautions

##### Giving a community caution

108

108.1

An authorised person may give a community caution to a person aged 18 or over
(“the offender”) in respect of an offence, other than an excluded offence, if
the following requirements are met.

108.2

The requirements are that—

108.2.a

an authorised person or a prosecution authority decides that—

108.2.a.i

there is sufficient evidence to charge the offender with the offence, and

108.2.a.ii

a community caution should be given to the offender in respect of the offence;

108.2.b

the offender admits to having committed the offence;

108.2.c

the offender consents to being given the caution;

108.2.d

an authorised person—

108.2.d.i

explains the effect of the caution to the offender, and

108.2.d.ii

in particular, warns the offender of the effect of failure to comply with any
of the conditions attached to the caution;

108.2.e

the offender signs a document which contains—

108.2.e.i

details of the offence,

108.2.e.ii

the offender’s admission to having committed the offence,

108.2.e.iii

the offender’s consent to being given the caution, and

108.2.e.iv

the conditions attached to the caution.

108.3

A community caution may not be given in respect of an offence committed before
the coming into force of this section.

108.4

The power to give a community caution under subsection  (1)  is also subject
to regulations under section 117 (restrictions on multiple use of cautions).

##### Deciding on the conditions

109

109.1

The conditions attached to a community caution are to be decided upon by—

109.1.a

an authorised person, or

109.1.b

in a case where a prosecution authority has taken the decision that the
caution should be given, the prosecution authority.

109.2

The conditions which may be attached to a community caution are those
authorised by—

109.2.a

section 110 (rehabilitation and reparation conditions), and

109.2.b

section 111 (financial penalty conditions).

109.3

When deciding what conditions to attach to a community caution the authorised
person or prosecution authority must—

109.3.a

make reasonable efforts, or ensure that reasonable efforts are or have been
made, to obtain the views of any victim or victims of the offence, and

109.3.b

take those views into account.

109.4

The views referred to in subsection  (3)  include in particular views as to
whether the offender should carry out any of the actions listed in the
community remedy document.

109.5

Where it is the view of the victim or all the victims that the offender should
carry out a particular action listed in the community remedy document, the
authorised person or prosecution authority must attach that as a condition
unless it seems to the authorised person or prosecution authority—

109.5.a

the action is not one that can be attached as a condition to a community
caution, or

109.5.b

it would be inappropriate to do so.

##### Rehabilitation and reparation conditions

110

110.1

Conditions with one or both of the objects in subsection  (2)  may be attached
to a community caution.

110.2

The objects are—

110.2.a

facilitating the rehabilitation of the offender;

110.2.b

ensuring that the offender makes reparation for the offence.

110.3

The conditions which may be attached to a community caution for the objects
referred to in subsection  (2)  include—

110.3.a

restrictive conditions,

110.3.b

unpaid work conditions, and

110.3.c

attendance conditions.

110.4

A restrictive condition is a condition requiring the offender—

110.4.a

not to meet or communicate with specified individuals;

110.4.b

not to be in or go to specified addresses, places or areas in the United
Kingdom;

110.4.c

not to carry out or participate in specified activities;

110.4.d

not to engage in specified conduct (which may include conduct constituting a
criminal offence).

110.5

An unpaid work condition is a condition requiring the offender to carry out
unpaid work of a specified description for a specified number of hours, which
may not exceed 10.

110.6

An attendance condition is a condition requiring the offender to attend a
specified place—

110.6.a

for a specified purpose, and

110.6.b

for a specified number of hours, which may not exceed 10 where the condition
only has the object referred to in subsection  (2)(b) .

110.7

Where an attendance condition requires the offender to attend somewhere for
the purpose of participating in any education or training, or receiving any
other service, the attendance condition may also require the offender to pay
for the reasonable cost of the provision of the education, training or service
to the offender.

110.8

Regulations may amend subsection  (5)  or  (6)(b)  (or both) so as to
substitute a different number of hours.

110.9

A condition authorised by this section may—

110.9.a

contain further details as to how it must be complied with (including the
times at or between which something must or must not be done);

110.9.b

provide for those details to be supplied, after the giving of the caution, by
a specified person or a person of a specified description.

110.10

A condition authorised by this section may not require a person to remain at
their own or anyone else’s residence for any period of time.

110.11

In this section “ specified ” means specified in the caution.

##### Financial penalty conditions

111

111.1

A condition requiring the offender to pay a financial penalty may be attached
to a community caution with the object of punishing the offender.

111.2

The condition must specify—

111.2.a

the amount of the financial penalty,

111.2.b

the person to whom the financial penalty must be paid,

111.2.c

how it must or may be paid,

111.2.d

the date on or before which the penalty must be paid, and

111.2.e

the consequences of non-payment.

111.3

The amount specified under subsection  (2)(a)  must not exceed an amount
prescribed in regulations.

111.4

Where the person specified under subsection  (2)(b)  is not the designated
officer for a magistrates’ court, once the penalty is paid to that person they
must give it to such an officer.

111.5

The date specified under subsection  (2)(d)  must be the last day of the
period of 28 days beginning with the day on which the caution is given.

111.6

If the financial penalty is not paid on or before the date specified under
subsection  (2)(d) , the amount of the penalty required to be paid by the
condition is increased by 50%.

111.7

Where subsection  (6)  applies, if the increased penalty is not paid within
the period of 21 days beginning with the day after the date specified under
subsection  (2)(d) , the amount of the increased penalty may be registered
under section 112 for enforcement against the offender as a fine.

##### Enforcement of financial penalties: registration

112

112.1

The chief officer of police may, in respect of any amount registrable under
section 111 (7) , issue a certificate (“a registration certificate”)—

112.1.a

giving particulars of the financial penalty,

112.1.b

stating that the amount is registrable for enforcement against the offender as
a fine, and

112.1.c

stating the name and last known address of the offender.

112.2

The chief officer of police issuing a registration certificate must cause it
to be sent to the designated officer for the local justice area in which the
offender appears to the chief officer to reside.

112.3

The designated officer for a local justice area in receipt of a registration
certificate must—

112.3.a

register the amount for enforcement as a fine in that area by entering it in
the register of a magistrates’ court acting for that area, or

112.3.b

if it appears to the designated officer that the offender does not reside in
that area, cause the certificate to be sent to the person appearing to the
officer to be the designated officer for the local justice area in which the
offender resides.

112.4

A designated officer registering an amount under this section for enforcement
as a fine must give the offender notice of the registration which—

112.4.a

specifies the amount registered, and

112.4.b

gives the information with respect to the financial penalty, and the authority
for registration, that was included in the registration certificate.

112.5

If an amount is registered in a magistrates’ court as a result of this
section, any enactment referring (in whatever terms) to a fine imposed, or
other sum adjudged to be paid, on conviction by such a court applies as if the
registered amount were a fine imposed by that court on the conviction of the
offender on the date on which the amount was registered.

##### Enforcement of financial penalties: court proceedings

113

113.1

This section applies where, in any proceedings for the enforcement of an
amount registered under this section, the person against whom the proceedings
are taken claims—

113.1.a

not to be the person to whom the community caution was given,

113.1.b

to have paid the amount that was required to be paid, or

113.1.c

to have a reasonable excuse for not paying.

113.2

The court may adjourn the proceedings, on one or more occasions, for the
purpose of allowing the claim to be investigated, but must not adjourn for
more than 28 days in total.

113.3

The court must accept a claim under subsection  (1)(a)  or  (b)  unless it is
shown, on the balance of probabilities, that the claim is unfounded.

113.4

Where a court accepts a claim under subsection  (1)(b) , the condition of the
caution by virtue of which the amount is required to be paid ceases to have
effect.

113.5

In the case of a claim under subsection  (1)(c) , the court must accept the
claim so far as relating to the facts claimed (leaving aside any question as
to the reasonableness of the excuse), unless it is shown, on the balance of
probabilities, that the claim so far as relating to those facts is unfounded.

113.6

Where a court accepts a claim under subsection  (1)(c) , the court may order
that the condition of the caution by virtue of which the amount is required to
be paid—

113.6.a

ceases to have effect, or

113.6.b

is varied so as to reduce the amount payable or to extend the time for payment
(or both).

##### Variation of conditions

114

114.1

An authorised person or prosecution authority may, with the consent of the
offender, vary the conditions attached to a community caution by—

114.1.a

varying or omitting any of the conditions;

114.1.b

adding a condition.

114.2

See also section 115 (2)  (addition of financial penalty).

##### Effect of community caution

115

115.1

Where a community caution is given, criminal proceedings may not be instituted
against the offender for the offence in respect of which the caution was
given.

115.2

If the offender fails without reasonable excuse to comply with any condition
imposed under section 110, an authorised person or prosecution authority may—

115.2.a

rescind the condition, and

115.2.b

attach a condition imposing a financial penalty (or further such condition)
under section 111.

#### General

##### Code of practice

116

116.1

The Secretary of State must prepare a code of practice in relation to
diversionary and community cautions.

116.2

The code may, in particular, include provision as to—

116.2.a

the circumstances in which diversionary and community cautions may be given;

116.2.b

the procedure to be followed in connection with the giving of diversionary and
community cautions;

116.2.c

the conditions which may be attached to diversionary and community cautions
and the time for which they may have effect;

116.2.d

the category of constable or investigating officer by whom diversionary and
community cautions may be given;

116.2.e

the persons whom a prosecution authority may authorise as authorised persons
for the purposes of this Part;

116.2.f

the form which diversionary and community cautions are to take and the manner
in which they are to be given and recorded;

116.2.g

the places where diversionary and community cautions may be given;

116.2.h

the provision which may be made in a condition under section 102 (2)(b)  or
111 (2)(b) ;

116.2.i

the monitoring of compliance with conditions attached to diversionary and
community cautions;

116.2.j

the exercise of the power of arrest conferred by section 106 (1) ;

116.2.k

who is to decide how a person should be dealt with under section 106 (2)  and
(3) .

116.3

After preparing a draft of the code the Secretary of State—

116.3.a

must publish the draft,

116.3.b

must consider any representations made to the Secretary of State about the
draft, and

116.3.c

may amend the draft accordingly,

but may not publish or amend the draft without the consent of the Attorney
General.

116.4

After complying with subsection  (3)  the Secretary of State must lay the code
before each House of Parliament.

116.5

After complying with subsection  (4)  the Secretary of State may bring the
code into force by regulations.

116.6

The Secretary of State may from time to time revise a code of practice brought
into force under this section.

116.7

Subsections  (3)  to  (6)  apply (with appropriate modifications) to a revised
code as they apply to the original code.

##### Restriction on multiple cautions

117

117.1

Regulations may prohibit the giving of a diversionary or community caution to
a person in respect of an offence where the person has already been given one
or more cautions.

117.2

A prohibition under subsection  (1)  may in particular be framed by reference
to—

117.2.a

the kinds of caution previously given to the person;

117.2.b

the number of times any kind of caution has been given to the person;

117.2.c

the period preceding the commission of the offence within which any kind of
caution has been given to the person;

117.2.d

the offence or description of offences in respect of which any kind of caution
has been given to the person.

117.3

For the purposes of this section “ caution ” means—

117.3.a

a diversionary or community caution;

117.3.b

a conditional caution under Part 3 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 given
before the coming into force of section 118;

117.3.c

any other caution given to the person before the coming into force of that
section in respect of an offence where—

117.3.c.i

the person admitted having committed the offence,

117.3.c.ii

the person was aged 18 or over when the caution was given, and

117.3.c.iii

the caution was given by a constable or other person authorised to give the
caution.

##### Abolition of other cautions and out-of-court disposals

118

118.1

No caution other than a diversionary or community caution may be given to a
person aged 18 or over who admits to having committed an offence.

118.2

In the Criminal Justice Act 2003, omit Part 3 (conditional cautions).

118.3

In the Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001, omit Chapter 1 of Part 1 (on-the-
spot penalties for disorderly behaviour).

118.4

Subsections (2) and (3) do not affect the continuing operation of the
provisions repealed by those subsections in relation to offences committed
before the day on which this section comes into force.

#### Supplementary

##### Consequential amendments relating to Part 6

119

Schedule 11 contains consequential amendments.

##### Regulations under Part 6

120

120.1

Regulations under this Part are to be made by the Secretary of State by
statutory instrument.

120.2

Regulations under this Part may make—

120.2.a

different provision for different purposes;

120.2.b

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional and transitory
provision and savings.

120.3

A statutory instrument containing the regulations specified in subsection  (4)
(with or without other provision) may not be made unless a draft of the
instrument has been laid before, and approved by resolution of, each House of
Parliament.

120.4

The regulations referred to in subsection  (3)  are—

120.4.a

regulations under section 98 (6)(b)  or  (c)  (excluded offences);

120.4.b

regulations under section 101 (8)  or 110 (8) ;

120.4.c

the first regulations under section 102 (3)  or 111 (3)  (maximum amount of
financial penalty);

120.4.d

any other regulations under section 102 (3)  or 111 (3)  which increase or
decrease the maximum amount of a financial penalty by more than is necessary
to reflect changes in the value of money;

120.4.e

regulations under section 116(5) (commencement of code);

120.4.f

regulations under section 117 (restriction on multiple cautions).

120.5

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this Part to which
subsection  (3)  does not apply is subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of either House of Parliament.

##### Interpretation of Part 6

121

In this Part—

“ the 1984 Act ” means the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984; “ authorised
person ” has the meaning given by section 98 (7) ; “ community remedy document
” means the community remedy document (as revised from time to time) published
under section 101 of the Anti-social Behaviour, Crime and Policing Act 2014
for the police area where the offence in question was committed; “ excluded
offence ” has the meaning given by section 98 (6) ; “ indictable-only offence
” means an offence which, if committed by an adult, is triable only on
indictment; “ investigating officer ” means— an officer of Revenue and Customs
appointed in accordance with section 2(1) of the Commissioners for Revenue and
Customs Act 2005, or a person designated as a policing support officer or a
policing support volunteer under section 38 of the Police Reform Act 2002; “
police detention ” has the same meaning as in the 1984 Act (see section 118(2)
of that Act); “ prosecution authority ” means— the Attorney General; the
Director of Public Prosecutions; the Director of the Serious Fraud Office; the
Secretary of State; a person prescribed in regulations; “ victim ”, in
relation to an offence, means the particular person who appears to have been
affected, or principally affected, by the offence.

###### Sentences of detention during Her Majesty’s pleasure: review of minimum term

128

128.1

Before the italic heading above section 28 of the Crime (Sentences) Act 1997
insert—

############ Sentence of detention during Her Majesty’s pleasure: review of minimum term

############# Sentence of detention during Her Majesty’s pleasure imposed on a person under 18: application for minimum term review

128.1.27A

128.1.27A.1

This section applies to a person who—

128.1.27A.1.a

is serving a DHMP sentence, and

128.1.27A.1.b

was under the age of 18 when sentenced;

and such a person is referred to in this section as a “ relevant young
offender ”.

128.1.27A.2

A relevant young offender may make an application for a minimum term review to
the Secretary of State after serving half of the minimum term.

128.1.27A.3

An “application for a minimum term review” is an application made by a
relevant young offender for a reduction in the minimum term.

128.1.27A.4

Where a relevant young offender has made an application for a minimum term
review under this section, the offender may only make a further such
application if—

128.1.27A.4.a

the period of 2 years beginning with the day on which the previous application
was determined has expired, and

128.1.27A.4.b

the offender is under the age of 18 on the day on which the further
application is made.

128.1.27A.5

Where the Secretary of State receives an application under this section, the
Secretary of State must—

128.1.27A.5.a

consider the application, and

128.1.27A.5.b

unless the Secretary of State forms the view that the application is frivolous
or vexatious, refer it to the High Court.

128.1.27A.6

Where the Secretary of State decides not to refer the application to the High
Court, the Secretary of State must give notice of that decision, and the
reasons for it, to the relevant young offender.

128.1.27A.7

If the relevant young offender makes representations or provides further
evidence in support of the application before the end of the period of 4 weeks
beginning with the day on which the notice under subsection  (6)  is given,
the Secretary of State must consider the representations or evidence and—

128.1.27A.7.a

if the Secretary of State is no longer of the view mentioned in subsection
(5)(b) , refer the application to the High Court, or

128.1.27A.7.b

give notice to the offender confirming the decision not to refer the
application.

128.1.27A.8

In this section—

“ DHMP sentence ” means a sentence of detention during Her Majesty’s pleasure
imposed (whether before or after this section comes into force) under a
provision listed in column 1 of the table in subsection  (9) ; “ minimum term
”, in relation to a person serving a DHMP sentence, means the part of the
sentence specified— in the minimum term order made in respect of the sentence,
or where one or more reduction orders have been made under section 27B in
respect of the sentence, in the most recent of those orders; “ minimum term
order ”, in relation to a DHMP sentence, means the order made under the
provision listed in column 2 of the table in subsection  (9)  that corresponds
to the entry in column 1 that relates to the sentence.

128.1.27A.9

The table is as follows—

Provision under which DHMP sentence imposed Provision under which minimum term
order made Section 259 of the Sentencing Code Section 322 of the Sentencing
Code Section 90 of the Powers of Criminal Courts (Sentencing) Act 2000 Section
82A of the Powers of Criminal Courts (Sentencing) Act 2000 or section 269 of
the Criminal Justice Act 2003 Section 218 of the Armed Forces Act 2006 Section
269 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 or section 322 of the Sentencing Code.

128.1.27A.10

For the purposes of subsection  (4) , an application for a minimum term review
is determined—

128.1.27A.10.a

when the court makes a reduction order or a decision confirming the minimum
term (see section 27B), or

128.1.27A.10.b

in a case where the application is not referred to the court, when the
Secretary of State gives the relevant young offender notice in relation to the
application under subsection  (6) .

128.1.27A.11

There is no right for any person who is serving a DHMP sentence to request a
review of the minimum term other than that conferred by this section.

############# Power of High Court to reduce minimum term

128.1.27B

128.1.27B.1

This section applies where the Secretary of State refers an application for a
minimum term review made by a relevant young offender under section 27A to the
High Court.

128.1.27B.2

The court may—

128.1.27B.2.a

make a reduction order in relation to relevant young offender, or

128.1.27B.2.b

confirm the minimum term in respect of the offender’s DHMP sentence,

and a decision of the court under this subsection is final.

128.1.27B.3

A reduction order is an order that the relevant young offender’s minimum term
is to be reduced to such part of the offender’s DHMP sentence as the court
considers appropriate and is specified in the reduction order.

128.1.27B.4

In deciding whether to make a reduction order, the court must, in particular,
take into account any evidence—

128.1.27B.4.a

that the relevant young offender’s rehabilitation has been exceptional;

128.1.27B.4.b

that the continued detention or imprisonment of the offender for the remainder
of the minimum term is likely to give rise to a serious risk to the welfare or
continued rehabilitation of the offender which cannot be eliminated or
mitigated to a significant degree.

128.1.27B.5

In this section “ DHMP sentence ”, “ minimum term ” and “ relevant young
offender ” have the same meaning as in section 27A.

128.2

In section 28 of that Act (duty to release certain life prisoners), in
subsection (1A), for the words from “the part of” to the end substitute—

128.2.a

the part of the sentence specified in the minimum term order, or

128.2.b

in a case where one or more reduction orders has been made in relation to the
prisoner (see section 27B), the part of the sentence specified in the most
recent of those orders.

128.3

A pre-commencement application—

128.3.a

is to be treated for the purposes of subsection  (4)  of section 27A of the
Crime (Sentences) Act 1997 as if it was made under that section if, at the
time the relevant young offender made the application, they had served at
least half of the minimum term;

128.3.b

if not determined before the day on which this section comes into force, is to
be dealt with in the manner in which it would have been dealt with immediately
before this section comes into force.

128.4

In this section—

“ minimum term ”, in relation to a relevant young offender, means the part of
the offender’s DHMP sentence specified in the minimum term order made in
respect of the sentence (and for these purposes “DHMP sentence” and “minimum
term order” have same meanings as in that section 27A); “ pre-commencement
application ” means an application by a relevant young offender for a review
of the minimum term that was made to the Secretary of State before the day on
which this section comes into force; “ relevant young offender ” has the same
meaning as in section 27A of the Crime (Sentences) Act 1997.

############ Release on licence of certain violent or sexual offenders

130.3.244ZA

130.3.244ZA.1

As soon as a fixed-term prisoner to whom this section applies has served the
requisite custodial period for the purposes of this section, it is the duty of
the Secretary of State to release the prisoner on licence under this section.

130.3.244ZA.2

This section applies to a prisoner who—

130.3.244ZA.2.a

is serving a fixed-term sentence within subsection  (4) ,  (5)  or  (6) ,

130.3.244ZA.2.b

is not a prisoner to whom section 244A, 246A or 247A applies, and

130.3.244ZA.2.c

has not been released on licence (provision for the release of persons

130.3.244ZA.3

130.3.244ZA.3.a

the prisoner’s case has been referred to the Board under section  244ZB , or

130.3.244ZA.3.b

a notice given to the prisoner under subsection  (4)  of that section is in

130.3.244ZA.4

130.3.244ZA.4.a

is a sentence of—

130.3.244ZA.4.a.i

130.3.244ZA.4.a.ii

detention under section 96 of the PCC(S)A 2000 or section 262 of the

130.3.244ZA.4.b

was imposed on or after 1 April 2020, and

130.3.244ZA.4.d

was imposed in respect of an offence—

130.3.244ZA.4.d.i

that is specified in Part 1 or 2 of Schedule 15, and

130.3.244ZA.4.d.ii

for which a sentence of life imprisonment could have been imposed (in the case
of an offender aged 21 or over) at the time when the actual sentence was
imposed.

130.3.244ZA.5

130.3.244ZA.5.a

130.3.244ZA.5.b

is for a term of at least 4 years but less than 7 years,

130.3.244ZA.5.c

Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 came into force, and

130.3.244ZA.5.d

was imposed in respect of an offence within subsection  (7) .

130.3.244ZA.6.c

was imposed on or after the day on which section 130 of the Police, Crime,

130.3.244ZA.6.d

was imposed in respect of an offence within subsection  (7) .

130.3.244ZA.7

paragraph 1 (manslaughter);

130.3.244ZA.7.a.ii

paragraph 6 (wounding with intent to cause grievous bodily harm);

130.3.244ZA.7.a.iv

in paragraph 1, 4 or 6;

130.3.244ZA.7.a.v

paragraph 65 (inchoate offences in relation to murder), or

130.3.244ZA.7.b

it is an offence—

130.3.244ZA.7.b.i

that is specified in Part 2 of that Schedule (sexual offences), and

130.3.244ZA.7.b.ii

for which a sentence of life imprisonment could have been imposed (in the case
of an offender aged 21 or over) at the time when the actual sentence was
imposed.

130.3.244ZA.8

130.3.244ZA.8.a

in relation to a prisoner serving one sentence, two-thirds of the prisoner’s

130.3.244ZA.8.b

sentences, the period determined under sections 263(2) and 264 (2B)  or  (2E)
.

###### Power to refer high-risk offenders to Parole Board in place of automatic release

132

132.1

The Criminal Justice Act 2003 is amended in accordance with subsections  (2)
to  (10) .

132.2

In section 243A (release of prisoners serving sentences of less than 12
months), after subsection (2) insert—

132.2.2A

Subsection (2) does not apply if—

132.2.2A.a

the prisoner’s case has been referred to the Board under section  244ZB , or

132.2.2A.b

a notice given to the prisoner under subsection  (4)  of that section is in
force.

132.3

In section 244 (general duty to release prisoners), after subsection (1)
insert—

132.3.1ZA

Subsection (1) does not apply if—

132.3.1ZA.a

the prisoner’s case has been referred to the Board under section  244ZB , or

132.3.1ZA.b

a notice given to the prisoner under subsection  (4)  of that section is in
force.

132.4

After section 244 insert—

############ Referral of high-risk offenders to Parole Board in place of automatic release

132.4.244ZB

132.4.244ZB.1

This section applies to a prisoner who—

132.4.244ZB.1.a

would (but for anything done under this section and ignoring any possibility
of release under section 246 or 248) be, or become, entitled to be released on
licence under section 243A(2), 244(1) or 244ZA(1), and

132.4.244ZB.1.b

is (or will be) aged 18 or over on the first day on which the prisoner would
be so entitled.

132.4.244ZB.2

For the purposes of this section, the Secretary of State is of the requisite
opinion if the Secretary of State believes on reasonable grounds that the
prisoner would, if released, pose a significant risk to members of the public
of serious harm occasioned by the commission of any of the following offences—

132.4.244ZB.2.a

murder;

132.4.244ZB.2.b

specified offences, within the meaning of section 306 of the Sentencing Code.

132.4.244ZB.3

If the Secretary of State is of the requisite opinion, the Secretary of State
may refer the prisoner’s case to the Board.

132.4.244ZB.4

Before referring the prisoner’s case to the Board, the Secretary of State must
notify the prisoner in writing of the Secretary of State’s intention to do so
(and the reference may be made only if the notice is in force).

132.4.244ZB.5

A notice given under subsection  (4)  must take effect before the prisoner
becomes entitled as mentioned in subsection  (1)(a) .

132.4.244ZB.6

A notice given under subsection  (4)  must explain—

132.4.244ZB.6.a

the effect of the notice (including its effect under section 243A (2A) , 244
(1ZA)  or  244ZA (3) ),

132.4.244ZB.6.b

why the Secretary of State is of the requisite opinion, and

132.4.244ZB.6.c

the prisoner’s right to make representations (see subsection  (12) ).

132.4.244ZB.7

A notice given under subsection  (4) —

132.4.244ZB.7.a

takes effect at whichever is the earlier of—

132.4.244ZB.7.a.i

the time when it is received by the prisoner, and

132.4.244ZB.7.a.ii

the time when it would ordinarily be received by the prisoner, and

132.4.244ZB.7.b

remains in force until—

132.4.244ZB.7.b.i

the Secretary of State refers the prisoner’s case to the Board under this
section, or

132.4.244ZB.7.b.ii

the notice is revoked.

132.4.244ZB.8

The Secretary of State—

132.4.244ZB.8.a

may revoke a notice given under subsection  (4) , and

132.4.244ZB.8.b

must do so if the Secretary of State is no longer of the requisite opinion.

132.4.244ZB.9

If a notice given under subsection  (4)  is in force and the prisoner would
but for the notice have become entitled as mentioned in subsection  (1)(a) —

132.4.244ZB.9.a

the prisoner may apply to the High Court on the ground that the prisoner’s
release has been delayed by the notice for longer than is reasonably necessary
in order for the Secretary of State to complete the referral of the prisoner’s
case to the Board, and

132.4.244ZB.9.b

the High Court, if satisfied that that ground is made out, must by order
revoke the notice.

132.4.244ZB.10

At any time before the Board disposes of a reference under this section, the
Secretary of State—

132.4.244ZB.10.a

may rescind the reference, and

132.4.244ZB.10.b

must do so if the Secretary of State is no longer of the requisite opinion.

132.4.244ZB.11

If the reference is rescinded, the prisoner is no longer to be treated as one
whose case has been referred to the Board under this section (but this does
not have the effect of reviving the notice under subsection  (4) ).

132.4.244ZB.12

The prisoner may make representations to the Secretary of State about the
referral, or proposed referral, of the prisoner’s case at any time after being
notified under subsection  (4)  and before the Board disposes of any ensuing
reference under this section.

But the Secretary of State is not required to delay the referral of the
prisoner’s case in order to give an opportunity for such representations to be
made.

############ Proceedings following reference under section 

132.4.244ZC

132.4.244ZC.1

This section applies to a prisoner whose case has been referred to the Parole
Board under section  244ZB .

132.4.244ZC.2

If, in disposing of that reference or any subsequent reference of the
prisoner’s case to the Board under this subsection, the Board does not direct
the prisoner’s release, it is the duty of the Secretary of State to refer the
prisoner’s case to the Board again no later than the first anniversary of the
disposal.

132.4.244ZC.3

It is the duty of the Secretary of State to release the prisoner on licence as
soon as—

132.4.244ZC.3.a

the prisoner has served the requisite custodial period, and

132.4.244ZC.3.b

the Board has directed the release of the prisoner under this section.

132.4.244ZC.4

The Board must not give a direction under subsection  (3)  in disposing of the
reference under section  244ZB  unless the Board is satisfied that it is no
longer necessary for the protection of the public that the prisoner should be
confined.

132.4.244ZC.5

The Board must not subsequently give a direction under subsection  (3)
unless—

132.4.244ZC.5.a

the Secretary of State has referred the prisoner’s case to the Board under
subsection  (2) , and

132.4.244ZC.5.b

the Board is satisfied that it is no longer necessary for the protection of
the public that the prisoner should be confined.

132.4.244ZC.6

For the purposes of this section, the “ requisite custodial period ” means the
period ending with the day on which the prisoner would have become entitled as
mentioned in section  244ZB (1)(a) .

132.5

132.5.fa

the prisoner’s case has been referred to the Board under section  244ZB ,

132.5.fb

###### Power to make provision for reconsideration and setting aside of Parole Board decisions

133

In section 239 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (the Parole Board), after
subsection (5) insert—

133.5A

Rules under subsection (5) may, in particular, make provision—

133.5A.a

requiring or permitting the Board to make provisional decisions;

133.5A.b

about the circumstances—

133.5A.b.i

in which the Board must or may reconsider such decisions;

133.5A.b.ii

in which such decisions become final;

133.5A.c

conferring power on the Board to set aside a decision or direction that is
within subsection (5B),

and any such provision may relate to cases referred to the Board under this
Chapter or under Chapter 2 of Part 2 of the 1997 Act.

133.5B

The following are within this subsection—

133.5B.a

a direction given by the Board for, or a decision made by it not to direct,
the release of a prisoner which the Board determines it would not have given
or made but for an error of law or fact, or

133.5B.b

a direction given by the Board for the release of a prisoner which the Board
determines it would not have given if—

133.5B.b.i

information that was not available to the Board when the direction was given
had been so available, or

133.5B.b.ii

a change in circumstances relating to the prisoner that occurred after the
direction was given had occurred before it was given.

133.5C

Provision made by virtue of subsection  (5A)(c) —

133.5C.a

may not confer power on the Board to set aside a direction for the release of
a prisoner at any time when the prisoner has already been released pursuant to
that direction, but

133.5C.b

may make provision for the suspension of any requirement under this Chapter or
under Chapter 2 of Part 2 of the 1997 Act for the Secretary of State to give
effect to a direction of the Board to release a prisoner, pending
consideration by the Board as to whether to set it aside.

134.2.5A.b

the Board, or

###### Increase in driving disqualification periods under certain existing orders: England and Wales

141

141.1

Subsection  (2)  applies where—

141.1.a

a driving disqualification order was made in accordance with an extended
disqualification provision,

141.1.b

the custodial sentence as a result of which the extended disqualification
provision applied was imposed before the day on which section 140 came into
force,

141.1.c

section 244ZA (inserted by section 130) or 247A of the Criminal Justice Act
2003 applies to the offender in respect of the sentence (the offender, in
particular, not having been released in respect of the sentence), and

141.1.d

the appropriate extension period for the purposes of the order would have been
longer had the sentence been imposed on the day on which section 140 came into
force.

141.2

The order has effect, on and after the day on which section 140 comes into
force, as if the period of disqualification included an appropriate extension
period of such length as it would have included had the custodial sentence
been imposed on that day.

141.3

For the purposes of this section, the “extended disqualification provisions”
are—

141.3.a

section 35A of the Road Traffic Offenders Act 1988,

141.3.b

section 147A of the Powers of Criminal Courts (Sentencing) Act 2000, and

141.3.c

section 166 of the Sentencing Code,

and “appropriate extension period”, “driving disqualification order” and
“custodial sentence” are to be read in accordance with the extended
disqualification provision concerned.

141.4

In the application of this section before section 130 comes into force, the
reference in subsection  (1)(c)  to section 244ZA of the Criminal Justice Act
2003 is to be read as a reference to section 244 of that Act as modified by
the Release of Prisoners (Alteration of Relevant Proportion of Sentence) Order
2020 ( S.I. 2020/158 ).

141.5

In the application of this section in relation to a custodial sentence imposed
under a provision repealed by the Sentencing Act 2020, the references to the
sentence in subsections  (1)(d)  and  (2)  are to be read as referring to an
equivalent sentence imposed under the corresponding provision of the
Sentencing Code.

###### Increase in driving disqualification periods under certain existing orders: Scotland

143

143.1

Subsection  (2)  applies where—

143.1.a

############## Life prisoners also serving fixed-term sentence

144.1.b.33A

144.1.b.33A.1

This section applies where a life prisoner is also serving one or more
sentences by virtue of which the fixed-term provisions apply to the offender.

144.1.b.33A.2

Nothing in this Chapter requires the Secretary of State to release the
prisoner unless the Secretary of State is also required by the fixed-term
provisions to release the prisoner.

144.1.b.33A.3

Nothing in this Chapter requires the Secretary of State to refer the
prisoner’s case to the Parole Board unless the Secretary of State is also
required by the fixed-term provisions to—

144.1.b.33A.3.a

refer the prisoner’s case to the Board, or

144.1.b.33A.3.b

release the prisoner.

144.1.b.33A.4

Subsection  (3)  does not apply to a reference by the Secretary of State under
section 31A(3).

144.1.b.33A.5

The fact that the prisoner is serving a life sentence is to be ignored in
determining, for the purposes of subsections  (2)  and  (3) , what the fixed-
term provisions require.

144.1.b.33A.6

In this section “ the fixed-term provisions ” means Chapter 6 of Part 12 of
the Criminal Justice Act 2003.

;

###### Application of release provisions to repatriated prisoners

145

145.1

In the Schedule to the Repatriation of Prisoners Act 1984, in paragraph 2
(application of early release provisions) as it applies in relation to
prisoners repatriated to England and Wales—

145.1.a

omit sub-paragraphs (3) and (3A);

145.1.b

for sub-paragraphs (3B) to (3F) (inserted by the Counter-Terrorism and
Sentencing Act 2021) substitute—

145.1.b.3ZA

The Secretary of State may specify in the warrant that the prisoner is to be
treated for the purposes of the enactments relating to release on licence as
if the sentence to be served by the prisoner was imposed in respect of—

145.1.b.3ZA.a

a particular offence under the law of England and Wales,

145.1.b.3ZA.b

such an offence carried out in a certain manner or in certain circumstances,
or

145.1.b.3ZA.c

such an offence in relation to which certain findings were made by the court
before which the prisoner was convicted or sentenced for the offence;

and if that is done those enactments have effect accordingly.

145.1.b.3ZB

An offence may be specified under sub-paragraph  (3ZA)  only if it corresponds
to the offence in respect of which the prisoner is required to be detained in
the country or territory from which the prisoner is transferred (“the overseas
offence”).

145.1.b.3ZC

A specification under sub-paragraph  (3ZA)(b)  may be made only if, in the
opinion of the Secretary of State, findings made by the court before which the
prisoner was convicted or sentenced for the overseas offence show that the
overseas offence was committed in the manner or circumstances to be specified
(or in a corresponding manner or corresponding circumstances).

145.1.b.3ZD

A finding may be specified under sub-paragraph  (3ZA)(c)  only if, in the
opinion of the Secretary of State, findings made by the court before which the
prisoner was convicted or sentenced for the overseas offence show that the
finding to be specified could properly have been made by a court in England
and Wales dealing with the prisoner.

145.1.b.3ZE

Sub-paragraph  (3ZA)  does not result in the enactments relating to release on
licence applying in a way in which they could not apply in relation to a
sentence imposed in respect of the offence specified under that sub-paragraph—

145.1.b.3ZE.a

that was committed at the same time as the overseas offence was committed, or

145.1.b.3ZE.b

in respect of which a conviction was made, or sentence passed, at the same
time as occurred in respect of the overseas offence.

145.1.b.3ZF

The Secretary of State may amend a warrant (whether issued before or after
sub-paragraph  (3ZA)  comes into force and whether or not the transfer it
authorised has taken place) so as to specify the matters there referred to.

;

145.1.c

in sub-paragraph (4), in the definition of “the enactments relating to release
on licence”, for “and Chapter 6 of Part 12 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003”
substitute  “, Chapter 6 of Part 12 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 and
section 28 of the Offender Management Act 2007” .

145.2

The repeal by subsection  (1)(b)  of sub-paragraphs (3B) to (3F) of the
amended paragraph does not affect the continued operation of the enactments
relating to release on licence (within the meaning of that paragraph as
amended by subsection  (1) ) in relation to a warrant issued or amended in
accordance with those sub-paragraphs before their repeal.

145.3

In Schedule 26 to the Criminal Justice and Immigration Act 2008, the following
provisions (which contain superseded amendments of or in connection with the
paragraph amended by subsection  (1) ) are repealed—

145.3.a

paragraph 19(4) and (5), and

145.3.b

paragraph 33(2) and (3).

the sentence imposed) is to be disregarded.

;

146.d

in subsection (4A) (inserted by the Counter-Terrorism and Sentencing Act
2021), omit paragraph (b) (but not the final “or”);

146.e

in subsection (4B) (also so inserted), omit paragraph (a);

146.f

after subsection (4B) insert—

146.f.4C

A sentence in respect of a service offence is to be treated for the purposes
of this section as if it were a sentence in respect of the corresponding
offence.

146.f.4D

In subsection  (4C) —

146.f.4D.a

“ service offence ” means an offence under—

146.f.4D.a.i

section 42 of the Armed Forces Act 2006,

146.f.4D.a.ii

section 70 of the Army Act 1955 or the Air Force Act 1955, or

146.f.4D.a.iii

section 42 of the Naval Discipline Act 1957;

146.f.4D.b

“ corresponding offence ” means—

146.f.4D.b.i

in relation to an offence under section 42 of the Armed Forces Act 2006, the
corresponding offence under the law of England and Wales within the meaning of
that section;

146.f.4D.b.ii

in relation to an offence under section 70 of the Army Act 1955 or the Air
Force Act 1955, the corresponding civil offence within the meaning of that
Act;

146.f.4D.b.iii

in relation to an offence under section 42 of the Naval Discipline Act 1957,
the civil offence within the meaning of that section.

146.f.4E

Section 48 of the Armed Forces Act 2006 (supplementary provisions relating to
ancillary service offences) applies for the purposes of subsection  (4D)(b)(i)
above as it applies for the purposes of the provisions of that Act referred to
in subsection (3)(b) of that section.

###### Power for responsible officer to vary curfew requirements etc

151

151.1

The Sentencing Code is amended as follows.

151.2

In Part 5 of Schedule 9 (community orders and suspended sentence orders:
curfew requirements), after paragraph 10 insert—

############ Power of responsible officer to vary curfew requirement

151.2.10A

151.2.10A.1

This paragraph applies where—

151.2.10A.1.a

a relevant order is in force,

151.2.10A.1.b

the order is in respect of an offence of which the offender was convicted on
or after the day on which section 151 of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and
Courts Act 2022 came into force,

151.2.10A.1.c

the order includes a curfew requirement imposed under paragraph 9, and

151.2.10A.1.d

the responsible officer considers that the variation condition is met.

151.2.10A.2

The variation condition is met if, having regard to a change in the offender’s
circumstances since the relevant order was made, it is appropriate to—

151.2.10A.2.a

vary the start time of any of the curfew periods;

151.2.10A.2.b

vary the relevant place in relation to any of those periods.

151.2.10A.3

The responsible officer may, with the consent of the offender, give the
offender notice (a “ variation notice ”) specifying—

151.2.10A.3.a

the new start time of such of the curfew periods as are specified in the
notice;

151.2.10A.3.b

the new relevant place for such of the curfew periods as are so specified.

151.2.10A.4

The effect of a variation notice is to vary the relevant order as specified in
the notice, with effect from the date so specified.

151.2.10A.5

A variation notice may specify different variations of the start time, or of
the relevant place, for different days.

151.2.10A.6

Before giving a variation notice containing provision pursuant to sub-
paragraph  (3)(b) , the responsible officer must obtain and consider
information about each place proposed to be specified in the notice.

151.2.10A.7

That information must include information as to the attitude of persons likely
to be affected by the offender’s enforced presence there.

151.2.10A.8

A variation notice must not—

151.2.10A.8.a

vary the length of any of the offender’s curfew periods;

151.2.10A.8.b

in a case where the relevant order includes a residence requirement under
paragraph 13, vary the relevant place in a way that is inconsistent with that
requirement;

151.2.10A.8.c

make any variation prohibited by sub-paragraph  (9) .

151.2.10A.9

A variation is prohibited by this sub-paragraph if—

151.2.10A.9.a

the relevant order concerned includes an electronic compliance monitoring
requirement imposed under paragraph 10(3) (a “monitoring requirement”), and

151.2.10A.9.b

the responsible officer considers that, if the court had made the relevant
order imposing the curfew requirement as varied by the variation, the court—

151.2.10A.9.b.i

would not have imposed the monitoring requirement, or

151.2.10A.9.b.ii

would have imposed a different monitoring requirement.

151.2.10A.10

The responsible officer must give the appropriate court—

151.2.10A.10.a

a copy of a variation notice given under this paragraph, and

151.2.10A.10.b

evidence of the offender’s consent to the notice.

151.2.10A.11

In this paragraph—

151.2.10A.11.a

“appropriate court”—

151.2.10A.11.a.i

in relation to a community order, has the same meaning as in Schedule 10 (see
paragraph 1 of that Schedule);

151.2.10A.11.a.ii

in relation to a suspended sentence order, has the same meaning as in Schedule
16 (see paragraph 1 of that Schedule);

151.2.10A.11.b

“ curfew periods ”, in relation to a relevant order, means the periods
specified in the order under paragraph 9(2)(a);

151.2.10A.11.c

“ relevant place ”, in relation to a curfew period, means the place specified
under paragraph 9(2)(b) at which the offender is required to remain for that
period;

151.2.10A.11.d

“ start time ”, in relation to a curfew period, means the time at which the
period is required to start pursuant to the relevant order.

151.3

In paragraph 16 of Schedule 10 (amendment of community order because of change
of residence), after sub-paragraph (2) insert—

151.3.3

If the permission is given by the responsible officer—

151.3.3.a

the officer must give notice to the appropriate court of the permission, and

151.3.3.b

the court must amend the order as set out in sub-paragraph (2).

151.4

After paragraph 17 of that Schedule insert—

############ Amendment because of variation of curfew requirement by responsible officer

151.4.17A

151.4.17A.1

This paragraph applies where at any time the responsible officer gives—

151.4.17A.1.a

a copy of a variation notice in relation to a community order, and

151.4.17A.1.b

evidence of the offender’s consent to the notice,

to the appropriate court under paragraph 10A of Schedule 9.

151.4.17A.2

The appropriate court must amend the order to reflect the effect of the
variation notice.

151.5

In paragraph 23 of Schedule 16 (amendment of suspended sentence order) because
of change of residence), after sub-paragraph (2) insert—

151.5.3

If the permission is given by the responsible officer—

151.5.3.a

the officer must give notice to the appropriate court of the permission, and

151.5.3.b

the court must amend the suspended sentence order as set out in sub-paragraph
(2).

151.6

After paragraph 24 of that Schedule insert—

############ Amendment because of variation of curfew requirement by responsible officer

151.6.24A

151.6.24A.1

This paragraph applies where at any time the responsible officer gives—

151.6.24A.1.a

a copy of a variation notice in relation to a suspended sentence order, and

151.6.24A.1.b

evidence of the offender’s consent to the notice,

to the appropriate court under paragraph 10A of Schedule 9.

151.6.24A.2

The appropriate court must amend the order to reflect the effect of the
variation notice.
