##### Unpaid work requirements

###### Duty to consult on unpaid work requirements

155

After section 10 of the Offender Management Act 2007 insert—

########## Duty to consult on unpaid work requirements

155.10A

155.10A.1

Each provider of probation services must, in each calendar year, consult the
prescribed persons about the work to be performed by persons who—

155.10A.1.a

are subject to unpaid work requirements, and

155.10A.1.b

are supervised by that provider.

155.10A.2

In this section “ prescribed person ” means a person, or a person of a
description, prescribed by regulations made by the Secretary of State.

155.10A.3

In this section “ unpaid work requirement ” means an unpaid work requirement
as defined by—

155.10A.3.a

paragraph 10(1) of Schedule 6 to the Sentencing Code (youth rehabilitation
orders),

155.10A.3.b

paragraph 1(1) of Schedule 9 to the Sentencing Code (community orders and
suspended sentence orders), or

155.10A.3.c

paragraph 3A(1) of Schedule A1 to the Children Act 1989 (enforcement orders).

155.10A.4

For the purposes of this section a person is supervised by a provider of
probation services if an officer of that provider has functions relating to
the person’s compliance with an unpaid work requirement.

#### Assaults on those providing a public service etc

##### Assaults on those providing a public service etc

156

In the Sentencing Act 2020, after section 68 insert—

######### Assaults on those providing a public service etc

156.68A

156.68A.1

This section applies where—

156.68A.1.a

a court is considering the seriousness of an offence listed in subsection (3),
and

156.68A.1.b

the offence is not aggravated under section 67(2).

156.68A.2

If the offence was committed against a person providing a public service,
performing a public duty or providing services to the public, the court—

156.68A.2.a

must treat that fact as an aggravating factor, and

156.68A.2.b

must state in open court that the offence is so aggravated.

156.68A.3

The offences referred to in subsection (1) are—

156.68A.3.a

an offence of common assault or battery, except where section 1 of the
Assaults on Emergency Workers (Offences) Act 2018 applies;

156.68A.3.b

an offence under any of the following provisions of the Offences against the
Person Act 1861—

156.68A.3.b.i

section 16 (threats to kill);

156.68A.3.b.ii

section 18 (wounding with intent to cause grievous bodily harm);

156.68A.3.b.iii

section 20 (malicious wounding);

156.68A.3.b.iv

section 47 (assault occasioning actual bodily harm);

156.68A.3.c

an inchoate offence in relation to any of the preceding offences.

156.68A.4

In this section—

156.68A.4.a

a reference to providing services to the public includes a reference to
providing goods or facilities to the public;

156.68A.4.b

a reference to the public includes a reference to a section of the public.

156.68A.5

Nothing in this section prevents a court from treating the fact that an
offence was committed against a person providing a public service, performing
a public duty or providing services to the public as an aggravating factor in
relation to offences not listed in subsection (3).

156.68A.6

This section has effect in relation to a person who is convicted of the
offence on or after the date on which section 156 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 comes into force.

##### Consecutive detention and training order and sentence of detention: effect of early release decision

159

159.1

In section 237 of the Sentencing Code (making of detention and training order
where offender subject to other order or sentence of detention), omit
subsection (5).

159.2

In section 241 of that Code (period of detention and training), after
subsection (5) insert—

########### Consecutive detention and training order and sentence of detention

159.2.5A

Where the offender is also subject to a sentence of any of the following kinds
that is to take effect, by virtue of an order to which subsection (7) applies,
when the offender would otherwise be released for supervision—

159.2.5A.a

a sentence of detention under section 250 or 252A,

159.2.5A.b

a sentence of detention under section 209 or 224A of the Armed Forces Act
2006, or

159.2.5A.c

an extended sentence of detention under section 254 (including one passed as a
result of section 221A of the Armed Forces Act 2006),

subsection (4) is to be read as if, instead of conferring a power to release
the offender, it conferred a power to determine that the Secretary of State
would, but for the sentence concerned, have released the offender.

159.3

In section 264AA of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (consecutive terms:
detention and training orders), after subsection (1) insert—

159.3.1A

In a case where the detention and training order was made on or after the day
on which section 159 of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 came
into force, section 246(1)(a) is to be read as if, instead of conferring a
power to release the offender, it conferred a power to determine that the
Secretary of State would, but for the detention and training order, have
directed the offender’s release under that section.

#### Youth rehabilitation orders

##### Youth rehabilitation orders

161

161.1

Schedule 17 contains amendments to provisions of the Criminal Justice and
Immigration Act 2008 and the Sentencing Act 2020 which relate to youth
rehabilitation orders.

161.2

In the following provisions of this section, “ the relevant YRO provisions ”
means—

161.2.a

Parts  2  and  3  of Schedule 17, and

161.2.b

subsection  (1)  of this section so far as relating to those Parts.

161.3

Regulations under section 208(1) which bring any of the relevant YRO
provisions into force only for a specified purpose or in relation to a
specified area may—

161.3.a

provide for that provision to be in force for that purpose or in relation to
that area for a specified period, and

161.3.b

make transitional or saving provision in connection with that provision
ceasing to be in force at the end of the specified period.

161.4

Regulations containing provision by virtue of subsection  (3)(a)  may be
amended by subsequent regulations under section 208(1) so as to continue any
of the relevant YRO provisions in force for the specified purpose or in
relation to the specified area for a further specified period.

161.5

Accordingly, the reference to section 419(1) of the Sentencing Act 2020, as
applied by section 206, to the coming into force of an amendment is to be read
as including a reference to the continuing in force of an amendment by reason
of subsection  (4) .

161.6

In subsections  (3)  and  (4) , “ specified ” means specified in regulations
under section 208(1).

161.7

Subsection  (8)  applies if—

161.7.a

the Secretary of State has made regulations under section 208(1) which make
provision permitted by subsection (3), and

161.7.b

the Secretary of State subsequently makes regulations under section 208(1)
which bring any of the relevant YRO provisions into force without making
provision permitted by subsection (3).

161.8

The regulations mentioned in subsection  (7) (b)  may—

161.8.a

provide that those provisions are to come into force with the amendments
specified in the regulations;

161.8.b

make amendments to the Criminal Justice and Immigration Act 2008 or the
Sentencing Act 2020 in consequence of the amendments made by paragraph (a).

161.9

A statutory instrument containing regulations under section 208(1) which make
provision permitted by subsection  (8)  (whether alone or with other
provision) may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid
before and approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

#### Abolition of reparation orders

##### Abolition of reparation orders

162

In section 110(1) of the Sentencing Code (availability of reparation order),
before paragraph (a) insert—

162.za

the offender is convicted of the offence before the day on which section 162
of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 comes into force,

.

### Secure children's homes and secure 16 to 19 Academies

#### Temporary release from secure children’s homes

163

163.1

This section applies to a person who is detained in a secure children’s home
in pursuance of—

163.1.a

a sentence of detention,

163.1.b

a detention and training order or a further detention order,

163.1.c

a detention order under Schedule 5A to the Policing and Crime Act 2009 (breach
of gang injunction), or

163.1.d

a detention order under Schedule 2 to the Anti-social Behaviour, Crime and
Policing Act 2014 (breach of anti-social behaviour injunction).

163.2

The Secretary of State or the manager of the home may temporarily release a
person to whom this section applies.

163.3

A temporary release under this section may be granted subject to conditions.

163.4

A person who is temporarily released under this section may be recalled at any
time by the Secretary of State or the manager of the home (irrespective of
which of those granted the release).

163.5

A manager of a secure children’s home must have regard to any guidance issued
by the Secretary of State about the use of powers of temporary release under
this section.

163.6

In this section—

      “ detention and training order ” has the same meaning as in the
Sentencing Code (see section 233 of that Code) and includes an order made
under section 100 of the Powers of Criminal Courts (Sentencing) Act 2000 or
section 211 of the Armed Forces Act 2006;           “ further detention order
” has the same meaning as in Schedule 12 to the Sentencing Code (see paragraph
1 of that Schedule) and includes an order made under section 104(3) of the
Powers of Criminal Courts (Sentencing) Act 2000 and a further detention order
made by virtue of section 213 of the Armed Forces Act 2006;
“manager”—         in relation to a secure children’s home in England, means
the person who is registered under Part 2 of the Care Standards Act 2000 as
the manager of the home or, in a case where no such person is registered, the
person who is registered under that Part as the person who carries on the
home;           in relation to a secure children’s home in Wales, means the
person who is designated as the responsible individual in respect of the home
for the purposes of Part 1 of the Regulation and Inspection of Social Care
(Wales) Act 2016;                 “secure children’s home”—         in
relation to England, means a children’s home, within the meaning of section 1
of the Care Standards Act 2000, which provides accommodation for the purposes
of restricting liberty;           in relation to Wales, means residential
premises which provide a secure accommodation service within the meaning of
Part 1 of the  Regulation and Inspection of Social Care (Wales) Act 2016 (anaw
2) .

163.7

In section 49 of the Prison Act 1952 (persons unlawfully at large), after
subsection (4) insert—

163.7.4ZA

For the purposes of this section a person who, after being temporarily
released in pursuance of section 163 of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and
Courts Act 2022 (temporary release from a secure children’s home), is at large
at any time during the period for which they are liable to be detained
pursuant to their sentence shall be deemed to be unlawfully at large if the
period for which they were temporarily released has expired or if they have
been recalled under that section.

A 16 to 19 Academy may provide secure accommodation for its students, but only

164.1.5

“ Secure accommodation ” means accommodation that is provided for the purpose

164.1.6

The Secretary of State may grant approval under subsection (4) subject to
conditions.

164.1.7

A 16 to 19 Academy which provides secure accommodation for its students is to
be known as a secure 16 to 19 Academy.

164.2

164.2.5

The setting up, establishment and running of a secure 16 to 19 Academy is to
be treated as a charitable purpose that falls within the description in
section 3(1)(b) of the Charities Act 2011 (advancement of education) for the
purposes of—

164.2.5.a

this section,

164.2.5.b

the Charities Act 2011, and

164.2.5.c

any other enactment that applies (in whatever way) the definition of
“charitable purpose” in section 2 of that Act.

164.2.6

But subsection (5) is to be disregarded in determining, in accordance with
section 3(1)(m) of the Charities Act 2011, whether a purpose may be regarded
as analogous to, or within the spirit of, a purpose falling within paragraph
(b) of section 3(1) of that Act.

164.3

In section 248(1) of the Sentencing Code (meaning of “ youth detention
accommodation ”), after paragraph (b) insert—

164.3.ba

a secure 16 to 19 Academy,

.

164.4.a.i

after “means” insert

—



;

      a secure 16 to 19 Academy (see section 1B(4) to (7) of the Academies Act
2010);

;

omit paragraph (1A).

### Management of offenders

#### Serious violence reduction orders

##### Serious violence reduction orders

165

165.1

In Part 11 of the Sentencing Code (behaviour orders) after Chapter 1 insert—

########### Serious violence reduction orders

############ Power to make serious violence reduction order

165.1.342A

165.1.342A.1

This section applies where—

165.1.342A.1.a

a person aged 18 or over (“the offender”) is convicted of an offence which was
committed on or after the first appointed day, and

165.1.342A.1.b

the prosecution makes an application to the court for a serious violence
reduction order to be made in respect of the offender.

165.1.342A.2

Subject to subsection (6), the court may make a serious violence reduction
order in respect of the offender if—

165.1.342A.2.a

the condition in subsection (3) or (4) is met, and

165.1.342A.2.b

the condition in subsection (5) is met.

165.1.342A.3

The condition in this subsection is that the court is satisfied on the balance
of probabilities that—

165.1.342A.3.a

a bladed article or offensive weapon was used by the offender in the
commission of the offence, or

165.1.342A.3.b

the offender had a bladed article or offensive weapon with them when the
offence was committed.

165.1.342A.4

The condition in this subsection is that the court is satisfied on the balance
of probabilities that—

165.1.342A.4.a

a bladed article or offensive weapon was used by another person in the
commission of the offence and the offender knew or ought to have known that
this would be the case, or

165.1.342A.4.b

another person who committed the offence had a bladed article or offensive
weapon with them when the offence was committed and the offender knew or ought
to have known that this would be the case.

165.1.342A.5

The condition in this subsection is that the court considers it necessary to
make a serious violence reduction order in respect of the offender to—

165.1.342A.5.a

protect the public in England and Wales from the risk of harm involving a
bladed article or offensive weapon,

165.1.342A.5.b

protect any particular members of the public in England and Wales (including
the offender) from such risk, or

165.1.342A.5.c

prevent the offender from committing an offence involving a bladed article or
offensive weapon.

165.1.342A.6

The court may make a serious violence reduction order in respect of the
offender only if it—

165.1.342A.6.a

does so in addition to dealing with the offender for the offence, and

165.1.342A.6.b

does not make an order for absolute discharge under section 79 in respect of
the offence.

165.1.342A.7

For the purpose of deciding whether to make a serious violence reduction order
the court may consider evidence led by the prosecution and evidence led by the
offender.

165.1.342A.8

It does not matter whether the evidence would have been admissible in the
proceedings in which the offender was convicted.

165.1.342A.9

The court may adjourn any proceedings on an application for a serious violence
reduction order even after sentencing the offender.

165.1.342A.10

If the offender does not appear for any adjourned proceedings the court may—

165.1.342A.10.a

further adjourn the proceedings,

165.1.342A.10.b

issue a warrant for the offender’s arrest, or

165.1.342A.10.c

hear the proceedings in the offender’s absence.

165.1.342A.11

The court may not act under subsection (10)(b) unless it is satisfied that the
offender has had adequate notice of the time and place of the adjourned
proceedings.

165.1.342A.12

The court may not act under subsection (10)(c) unless it is satisfied that the
offender—

165.1.342A.12.a

has had adequate notice of the time and place of the adjourned proceedings,
and

165.1.342A.12.b

has been informed that if the offender does not appear for those proceedings
the court may hear the proceedings in the offender’s absence.

165.1.342A.13

On making a serious violence reduction order the court must in ordinary
language explain to the offender—

165.1.342A.13.a

the effects of the order, and

165.1.342A.13.b

the powers that a constable has in respect of the offender under section  342E
while the order is in effect.

165.1.342A.14

In subsection (1)(a) “ the first appointed day ” means the first day appointed
by regulations under section 208(1) of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and
Courts Act 2022 for the coming into force to any extent of section 165 of that
Act.

165.1.342A.15

In subsection (4) the references to the offence include references to any
offence arising out of the same facts as the offence.

############ Meaning of “serious violence reduction order”

165.1.342B

165.1.342B.1

In this Chapter, “ serious violence reduction order ” means an order made in
respect of an offender that imposes on the offender—

165.1.342B.1.a

the requirements specified in subsections (2) and (4), and

165.1.342B.1.b

the requirements and prohibitions, if any, specified in regulations made by
the Secretary of State for the purposes of this section.

165.1.342B.2

The offender must be required to notify the information in subsection (3) to
the police within the period of 3 days beginning with the day on which the
order takes effect.

165.1.342B.3

That information is—

165.1.342B.3.a

the offender’s name on the day that the notification is given and, where the
offender uses one or more other names on that day, each of those names,

165.1.342B.3.b

the offender’s home address on that day, and

165.1.342B.3.c

the address of any other premises at which, on that day, the offender
regularly resides or stays.

165.1.342B.4

The offender must be required to notify the information mentioned in
subsection (5) to the police within the period of 3 days beginning with the
day on which the offender—

165.1.342B.4.a

uses a name which has not been previously notified to the police in accordance
with the order,

165.1.342B.4.b

changes their home address, or

165.1.342B.4.c

decides to live for a period of one month or more at any premises the address
of which has not been previously notified to the police in accordance with the
order.

165.1.342B.5

That information is—

165.1.342B.5.a

in a case within subsection (4)(a), the name which has not previously been
notified,

165.1.342B.5.b

in a case within subsection (4)(b), the new home address, and

165.1.342B.5.c

in a case within subsection (4)(c), the address of the premises at which the
offender has decided to live.

165.1.342B.6

A serious violence reduction order must provide that the offender gives a
notification of the kind mentioned in subsection (2) or (4) by—

165.1.342B.6.a

attending at a police station in a police area in which the offender lives,
and

165.1.342B.6.b

giving an oral notification to a police officer, or to any person authorised
for the purpose by the officer in charge of the station.

165.1.342B.7

The Secretary of State may make regulations under subsection (1)(b) only if—

165.1.342B.7.a

the Secretary of State has laid a report before Parliament under section
166(3) of the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (report to be laid
after piloting of serious violence reduction orders), and

165.1.342B.7.b

the Secretary of State considers that it is appropriate to make the
regulations for the purpose of assisting constables to exercise the powers
conferred by section  342E .

165.1.342B.8

Regulations under subsection (1)(b) are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

165.1.342B.9

In this section, “ home address ”, in relation to the offender, means—

165.1.342B.9.a

the address of the offender’s sole or main residence, or

165.1.342B.9.b

if the offender has no such residence, the address or location of a place
where the offender can regularly be found and, if there is more than one such
place, such one of those places as the offender may select.

############ Serious violence reduction orders: additional requirements etc

165.1.342C

165.1.342C.1

A serious violence reduction order may impose on the offender any requirement
or prohibition specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State for the
purposes of this section if the condition in subsection (2) is met.

165.1.342C.2

The condition in this subsection is that the court considers it appropriate
for the order to impose the requirement or prohibition on the offender for the
purpose of assisting constables to exercise the powers conferred by section
342E in respect of the offender.

165.1.342C.3

Regulations under this section may be made only after the Secretary of State
has laid a report before Parliament under section 166(3) of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (report to be laid after piloting of serious
violence reduction orders).

165.1.342C.4

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative resolution
procedure.

############ Duration of serious violence reduction orders

165.1.342D

165.1.342D.1

A serious violence reduction order takes effect on the day it is made, subject
to subsections (3) and (4).

165.1.342D.2

A serious violence reduction order must specify the period for which it has
effect, which must be a fixed period of not less than 6 months and not more
than 2 years.

165.1.342D.3

Subsection (4) applies in relation to a serious violence reduction order if—

165.1.342D.3.a

the offender has been remanded in or committed to custody by an order of a
court, or

165.1.342D.3.b

a custodial sentence has been imposed on the offender or the offender is
serving or otherwise subject to a such a sentence.

165.1.342D.4

The order may provide that it does not take effect until the offender is
released from custody or ceases to be subject to a custodial sentence.

165.1.342D.5

Where a court makes a serious violence reduction order and the offender is
already subject to such an order, the earlier order ceases to have effect.

############ Serious violence reduction orders: powers of constables

165.1.342E

165.1.342E.1

This section applies where a serious violence reduction order is in effect.

165.1.342E.2

A constable may search the offender for the purpose of ascertaining whether
the offender has a bladed article or an offensive weapon with them.

165.1.342E.3

A constable may detain the offender for the purpose of carrying out the
search.

165.1.342E.4

A constable may seize anything that the constable finds in the course of the
search if the constable reasonably suspects it to be a bladed article or an
offensive weapon.

165.1.342E.5

The powers in this section may be exercised only while the offender is in a
public place.

165.1.342E.6

A constable may use reasonable force, if necessary, for the purpose of
exercising a power conferred by this section.

165.1.342E.7

The powers conferred on a constable by this section are additional to powers
which the constable has at common law or by virtue of any other enactment and
does not affect those powers.

############ Retention and disposal of things seized under section 

165.1.342F

165.1.342F.1

Any thing seized by a constable under section  342E  may be retained in
accordance with regulations made by the Secretary of State under this section.

165.1.342F.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision—

165.1.342F.2.a

regulating the retention and safekeeping of things seized by a constable under
section  342E , and

165.1.342F.2.b

regulating the disposal and destruction of such things in such circumstances
as the regulations may prescribed.

165.1.342F.3

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative resolution
procedure.

############ Offences relating to a serious violence reduction order

165.1.342G

165.1.342G.1

Where a serious violence reduction order is in effect, the offender commits an
offence if the offender—

165.1.342G.1.a

fails without reasonable excuse to do anything the offender is required to do
by the order,

165.1.342G.1.b

without reasonable excuse does anything the offender is prohibited from doing
by the order,

165.1.342G.1.c

notifies to the police, in purported compliance with the order, any
information which the offender knows to be false,

165.1.342G.1.d

tells a constable that they are not subject to a serious violence reduction
order, or

165.1.342G.1.e

intentionally obstructs a constable in the exercise of any power conferred by
section  342E .

165.1.342G.2

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

165.1.342G.2.a

on summary conviction, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12 months, or
a fine, or both;

165.1.342G.2.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years,
or a fine, or both.

165.1.342G.3

In relation to an offence committed before the coming into force of paragraph
24(2) of Schedule 22 (maximum sentence that may be imposed on summary
conviction of offence triable either way) the reference in subsection (2)(a)
to 12 months is to be read as a reference to 6 months.

165.1.342G.4

If a person is convicted of an offence under this section, an order for
conditional discharge under section 80 is not available to the court by or
before which the person is convicted.

############ Variation, renewal or discharge of serious violence reduction order

165.1.342H

165.1.342H.1

A person within subsection (2) may apply to the appropriate court for an order
varying, renewing or discharging a serious violence reduction order.

165.1.342H.2

Those persons are—

165.1.342H.2.a

the offender;

165.1.342H.2.b

the chief officer of police for the police area in which the offender lives;

165.1.342H.2.c

the chief officer of police for the police area in which the offender
committed the offence on the basis of which the order was made;

165.1.342H.2.d

a chief officer of police who believes that the offender is in, or is
intending to come to, the chief officer’s police area;

165.1.342H.2.e

where the offence on the basis of which the order was made is an offence to
which this paragraph applies, the chief constable of the British Transport
Police Force.

165.1.342H.3

Paragraph (e) of subsection (2) applies to an offence which—

165.1.342H.3.a

was committed at, or in relation to, a place within section 31(1)(a) to (f) of
the Railways and Transport Safety Act 2003 (jurisdiction of British Transport
Police Force), or

165.1.342H.3.b

otherwise related to a railway within the meaning given by section 67 of the
Transport and Works Act 1992 or a tramway within the meaning given by that
section.

165.1.342H.4

An application under this section must be made in accordance with rules of
court.

165.1.342H.5

Before making a decision on an application under this section, the court must
hear—

165.1.342H.5.a

the person making the application, and

165.1.342H.5.b

any other person within subsection (2) who wishes to be heard.

165.1.342H.6

Subject to subsection (7), on an application under this section the court may
make such order varying, renewing or discharging the serious violence
reduction order as it thinks appropriate.

165.1.342H.7

The court may renew a serious violence reduction order, or vary such an order
so as to lengthen its duration, only if it considers that to do so is
necessary—

165.1.342H.7.a

to protect the public in England and Wales from the risk of harm involving a
bladed article or offensive weapon,

165.1.342H.7.b

to protect any particular members of the public in England and Wales
(including the offender) from such risk, or

165.1.342H.7.c

to prevent the offender from committing an offence involving a bladed article
or offensive weapon.

165.1.342H.8

On making an order under this section varying or renewing a serious violence
reduction order, the court must in ordinary language explain to the offender—

165.1.342H.8.a

the effects of the serious violence reduction order (as varied or renewed),
and

165.1.342H.8.b

the powers that a constable has in respect of the offender under section 342E
while the serious violence reduction order is in effect.

165.1.342H.9

In this section the “ appropriate court ” means—

165.1.342H.9.a

where the Crown Court or the Court of Appeal made the serious violence
reduction order, the Crown Court;

165.1.342H.9.b

where a magistrates’ court made the serious violence reduction order and the
application is made by the offender or the chief constable of the British
Transport Police Force—

165.1.342H.9.b.i

that magistrates’ court, or

165.1.342H.9.b.ii

a magistrates’ court for the area in which the offender lives;

165.1.342H.9.c

where a magistrates’ court made the serious violence reduction order and the
application is made by a chief officer of police—

165.1.342H.9.c.i

that magistrates’ court,

165.1.342H.9.c.ii

a magistrates’ court for the area in which the offender lives, or

165.1.342H.9.c.iii

a magistrates’ court acting for a local justice area that includes any part of
the chief officer’s police area.

############ Appeal against serious violence reduction order etc

165.1.342I

165.1.342I.1

An appeal against the making of a serious violence reduction order may be
brought by the offender as if the order were a sentence passed on the offender
for an offence.

165.1.342I.2

Where an application is made under section  342H  for an order varying,
renewing or discharging a serious violence reduction order—

165.1.342I.2.a

the person who made the application may appeal against a refusal to make an
order under that section;

165.1.342I.2.b

the offender may appeal against the making of an order under that section
which was made on the application of a chief officer of police or the chief
constable of the British Transport Police Force;

165.1.342I.2.c

a chief officer of police within subsection (2) of that section may appeal
against the making of an order under that section which was made on the
application of the offender;

165.1.342I.2.d

where the offence on the basis of which the serious violence reduction order
was made is an offence to which this paragraph applies, the chief constable of
the British Transport Police Force may appeal against the making of an order
under that section which was made on the application of the offender.

165.1.342I.3

Paragraph (d) of subsection (2) applies to an offence which—

165.1.342I.3.a

was committed at, or in relation to, a place within section 31(1)(a) to (f) of
the Railways and Transport Safety Act 2003 (jurisdiction of British Transport
Police Force), or

165.1.342I.3.b

otherwise related to a railway within the meaning given by section 67 of the
Transport and Works Act 1992 or a tramway within the meaning given by that
section.

165.1.342I.4

An appeal under subsection (2)—

165.1.342I.4.a

is to be made to the Court of Appeal if the application under section  342H
was made to the Crown Court;

165.1.342I.4.b

is to be made to the Crown Court in any other case.

165.1.342I.5

On an appeal under subsection (2) to the Crown Court, the court may make—

165.1.342I.5.a

such orders as may be necessary to give effect to its determination of the
appeal, and

165.1.342I.5.b

such incidental and consequential orders as appear to it to be appropriate.

############ Guidance

165.1.342J

165.1.342J.1

The Secretary of State may issue guidance to—

165.1.342J.1.a

constables,

165.1.342J.1.b

chief officers of police, and

165.1.342J.1.c

the chief constable of the British Transport Police Force,

in relation to serious violence reduction orders.

165.1.342J.2

The guidance may in particular include—

165.1.342J.2.a

guidance about the exercise by constables, chief officers of police and the
chief constable of the British Transport Police Force of their functions under
this Chapter,

165.1.342J.2.b

guidance about identifying offenders in respect of whom it may be appropriate
for applications for serious violence reduction orders to be made, and

165.1.342J.2.c

guidance about providing assistance to prosecutors in connection with
applications for serious violence reduction orders.

165.1.342J.3

The Secretary of State may revise any guidance issued under this section.

165.1.342J.4

The Secretary of State must arrange for any guidance issued under this section
to be published.

165.1.342J.5

A constable, chief officer of police or the chief constable of the British
Transport Police Force must have regard to any guidance issued under this
section.

############ Guidance: Parliamentary procedure

165.1.342K

165.1.342K.1

Before issuing guidance under section 342J, the Secretary of State must lay a
draft of the guidance before Parliament.

165.1.342K.2

If, within the 40-day period, either House of Parliament resolves not to
approve the draft guidance, the guidance may not be issued.

165.1.342K.3

If no such resolution is made within that period, the Secretary of State may
issue the guidance.

165.1.342K.4

In this section “ the 40-day period ”, in relation to draft guidance, means
the period of 40 days beginning with the day on which the draft is laid before
Parliament (or, if it is not laid before each House on the same day, the later
of the days on which it is laid).

165.1.342K.5

In calculating the 40-day period, no account is to be taken of any period
during which—

165.1.342K.5.a

Parliament is dissolved or prorogued, or

165.1.342K.5.b

both Houses are adjourned for more than 4 days.

############ Serious violence reduction orders: interpretation

165.1.342L

In this Chapter—

“ bladed article ” means an article to which section 139 of the Criminal
Justice Act 1988 applies; “ custodial sentence ” includes a pre-Code custodial
sentence (see section 222(4)); “ harm ” includes physical and psychological
harm; “ offensive weapon ” has the same meaning as in section 1(4) of the
Prevention of Crime Act 1953; “ public place ” means— any place to which the
public or any section of the public has access, on payment or otherwise, as of
right or by virtue of express or implied permission, or any other place to
which people have ready access but which is not a dwelling; “ the offender ”,
in relation to a serious violence reduction order, means the offender in
respect of whom the order or the application for the order has been made.

165.2

In section 80(3) of the Sentencing Code (list of circumstances where an order
for conditional discharge is not available) after paragraph (d) insert—

165.2.da

section  342G (4) (offences relating to a serious violence reduction order);

.

165.3

In section 3(2) of the Prosecution of Offences Act 1985 (functions of the
Director of Public Prosecutions) after paragraph (fg) insert—

165.3.fh

to have the conduct of applications for orders under section  342A  of the
Sentencing Code (serious violence reduction orders);

.

##### Serious violence reduction orders: piloting

166

166.1

The Secretary of State may exercise the power in section 208(1) so as to bring
section 165 into force—

166.1.a

for all purposes, and

166.1.b

in relation to the whole of England and Wales,

only if the conditions in subsections (2) and (3) are met.

166.2

The condition in this subsection is that regulations under section 208(1) have
brought section 165 into force only—

166.2.a

for one or more specified purposes, or

166.2.b

in relation to one or more specified areas.

166.3

The condition in this subsection is that the Secretary of State has laid
before Parliament a report on the operation of Chapter 1A of Part 11 of the
Sentencing Code (inserted by section 165)—

166.3.a

for one or more of those purposes, or

166.3.b

in relation to one or more of those areas.

166.4

A report under subsection (3) must in particular include—

166.4.a

information about the number of offenders in respect of whom serious violence
reduction orders have been made;

166.4.b

information about the offences that were the basis for applications as a
result of which serious violence reduction orders were made;

166.4.c

information about the exercise by constables of the powers in section 342E of
the Sentencing Code (serious violence reduction orders: powers of constables);

166.4.d

an assessment of the impact of the operation of Chapter 1A of Part 11 of the
Sentencing Code on people with protected characteristics (within the meaning
of the Equality Act 2010);

166.4.e

an initial assessment of the impact of serious violence reduction orders on
the reoffending rates of offenders in respect of whom such orders have been
made;

166.4.f

an assessment of the impact on offenders of being subject to a serious
violence reduction order;

166.4.g

information about the number of offences committed under section 342G of the
Sentencing Code (offences relating to a serious violence reduction order) and
the number of suspected offences under that section that have been
investigated.

166.5

Regulations under section 208(1) which bring section 165 into force only for a
specified purpose or in relation to a specified area may—

166.5.a

provide for section 165 to be in force for that purpose or in relation to that
area for a specified period;

166.5.b

make transitional or saving provision in connection with section 165 ceasing
to be in force at the end of the specified period.

166.6

Regulations containing provision by virtue of subsection (5)(a) may be amended
by subsequent regulations under section 208(1) so as to continue section 165
in force—

166.6.a

for the specified purpose, or

166.6.b

in relation to the specified area,

for a further specified period.

166.7

Accordingly, the reference in section 419(1) of the Sentencing Act 2020, as
applied by section 206, to the coming into force of an amendment is to be read
as including a reference to the continuing in force of an amendment by reason
of subsection  (6) .

166.8

In this section—

“ serious violence reduction order ” has the same meaning as in Chapter 1A of
Part 11 of the Sentencing Code (see section 342B of the Sentencing Code); “
specified ” means specified in regulations under section 208(1).

#### Knife crime prevention orders

##### Knife crime prevention order on conviction: adjournment of proceedings

167

167.1

In section 19 of the Offensive Weapons Act 2019 (knife crime prevention orders
made on conviction), after subsection (9) insert—

167.1.9A

The court may adjourn any proceedings on an application for a knife crime
prevention order even after sentencing the defendant.

167.1.9B

If the defendant does not appear for any adjourned proceedings the court may—

167.1.9B.a

further adjourn the proceedings,

167.1.9B.b

issue a warrant for the defendant’s arrest, or

167.1.9B.c

hear the proceedings in the defendant’s absence.

167.1.9C

The court may not act under subsection (9B)(b) unless it is satisfied that the
defendant has had adequate notice of the time and place of the adjourned
proceedings.

167.1.9D

The court may not act under subsection (9B)(c) unless it is satisfied that the
defendant—

167.1.9D.a

has had adequate notice of the time and place of the adjourned proceedings,
and

167.1.9D.b

has been informed that if the defendant does not appear for those proceedings
the court may hear the proceedings in the defendant’s absence.

167.2

Regulations under section 208(1) which bring subsection  (1)  into force only
for a specified purpose or in relation to a specified area may—

167.2.a

provide for that provision to be in force for that purpose or in relation to
that area for a specified period;

167.2.b

make transitional or saving provision in relation to that provision ceasing to
be in force at the end of the specified period.

167.3

Regulations containing provision by virtue of subsection  (2)(a)  may be
amended by subsequent regulations under section 208(1) so as to continue
subsection  (1)  in force for the specified purpose or in relation to the
specified area for a further specified period.

167.4

In this section “ specified ” means specified in regulations under section
208(1).

###### Offences outside the United Kingdom: notification requirements

169

169.1

The Sexual Offences Act 2003 is amended as follows.

169.2

After section 96 insert—

############ Offences outside the United Kingdom: notification requirements

############# Offences outside the United Kingdom: notification requirements

169.2.96ZA

169.2.96ZA.1

Where this section applies to a person (“ P ”), P is subject to the
notification requirements of this Part for the notification period set out in
section 82.

This is subject to sections 96ZB (young offenders: parental notices) and 96ZC
(modifications of notification requirements).

169.2.96ZA.2

This section applies to P if P has been given a notice under subsection (3)
and that notice has not been cancelled.

169.2.96ZA.3

A constable may give a notice to P if—

169.2.96ZA.3.a

the conditions in subsections (6), (7) and (8) are met in respect of P, and

169.2.96ZA.3.b

an officer of at least the rank of inspector has authorised the giving of the
notice to P.

169.2.96ZA.4

A notice given to P under subsection (3) must be given to P in person and must
contain details of—

169.2.96ZA.4.a

the notifications that P is required to give under this Part,

169.2.96ZA.4.b

when those notifications must be given, and

169.2.96ZA.4.c

where those notifications may be given.

169.2.96ZA.5

A notice given under subsection (3) may be cancelled by a constable giving
notice in writing to P in person but such a cancellation must be authorised by
an officer of at least the rank of inspector.

169.2.96ZA.6

The first condition is that under the law in force in a country outside the
United Kingdom—

169.2.96ZA.6.a

P has been convicted of a relevant offence (whether or not P has been punished
for it),

169.2.96ZA.6.b

a court exercising jurisdiction under that law has made in respect of a
relevant offence a finding equivalent to a finding that P is not guilty by
reason of insanity,

169.2.96ZA.6.c

such a court has made in respect of a relevant offence a finding equivalent to
a finding that P is under a disability and did the act charged against P in
respect of the offence, or

169.2.96ZA.6.d

P has been cautioned in respect of a relevant offence.

169.2.96ZA.7

The second condition is that—

169.2.96ZA.7.a

the first condition is met because of a conviction, finding or caution which
occurred on or after 1 September 1997,

169.2.96ZA.7.b

the first condition is met because of a conviction or finding which occurred
before that date, but P was dealt with in respect of the offence or finding on
or after that date, or has yet to be dealt with in respect of it, or

169.2.96ZA.7.c

the first condition is met because of a conviction or finding which occurred
before that date, but on that date P was, in respect of the offence or
finding, subject under the law in force in the country concerned to detention,
supervision or any other disposal equivalent to any of those mentioned in
section 81(3) (read with sections 81(6) and 131).

169.2.96ZA.8

The third condition is that the period set out in section 82 (as it would have
effect as modified by section 96ZC(2) and (3) if this section applied to P) in
respect of the relevant offence has not expired.

169.2.96ZA.9

In this section and section 96ZC “ relevant offence ” means an act which—

169.2.96ZA.9.a

constituted an offence under the law in force in the country concerned, and

169.2.96ZA.9.b

would have constituted an offence listed in Schedule 3 (other than at
paragraph 60) if it had been done in any part of the United Kingdom.

169.2.96ZA.10

For the purposes of subsection (9)(a), an act punishable under the law in
force in a country outside the United Kingdom constitutes an offence under
that law however it is described in that law.

############# Young offenders: parental notices

169.2.96ZB

169.2.96ZB.1

Where the person (“ P ”) given a notice under section 96ZA is under 18 a
constable may also give a notice (a “parental notice”) to a person (“the
parent”) with parental responsibility for P.

169.2.96ZB.2

Subsections (3)(b) to (5) of section 96ZA apply to the giving of a parental
notice as if references to P were references to the parent.

169.2.96ZB.3

If a parental notice has been given to the parent and has not been cancelled
or ceased to have effect—

169.2.96ZB.3.a

the obligations that would (apart from this subsection) be imposed by virtue
of section 96ZA on P are to be treated instead as obligations on the parent,
and

169.2.96ZB.3.b

the parent must ensure that P attends with them at the police station when a
notification under this Part is being given.

169.2.96ZB.4

The parental notice ceases to have effect when P reaches the age of 18.

169.2.96ZB.5

If a parental notice is to be given, section 96ZA(4)(a) has effect in relation
to the notice given to P as if the reference to the notifications that P is
required to give under this Part were a reference to—

169.2.96ZB.5.a

the notifications that the parent is required to give under this Part, and

169.2.96ZB.5.b

the notifications (if any) that P is required to give under this Part once the
parental notice ceases to have effect.

############# Modifications of notification requirements

169.2.96ZC

169.2.96ZC.1

The application of this Part to a person (“ P ”) to whom section 96ZA applies
in respect of a conviction, finding or caution is subject to the modifications
set out in this section.

169.2.96ZC.2

References to the “relevant date”—

169.2.96ZC.2.a

in a case where P is within section 96ZA(6)(a), are to the date of the
conviction,

169.2.96ZC.2.b

in a case where P is within section 96ZA(6)(b) or (c), are to the date of the
finding, and

169.2.96ZC.2.c

in a case where P is within section 96ZA(6)(d), are to the date of the
caution.

169.2.96ZC.3

In section 82—

169.2.96ZC.3.a

references, except in the Table, to a person (or relevant offender) within any
provision of section 80 are to be read as references to P;

169.2.96ZC.3.b

the reference in the Table to section 80(1)(d) is to be read as a reference to
section 96ZA(6)(d);

169.2.96ZC.3.c

references to an order of any description are to be read as references to any
corresponding disposal made in relation to P in respect of an offence or
finding by reference to which a notice has been given to P under section 96ZA;

169.2.96ZC.3.d

the reference to offences listed in Schedule 3 is to be read as a reference to
relevant offences (see section 96ZA(9)).

169.2.96ZC.4

Section 83 has effect as if after subsection (1) there were inserted—

169.2.96ZC.4.1A

In the case of a relevant offender who is subject to the notification
requirements of this Part by virtue of a notice being given to the relevant
offender under section 96ZA, the reference in subsection (1) to the period of
3 days beginning with the relevant date (or if later the commencement of this
Part) is to be read as a reference to the period of 3 days beginning with the
day on which the notice was given to the relevant offender.

169.2.96ZC.5

Section 83(4) has effect as if—

169.2.96ZC.5.a

for the words “Where a notification order is made” there were substituted
“Where a relevant offender is subject to the notification requirements of this
Part by virtue of a notice given under section 96ZA” , and

169.2.96ZC.5.b

in paragraph (a) for the words “the order was made” there were substituted
“the notice was given to the relevant offender” .

############# Appeal against the issue of a notice under section 96ZA or 96ZB

169.2.96ZD

169.2.96ZD.1

A person (“ P ”) may appeal to a magistrates’ court against the decision to
give them a notice under section 96ZA.

169.2.96ZD.2

The grounds for bringing an appeal under subsection (1) include—

169.2.96ZD.2.a

that one or more of the conditions for the giving of the notice were not met
in respect of P at the time the notice was given;

169.2.96ZD.2.b

that the conviction, finding or caution by reason of which P was given the
notice falls within subsection (3).

169.2.96ZD.3

A conviction, finding or caution falls within this subsection if—

169.2.96ZD.3.a

any investigations or proceedings leading to it were conducted in a way which
contravened any of the Convention rights (within the meaning of section 1 of
the Human Rights Act 1998) which P would have had if those investigations or
proceedings had taken place in the United Kingdom, and

169.2.96ZD.3.b

that contravention was such that the conviction, finding or caution cannot be
safely relied on for the purposes of meeting the condition in section 96ZA(6).

169.2.96ZD.4

A person (“the parent”) may appeal to a magistrates’ court against the
decision to give them a parental notice under section 96ZB.

169.2.96ZD.5

The grounds for bringing an appeal under subsection (4) include—

169.2.96ZD.5.a

that one or more of the conditions for the giving of a notice under section
96ZA to the person (“ P ”) for whom the parent has parental responsibility
were not met in respect of P at the time the notice under section 96ZA was
given;

169.2.96ZD.5.b

that the conviction, finding or caution by reason of which P was given a
notice under section 96ZA falls within subsection (3);

169.2.96ZD.5.c

that one or more of the requirements for giving the parent a parental notice
under section 96ZB were not met at the time the parental notice was given.

169.2.96ZD.6

On an appeal under subsection (1) or (4) a magistrates’ court may cancel or
confirm the notice which is the subject of the appeal.

169.3

In section 91(1)(a) (offences relating to notification) for “or 89(2)(b)”
substitute  “, 89(2)(b) or 96ZB(3)(b)” .

169.4

In section 91A(3) (review of indefinite notification requirements) for
paragraph (c) substitute—

169.4.c

a notice given under section 96ZA.

169.5

Omit sections 97 to 103 (notification orders) and section 103G(6) and (7)
(notification order made on application for sexual harm prevention order or
interim sexual harm prevention order).

169.6

In section 133(1) (general interpretation), in the definition of “relevant
date” for “98, 100” substitute  “, 96ZC” .

169.7

Subsection (5) does not affect—

169.7.a

the validity or effect of any order made under section 97 or 100 of the Sexual
Offences Act 2003 before the coming into force of this section or the
application of Part 2 of that Act to any person in respect of whom such an
order was so made;

169.7.b

in respect of an application made under section 97(1) or section 100(2) of
that Act before the coming into force of this section—

169.7.b.i

the determination of such an application, or

169.7.b.ii

the validity and effect of any order made on such an application or the
application of Part 2 of that Act to any person in respect of whom such an
order was so made.

169.8

The amendments made by subsections (4) and (6) do not apply in respect of any
order to which, or any person to whom, subsection (7) applies.

172

172.1

The Secretary of State may—

172.1.a

prepare a list of countries and territories outside the United Kingdom in
which the Secretary of State considers children are at a high risk of sexual
abuse or sexual exploitation from United Kingdom nationals or United Kingdom
residents, or

172.1.b

direct a relevant person to prepare a list of countries and territories
outside the United Kingdom in which the relevant person considers children are
at a high risk of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation from United Kingdom
nationals or United Kingdom residents.

172.2

If a list is prepared by the Secretary of State, the Secretary of State must
lay the list before Parliament.

172.3

If a list is prepared by a relevant person—

172.3.a

the relevant person must submit the list to the Secretary of State, and

172.3.b

the Secretary of State must lay the list before Parliament.

172.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after a list has been laid before
Parliament, the person who prepared the list must publish it.

172.5

A list published under subsection (4) has effect for the purposes of—

172.5.a

section 346 of the Sentencing Code (exercise of power to make sexual harm
prevention order),

172.5.b

section 350 of the Sentencing Code (sexual harm prevention orders: variations,
renewals and discharges),

172.5.c

section 103A of the Sexual Offences Act 2003 (sexual harm prevention orders:
applications and grounds),

172.5.d

section 103E of that Act (sexual harm prevention orders: variations, renewals
and discharges),

172.5.e

section 103F of that Act (interim sexual harm prevention orders),

172.5.f

section 122A of that Act (sexual risk orders: applications, grounds and
effect),

172.5.g

section 122D of that Act (sexual risk orders: variations, renewals and
discharges),

172.5.h

section 122E of that Act (interim sexual risk orders),

172.5.i

section 136ZG of that Act (variation of sexual harm prevention order made in
Scotland by court in England and Wales),

172.5.j

section 136ZH of that Act (variation of sexual offences prevention order or
foreign travel order by court in England and Wales), and

172.5.k

section 136ZI of that Act (variation of sexual risk order made in Scotland by
court in England and Wales).

172.6

If a list has been published, the person who prepared it must keep it under
review and may, from time to time, prepare a revised list (but see subsections
(7) and (8)).

172.7

If the function under subsection (6) is for the time being exercisable by the
Secretary of State, the Secretary of State may direct a relevant person to
exercise that function.

172.8

If the function under subsection (6) is for the time being exercisable by a
relevant person, the Secretary of State may direct that the function is to be
exercisable by another relevant person or by the Secretary of State.

172.9

A list published under this section may at any time be withdrawn by the
Secretary of State.

172.10

Subsections (2) to (9) apply to a revised list as they apply to a list
prepared under subsection (1).

172.11

In this section—

“ child ” means a person under 18; “ relevant person ” means a person whose
statutory functions relate to— the prevention or detection of crime, or other
law enforcement purposes; “ United Kingdom national ” means— a British
citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National (Overseas)
or a British Overseas citizen, a person who under the British Nationality Act
1981 is a British subject, or a British protected person within the meaning of
that Act; “ United Kingdom resident ” means an individual who is resident in
the United Kingdom.

###### Requirement for courts and certain persons to have regard to the list of countries

173

173.1

In section 346 of the Sentencing Code (exercise of power to make sexual harm
prevention order)—

173.1.a

the existing text becomes subsection (1), and

173.1.b

after that subsection insert—

173.1.b.2

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (list of countries where children are at a high
risk of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation) and has not been withdrawn, the
court must have regard to the list in considering—

173.1.b.2.a

whether a sexual harm prevention order is necessary for the purpose of
protecting children generally, or any particular children, from sexual harm
from the offender outside the United Kingdom, and

173.1.b.2.b

in particular, whether a prohibition on foreign travel (see section 348) is
necessary for that purpose.

173.2

In section 350 of the Sentencing Code (sexual harm prevention orders:
variations, renewals and discharges)—

173.2.a

after subsection (3) insert—

173.2.a.3A

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (list of countries where children are at high
risk of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation) and has not been withdrawn, a
person mentioned in subsection (2)(b) or (c) must have regard to the list in
considering—

173.2.a.3A.a

whether to apply for an order varying or renewing a sexual harm prevention
order for the purpose of protecting children generally, or any particular
children, from sexual harm from the offender outside the United Kingdom, and

173.2.a.3A.b

in particular, whether to apply for an order imposing, varying or renewing a
prohibition on foreign travel for that purpose.

, and

173.2.b

after subsection (6A) (inserted by section 175) insert—

173.2.b.6B

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 and has not been withdrawn, the court must have
regard to the list in considering—

173.2.b.6B.a

whether an order varying or renewing the sexual harm prevention order is
necessary for the purpose of protecting children generally, or any particular
children, from sexual harm from the offender outside the United Kingdom, and

173.2.b.6B.b

in particular, whether an order imposing, varying or renewing a prohibition on
foreign travel is necessary for that purpose.

The Sexual Offences Act 2003 is amended as follows.

173.4

In section 103A (sexual harm prevention orders: applications and grounds)—

173.4.a

after subsection (3) insert—

173.4.a.3A

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (list of countries where children are at high
risk of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation) and has not been withdrawn, the
court must have regard to the list in considering—

173.4.a.3A.a

whether a sexual harm prevention order is necessary for the purpose of
protecting children generally, or any particular children, from sexual harm
from the defendant outside the United Kingdom, and

173.4.a.3A.b

in particular, whether a prohibition on foreign travel (see section 103D) is
necessary for that purpose.

, and

173.4.b

after subsection (4A) (inserted by section 171) insert—

173.4.b.4B

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 and has not been withdrawn, a person mentioned
in subsection (4A) must have regard to the list in considering—

173.4.b.4B.a

whether a person has since the appropriate date acted in such a way as to give
reasonable cause to believe that it is necessary for a sexual harm prevention
order to be made for the purpose of protecting children generally, or any
particular children, from sexual harm from that person outside the United
Kingdom, and

173.4.b.4B.b

whether to apply for a prohibition on foreign travel (see section 103D) to be
included in any such order for that purpose.

,

173.5.b.5B.a

whether any order varying or renewing the sexual harm prevention order is

173.5.b.5B.b

in particular, whether an order imposing, varying or renewing a prohibition on

, and

173.5.c

###### Standard of proof

174

174.1

The Sexual Offences Act 2003 is amended as follows.

174.2

In section 103A(3) (sexual harm prevention orders: applications and grounds)—

174.2.a

omit “and” at the end of paragraph (a), and

174.2.b

for paragraph (b) substitute—

174.2.b.b

the court is satisfied on the balance of probabilities that since the
appropriate date the defendant has acted in one or more of the ways alleged by
the person making the application, and

174.2.b.c

the court is satisfied that the defendant having acted in such a way makes it
necessary to make a sexual harm prevention order, for the purpose of—

174.2.b.c.i

protecting the public or any particular members of the public from sexual harm
from the defendant, or

174.2.b.c.ii

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United
Kingdom.

174.3

In section 122A (sexual risk orders: applications, grounds and effect), for
subsection (6) substitute—

174.3.6

On an application under subsection (1), the court may make a sexual risk order
if—

174.3.6.a

the court is satisfied on the balance of probabilities that the defendant has,
whether before or after the commencement of this Part, done one or more of the
acts of a sexual nature alleged by the person making the application, and

174.3.6.b

the court is satisfied that as a result of the defendant acting in such a way
it is necessary to make such an order for the purpose of—

174.3.6.b.i

protecting the public or any particular members of the public from harm from
the defendant, or

174.3.6.b.ii

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

###### Sexual harm prevention orders: power to impose positive requirements

175

175.1

The Sentencing Code is amended in accordance with subsections (2) to (6).

175.2

In section 343 (sexual harm prevention order)—

175.2.a

for subsection (1) substitute—

175.2.a.1

In this Code a “ sexual harm prevention order ” means an order made under this
Chapter in respect of an offender.

175.2.a.1A

A sexual harm prevention order may—

175.2.a.1A.a

prohibit the offender from doing anything described in the order;

175.2.a.1A.b

require the offender to do anything described in the order.

,

175.b

in subsection (2), after “prohibitions” insert  “or requirements” , and

175.c

after subsection (2) insert—

175.c.3

The prohibitions or requirements which are imposed on the offender by a sexual
harm prevention order must, so far as practicable, be such as to avoid—

175.c.3.a

any conflict with the offender’s religious beliefs,

175.c.3.b

any interference with the times, if any, at which the offender normally works
or attends any educational establishment, and

175.c.3.c

any conflict with any other court order or injunction to which the offender
may be subject (but see section 349).

175.3

In section 347 (sexual harm prevention order: matters to be specified)—

175.3.a

in subsection (1)(a), after “prohibitions” insert  “and requirements” ,

175.3.b

in subsection (1)(b)—

175.3.b.i

after “each prohibition” insert  “or requirement” , and

175.3.b.ii

for ““prohibition period”” substitute  ““specified period”” ,

175.3.c

in subsection (2)—

175.3.c.i

in the words before paragraph (a), for “prohibition period” substitute
“specified period” , and

175.3.c.ii

in paragraph (b), after “prohibition” insert  “or requirement” , and

175.3.d

in subsection (3), after “prohibitions”, in both places it occurs, insert  “or
requirements” .

175.4

After section 347 insert—

############ Sexual harm prevention orders: requirements included in order etc.

175.4.347A

175.4.347A.1

A sexual harm prevention order that imposes a requirement to do something on
an offender must specify a person who is to be responsible for supervising
compliance with the requirement.

The person may be an individual or an organisation.

175.4.347A.2

Before including such a requirement in a sexual harm prevention order, the
court must receive evidence about its suitability and enforceability from—

175.4.347A.2.a

the individual to be specified under subsection (1), if an individual is to be
specified;

175.4.347A.2.b

an individual representing the organisation to be specified under subsection
(1), if an organisation is to be specified.

175.4.347A.3

Subsections (1) and (2) do not apply in relation to electronic monitoring
requirements (see instead section 348A(5) and (6)).

175.4.347A.4

It is the duty of a person specified under subsection (1)—

175.4.347A.4.a

to make any necessary arrangements in connection with the requirements for
which the person has responsibility (“the relevant requirements”);

175.4.347A.4.b

to promote the offender’s compliance with the relevant requirements;

175.4.347A.4.c

if the person considers that—

175.4.347A.4.c.i

the offender has complied with all the relevant requirements, or

175.4.347A.4.c.ii

the offender has failed to comply with a relevant requirement,

to inform the appropriate chief officer of police.

175.4.347A.5

In subsection (4)(c) the “appropriate chief officer of police means—

175.4.347A.5.a

the chief officer of police for the police area in which it appears to the
person specified under subsection (1) that the offender lives, or

175.4.347A.5.b

if it appears to that person that the offender lives in more than one police
area, whichever of the chief officers of police of those areas the person
thinks it is most appropriate to inform.

175.4.347A.6

An offender subject to a requirement imposed by a sexual harm prevention order
must—

175.4.347A.6.a

keep in touch with the person specified under subsection (1) in relation to
that requirement, in accordance with any instructions given by that person
from time to time, and

175.4.347A.6.b

notify that person of any change of the offender’s home address.

These obligations have effect as requirements of the order.

175.4.347A.7

In this section “ home address ”, in relation to an offender, means—

175.4.347A.7.a

the address of the offender’s sole or main residence in the United Kingdom, or

175.4.347A.7.b

where the offender has no such residence, the address or location of a place
in the United Kingdom where the offender can regularly be found and, if there
is more than one such place, such one of those places as the offender may
select.

175.5

In section 350 (sexual harm prevention orders: variations, renewals and
discharges)—

175.5.a

in subsection (6)—

175.5.a.i

in the words before paragraph (a), after “prohibitions” insert  “or
requirements” , and

175.5.a.ii

in the words after paragraph (b), after “prohibitions” insert  “and
requirements” ,

175.5.b

after subsection (6) insert—

175.5.b.6A

Any additional prohibitions or requirements that are imposed on the offender
must, so far as practicable, be such as to avoid—

175.5.b.6A.a

any conflict with the offender’s religious beliefs,

175.5.b.6A.b

any interference with the times, if any, at which the offender normally works
or attends any educational establishment, and

175.5.b.6A.c

any conflict with any other court order or injunction to which the offender
may be subject.

, and

175.5.c

in subsection (8), after “other prohibitions” insert  “or requirements” .

prevention order, or

175.6.a.1.b

fails to do something that the person is required to do by a sexual harm
prevention order.

,

175.6.b

“breaching such an order” , and

175.6.c

omit subsection (3).

order”.

175.10

After section 103C insert—

############ SHPOs: requirements included in order etc.

175.10.103CA

175.10.103CA.1

A sexual harm prevention order that imposes a requirement to do something on a
defendant must specify a person who is to be responsible for supervising
compliance with the requirement.

The person may be an individual or an organisation.

175.10.103CA.2

Before including such a requirement in a sexual harm prevention order, the
court must receive evidence about its suitability and enforceability from—

175.10.103CA.2.a

the individual to be specified under subsection (1), if an individual is to be
specified;

175.10.103CA.2.b

an individual representing the organisation to be specified under subsection
(1), if an organisation is to be specified.

175.10.103CA.3

Subsections (1) and (2) do not apply in relation to electronic monitoring
requirements (see instead section 103FA(5) and (6)).

175.10.103CA.4

It is the duty of a person specified under subsection (1)—

175.10.103CA.4.a

to make any necessary arrangements in connection with the requirements for
which the person has responsibility (“the relevant requirements”);

175.10.103CA.4.b

to promote the defendant’s compliance with the relevant requirements;

175.10.103CA.4.c

if the person considers that—

175.10.103CA.4.c.i

the defendant has complied with all the relevant requirements, or

175.10.103CA.4.c.ii

the defendant has failed to comply with a relevant requirement,

to inform the appropriate chief officer of police.

175.10.103CA.5

In subsection (4)(c) the “appropriate chief officer of police means—

175.10.103CA.5.a

the chief officer of police for the police area in which it appears to the
person specified under subsection (1) that the defendant resides, or

175.10.103CA.5.b

if it appears to that person that the defendant resides in more than one
police area, whichever of the chief officers of police of those areas the
person thinks it is most appropriate to inform.

175.10.103CA.6

A defendant subject to a requirement imposed by a sexual harm prevention order
must—

175.10.103CA.6.a

keep in touch with the person specified under subsection (1) in relation to
that requirement, in accordance with any instructions given by that person
from time to time, and

175.10.103CA.6.b

notify that person of any change of the defendant’s home address.

These obligations have effect as requirements of the order.

175.13

In section 103I (offence: breach of sexual harm prevention order or interim
sexual harm prevention order)—

175.13.a

before subsection (1) insert—

175.13.a.A1

A person who, without reasonable excuse—

175.13.a.A1.a

does anything that the person is prohibited from doing by a sexual harm
prevention order or an interim sexual harm prevention order, or

175.13.a.A1.b

fails to do something that the person is required to do by a sexual harm
prevention order or an interim sexual harm prevention order,

commits an offence.

,

175.13.b

in subsection (1), omit paragraphs (a) and (b), and

175.13.c

omit subsection (2).

###### Sexual risk orders: power to impose positive requirements

176

176.1

The Sexual Offences Act 2003 is amended as follows.

176.2

In section 122A (sexual risk orders: applications, grounds and effect)—

176.2.a

for subsection (7) substitute—

176.2.a.7

A sexual risk order may—

176.2.a.7.a

prohibit the defendant from doing anything described in the order;

176.2.a.7.b

require the defendant to do anything described in the order.

,

176.2.b

in subsection (8), for the words from “may specify” to the end of the
subsection substitute

—

176.2.b.a

has effect for a fixed period (not less than 2 years) specified in the order
or until further order, and

176.2.b.b

may specify different periods for different prohibitions or requirements.

,

176.2.c

in subsection (9), after “prohibitions” insert  “or requirements” , and

176.2.d

after subsection (9) insert—

176.2.d.9A

The prohibitions or requirements which are imposed on the defendant by a
sexual risk order must, so far as practicable, be such as to avoid—

176.2.d.9A.a

any conflict with the defendant’s religious beliefs,

176.2.d.9A.b

any interference with the times, if any, at which the defendant normally works
or attends any educational establishment, and

176.2.d.9A.c

any conflict with any other court order or injunction to which the defendant
may be subject (but see subsection (10)).

176.3

After section 122B insert—

############ Sexual risk orders: requirements included in order etc.

176.3.122BA

176.3.122BA.1

A sexual risk order that imposes a requirement to do something on a defendant
must specify a person who is to be responsible for supervising compliance with
the requirement.

The person may be an individual or an organisation.

176.3.122BA.2

Before including such a requirement in a sexual risk order, the court must
receive evidence about its suitability and enforceability from—

176.3.122BA.2.a

the individual to be specified under subsection (1), if an individual is to be
specified;

176.3.122BA.2.b

an individual representing the organisation to be specified under subsection
(1), if an organisation is to be specified.

176.3.122BA.3

Subsections (1) and (2) do not apply in relation to electronic monitoring
requirements (see instead section 122EA(5) and (6)).

176.3.122BA.4

It is the duty of a person specified under subsection (1)—

176.3.122BA.4.a

to make any necessary arrangements in connection with the requirements for
which the person has responsibility (“the relevant requirements”);

176.3.122BA.4.b

to promote the defendant’s compliance with the relevant requirements;

176.3.122BA.4.c

if the person considers that—

176.3.122BA.4.c.i

the defendant has complied with all the relevant requirements, or

176.3.122BA.4.c.ii

the defendant has failed to comply with a relevant requirement,

to inform the appropriate chief officer of police.

176.3.122BA.5

In subsection (4)(c) the “appropriate chief officer of police means—

176.3.122BA.5.a

the chief officer of police for the police area in which it appears to the
person specified under subsection (1) that the defendant resides, or

176.3.122BA.5.b

if it appears to that person that the defendant resides in more than one
police area, whichever of the chief officers of police of those areas the
person thinks it is most appropriate to inform.

176.3.122BA.6

A defendant subject to a requirement imposed by a sexual risk order must—

176.3.122BA.6.a

keep in touch with the person specified under subsection (1) in relation to
that requirement, in accordance with any instructions given by that person
from time to time, and

176.3.122BA.6.b

notify that person of any change of the defendant’s home address.

These obligations have effect as requirements of the order.

176.4

In section 122D (sexual risk orders: variations, renewals and discharges)—

176.4.a

in subsection (4)—

176.4.a.i

in the words before paragraph (a), after “prohibitions” insert  “or
requirements” , and

176.4.a.ii

in the words after paragraph (b), after “prohibitions” insert  “and
requirements” , and

176.4.b

after that subsection, insert—

176.4.b.4A

Any additional prohibitions or requirements that are imposed on the defendant
must, so far as practicable, be such as to avoid—

176.4.b.4A.a

any conflict with the defendant’s religious beliefs,

176.4.b.4A.b

any interference with the times, if any, at which the defendant normally works
or attends any educational establishment, and

176.4.b.4A.c

any conflict with any other court order or injunction to which the defendant
may be subject.

176.5

In section 122E(3) (interim sexual risk orders), for the words from “,
prohibiting the defendant” to the end of the subsection substitute  “—

176.5.a

prohibiting the defendant from doing anything described in the order;

176.5.b

requiring the defendant to do anything described in the order.”

176.6

In section 122H (offence: breach of sexual risk order or interim sexual risk
order etc)—

176.6.a

before subsection (1) insert—

176.6.a.A1

A person who, without reasonable excuse—

176.6.a.A1.a

does anything that the person is prohibited from doing by a sexual risk order
or an interim sexual risk order, or

176.6.a.A1.b

fails to do something that the person is required to do by a sexual risk order
or an interim sexual risk order,

commits an offence.

,

176.6.b

in subsection (1), omit paragraphs (a) and (b), and

176.6.c

omit subsection (2).
