###### Electronic monitoring requirements

178

178.1

The Sentencing Code is amended in accordance with subsections (2) to (5).

178.2

In section 343 (sexual harm prevention order), after subsection (3) (inserted
by section 175 of this Act) insert—

178.2.4

A sexual harm prevention order may require the offender to submit to
electronic monitoring of the offender’s compliance with the prohibitions and
requirements imposed by the order (see section 348A for further provision
about such a requirement).

178.3

In section 347 (sexual harm prevention orders: matters to be specified)—

178.3.a

in subsection (1), in the words after paragraph (b), after “United Kingdom”
insert  “and section 348A for further matters to be included in the case of an
electronic monitoring requirement” , and

178.3.b

in subsection (2), in the words after paragraph (b), after “travel)” insert
“and section 348A(8) (electronic monitoring requirements)” .

178.4

After section 348 insert—

############ Sexual harm prevention orders: electronic monitoring requirements

178.4.348A

178.4.348A.1

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply for the purpose of determining whether a
court may impose, under section 343(4), an electronic monitoring requirement
on the offender in a sexual harm prevention order.

178.4.348A.2

If there is a person (other than the offender) without whose co-operation it
would be impracticable to secure the monitoring in question, the requirement
may not be imposed without that person’s consent.

178.4.348A.3

The court may impose the requirement only if—

178.4.348A.3.a

it has been notified by the Secretary of State that electronic monitoring
arrangements are available in the relevant area, and

178.4.348A.3.b

it is satisfied that the necessary provision can be made under the
arrangements currently available.

178.4.348A.4

In subsection (3)(a) “ the relevant area ” means—

178.4.348A.4.a

the local justice area in which it appears to the court that the offender
resides or will reside, and

178.4.348A.4.b

in a case where it is proposed to include in the order—

178.4.348A.4.b.i

a requirement that the offender must remain, for specified periods, at a
specified place, or

178.4.348A.4.b.ii

a provision prohibiting the offender from entering a specified place or area,

the local justice area in which the place or area proposed to be specified is
situated.

“ Specified ” means specified in the sexual harm prevention order under which
the electronic monitoring requirement is imposed.

178.4.348A.5

A sexual harm prevention order that includes an electronic monitoring
requirement must specify the person who is to be responsible for the
monitoring.

178.4.348A.6

The person specified under subsection (5) (“the responsible person”) must be
of a description specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State.

178.4.348A.7

Where a sexual harm prevention order imposes an electronic monitoring
requirement on the offender, the offender must (among other things)—

178.4.348A.7.a

submit, as required from time to time by the responsible person, to—

178.4.348A.7.a.i

being fitted with, or the installation of, any necessary apparatus, and

178.4.348A.7.a.ii

the inspection or repair of any apparatus fitted or installed for the purposes
of the monitoring,

178.4.348A.7.b

not interfere with, or with the working of, any apparatus fitted or installed
for the purposes of the monitoring, and

178.4.348A.7.c

take any steps required by the responsible person for the purpose of keeping
in working order any apparatus fitted or installed for the purpose of the
monitoring.

These obligations have effect as requirements of the sexual harm prevention
order under which the electronic monitoring requirement is imposed.

178.4.348A.8

A sexual harm prevention order may not provide for an electronic monitoring
requirement to have effect for more than 12 months.

178.4.348A.9

Subsection (8) does not prevent an electronic monitoring requirement from
being extended for a further period (of no more than 12 months each time)
under section 350.

############ Data from electronic monitoring: code of practice

178.4.348B

178.4.348B.1

The Secretary of State must issue a code of practice relating to the
processing of data gathered in the course of electronic monitoring of
offenders under electronic monitoring requirements imposed by sexual harm
prevention orders.

178.4.348B.2

A failure to observe a code issued under this section does not of itself make
a person liable to any criminal or civil proceedings.

178.5

In section 350 (sexual harm prevention orders: variations, renewals,
discharges), after subsection (6B) (inserted by section 173 of this Act)
insert—

178.5.6C

Section 348A (electronic monitoring requirements) applies in relation to—

178.5.6C.a

the variation of an order to require the defendant to submit to electronic
monitoring of the defendant’s compliance with the prohibitions and
requirements imposed by the order, or

178.5.6C.b

the renewal of an order to continue such a requirement,

as it applies in relation to the making of a sexual harm prevention order,
subject to subsection (6D).

178.5.6D

In its application to the variation or renewal of an order, section 348A(4)(b)
has effect as if—

178.5.6D.a

the reference to a case where it is proposed to include in the order a
requirement or provision mentioned in sub-paragraph (i) or (ii) included a
case where the order already includes such a requirement or provision, and

178.5.6D.b

the reference to the local justice area in which the place or area proposed to
be specified is situated included the local justice area in which the place or
area already specified is situated.

###### Positive requirements and electronic monitoring requirements: service courts

179

In section 137(3) of the Sexual Offences Act 2003 (service courts: sexual harm

179.a

###### Variation etc of order by court in another part of the United Kingdom

183

183.1

Schedule 18 contains amendments enabling a court in one part of the United
Kingdom to vary, renew or discharge an order made in another.

183.2

In that Schedule—

183.2.a

Part 1 enables a court in Northern Ireland to renew or discharge orders made
in England and Wales and to vary, renew or discharge orders made in Scotland;

183.2.b

Part 2 enables a court in Scotland to vary, renew or discharge orders made in
England and Wales or Northern Ireland;

183.2.c

Part 3 enables a court in England and Wales to vary, renew or discharge orders
made in Scotland or Northern Ireland.

#### Management of terrorist offenders

##### Terrorist offenders released on licence: arrest without warrant pending recall decision

184

184.1

After section 43A of the Terrorism Act 2000 insert—

########### Offenders released on licence: powers in connection with protecting public from risk of terrorism

############ Terrorist offenders released on licence: arrest without warrant pending recall decision

184.1.43B

184.1.43B.1

Subject to subsection  (2) , a constable may arrest without warrant a
terrorist offender who has been released on licence if the constable—

184.1.43B.1.a

has reasonable grounds for suspecting that the offender has breached a
condition of their licence, and

184.1.43B.1.b

reasonably considers that it is necessary, for purposes connected with
protecting members of the public from a risk of terrorism, to detain the
offender until a recall decision is made.

184.1.43B.2

A terrorist offender who is detained under this section must (unless recalled
or otherwise detained under any other power) be released—

184.1.43B.2.a

if a recall decision is made not to revoke the offender’s licence (and
accordingly the offender is not recalled to prison), as soon as practicable
after that decision is made, or

184.1.43B.2.b

if a recall decision has not been made by the end of the relevant period, at
the end of that period.

184.1.43B.3

Part 1 of Schedule 8 makes provision that applies where a terrorist offender
is arrested under this section.

184.1.43B.4

In this section “ terrorist offender ” means—

184.1.43B.4.a

an offender to whom a restricted release provision applies or would apply but
for the fact that the offender has been released on licence;

184.1.43B.4.b

a life prisoner within the meaning of Chapter 2 of Part 2 of the Crime
(Sentences) Act 1997 (see section 34 of that Act) who is serving a sentence
for an offence within section 247A(2) of the Criminal Justice Act 2003;

184.1.43B.4.c

a life prisoner within the meaning of Part 1 of the Prisoners and Criminal
Proceedings (Scotland) Act 1993 (see section 27 of that Act) who is serving a
sentence, or is subject to an order for lifelong restriction, for an offence
within section 1AB(2) of that Act;

184.1.43B.4.d

a life prisoner within the meaning of the Life Sentences (Northern Ireland)
Order 2001 ( S.I. 2001/2564 (N.I. 2) ) (see Article 2 of that Order) who is
serving a sentence for an offence within Article 20A(2) of the Criminal
Justice (Northern Ireland) Order 2008 ( S.I. 2008/1216 (N.I. 1) ).

184.1.43B.5

For the purposes of this section—

184.1.43B.5.a

a reference to an offender who has been released on licence includes an
offender who —

184.1.43B.5.a.i

has been released temporarily pursuant to rules made under section 47(5) of
the Prison Act 1952 or section 13(1)(c) of the  Prison Act (Northern Ireland)
1953 (c. 18 (N.I.)) , or

184.1.43B.5.a.ii

has been released temporarily on licence pursuant to rules made under section
39(6) of the Prisons (Scotland) Act 1989;

184.1.43B.5.b

a reference to a condition of an offender’s licence includes a condition to
which an offender’s temporary release is subject;

184.1.43B.5.c

a reference to revocation of an offender’s licence includes recall of an
offender from temporary release.

184.1.43B.6

In this section—

“ prison ” includes any place where a person is liable to be detained; “
recall decision ”, in relation to a terrorist offender who has been released
on licence, means a decision by any person with the power to revoke the
offender’s licence and recall the offender to prison whether or not to
exercise that power; the “ relevant period ” means— in relation to a terrorist
offender who has been released on licence under the law of England and Wales,
the period of 6 hours beginning with the time of the arrest under this
section; in relation to a terrorist offender who has been released on licence
under the law of Scotland or Northern Ireland, the period of 12 hours
beginning with the time of the arrest under this section; “ restricted release
provision ” means— section 247A of the Criminal Justice Act 2003; section 1AB
of the Prisoners and Criminal Proceedings (Scotland) Act 1993; Article 20A of
the Criminal Justice (Northern Ireland) Order 2008.

184.1.43B.7

A person who has the powers of a constable in one part of the United Kingdom
may exercise the power under subsection (1) in any part of the United Kingdom.

184.2

In Schedule 8 to the Terrorism Act 2000 (detention)—

184.2.a

in the shoulder reference, for “Section 41” substitute  “Sections 41 and 43B”
;

184.2.b

in the heading for Part 1, after “41” insert  “or 43B” ;

184.2.c

in paragraph 1, in sub-paragraphs (1), (2) and (4), after “41” insert  “or
43B” ;

184.2.d

in paragraph 2, before sub-paragraph (1) insert—

184.2.d.A1

This paragraph applies in the case of a person detained under Schedule 7 or
section 41.

;

184.2.e

in paragraph 6—

184.2.e.i

in sub-paragraph (1), for the words from “Subject to” to “section 41”
substitute  “A person detained under Schedule 7 or section 41 or 43B” ;

184.2.e.ii

after sub-paragraph (1) insert—

184.2.e.ii.1A

In the case of a person detained under Schedule 7 or section 41, sub-paragraph
(1) is subject to paragraph 8.

;

184.2.f

in paragraph 7—

184.2.f.i

in sub-paragraph (1), for the words from “Subject to” to “section 41”
substitute  “A person detained under Schedule 7 or section 41 or 43B” ;

184.2.f.ii

after sub-paragraph (1) insert—

184.2.f.ii.1A

Sub-paragraph (1) is subject—

184.2.f.ii.1A.a

in the case of a person detained under Schedule 7 or section 41, to paragraphs
8 and 9, and

184.2.f.ii.1A.b

in the case of a person detained under section 43B, to paragraph 9.

;

184.2.g

in paragraph 8, before sub-paragraph (1) insert—

184.2.g.A1

This paragraph does not apply in the case of a person detained under section
43B (except for the purposes of paragraph 9(3)(a)).

;

184.2.h

after paragraph 13 insert—

184.2.h.13A

No fingerprint, intimate sample or non-intimate sample may be taken from a
person detained under section 43B.

;

184.2.i

in paragraph 16—

184.2.i.i

in sub-paragraph (1), after “41” insert  “or 43B” ;

184.2.i.ii

in sub-paragraphs (4) and (7), at the beginning insert  “Where a person is
detained under Schedule 7 or section 41,” ;

184.2.j

in paragraph 18, in sub-paragraphs (1) and (2), after “41” insert  “or 43B” .

##### Power to search terrorist offenders released on licence

185

After section 43B of the Terrorism Act 2000 insert—

######### Power to search terrorist offenders released on licence

185.43C

185.43C.1

A constable may stop and search a terrorist offender who is within subsection
(2)  if the constable is satisfied that it is necessary to do so for purposes
connected with protecting members of the public from a risk of terrorism.

185.43C.2

A terrorist offender is within this subsection if—

185.43C.2.a

the offender has been released on licence (and not recalled), and

185.43C.2.b

the offender’s licence includes a search condition.

185.43C.3

The power in subsection (1) may be exercised in any place to which the
constable lawfully has access (whether or not it is a place to which the
public has access).

185.43C.4

Subsection  (5)  applies if a constable, in exercising the power in subsection
(1) to stop a terrorist offender, stops a vehicle (see section 116(2)).

185.43C.5

The constable may search the vehicle and anything in or on it for purposes
connected with protecting members of the public from a risk of terrorism.

185.43C.6

Nothing in subsection  (5)  confers a power to search any person, but the
power to search in that subsection is in addition to the power in subsection
(1) to search a terrorist offender.

185.43C.7

The power in subsection (1) to search a terrorist offender includes power to
search anything carried by the offender.

185.43C.8

Subsection  (5)  of section 43B applies for the purposes of this section as it
applies for the purposes of that section.

185.43C.9

In this section—

“ search condition ” means a condition requiring the offender to submit to a
search of their person under this section; “ terrorist offender ” has the same
meaning as in section 43B.

185.43C.10

A person who has the powers of a constable in one part of the United Kingdom
may exercise a power under this section in any part of the United Kingdom.

##### Search of premises of offender released on licence for purposes connected with protection from risk of terrorism

186

After section 43C of the Terrorism Act 2000 insert—

######### Search of premises of offender released on licence for purposes connected with protection from risk of terrorism

186.43D

186.43D.1

A justice may issue a warrant under this section if, on the application of a
senior police officer of the relevant force, the justice is satisfied that the
requirements in subsection (2) are met.

186.43D.2

The requirements are—

186.43D.2.a

that the person specified in the application is a relevant offender who has
been released on licence (and not recalled),

186.43D.2.b

that there are reasonable grounds for believing that the person resides, or
may regularly be found, at premises (whether residential or otherwise)
specified in the application,

186.43D.2.c

that it is necessary, for purposes connected with protecting members of the
public from a risk of terrorism, for a constable to enter and search premises
specified in the application, and

186.43D.2.d

the occupier of the premises is unlikely to consent to a constable entering or
searching the premises specified in the application.

186.43D.3

A warrant under this section must specify each set of premises to which it
relates (which are to be premises in relation to which the requirements in
subsection  (2)(b)  to (d) are met).

186.43D.4

A warrant under this section is a warrant that authorises a constable of the
relevant force, for the purposes referred to in subsection  (2)(c) —

186.43D.4.a

to enter the premises to which it relates, and

186.43D.4.b

to search the premises or, if the premises are multiple occupancy premises,
the relevant parts of the premises.

186.43D.5

A warrant under this section may—

186.43D.5.a

authorise the constable executing it to use reasonable force if necessary to
enter and search the premises;

186.43D.5.b

authorise entry to, and search of, the premises on more than one occasion
(whether on a certain number of occasions or without limit), so far as the
justice who issues the warrant is satisfied that such authorisation is
necessary for the purposes referred to in subsection (2)(c).

186.43D.6

For the purposes of subsection  (4) —

186.43D.6.a

“multiple occupancy premises” are premises at which two or more individuals
who are not members of the same household reside;

186.43D.6.b

the reference to the “ relevant parts ” of multiple occupancy premises is to
those parts of the premises to which the constable has reasonable grounds for
believing that the person to whom the warrant relates has access.

186.43D.7

Subsection  (5)  of section 43B applies for the purposes of this section as it
applies for the purposes of that section.

186.43D.8

In this section “ relevant offender ” means—

186.43D.8.a

a prisoner to whom Chapter 6 of Part 12 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003
applies (release of fixed-term prisoners);

186.43D.8.b

a life prisoner within the meaning of Chapter 2 of Part 2 of the Crime
(Sentences) Act 1997 (see section 34 of that Act);

186.43D.8.c

a short-term prisoner, long-term prisoner or life prisoner within the meaning
of Part 1 of the Prisoners and Criminal Proceedings (Scotland) Act 1993 (see
section 27 of that Act);

186.43D.8.d

a fixed-term prisoner within the meaning of Chapter 4 of Part 2 of the
Criminal Justice (Northern Ireland) Order 2008 ( S.I. 2008/1216 (N.I. 1) )
(see Article 16 of that Order);

186.43D.8.e

a life prisoner within the meaning of the Life Sentences (Northern Ireland)
Order 2001 ( S.I. 2001/2564 (N.I. 2) ) (see Article 2 of that Order).

186.43D.9

In this section—

“ justice ” means— a justice of the peace in England and Wales, a sheriff or
summary sheriff in Scotland, or a lay magistrate in Northern Ireland; “
relevant force ” means— if the premises specified in the application for the
warrant are in England or Wales, the police force maintained for the police
area in which those premises are situated, if those premises are in Scotland,
the Police Service of Scotland, or if those premises are in Northern Ireland,
the Police Service of Northern Ireland; “ senior police officer ” means a
constable of the rank of superintendent or above.

##### Powers of seizure and retention

187

After section 43D of the Terrorism Act 2000 insert—

######### Seizure and retention of items found in search under section 43C or 43D

187.43E

187.43E.1

This section applies where a constable carries out—

187.43E.1.a

a search of a terrorist offender under section 43C(1),

187.43E.1.b

a search of a vehicle, or anything in or on a vehicle, under section 43C(5),
or

187.43E.1.c

a search of premises further to a warrant issued under section 43D.

187.43E.2

A constable may seize anything that the constable finds in the course of the
search if—

187.43E.2.a

the constable reasonably suspects that—

187.43E.2.a.i

the thing is or contains evidence in relation to an offence, and

187.43E.2.a.ii

it is necessary to seize it in order to prevent it being concealed, lost,
damaged, altered or destroyed, or

187.43E.2.b

the constable reasonably believes that it is necessary to do so for the
purpose of ascertaining—

187.43E.2.b.i

whether the offender has breached a condition of the offender’s licence, and

187.43E.2.b.ii

if so, whether the breach affects the risk of terrorism to which members of
the public are exposed.

187.43E.3

Anything seized under subsection (2) may be—

187.43E.3.a

subjected to tests;

187.43E.3.b

retained for as long as is necessary in all the circumstances (but see
subsection (5)).

187.43E.4

In particular (and regardless of the ground on which the thing was seized)—

187.43E.4.a

if a constable has reasonable grounds for believing that the thing is or
contains evidence in relation to an offence, it may be retained—

187.43E.4.a.i

for use as evidence at a trial for an offence, or

187.43E.4.a.ii

for forensic examination or for investigation in connection with an offence;

187.43E.4.b

if a constable has reasonable grounds for believing that the thing has been
obtained in consequence of the commission of an offence, it may be retained in
order to establish its lawful owner.

187.43E.5

Anything seized under subsection (2)(b) that is not retained as mentioned in
subsection (4)(a) or (b) may be retained for a maximum period of 7 days
beginning with the day after the day on which the thing is seized.

187.43E.6

Nothing may be retained for either of the purposes mentioned in subsection
(4)(a) if a photograph or copy would be sufficient for that purpose.

187.43E.7

In this section “ offender ” means—

187.43E.7.a

in relation to a search under section 43C, the terrorist offender to whom the
search relates;

187.43E.7.b

in relation to a search under section 43D, the relevant offender in relation
to whom the warrant authorising the search was issued.

187.43E.8

Nothing in this section affects any power of a court to make an order under
section 1 of the Police (Property) Act 1897.

##### Sections 184 to 187: consequential provision

188

Schedule 19 makes provision that is consequential on sections 184 to 187.

##### Arrangements for assessing etc risks posed by certain offenders

189

189.1

Section 325 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (arrangements for assessing etc
risks posed by certain offenders) is amended in accordance with subsections
(2)  to  (6) .

189.2

for “has the meaning” substitute  “and “relevant terrorist offender” have the
meanings” .

189.3

In subsection (2)—

189.3.a

189.3.a.aa

relevant terrorist offenders,

189.3.b

at the end of paragraph (b) insert

, and

189.3.b.c

other persons who have committed offences (wherever committed) and are
considered by the responsible authority to be persons who may be at risk of
involvement in terrorism-related activity.

189.4

For subsection (4) substitute—

189.4.4

A person to whom subsection (4A) applies may, for the purpose described in
subsection (2), disclose information to another person to whom subsection (4A)
applies.

189.4.4A

This subsection applies to—

189.4.4A.a

the responsible authority,

189.4.4A.b

a person specified in subsection (6), and

189.4.4A.c

a person who the responsible authority considers may contribute to the
achievement of the purpose described in subsection (2).

189.4.4B

A disclosure under subsection (4) does not breach—

189.4.4B.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

189.4.4B.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

189.4.4C

But subsection (4) does not authorise a disclosure of information that—

189.4.4C.a

would contravene the data protection legislation (but in determining whether
it would do so, the power in that subsection is to be taken into account), or

189.4.4C.b

would be prohibited by any of Parts 1 to 7 or Chapter 1 of Part 9 of the
Investigatory Powers Act 2016.

189.4.4D

Subsection (4E) applies if a person who may disclose or receive information by
virtue of subsection (4) would not otherwise be a competent authority for the
purposes of Part 3 of the Data Protection Act 2018 (law enforcement
processing) in relation to the processing by that person of personal data by
virtue of that subsection.

189.4.4E

The person is to be treated as a competent authority for the purposes of that
Part in relation to the processing by that person of personal data by virtue
of subsection (4).

189.4.4F

But subsection (4E) does not apply to an intelligence service within the
meaning of Part 4 of the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 82(2) of that
Act).

189.4.4G

Subsections (4) to (4F) do not affect any power to disclose information apart
from that conferred by subsection (4).

189.5

In subsection (6), in the opening words, after “(3)” insert  “,  (4A)(b) ” .

189.6

In subsection (9), at the appropriate places insert—

“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);

;

“ involvement in terrorism-related activity ” has the same meaning as in the
Terrorism Prevention and Investigation Measures Act 2011 (see section 4 of
that Act);

;

“ personal data ” has the same meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see
section 3(2) of that Act);

;

“ processing ” has the same meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see
section 3(4) of that Act);

.

189.7

Section 327 of the Criminal Justice Act 2003 (interpretation of section 325)
is amended in accordance with subsections  (8)  to  (10) .

189.8

In subsection (3)—

189.8.a

in paragraph (a)—

189.8.a.i

189.8.a.ii

is not for a term of less than 12 months” , and

189.8.b.iii

189.8.b.iii.va

.

189.9

In subsection (4)(a), after “specified in” insert  “Part 1 or 2 of” .

189.10

After subsection (4A) insert—

189.10.4B

For the purposes of section 325, a person is a relevant terrorist offender if
the person falls within one or both of subsections  (4C)  and  (4D) .

189.10.4C

A person falls within this subsection if the person is subject to the
notification requirements of Part 4 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008.

189.10.4D

A person falls within this subsection if the person has been convicted of and
sentenced for a relevant terrorist offence, or otherwise dealt within in
relation to such an offence, as described in—

189.10.4D.a

paragraph (a) or (b) of section 45(1) of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008,

189.10.4D.b

paragraph (a) or (b) of section 45(2) of that Act,

189.10.4D.c

paragraph (a) or (b) of section 45(3) of that Act, or

189.10.4D.d

paragraph (a) or (b) of paragraph 5(1) of Schedule 6 to that Act.

189.10.4E

For the purposes of subsection  (4D) —

189.10.4E.a

any reference in the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 to an offence to which Part 4
of that Act applies is to be read as if it were a reference to a relevant
terrorist offence, and

189.10.4E.b

any reference in that Act to a hospital order is to be read as if it included
a guardianship order within the meaning of the Mental Health Act 1983 or the
Mental Health (Northern Ireland) Order 1986 ( S.I. 1986/595 (N.I. 4) ).

189.10.4F

In subsections  (4D)  and  (4E)  “ relevant terrorist offence ” means—

189.10.4F.a

an offence specified in Part 1 or 2 of Schedule 19ZA (terrorism offences
punishable with imprisonment for life or for more than two years),

189.10.4F.b

a service offence as respects which the corresponding civil offence is so
specified, or

189.10.4F.c

an offence which was determined to have a terrorist connection (see subsection
(4G) );

and in paragraph  (b)  “ service offence ” and “ corresponding civil offence ”
have the same meanings as in the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (see section 95 of
that Act).

189.10.4G

For the purposes of subsection  (4F)(c) , an offence was determined to have a
terrorist connection if it was—

189.10.4G.a

determined to have a terrorist connection under—

189.10.4G.a.i

section 69 of the Sentencing Code (including as applied by section 238(6) of
the Armed Forces Act 2006),

189.10.4G.a.ii

section 30 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of an offender
sentenced in England and Wales before the Sentencing Code applied, or an
offender sentenced in Northern Ireland but now capable of posing a risk in an
area in England and Wales), or

189.10.4G.a.iii

section 32 of that Act (in the case of a person sentenced for a service
offence before the Sentencing Code applied), or

189.10.4G.b

proved to have been aggravated by reason of having a terrorist connection
under section 31 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of an offender
sentenced in Scotland but now capable of posing a risk in an area in England
and Wales).

### Procedures in courts and tribunals

#### Juries

##### British Sign Language interpreters for deaf jurors

196

196.1

The Juries Act 1974 is amended as follows.

196.2

After section 9B insert—

########### British Sign Language interpreters for deaf jurors

196.2.9C

196.2.9C.1

For the purpose of section 9B(2), in determining whether or not a person who
is deaf should act as a juror, the judge must consider whether the assistance
of a British Sign Language interpreter would enable that person to be capable
of acting effectively as a juror.

196.2.9C.2

Where the judge considers that the assistance of a British Sign Language
interpreter would enable the person to be capable of acting effectively as a
juror, the judge may appoint one or more interpreters to provide that
assistance, and affirm the summons.

196.2.9C.3

An interpreter appointed under subsection (2) may remain with the jury in the
course of their deliberations in proceedings before a court for the purpose of
enabling the person the interpreter is assisting to act effectively as a
juror.

196.2.9C.4

The interpreter must not interfere in or influence the deliberations of the
jury (see section 20I as to the offence).

196.3

After section 20G insert—

########### Application of certain provisions to British Sign Language interpreters

196.3.20H

196.3.20H.1

Section 12(1) and (2) (challenge for cause) apply to an interpreter appointed
under section 9C(2) as those provisions apply to jurors.

196.3.20H.2

Section 15A (surrender of electronic communications devices) applies to an
interpreter appointed under section 9C(2) as it applies to members of a jury.

196.3.20H.3

Section 20A (offence of research by jurors) applies to an interpreter
appointed under section 9C(2) as it applies to members of a jury with the
modification that the reference to “the trial period” in subsection (5), in
relation to an interpreter, is the period—

196.3.20H.3.a

beginning when the interpreter is appointed under section 9C(2), and

196.3.20H.3.b

ending when the judge discharges the jury or, if earlier, when the judge
discharges the interpreter.

196.3.20H.4

Section 20B (offence of sharing research with other jurors) applies to an
interpreter appointed under section 9C(2) as it applies to members of a jury,
but the references in section 20B to “section 20A” and “the trial period” are
to be read as references to “section 20A” and “the trial period” as modified
by subsection (3) of this section.

196.3.20H.5

In the following provisions of section 20F (exceptions to offence of
disclosing jury deliberations), the references to the conduct of a juror
include the conduct of an interpreter appointed under section 9C(2)—

196.3.20H.5.a

subsection (1)(b)(ii);

196.3.20H.5.b

subsection (4)(b);

196.3.20H.5.c

subsection (5).

########### Offence: interpreters interfering in or influencing jury deliberations

196.3.20I

196.3.20I.1

It is an offence for an interpreter appointed under section 9C(2)
intentionally to interfere in or influence the deliberations of the jury in
proceedings before a court.

196.3.20I.2

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable, on conviction on
indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years or a fine (or
both).

196.3.20I.3

Proceedings for an offence under this section may only be instituted by or
with the consent of the Attorney General.

196.4

In section 22(A1) (offences which do not affect contempt of court at common
law) for “or 20C” substitute  “, 20C or 20I” .

#### Transmission and recording of court and tribunal proceedings

##### Remote observation and recording of court and tribunal proceedings

198

198.1

In the Courts Act 2003, after section 85 insert—

########### Transmission and recording of court and tribunal proceedings

############ Remote observation and recording

############# Remote observation and recording of proceedings by direction of a court or tribunal

198.1.85A

198.1.85A.1

This section applies (subject to subsections (12) and (13)) to proceedings in
any court; and in this section “ court ” has the same meaning as in the
Contempt of Court Act 1981 (see section 19 of that Act).

198.1.85A.2

If the proceedings are specified under subsection  (8)(a) , the court may
direct that images or sounds of the proceedings are to be transmitted
electronically for the purpose of enabling persons not taking part in the
proceedings to watch or listen to the proceedings.

198.1.85A.3

A direction under subsection  (2)  may authorise only the following types of
transmission—

198.1.85A.3.a

transmission to designated live-streaming premises, or

198.1.85A.3.b

transmission to which individuals are given access only having first
identified themselves to the court (or to a person acting on behalf of the
court).

198.1.85A.4

In subsection  (3)(a) , “ designated live-streaming premises ” means premises
that are designated by the Lord Chancellor as premises that are made available
for members of the public to watch or listen to proceedings in accordance with
directions under subsection  (2) .

198.1.85A.5

A direction under subsection  (2)  may include further provision about—

198.1.85A.5.a

the manner of transmission, or

198.1.85A.5.b

the persons who are to be able to watch or listen to the transmission
(including provision making that ability subject to conditions, or aimed at
preventing persons who are not meant to watch or listen from being able to do
so).

198.1.85A.6

If images or sounds of the proceedings are transmitted electronically (whether
under a direction under subsection  (2)  or any other power), the court may
direct that a recording of the transmission is to be made, in the manner
specified in the direction, for the purpose of enabling the court to keep a
record of the proceedings.

198.1.85A.7

A direction under subsection  (2)  or  (6) —

198.1.85A.7.a

may relate to the whole, or to part, of the proceedings concerned, and

198.1.85A.7.b

may be varied or revoked.

198.1.85A.8

The Lord Chancellor may by regulations—

198.1.85A.8.a

specify proceedings (by reference to their type, the court in which they take
place, or any other circumstance) in relation to which directions under
subsection  (2)  may be made;

198.1.85A.8.b

specify matters of which the court must be satisfied before deciding to make
such a direction;

198.1.85A.8.c

specify matters that the court must take into account when deciding whether,
and on what terms, to make such a direction;

198.1.85A.8.d

require directions under subsection  (2)  to include certain provision under
subsection  (5) .

198.1.85A.9

Before making regulations under subsection  (8) , the Lord Chancellor must
determine whether the function of giving or withholding concurrence to the
regulations would most appropriately be exercised by—

198.1.85A.9.a

the Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales,

198.1.85A.9.b

the Senior President of Tribunals, or

198.1.85A.9.c

both of them.

198.1.85A.10

Regulations under subsection  (8)  may be made only with the concurrence of
the Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales, the Senior President of
Tribunals, or both of them, as determined under subsection  (9) .

198.1.85A.11

Regulations under subsection  (8)  may make different provision for different
purposes.

198.1.85A.12

This section does not apply to proceedings in the Supreme Court.

198.1.85A.13

This section does not apply to proceedings if provision regulating the
procedure to be followed in those proceedings could be made by—

198.1.85A.13.a

an Act of the Scottish Parliament,

198.1.85A.13.b

an Act of Senedd Cymru (including one passed with the consent of a Minister of
the Crown within the meaning of section 158(1) of the Government of Wales Act
2006), or

198.1.85A.13.c

an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly passed without the consent of the
Secretary of State.

198.2

In section 41 of the Criminal Justice Act 1925 (prohibition of photography etc
in court)—

198.2.a

after subsection (1) insert—

198.2.a.1ZA

Subsection (1) does not apply to anything done in accordance with a direction
under section  85A  of the Courts Act 2003 (remote observation and recording
of court and tribunal proceedings).

;

198.2.b

in subsection (1A), after “provide for” insert  “further” .

198.3

In section 29 of the  Criminal Justice Act (Northern Ireland) 1945 (c. 15
(N.I.))  (prohibition of photography etc in court), after subsection (1)
insert—

198.3.1A

Subsection (1) does not apply to anything done in accordance with a direction
under section 85A of the Courts Act 2003 (remote observation and recording of
court and tribunal proceedings).

198.4

In section 9 of the Contempt of Court Act 1981 (prohibition of tape recording
etc), after subsection (4) insert—

198.4.4A

This section does not apply to anything done in accordance with a direction
under section  85A  of the Courts Act 2003 (remote observation and recording
of court and tribunal proceedings).

198.5

In section 108(3) of the Courts Act 2003 (regulations and orders under that
Act subject to affirmative procedure), after paragraph (c) insert—

198.5.ca

regulations under section  85A (8)  (provision about directions for remote
observation of court and tribunal proceedings);

.

##### Offence of recording or transmission in relation to remote proceedings

199

In the Courts Act 2003, after section  85A  (inserted by section 198) insert—

######### Offence of recording or transmission

########## Offence of recording or transmission in relation to remote proceedings

199.85B

199.85B.1

It is an offence for a person to make, or attempt to make—

199.85B.1.a

an unauthorised recording, or

199.85B.1.b

an unauthorised transmission,

of an image or sound within subsection  (2)  or  (3) .

199.85B.2

An image or sound is within this subsection if it is an image or sound of
court proceedings that is being transmitted to the place where the recording
or transmission referred to in subsection  (1)  is made or attempted to be
made.

199.85B.3

An image or sound is within this subsection if it is an image or sound of a
person while that person is remotely attending court proceedings.

199.85B.4

A person is remotely attending court proceedings at any time when the person—

199.85B.4.a

is not in the same place as any member of the court, and

199.85B.4.b

is taking part in, watching or listening to the proceedings by way of a
transmission.

199.85B.5

For the purposes of this section a recording or transmission is “unauthorised”
unless it is—

199.85B.5.a

authorised (generally or specifically) by the court in which the proceedings
concerned are being conducted, or

199.85B.5.b

authorised (generally or specifically) by the Lord Chancellor.

199.85B.6

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (1)  to
prove that, at the time of the actual or attempted recording or transmission,
the person—

199.85B.6.a

was not in designated live-streaming premises, and

199.85B.6.b

did not know that the image or sound concerned was of a sort within subsection
(2)  or  (3) .

199.85B.7

In subsection  (6)(a) , “ designated live-streaming premises ” has the meaning
given by section  85A (4) .

199.85B.8

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (1)  is liable on summary
conviction to a fine not exceeding level 3 on the standard scale.

199.85B.9

Conduct that amounts to an offence under subsection  (1)  is also a contempt
of court.

But a person cannot, in respect of the same conduct, be both convicted of the
offence and punished for the contempt.

199.85B.10

For the purposes of this section it does not matter whether a person making,
or attempting to make, a recording or transmission intends the recording or
transmission, or anything comprised in it, to be seen or heard by any other
person.

199.85B.11

This section does not apply to proceedings in the Supreme Court.

199.85B.12

This section does not apply to court proceedings if provision regulating the
procedure to be followed in those proceedings could be made by—

199.85B.12.a

an Act of the Scottish Parliament,

199.85B.12.b

an Act of Senedd Cymru (including one passed with the consent of a Minister of
the Crown within the meaning of section 158(1) of the Government of Wales Act
2006), or

199.85B.12.c

an Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly passed without the consent of the
Secretary of State.

199.85B.13

In this section—

      “ court ” has the same meaning as in the Contempt of Court Act 1981 (see
section 19 of that Act);           “ court proceedings ” means proceedings in
any court;           “ recording ” means a recording on any medium—         of
a single image, a moving image or any sound, or           from which a single
image, a moving image or any sound may be produced or reproduced;
“ transmission ” means any transmission by electronic means of a single image,
a moving image or any sound (and “ transmitted ” is to be construed
accordingly).

##### Expansion of use of video and audio links in criminal proceedings

200

200.1

In the Criminal Justice Act 2003, for section 51 substitute—

########### Directions for live links in criminal proceedings

200.1.51

200.1.51.1

The court may, by a direction, require or permit a person to take part in
eligible criminal proceedings through—

200.1.51.1.a

a live audio link, or

200.1.51.1.b

a live video link.

200.1.51.2

A direction under this section may be given in relation to a member of a jury
only if the direction requires all members of the jury to take part through a
live video link while present at the same place.

200.1.51.3

In this Part “ eligible criminal proceedings ” means—

200.1.51.3.a

a preliminary hearing (see section 56(1)),

200.1.51.3.b

a summary trial,

200.1.51.3.c

a criminal appeal to the Crown Court and any proceedings that are preliminary
or incidental to such an appeal,

200.1.51.3.d

a trial on indictment or any other trial in the Crown Court for an offence,

200.1.51.3.e

proceedings under section 4A or 5 of the Criminal Procedure (Insanity) Act
1964,

200.1.51.3.f

proceedings under Part 3 of the Mental Health Act 1983,

200.1.51.3.g

proceedings under—

200.1.51.3.g.i

section 11 of the Powers of Criminal Courts (Sentencing) Act 2000, or

200.1.51.3.g.ii

section 81(1)(g) of the Senior Courts Act 1981 or section 16 of this Act in
respect of a person who has been remanded by a magistrates’ court on
adjourning a case under that section of the 2000 Act,

200.1.51.3.h

an appeal to the criminal division of the Court of Appeal and any proceedings
that are preliminary or incidental to such an appeal,

200.1.51.3.i

a reference to the Court of Appeal by the Attorney General under Part 4 of the
Criminal Justice Act 1988 and any proceedings that are preliminary or
incidental to such a reference,

200.1.51.3.j

the hearing of a reference under section 9 or 11 of the Criminal Appeal Act
1995 and any proceedings that are preliminary or incidental to such a hearing,

200.1.51.3.k

a hearing before a magistrates’ court or the Crown Court which is held after
the defendant has entered a plea of guilty,

200.1.51.3.l

a hearing under section 142(1) or (2) of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980,

200.1.51.3.m

a hearing before the Court of Appeal under section 80 of this Act and any
proceedings that are preliminary or incidental to such a hearing,

200.1.51.3.n

any hearing following conviction held for the purpose of making a decision
about bail in respect of the person convicted,

200.1.51.3.o

a sentencing hearing (see section 56(1)), or

200.1.51.3.p

an enforcement hearing (see section 56(1)).

200.1.51.4

The court may not give a direction under this section unless—

200.1.51.4.a

the court is satisfied that it is in the interests of justice for the person
to whom the direction relates to take part in the proceedings in accordance
with the direction through the live audio link or live video link,

200.1.51.4.b

the parties to the proceedings have been given the opportunity to make
representations, and

200.1.51.4.c

if so required by section  52 (9) , the relevant youth offending team has been
given the opportunity to make representations.

200.1.51.5

In deciding whether to give a direction under this section, the court must
consider—

200.1.51.5.a

any guidance given by the Lord Chief Justice, and

200.1.51.5.b

all the circumstances of the case.

200.1.51.6

Those circumstances include in particular—

200.1.51.6.a

the availability of the person to whom the direction would relate,

200.1.51.6.b

any need for that person to attend in person,

200.1.51.6.c

the views of that person,

200.1.51.6.d

the suitability of the facilities at the place where that person would take
part in the proceedings in accordance with the direction,

200.1.51.6.e

whether that person would be able to take part in the proceedings effectively
if the person took part in accordance with the direction,

200.1.51.6.f

in the case of a direction relating to a witness—

200.1.51.6.f.i

the importance of the witness’s evidence to the proceedings, and

200.1.51.6.f.ii

whether the direction might tend to inhibit any party to the proceedings from
effectively testing the witness’s evidence, and

200.1.51.6.g

the arrangements that would or could be put in place for members of the public
to see or hear the proceedings as conducted in accordance with the direction.

200.2

In the Crime and Disorder Act 1998, omit Part 3A (live links in preliminary,
sentencing and enforcement hearings).

200.3

Schedule 20 makes further provision in connection with the provision made by
subsections  (1)  and  (2) .

##### Repeal of temporary provision

201

201.1

In the Coronavirus Act 2020, sections 53 and 54 and Schedules 23 and 24 (which
make temporary modifications that are superseded by the provision made by
section 200) are repealed.

201.2

In the Coronavirus Act 2020, section 55 and Schedule 25 (which make temporary
modifications that are superseded by the provision made by sections 198 and
199) are repealed.

##### Expedited procedure for initial regulations about remote observation of proceedings

202

202.1

This section applies in relation to the first regulations made under section
85A(8) of the Courts Act 2003 (as inserted by section 198(1)).

202.2

The regulations may be made without a draft of the instrument containing them
having been laid before and approved by a resolution of each House of
Parliament (notwithstanding section 108(3) of the Courts Act 2003).

202.3

If regulations are made in reliance on subsection  (2) , the statutory
instrument containing them must be laid before Parliament after being made.

202.4

Regulations contained in a statutory instrument laid before Parliament under
subsection  (3)  cease to have effect at the end of the period of 28 days
beginning with the day on which the instrument is made unless, during that
period, the instrument is approved by a resolution of each House of
Parliament.

202.5

In calculating the period of 28 days, no account is to be taken of any whole
days that fall within a period during which—

202.5.a

Parliament is dissolved or prorogued, or

202.5.b

either House of Parliament is adjourned for more than four days.

202.6

If regulations cease to have effect as a result of subsection  (4) , that does
not—

202.6.a

affect the validity of anything previously done under or by virtue of the
regulations, or

202.6.b

prevent the making of new regulations.

### Final provisions

#### Financial provision

203

There is to be paid out of money provided by Parliament—

203.a

any expenditure incurred under or by virtue of this Act by a Minister of the
Crown, government department or other public authority, and

203.b

any increase attributable to this Act in the sums payable under any other Act
out of money so provided.

#### Minor amendments arising out of sentencing consolidation

204

Schedule 21 makes minor amendments to the Sentencing Act 2020 and other
enactments in connection with the consolidation that led to that Act.

#### Power to make consequential provision

205

205.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument make
provision that is consequential on this Act.

205.2

Regulations under subsection  (1)  may, in particular, amend, repeal or revoke
any enactment passed or made before, or in the same Session as, this Act.

205.3

In subsection  (2)  “ enactment ” includes—

205.3.a

an enactment contained in subordinate legislation within the meaning of the
Interpretation Act 1978,

205.3.b

an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, an Act or Measure
of Senedd Cymru,

205.3.c

an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, an Act of the
Scottish Parliament, and

205.3.d

an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland
legislation.

205.4

Regulations under subsection  (1) —

205.4.a

may make different provision for different purposes;

205.4.b

may make transitional, transitory or saving provision.

205.5

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with any other provision)
regulations under subsection  (1)  which amend, repeal or revoke primary
legislation may not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid
before, and approved by a resolution of, each House of Parliament.

205.6

Any other statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (1)
is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

205.7

In this section “ primary legislation ” means—

205.7.a

an Act of Parliament,

205.7.b

an Act or Measure of Senedd Cymru,

205.7.c

an Act of the Scottish Parliament, or

205.7.d

Northern Ireland legislation.

#### Power to state effect in Sentencing Act 2020 of commencement of amendments made by this Act

206

The power in section 419(1) of the Sentencing Act 2020 (power to state effect
of commencement provisions) applies in relation to any amendment or repeal
made by or under this Act of that Act as it applies in relation to an
amendment or repeal made by Schedule 22 to that Act.

207

207.1

207.4

Section 161 extends to England and Wales and Northern Ireland.

207.5

A provision of this Act which amends, repeals or revokes an enactment has the
same extent within the United Kingdom as the enactment amended, repealed or
revoked, subject to subsections  (6)  to  (9) .

207.10

207.12.b.iii

Extraction of information from electronic devices: authorised persons

Section 44

##### Authorised persons in relation to all purposes within section 37 or 41

A constable of a police force in England and Wales. A member of staff
appointed by the chief officer of police of a police force in England and
Wales. An employee of the Common Council of the City of London who is under
the direction and control of a chief officer of police. A constable within the
meaning of Part 1 of the Police and Fire Reform (Scotland) Act  2012 (asp 8)
(see section 99 of that Act). A member of staff appointed by the Scottish
Police Authority under section 26(1) of the Police and Fire Reform (Scotland)
Act 2012. A police officer within the meaning of the Police (Northern Ireland)
Act 2000 (see section 77(1) of that Act). A constable of the British Transport
Police Force. An employee of the British Transport Police Authority appointed
under section 27 of the Railways and Transport Safety Act 2003. A constable of
the Ministry of Defence police. A National Crime Agency officer.   A member of
the Royal Navy Police, the Royal Military Police or the Royal Air Force
Police.   A person who has been engaged to provide services consisting of or
including the extraction of information from electronic devices for the
purposes of the exercise of functions by a person listed in this Part of this
Schedule.

##### Authorised persons in relation to all purposes within section 37

... A person appointed as an immigration officer under paragraph 1 of Schedule
2 to the Immigration Act 1971. A person who is an enforcement officer by
virtue of section 15 of the Gangmasters (Licensing) Act 2004. A person who has
been engaged to provide services consisting of or including the extraction of
information from electronic devices for the purposes of the exercise of
functions by a person listed in this Part of this Schedule.

##### Authorised persons in relation to the prevention of crime etc only

An officer of Revenue and Customs. A person designated as a general customs
official or a customs revenue official under the Borders, Citizenship and
Immigration Act 2009 (see sections 3 and 11 of that Act).    An officer of the
department of the Secretary of State for Business and Trade. An officer of the
department of the Secretary of State for Energy Security and Net Zero. An
officer of the department of the Secretary of State for Science, Innovation
and Technology. A member of the Serious Fraud Office. A person appointed by
the Financial Conduct Authority under the Financial Services and Markets Act
2000 to conduct an investigation. An officer of the Competition and Markets
Authority. A person who is authorised by the Food Standards Agency to act in
matters arising under or by virtue of the Food Safety Act 1990. A person who
is authorised for the purposes of Part 6 of the Social Security Administration
Act 1992. An inspector appointed under section 15 of the Child Support Act
1991. A person designated by the Director General of the Independent Office
for Police Conduct under paragraph 19(2) of Schedule 3 to the Police Reform
Act 2002. The Police Investigations and Review Commissioner. A person
designated by the Police Investigations and Review Commissioner under
paragraph 7B(1) of Schedule 4 to the Police, Public Order and Criminal Justice
(Scotland) Act  2006 (asp 10) . An officer appointed by the Police Ombudsman
for Northern Ireland under section 56(1) or (1A) of the Police (Northern
Ireland) Act 1998. A person who is an enforcement officer by virtue of section
303 of the Gambling Act 2005. A person who has been engaged to provide
services consisting of or including the extraction of information from
electronic devices for the purposes of the exercise of functions by a person
listed in this Part of this Schedule.

##### Factors to be taken into account in deciding whether to grant pre-charge bail

17

In section 30A of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (release of person
arrested elsewhere than at police station), after subsection (1A) insert—

17.1B

In determining whether releasing the person on bail is necessary and
proportionate in all the circumstances, the constable must have regard in
particular to—

17.1B.a

the need to secure that the person surrenders to custody,

17.1B.b

the need to prevent offending by the person,

17.1B.c

the need to safeguard victims of crime and witnesses, taking into account any
vulnerabilities of any alleged victim of, or alleged witness to, the offence
for which the person was arrested where these vulnerabilities have been
identified by the constable,

17.1B.d

the need to safeguard the person, taking into account any vulnerabilities of
the person where these vulnerabilities have been identified by the constable,
and

17.1B.e

the need to manage risks to the public.

18.1

references to pre-conditions for bail) is amended as follows.

18.2

18.3.2

In determining whether releasing the person on bail is necessary and
proportionate in all the circumstances, the custody officer must have regard
in particular to—

18.3.2.a

18.3.2.b

the need to prevent offending by the person,

18.3.2.c

the need to safeguard victims of crime and witnesses, taking into account any
vulnerabilities of any alleged victim of, or alleged witness to, the offence
for which the person was arrested where these vulnerabilities have been
identified by the custody officer,

18.3.2.d

the need to safeguard the person, taking into account any vulnerabilities of
the person where these vulnerabilities have been identified by the custody
officer, and

18.3.2.e

the need to manage risks to the public.

###### Amendments to the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 

20

The Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 is amended as follows.

21

21.1

Section 30CA (bail under section 30A: variation of conditions by police) is
amended as follows.

21.2

After subsection (4) insert—

21.2.4A

If it is reasonably practicable to do so, the investigating officer must seek
the views of the alleged victim (if any) of the relevant offence on—

21.2.4A.a

whether any of the conditions that are relevant conditions should be varied
under subsection (1), and

21.2.4A.b

if so, what variations should be made to those conditions.

21.2.4B

The investigating officer must inform the relevant officer of any views
obtained under subsection (4A).

21.2.4C

If any of the conditions which are relevant conditions are varied under
subsection (1), the investigating officer must, if it is reasonably
practicable to do so, notify the alleged victim of the variations.

21.2.4D

If the alleged victim of the relevant offence appears to the investigating
officer to be vulnerable, subsections (4A) and (4C) apply as if references to
the alleged victim of the offence were to a person appearing to the officer to
represent the alleged victim.

21.3

For subsection (5) substitute—

21.3.5

In this section—

“ investigating officer ”, in relation to the relevant offence, means the
constable or other person in charge of the investigation of the offence; “
relevant condition ”, in relation to the relevant offence and an alleged
victim of that offence, means a condition that relates to the safeguarding of
the alleged victim; “ relevant offence ” means the offence for which the
person making the request under subsection (1) was under arrest when granted
bail under section 30A(1); “ relevant officer ”, in relation to a designated
police station, means a custody officer but, in relation to any other police
station— means a constable who is not involved in the investigation of the
relevant offence, if such a constable is readily available, and if no such
constable is readily available— means a constable other than the one who
granted bail to the person, if such a constable is readily available, and if
no such constable is readily available, means the constable who granted bail.

21.3.6

For the purposes of this section a person (“ P ”) is an alleged victim of an
offence if—

21.3.6.a

an allegation has been made to a constable or other person involved in the
investigation of the offence that P has suffered physical, mental or emotional
harm, or economic loss, which was directly caused by the offence, and

21.3.6.b

P is an individual.

21.3.7

For the purposes of this section an alleged victim of an offence is vulnerable
if the alleged victim—

21.3.7.a

was aged under 18 at the time of the offence, or

21.3.7.b

may have difficulty understanding a communication from an investigating
officer under this section, or communicating effectively in response to it, by
reason of—

21.3.7.b.i

a physical disability or disorder,

21.3.7.b.ii

a mental disorder within the meaning of the Mental Health Act 1983, or

21.3.7.b.iii

a significant impairment of intelligence and social functioning.

22

After section 47 insert—

########## Duty to seek views of alleged victims on conditions of pre-charge bail

22.47ZZA

22.47ZZA.1

Subsections (2) to (5) apply if—

22.47ZZA.1.a

a person has been arrested for an offence, and

22.47ZZA.1.b

a custody officer proposes to release the person on bail under this Part
(except section 37C(2)(b) or 37CA(2)(b)).

22.47ZZA.2

If it is reasonably practicable to do so, the investigating officer must seek
the views of the alleged victim (if any) of the offence on—

22.47ZZA.2.a

whether relevant conditions should be imposed on the person’s bail, and

22.47ZZA.2.b

if so, what relevant conditions should be imposed.

22.47ZZA.3

In this section “ relevant condition ”, in relation to an offence and an
alleged victim of that offence, means a condition that relates to the
safeguarding of the alleged victim.

22.47ZZA.4

The investigating officer must inform the custody officer of any views
obtained under subsection (2).

22.47ZZA.5

If the person is granted bail subject to relevant conditions, the
investigating officer must, if it is reasonably practicable to do so, notify
the alleged victim of the offence of those conditions.

22.47ZZA.6

If the alleged victim of the offence appears to the investigating officer to
be vulnerable, subsections (2) and (5) apply as if references to the alleged
victim of the offence were to a person appearing to the officer to represent
the alleged victim.

22.47ZZA.7

Subsections (8) to (11) apply if—

22.47ZZA.7.a

a person has been arrested for an offence,

22.47ZZA.7.b

the person has been released on bail under this Part subject to conditions,
and

22.47ZZA.7.c

the person requests a custody officer to vary the conditions under section
3A(8) of the Bail Act 1976.

22.47ZZA.8

If it is reasonably practicable to do so, the investigating officer must seek
the views of the alleged victim (if any) of the offence on—

22.47ZZA.8.a

whether any of the conditions that are relevant conditions should be varied,
and

22.47ZZA.8.b

if so, what variations should be made to those conditions.

22.47ZZA.9

The investigating officer must inform the custody officer of any views
obtained under subsection (8).

22.47ZZA.10

If any of the conditions which are relevant conditions are varied, the
investigating officer must, if it is reasonably practicable to do so, notify
the alleged victim of the variations.

22.47ZZA.11

If the alleged victim of the offence appears to the investigating officer to
be vulnerable, subsections (8) and (10) apply as if references to the alleged
victim of the offence were to a person appearing to the officer to represent
the alleged victim.

22.47ZZA.12

In this section “ investigating officer ”, in relation to an offence, means
the constable or other person in charge of the investigation of the offence.

22.47ZZA.13

For the purposes of this section a person (“ P ”) is an alleged victim of an
offence if—

22.47ZZA.13.a

an allegation has been made to a constable or other person involved in the
investigation of the offence that P has suffered physical, mental or emotional
harm, or economic loss, which was directly caused by the offence, and

22.47ZZA.13.b

P is an individual.

22.47ZZA.14

For the purposes of this section an alleged victim of an offence is vulnerable
if the alleged victim—

22.47ZZA.14.a

was aged under 18 at the time of the offence, or

22.47ZZA.14.b

may have difficulty understanding a communication from an investigating
officer under this section, or communicating effectively in response to it, by
reason of—

22.47ZZA.14.b.i

a physical disability or disorder,

22.47ZZA.14.b.ii

a mental disorder within the meaning of the Mental Health Act 1983, or

22.47ZZA.14.b.iii

a significant impairment of intelligence and social functioning.

After section 47ZD insert—

######### Applicable bail period: further extension of limit in standard cases

29.47ZDA

29.47ZDA.1

This section applies in relation to a person if—

29.47ZDA.1.a

a relevant officer has authorised an extension of the applicable bail period
in relation to the person under section 47ZD,

29.47ZDA.1.b

that period has not ended, and

29.47ZDA.1.c

a senior officer is satisfied that conditions A to D are met in relation to
the person.

29.47ZDA.2

The senior officer may authorise the applicable bail period in relation to the
person to be extended so that it ends at the end of the period of 9 months
beginning with the person’s bail start date.

29.47ZDA.3

Before determining whether to give an authorisation under subsection (2) in
relation to a person, the senior officer must arrange for the person or the
person’s legal representative to be informed that a determination is to be
made.

29.47ZDA.4

In determining whether to give an authorisation under subsection (2) in
relation to a person, the senior officer must consider any representations
made by the person or the person’s legal representative.

29.47ZDA.5

The senior officer must arrange for the person or the person’s legal
representative to be informed whether an authorisation under subsection (2)
has been given in relation to the person.

29.47ZDA.6

For the purposes of this Part “ senior officer ” means a police officer of the
rank of superintendent or above.

######### Applicable bail period: extension of limit in non-standard cases

29.47ZDB

29.47ZDB.1

This section applies in relation to a person if—

29.47ZDB.1.a

the applicable bail period in relation to a person is the period mentioned in
section 47ZB(1)(a),

29.47ZDB.1.b

that period has not ended, and

29.47ZDB.1.c

an appropriate decision-maker is satisfied that conditions A to D are met in
relation to the person.

29.47ZDB.2

The appropriate decision-maker may authorise the applicable bail period in
relation to the person to be extended so that it ends at the end of the period
of 12 months beginning with the person’s bail start date.

29.47ZDB.3

Before determining whether to give an authorisation under subsection (2) in
relation to a person, the appropriate decision-maker must arrange for the
person or the person’s legal representative to be informed that a
determination is to be made.

29.47ZDB.4

In determining whether to give an authorisation under subsection (2) in
relation to a person, the appropriate decision-maker must consider any
representations made by the person or the person’s legal representative.

29.47ZDB.5

The appropriate decision-maker must arrange for the person or the person’s
legal representative to be informed whether an authorisation under subsection
(2) has been given in relation to the person.

29.47ZDB.6

For the purposes of this Part “ appropriate decision-maker ” means—

29.47ZDB.6.a

in an FCA case, a member of staff of the Financial Conduct Authority who is of
the description designated for the purposes of this section by the Chief
Executive of that Authority,

29.47ZDB.6.b

in an HMRC case, an officer of Revenue and Customs of a grade that is
equivalent to the rank of superintendent or above,

29.47ZDB.6.c

in an NCA case, a National Crime Agency officer of a grade that is equivalent
to the rank of superintendent or above, and

29.47ZDB.6.d

in an SFO case, a member of the Serious Fraud Office who is of the Senior
Civil Service.

##### Guidance on pre-charge bail

37

In the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984, after section 50A insert—

######### Guidance from the College of Policing on pre-charge bail

37.50B

37.50B.1

The College of Policing may, with the approval of the Secretary of State,
issue guidance on bail that is granted to a person under Part 3 or this Part
(“pre-charge bail”).

37.50B.2

Guidance on pre-charge bail may in particular cover—

37.50B.2.a

the exercise of powers to release a person on pre-charge bail;

37.50B.2.b

the exercise of powers to impose or vary conditions of pre-charge bail;

37.50B.2.c

the exercise of powers to arrest a person—

37.50B.2.c.i

for failing to answer pre-charge bail, or

37.50B.2.c.ii

for breaching any conditions of pre-charge bail;

37.50B.2.d

the exercise of powers to extend the period of pre-charge bail;

37.50B.2.e

the duty to seek the views of alleged victims about conditions of pre-charge
bail.

37.50B.3

The College of Policing may, with the approval of the Secretary of State, from
time to time revise the whole or any part of its guidance on pre-charge bail.

37.50B.4

Before issuing or revising guidance on pre-charge bail, the College of
Policing must consult—

37.50B.4.a

the National Police Chiefs’ Council,

37.50B.4.b

such persons as appear to the College to represent the views of local policing
bodies, and

37.50B.4.c

such other persons as the College thinks fit.

37.50B.5

The Secretary of State must lay before Parliament any guidance on pre-charge
bail issued by the College of Policing, and any revision of such guidance.

37.50B.6

The Secretary of State is not required by subsection  (5)  to lay before
Parliament, or may exclude from what is laid, anything the publication of
which, in the opinion of the Secretary of State—

37.50B.6.a

could prejudice the prevention or detection of crime or the apprehension or
prosecution of offenders, or

37.50B.6.b

could jeopardise the safety of any person.

37.50B.7

A person who exercises functions relating to pre-charge bail must have regard
to the guidance.

37.50B.8

But subsection (7) does not apply to—

37.50B.8.a

a member of the Serious Fraud Office,

37.50B.8.b

a member of staff of the Financial Conduct Authority,

37.50B.8.c

an officer of Revenue and Customs, or

37.50B.8.d

a National Crime Agency officer.

37.50B.9

A failure on the part of a person to whom subsection (7) applies to comply
with the guidance does not of itself render the person liable to any criminal
or civil proceedings.

37.50B.10

But guidance on pre-charge bail is admissible in evidence in criminal or civil
proceedings and a court may take into account a failure to comply with it in
determining a question in the proceedings.

Special procedure for access to material relating to human remains

Section 56

##### Making of orders by judge

1

1.1

On an application made by a constable, a judge may make an order under
paragraph  2  if the judge is satisfied that the following conditions are met.

1.2

The first condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that
material that consists of, or may relate to the location of, relevant human
remains—

1.2.a

is in the possession or control of a person specified in the application, or

1.2.b

is on premises occupied or controlled by a person specified in the
application.

1.3

The second condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that
the material consists of or includes excluded material or special procedure
material.

1.4

The third condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that
the material does not consist of or include items subject to legal privilege.

1.5

The fourth condition is that other methods of obtaining the material—

1.5.a

have been tried without success, or

1.5.b

have not been tried because it appeared that they were bound to fail.

1.6

The fifth condition is that it is in the public interest, having regard—

1.6.a

to the need to ensure that human remains are located and disposed of in a
lawful manner, and

1.6.b

to the circumstances under which the person in possession of the material
holds it,

that the material should be produced or access to it should be given.

2

2.1

An order under this paragraph is an order that, before the end of the relevant
period, the person specified in the application must—

2.1.a

produce the material to a constable for the constable to take it away, or

2.1.b

give a constable access to it.

2.2

In sub-paragraph  (1)  “ the relevant period ” means 7 days from the date of
the order or such longer period as the order may specify.

3

Where the material consists of information stored in any electronic form—

3.a

an order under paragraph  2 (1) (a)  has effect as an order to produce the
material in a form in which it can be taken away and in which it is visible
and legible or from which it can readily be produced in a visible or legible
form, and

3.b

an order under paragraph  2 (1) (b)  has effect as an order to give a
constable access to the material in a form in which it is visible and legible.

4

For the purposes of sections 21 and 22 of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act
1984, material produced in pursuance of an order under paragraph  2 (1) (a)
is to be treated as if it were material seized by a constable.

##### Notices of applications for orders

5

5.1

An application for an order under paragraph  2  that relates to material that
consists of or includes journalistic material is to be made inter partes.

5.2

Notice of an application for an order under paragraph  2  that relates to such
material may be served on a person—

5.2.a

by delivering it to the person,

5.2.b

by leaving it at the person’s proper address, or

5.2.c

by sending it by post to the person in a registered letter or by a recorded
delivery service.

5.3

Notice of an application for an order under paragraph  2  that relates to such
material may be served—

5.3.a

on a body corporate, by serving it on the body’s secretary or clerk or other
similar officer;

5.3.b

on a partnership, by serving it on one of the partners.

5.4

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2) , and of section 7 of the
Interpretation Act 1978 in its application to that sub-paragraph, the proper
address of a person—

5.4.a

in the case of a secretary or clerk or other similar officer of a body
corporate, is that of the registered or principal office of that body;

5.4.b

in the case of a partner of a firm is that of the principal office of the
firm;

5.4.c

in any other case is the last known address of the person to be served.

6

6.1

Where notice of an application for an order under paragraph  2  has been
served on a person, the person must not conceal, destroy, alter or dispose of
the material to which the application relates until sub-paragraph  (2)
applies except—

6.1.a

with the leave of a judge, or

6.1.b

with the written permission of a constable.

6.2

This paragraph applies when—

6.2.a

the application is dismissed or abandoned, or

6.2.b

the person has complied with an order under paragraph  2  made on the
application.

##### Failure to comply with order

7

7.1

If a person fails to comply with an order under paragraph  2 , a judge may
deal with the person as if the person had committed a contempt of the Crown
Court.

7.2

Any enactment relating to contempt of the Crown Court has effect in relation
to such a failure as if it were such a contempt.

##### Issue of warrants by judge

8

8.1

On an application made by a constable, a judge may issue a warrant authorising
a constable to enter and search premises if the judge is satisfied that the
conditions in this paragraph are met.

8.2

The first condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that
there is material on the premises mentioned in sub-paragraph  (5)  below that
consists of, or may relate to the location of, relevant human remains.

8.3

The second condition is that each of the conditions set out in paragraph  1(3)
to  (6)  is met in relation to the material.

8.4

The third condition is that there are reasonable grounds for believing, in
relation to each set of premises specified in the application—

8.4.a

that it is not practicable to communicate with any person entitled to grant
entry to the premises,

8.4.b

that it is practicable to communicate with a person entitled to grant entry to
the premises but it is not practicable to communicate with any person entitled
to grant access to the material,

8.4.c

that the material on the premises contains information which—

8.4.c.i

is subject to a restriction on disclosure or an obligation of secrecy
contained in any enactment, including an enactment contained in an Act passed
after this Act, and

8.4.c.ii

is likely to be disclosed in breach of it if a warrant is not issued, or

8.4.d

that service of notice of an application for an order under paragraph  2  may
seriously prejudice the purpose of the search.

8.5

The premises referred to in sub-paragraph  (2)  are—

8.5.a

one or more sets of premises specified in the application (in which case the
application is for a “specific premises warrant”), or

8.5.b

any premises occupied or controlled by a person specified in the application,
including such sets of premises as are so specified (in which case the
application is for an “all premises warrant”).

9

If the application is for an all premises warrant, the judge must also be
satisfied—

9.a

that there are reasonable grounds for believing that it is necessary to search
premises occupied or controlled by the person in question which are not
specified in the application, as well as those which are, in order to find the
material in question, and

9.b

that it is not reasonably practicable to specify in the application all the
premises which the person occupies or controls and which might need to be
searched.

10

10.1

The warrant may authorise entry to and search of premises on more than one
occasion if, on the application, the judge is satisfied that it is necessary
to authorise multiple entries in order to achieve the purpose for which the
judge issues the warrant.

10.2

If the warrant authorises multiple entries, the number of entries authorised
may be unlimited, or limited to a maximum.

11

A constable may—

11.a

seize and retain anything for which a search has been authorised under
paragraph  8 , and

11.b

if necessary, use reasonable force in the exercise of a power conferred by a
warrant issued under that paragraph.

##### Procedural rules

12

Criminal Procedure Rules may make provision about proceedings under this
Schedule, other than proceedings for an order under paragraph  2  that relates
to material that consists of or includes journalistic material.

##### Costs

13

The costs of any application under this Schedule and of anything done or to be
done in pursuance of an order made under it shall be in the discretion of the
judge.

##### Interpretation

14

In this Schedule—

“ journalistic material ” has the same meaning as in the Police and Criminal
Evidence Act 1984 (see section 13 of that Act); “ judge ” means a Circuit
judge, a qualifying judge advocate (within the meaning of the Senior Courts
Act 1981) or a District Judge (Magistrates’ Courts).
