Community and suspended sentence orders: special procedures relating to review
and breach

Section 153

##### Amendments to the Sentencing Code

###### Introductory

1

The Sentencing Code is amended as specified in this Part of this Schedule.

###### Orders that qualify for special procedures

2

After section 395 insert—

########## Community and suspended sentence orders qualifying for special procedures

2.395A

2.395A.1

A community order or suspended sentence order qualifies for special procedures
for the purposes of a relevant provision if the order—

2.395A.1.a

is of a description specified in regulations for the purposes of that
provision, and

2.395A.1.b

is made within a period, or after a time, so specified.

2.395A.2

In subsection (1) “ relevant provision ” means—

2.395A.2.a

section 217A;

2.395A.2.b

section 293A;

2.395A.2.c

paragraphs 10(5)(ba) and 11(2)(ba) of Schedule 10;

2.395A.2.d

paragraph 13(1)(da) of Schedule 16.

2.395A.3

A description specified under subsection (1)(a) may, among other things, be
framed by reference to—

2.395A.3.a

the courts by which the orders are made (for example, courts sitting in
particular places or areas);

2.395A.3.b

the persons who are subject to the orders (for example, persons of a
particular sex);

2.395A.3.c

the offences to which the orders relate.

2.395A.4

Where regulations under subsection (1)(a) specify a description of community
or suspended sentence order for the first time, they must under subsection
(1)(b) specify, in relation to that description of order, a period of 18
months beginning with the day on which the regulations come into force.

2.395A.5

Regulations under this section are to be made by the Secretary of State.

2.395A.6

Regulations under this section are subject to—

2.395A.6.a

the negative resolution procedure, where under subsection (1)(b) the
regulations specify a period, and

2.395A.6.b

the affirmative resolution procedure, in any other case.

###### Review of community orders

3

3.1

Section 211 (power of Crown Court to direct magistrates’ court supervision) is
amended as follows.

3.2

The existing provision becomes subsection (1).

3.3

After that subsection insert—

3.3.2

Subsection (1) does not apply to a community order that qualifies for special
procedures for the purposes of section 217A.

4

In section 217 (power to provide for court review of community orders), after
subsection (2) insert—

4.2A

Regulations under this section may not make provision in respect of community
orders which for the purposes of section 217A qualify for special procedures.

5

After section 217 insert—

########## Review of community order qualifying for special procedures

5.217A

5.217A.1

A community order that—

5.217A.1.a

imposes one or more community order requirements, and

5.217A.1.b

qualifies for special procedures for the purposes of this section,

may make provision for the order to be reviewed periodically (“provision for
review”).

5.217A.2

Where a community order contains provision for review under this section, it
must—

5.217A.2.a

specify the intervals at which the order is to be reviewed,

5.217A.2.b

provide for each review to be made, subject to section 217B, at a hearing held
for the purpose by the responsible court (a “review hearing”),

5.217A.2.c

require the offender to attend each review hearing, and

5.217A.2.d

provide for a report by an officer of a provider of probation services on the
offender’s progress in complying with the community order requirements of the
order (a “progress report”) to be made to the responsible court before each
review.

5.217A.3

In this section “ the responsible court ”, in relation to a community order,
means the court by which the order is made.

5.217A.4

For more about community orders that qualify for special procedures, see
section 395A.

########## Powers on review

5.217B

5.217B.1

This section applies where a review hearing is held on a review of a community
order by virtue of section 217A.

5.217B.2

The court may, after considering the progress report, amend—

5.217B.2.a

the community order requirements of the order, or

5.217B.2.b

any provision of the order which relates to those requirements.

5.217B.3

But the court—

5.217B.3.a

may not amend the community order requirements of the order so as to impose a
requirement of a different kind unless the offender expresses willingness to
comply with that requirement,

5.217B.3.b

may not amend—

5.217B.3.b.i

a mental health treatment requirement,

5.217B.3.b.ii

a drug rehabilitation requirement, or

5.217B.3.b.iii

an alcohol treatment requirement,

unless the offender expresses willingness to comply with the requirement as
amended, and

5.217B.3.c

except with the consent of the offender, may not amend the order while an
appeal against the order is pending.

5.217B.4

For the purposes of subsection (3)(a)—

5.217B.4.a

a community order requirement of a kind within any entry in the table in
section 201 is of the same kind as any other community requirement within that
entry, and

5.217B.4.b

an electronic compliance monitoring requirement is a requirement of the same
kind as any requirement within that table to which it relates.

5.217B.5

If the court is of the opinion that the offender has without reasonable excuse
breached a community order requirement of the order, the court may adjourn the
hearing so that the court can deal with the case forthwith under paragraph 10
or 11 of Schedule 10 (powers of court to deal with offender on breach of
requirement).

5.217B.6

For some powers available where the court is of the opinion referred to in
subsection (5) but does not deal with the case forthwith, see paragraph 9A of
Schedule 10.

5.217B.7

In this section—

“review hearing”, and “progress report”,

have the same meanings as in section 217A.

########## Alteration of review arrangements

5.217C

5.217C.1

Subsections (2) and (3) apply where a court—

5.217C.1.a

considers the progress report relating to a review under section 217A (the
“current review”), and

5.217C.1.b

forms the opinion that the offender’s progress in complying with the community
order requirements of the community order is satisfactory.

5.217C.2

If the court forms that opinion before a review hearing is held at the current
review—

5.217C.2.a

it may order that no review hearing is to be held at the current review, and

5.217C.2.b

it may amend the community order so as to provide for each subsequent review
to be held without a review hearing.

5.217C.3

If a review hearing is held at the current review, the court may at the
hearing amend the community order so as to provide for each subsequent review
to be held without a review hearing.

5.217C.4

If at a review held without a review hearing the court—

5.217C.4.a

considers the progress report, and

5.217C.4.b

forms the opinion that the offender’s progress under the order is no longer
satisfactory,

it may require the offender to attend a hearing of the court at a specified
time and place.

5.217C.5

At a review hearing the court may amend the community order so as to vary the
intervals specified under section 217A(2)(a).

5.217C.6

The functions of a court under this section that are exercisable in relation
to a review without a hearing are to be exercised—

5.217C.6.a

where the court is the Crown Court, by a judge of the court, and

5.217C.6.b

where the court is a magistrates’ court, by a justice of the peace.

5.217C.7

In this section—

“review hearing”, and “progress report”,

have the same meanings as in section 217A.

may make provision for the order to be reviewed periodically (“provision for
review”).

7.293A.2

specify the intervals at which the order is to be reviewed,

7.293A.2.b

7.293A.2.d

provide for a report by an officer of a provider of probation services on the

7.293A.3

7.293A.4

For more about suspended sentence orders that qualify for special procedures,
see section 395A.

Community and suspended sentence orders: drug testing requirement

Section 154

1

The Sentencing Code is amended as follows.

2

In section 201 (community order: community order requirements table), after
the entry in the table relating to the drug rehabilitation requirement,
insert—

drug testing requirement Part 10A  section 207(3A)

.

3

In section 207 (community order: availability of particular requirements),
after subsection (3) insert—

######## Drug testing requirement

3.3A

A drug testing requirement is not an available requirement if the offender was
convicted of the offence before the day on which section 154 of the Police,
Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 came into force.

4

In section 287 (suspended sentence order: community requirements table), after
the entry in the table relating to the drug rehabilitation requirement,
insert—

drug testing requirement Part 10A section 291(3A)

.

5

In section 291 (suspended sentence order: availability of particular
requirements), after subsection (3) insert—

######## Drug testing requirement

5.3A

A drug testing requirement is not an available requirement if the offender was
convicted of the offence before the day on which section 154 of the Police,
Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 came into force.

6

In Schedule 9 (community orders and suspended sentence orders: requirements),
after Part 10 insert—

######## Drug testing requirement

######### Requirement

6.22A

6.22A.1

In this Code, “ drug testing requirement ”, in relation to a relevant order,
means a requirement that during a period specified in the order, the offender
must, for the purpose of ascertaining whether there is any drug or
psychoactive substance in the offender’s body during that period, provide
samples in accordance with directions given by the responsible officer.

6.22A.2

The order—

6.22A.2.a

must provide that if the offender provides samples to a person other than the
responsible officer, the results of the tests carried out on the samples are
to be communicated to the responsible officer;

6.22A.2.b

may make provision about the provision of samples by virtue of sub-paragraph
(1).

6.22A.3

The power of the responsible officer to give directions by virtue of sub-
paragraph (1) about the provision of samples—

6.22A.3.a

is a power to give directions as to—

6.22A.3.a.i

the type of samples to be provided, and

6.22A.3.a.ii

the times at which, or circumstances in which, they are to be provided,

6.22A.3.b

is subject to any provision made by the order, and

6.22A.3.c

is to be exercised in accordance with guidance issued by the Secretary of
State.

6.22A.4

The Secretary of State may revise any guidance issued under sub-paragraph
(3)(c).

6.22A.5

In this paragraph and paragraph 22B—

“ drug ” means a controlled drug as defined by section 2 of the Misuse of
Drugs Act 1971; “ psychoactive substance ” has the meaning given by section
2(1) of the Psychoactive Substances Act 2016.

######### Restrictions on imposing drug testing requirement

6.22B

6.22B.1

A court may not impose a drug testing requirement unless the following
conditions are met—

6.22B.1.a

the misuse condition, and

6.22B.1.b

the availability of arrangements condition.

6.22B.2

The misuse condition is that the court is satisfied that the offender’s misuse
of a drug or psychoactive substance—

6.22B.2.a

caused or contributed to the offence to which the order relates or an
associated offence, or

6.22B.2.b

is likely to cause or contribute to the commission of further offences by the
offender.

6.22B.3

The availability of arrangements condition is that the court has been notified
by the Secretary of State that arrangements for implementing drug testing
requirements are available in the offender’s home local justice area (and the
notice has not been withdrawn).

Detention and training orders: time to count as served

Section 160

##### Detention and training orders made under Sentencing Code

###### Criminal Justice Act 2003 (c. 44)

1

This section also applies where—

2.3.1A.a

order in respect of an offender for an offence, and

2.3.1A.b

is to—

2.3.1B.a

a term of imprisonment being served by the offender as mentioned in subsection
(1)(a), or

2.3.1B.b

a detention and training order made in respect of the offender as mentioned in
subsection (1A)(a).

2.4

(1)(b) or (1A)(b)” .

2.5

For subsection (9) substitute—

2.5.8A

Subsection (9) applies in relation to an offender who is sentenced to two or
more consecutive sentences or sentences which are wholly or partly concurrent
if—

2.5.8A.a

the sentences were imposed on the same occasion, or

2.5.8A.b

where they were imposed on different occasions, the offender has not been
released during the period beginning with the first and ending with the last
of those occasions.

2.5.9

For the purposes of subsections (3) and (5), the sentences are to be treated
as a single sentence.

3

3.1

Section 240A (time remanded on bail to count towards time served: terms of
imprisonment and detention) is amended as follows.

After section 213 insert—

######### Period in service custody: effect on term of detention and training order

16.213A

16.213A.1

Subsection (2) applies where—

16.213A.1.a

the Court Martial or the Service Civilian Court proposes to make an order
under section 211 in respect of an offence, and

16.213A.1.b

the offender has been kept in service custody in connection with the offence
or any other offence the charge for which was founded on the same facts or
evidence.

16.213A.2

In determining the term of the order under section 211, the court must take
account of the period for which the offender was kept in service custody.

16.213A.3

If the court proposes to make two or more orders under section 211 in respect
of two or more offences—

16.213A.3.a

subsection (2) does not apply, but

16.213A.3.b

in determining the total term of those orders, the court must take account of
the total period for which the offender has been kept in service custody in
connection with—

16.213A.3.b.i

any of those offences, or

16.213A.3.b.ii

any other offence the charge for which was founded on the same facts or
evidence.

16.213A.4

A period of service custody may be taken account of under this section only
once.

######### Period of custody awaiting extradition: effect on term of detention and training order

16.213B

16.213B.1

This section applies where—

16.213B.1.a

the Court Martial or the Service Civilian Court proposes to make an order
under section 211 in respect of an offence,

16.213B.1.b

the offender was tried for the offence, or is to be sentenced—

16.213B.1.b.i

after having been extradited to the United Kingdom, and

16.213B.1.b.ii

without having first been restored or had an opportunity of leaving the United
Kingdom, and

16.213B.1.c

the offender was kept in custody for any period while awaiting extradition to
the United Kingdom.

16.213B.2

The court must—

16.213B.2.a

specify in open court the number of days for which the offender was kept in
custody while awaiting extradition, and

16.213B.2.b

take account of those days in determining the term of the order.

Youth rehabilitation orders

Section 161

##### Electronic monitoring: general requirements

1

In Part 17 of Schedule 6 to the Sentencing Code (electronic monitoring
requirement) after paragraph 43 insert—

######### Electronic monitoring: general

1.43A

Where a youth rehabilitation order made on or after the day on which paragraph
1  of Schedule 17 to the Police, Crime, Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 came
into force imposes an electronic monitoring requirement, the offender must (in
particular)—

1.43A.a

submit, as required from time to time by the responsible officer or the person
responsible for the monitoring, to—

1.43A.a.i

being fitted with, or installation of, any necessary apparatus, and

1.43A.a.ii

inspection or repair of any apparatus fitted or installed for the purposes of
the monitoring,

1.43A.b

not interfere with, or with the working of, any apparatus fitted or installed
for the purposes of the monitoring, and

1.43A.c

take any steps required by the responsible officer, or the person responsible
for the monitoring, for the purpose of keeping in working order any apparatus
fitted or installed for the purposes of the monitoring.

12.13

After paragraph 44 insert—

############ Electronic whereabouts monitoring requirement

12.13.45

In this Code “ electronic whereabouts monitoring requirement ”, in relation to
a youth rehabilitation order, means a requirement to submit to electronic
monitoring of the offender’s whereabouts (otherwise than for the purpose of
monitoring the offender’s compliance with any other requirement included in
the order) during a period specified in the order.

############ Person responsible for electronic monitoring: electronic whereabouts monitoring order

12.13.46

12.13.46.1

A youth rehabilitation order which imposes an electronic whereabouts
monitoring requirement must include provision for making a person responsible
for the monitoring.

12.13.46.2

The person who is made responsible for the monitoring must be of a description
specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State.

############ Electronic whereabouts monitoring requirement: general

12.13.47

Where a youth rehabilitation order imposes an electronic whereabouts
monitoring requirement, the offender must (in particular)—

12.13.47.a

submit, as required from time to time by the responsible officer or the person
responsible for the monitoring, to—

12.13.47.a.i

being fitted with, or installation of, any necessary apparatus, and

12.13.47.a.ii

inspection or repair of any apparatus fitted or installed for the purposes of
the monitoring,

12.13.47.b

not interfere with, or with the working of, any apparatus fitted or installed
for the purposes of the monitoring, and

12.13.47.c

take any steps required by the responsible officer, or the person responsible
for the monitoring, for the purpose of keeping in working order any apparatus
fitted or installed for the purposes of the monitoring.

############ Restrictions on imposing electronic whereabouts monitoring requirement

12.13.48

12.13.48.1

Where—

12.13.48.1.a

it is proposed to include an electronic whereabouts monitoring requirement in
a youth rehabilitation order, but

12.13.48.1.b

there is a person (other than the offender) without whose co-operation it will
not be practicable to secure the monitoring,

the requirement may not be included in the order without that person’s
consent.

12.13.48.2

A court may not include an electronic whereabouts monitoring requirement in a
youth rehabilitation order in respect of an offender unless—

12.13.48.2.a

the court has been notified by the Secretary of State that electronic
monitoring arrangements are available in the local justice area proposed to be
specified in the order (and the notice has not been withdrawn),

12.13.48.2.b

the court is satisfied that—

12.13.48.2.b.i

the offender can be fitted with any necessary apparatus under the arrangements
currently available, and

12.13.48.2.b.ii

any other necessary provision can be made under those arrangements, and

12.13.48.2.c

the court is satisfied that arrangements are generally operational throughout
England and Wales (even if not always operational everywhere there) under
which the offender’s whereabouts can be electronically monitored.

by court in Northern Ireland) is amended as follows.

3.2

In the heading, after “Variation” insert  “, renewal or discharge” .

3.3

In subsection (2), in the words after paragraph (b), after “varying” insert
“, renewing or discharging” .

3.4

In subsection (5), in the words after paragraph (b)—

3.4.a

after “varying” insert  “, renewing or discharging” , and

3.4.b

for “subsections (6) and (7)” substitute  “subsections (5A) to (7A)” .

3.5

After subsection (5) insert—

3.5.5A

In determining the application the court must have regard to—

3.5.5A.a

the time for which the defendant is likely to remain in Northern Ireland, and

3.5.5A.b

whether the defendant is likely to return to, or to visit, England and Wales.

3.6

In subsection (6), in the words before paragraph (a)—

3.6.a

after “An order may be” insert  “renewed, or” , and

3.6.b

for “only” substitute  “, only” .

3.7

In subsection (7), in the words before paragraph (a), after “An order as”
insert  “renewed or” .

3.8

After subsection (7) insert—

3.8.7A

The court must not discharge an order before the end of the period of 5 years
beginning with the day on which the order was made without the consent of the
defendant and the Chief Constable of the Police Service of Northern Ireland.

##### Variation of order by court in Scotland

###### Amendments of the Sexual Offences Act 

4

After section 136ZD of the Sexual Offences Act 2003 insert—

########## Variation, renewal or discharge of sexual harm prevention order etc by court in Scotland

4.136ZE

4.136ZE.1

This section applies where a relevant order has been made in respect of a
person who now—

4.136ZE.1.a

is residing in Scotland, or

4.136ZE.1.b

is in or is intending to come to Scotland.

4.136ZE.2

In this section “ relevant order ” means—

4.136ZE.2.a

a sexual harm prevention order,

4.136ZE.2.b

a sexual offences prevention order, or

4.136ZE.2.c

a foreign travel order.

4.136ZE.3

An application may be made to the appropriate sheriff in Scotland—

4.136ZE.3.a

by the defendant, or

4.136ZE.3.b

by the chief constable,

for an order varying, renewing or discharging the relevant order.

4.136ZE.4

Subject to subsections (5) to (12), on the application the court, after
hearing the person making the application and the other person mentioned in
subsection (3) (if that person wishes to be heard), may make any order
varying, renewing or discharging the relevant order that the appropriate
sheriff considers appropriate.

4.136ZE.5

In determining the application the court must have regard to—

4.136ZE.5.a

the time for which the defendant is likely to remain in Scotland, and

4.136ZE.5.b

whether—

4.136ZE.5.b.i

in the case of a sexual harm prevention order, the defendant is likely to
return to, or to visit, England and Wales, or

4.136ZE.5.b.ii

in the case of a sexual offences prevention order or foreign travel order, the
defendant is likely to return to, or to visit, Northern Ireland.

4.136ZE.6

A sexual harm prevention order may be renewed, or varied under this section so
as to impose additional prohibitions or requirements on the defendant, only if
it is necessary to do so for the purpose of—

4.136ZE.6.a

protecting the public in Scotland, or any particular members of the public in
Scotland, from sexual harm from the defendant, or

4.136ZE.6.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United
Kingdom.

4.136ZE.7

A sexual harm prevention order as renewed or varied under this section may
contain only such prohibitions and requirements as are necessary for the
purpose of—

4.136ZE.7.a

protecting the public or any particular members of the public from sexual harm
from the defendant, or

4.136ZE.7.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United
Kingdom.

4.136ZE.8

A sexual offences prevention order may be renewed, or varied under this
section so as to impose additional prohibitions or requirements on the
defendant, only if it is necessary to do so for the purpose of protecting the
public in Scotland, or any particular members of the public in Scotland, from
serious sexual harm from the defendant.

4.136ZE.9

A sexual offences prevention order as renewed or varied under this section may
contain only such prohibitions and requirements as are necessary for the
purpose of protecting the public or any particular members of the public from
serious sexual harm from the defendant.

4.136ZE.10

A foreign travel order may be renewed, or varied under this section so as to
impose additional prohibitions on the defendant, only if it is necessary to do
so for the purpose of protecting children generally or any child from serious
sexual harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

4.136ZE.11

A foreign travel order as renewed or varied under this section may contain
only such prohibitions as are necessary for the purpose mentioned in
subsection (10).

4.136ZE.12

The court must not discharge a sexual harm prevention order or a sexual
offences prevention order before the end of 5 years beginning with the day on
which the order was made without the consent of the defendant and the chief
constable.

4.136ZE.13

The defendant may appeal against the making of an order under this section, or
the refusal to make such an order, as if it were a decision constituting final
judgment in civil proceedings within the meaning of the Courts Reform
(Scotland) Act  2014 (asp 18) .

4.136ZE.14

In this section—

“ the appropriate sheriff ” means— in any case, a sheriff in whose sheriffdom
the defendant resides, or in a case where the application is made by the chief
constable— a sheriff in whose sheriffdom the defendant is believed by the
chief constable to be, or a sheriff to whose sheriffdom the defendant is
believed by the chief constable to be intending to come; “ the chief constable
” means the chief constable of the Police Service of Scotland; “ child ” means
a person under 18; “ serious sexual harm ”, in relation to the renewal or
variation of a sexual offences prevention order, means serious physical or
psychological harm caused by the defendant committing one or more of the
offences listed in Schedule 3; “ serious sexual harm ”, in relation to the
renewal or variation of a foreign travel order, means serious physical or
psychological harm caused by the defendant doing, outside the United Kingdom,
anything which would constitute an offence listed in Schedule 3 if done in any
part of the United Kingdom; “sexual harm” and “ vulnerable adult ”, in
relation to the renewal or variation of a sexual harm prevention order, have
the meanings given by section 103B(1).

########## Variation, renewal or discharge of sexual risk order etc by court in Scotland

4.136ZF

4.136ZF.1

This section applies where a relevant order has been made in respect of a
person who now—

4.136ZF.1.a

is residing in Scotland, or

4.136ZF.1.b

is in or is intending to come to Scotland.

4.136ZF.2

In this section “ relevant order ” means—

4.136ZF.2.a

a sexual risk order, or

4.136ZF.2.b

a risk of sexual harm order.

4.136ZF.3

An application may be made to the appropriate sheriff in Scotland—

4.136ZF.3.a

by the defendant, or

4.136ZF.3.b

by the chief constable,

for an order varying, renewing or discharging the relevant order.

4.136ZF.4

Subject to subsections (5) to (10), on the application the court, after
hearing the person making the application and the other person mentioned in
subsection (3) (if that person wishes to be heard), may make any order
varying, renewing or discharging the relevant order that the appropriate
sheriff considers appropriate.

4.136ZF.5

In determining the application the court must have regard to—

4.136ZF.5.a

the time for which the defendant is likely to remain in Scotland, and

4.136ZF.5.b

whether—

4.136ZF.5.b.i

in the case of a sexual risk order, the defendant is likely to return to, or
to visit, England and Wales, or

4.136ZF.5.b.ii

in the case of a risk of sexual harm order, the defendant is likely to return
to, or to visit, Northern Ireland.

4.136ZF.6

A sexual risk order may be renewed, or varied under this section so as to
impose additional prohibitions or requirements on the defendant, only if it is
necessary to do so for the purpose of—

4.136ZF.6.a

protecting the public in Scotland, or any particular members of the public in
Scotland, from harm from the defendant, or

4.136ZF.6.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

4.136ZF.7

A sexual risk order as renewed or varied under this section may contain only
such prohibitions and requirements as are necessary for the purpose of—

4.136ZF.7.a

protecting the public or any particular members of the public from harm from
the defendant, or

4.136ZF.7.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

4.136ZF.8

A risk of sexual harm order may be renewed, or varied under this section so as
to impose additional prohibitions on the defendant, only if it is necessary to
do so for the purpose of protecting children generally or any child from
physical or psychological harm from the defendant doing acts within section
123(3).

4.136ZF.9

A risk of sexual harm order as renewed or varied under this section may
contain only such prohibitions as are necessary for the purpose mentioned in
subsection  (8) .

4.136ZF.10

The court must not discharge a relevant order before the end of 2 years
beginning with the day on which the order was made without the consent of the
defendant and the chief constable.

4.136ZF.11

The defendant may appeal against the making of an order under this section, or
the refusal to make such an order, as if it were a decision constituting final
judgment in civil proceedings within the meaning of the Courts Reform
(Scotland) Act  2014 (asp 18) .

4.136ZF.12

In this section—

“ the appropriate sheriff ” means— in any case, a sheriff in whose sheriffdom
the defendant resides, or in a case where the application is made by the chief
constable— a sheriff in whose sheriffdom the defendant is believed by the
chief constable to be, or a sheriff to whose sheriffdom the defendant is
believed by the chief constable to be intending to come; “ the chief constable
” means the chief constable of the Police Service of Scotland; “child”— in
relation to the renewal or variation of a sexual risk order, means a person
under 18; in relation to the renewal or variation of a risk of sexual harm
order, means a person under 16; “harm” and “ vulnerable adult ”, in relation
to the renewal or variation of a sexual risk order, have the meanings given by
section 122B(1).

###### Amendments of the Sentencing Code

5

After section 351 of the Sentencing Code insert—

########## Variation, renewal or discharge of sexual harm prevention order by court in Scotland

5.351A

5.351A.1

This section applies where a sexual harm prevention order has been made in
respect of an offender who—

5.351A.1.a

is residing in Scotland, or

5.351A.1.b

is in or intends to come to Scotland.

5.351A.2

An application may be made to the appropriate sheriff in Scotland—

5.351A.2.a

by the offender, or

5.351A.2.b

by the chief constable,

for an order varying, renewing or discharging the sexual harm prevention
order.

5.351A.3

Subsection  (4)  applies where an application under subsection  (2)  is made.

5.351A.4

After hearing—

5.351A.4.a

the person making the application, and

5.351A.4.b

the other person mentioned in subsection  (2)  (if that person wishes to be
heard),

the sheriff may make any order varying, renewing or discharging the sexual
harm prevention order that the sheriff considers appropriate.

This is subject to subsections (5) to (8).

5.351A.5

In determining the application the court must have regard to—

5.351A.5.a

the time for which the defendant is likely to remain in Scotland, and

5.351A.5.b

whether the defendant is likely to return to, or to visit, England and Wales.

5.351A.6

An order may be renewed, or varied so as to impose additional prohibitions or
requirements on the offender, only if it is necessary to do so for the purpose
of—

5.351A.6.a

protecting the public in Scotland, or any particular members of the public in
Scotland, from sexual harm from the offender, or

5.351A.6.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the offender outside the United
Kingdom.

5.351A.7

An order as renewed or varied under this section may contain only such
prohibitions and requirements as are necessary for the purpose of—

5.351A.7.a

protecting the public or any particular members of the public from sexual harm
from the offender, or

5.351A.7.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the offender outside the United
Kingdom.

5.351A.8

The court must not discharge an order before the end of the period of 5 years
beginning with the day on which the order was made without the consent of the
defendant and the chief constable.

5.351A.9

The offender may appeal against the making of an order under this section, or
the refusal to make such an order, as if it were a decision constituting final
judgment in civil proceedings within the meaning of the Courts Reform
(Scotland) Act  2014 (asp 18) .

5.351A.10

In this section—

“ the appropriate sheriff ” means— in any case, a sheriff in whose sheriffdom
the offender resides, or in a case where the application is made by the chief
constable— a sheriff in whose sheriffdom the offender is believed by the chief
constable to be, or a sheriff to whose sheriffdom the offender is believed by
the chief constable to be intending to come; “ the chief constable ” means the
chief constable of the Police Service of Scotland.

##### Variation of order by court in England and Wales

6

After section 136ZF of the Sexual Offences Act 2003 (inserted by paragraph  4
) insert—

######### Variation, renewal or discharge of sexual harm prevention order made in Scotland by court in England and Wales

6.136ZG

6.136ZG.1

This section applies where a relevant Scottish order has been made in respect
of a person (“ the defendant ”) who now—

6.136ZG.1.a

is residing in England and Wales, or

6.136ZG.1.b

is in or is intending to come to England and Wales.

6.136ZG.2

In this section “ relevant Scottish order ” means a sexual harm prevention
order made under section 11 or 12 of the Abusive Behaviour and Sexual Harm
(Scotland) Act  2016 (asp 22) .

6.136ZG.3

A person within subsection (4) may by complaint to the appropriate court apply
for an order varying, renewing or discharging the relevant order.

6.136ZG.4

Those persons are—

6.136ZG.4.a

the defendant;

6.136ZG.4.b

the chief officer of police for the area in which the defendant resides;

6.136ZG.4.c

a chief officer of police who believes that the defendant is in, or is
intending to come to, that officer’s police area.

6.136ZG.5

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (list of countries where children are at high
risk of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation) and has not been withdrawn, a
person mentioned in subsection (4)(b) or (c) must have regard to the list in
considering—

6.136ZG.5.a

whether to apply for an order varying or renewing the relevant Scottish order
for the purpose of protecting children generally, or any particular children,
from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom, and

6.136ZG.5.b

in particular, whether to apply for an order imposing, varying or renewing a
prohibition on foreign travel for that purpose.

6.136ZG.6

Subject to subsections (7) to (14), on an application under this section the
court, after hearing the person making the application and (if they wish to be
heard) the other persons mentioned in subsection (4), may make any order
varying, renewing or discharging the relevant Scottish order that the court
considers appropriate.

6.136ZG.7

In determining the application the court must have regard to—

6.136ZG.7.a

the time for which the defendant is likely to remain in England and Wales, and

6.136ZG.7.b

whether the defendant is likely to return to, or to visit, Scotland.

6.136ZG.8

A relevant Scottish order may be renewed, or varied under this section so as
to impose additional prohibitions or requirements on the defendant, only if it
is necessary to do so for the purpose of—

6.136ZG.8.a

protecting the public in England and Wales, or any particular members of the
public in England and Wales, from sexual harm from the defendant, or

6.136ZG.8.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United
Kingdom.

6.136ZG.9

A relevant Scottish order as renewed or varied under this section may contain
only such prohibitions and requirements as are necessary for the purpose of—

6.136ZG.9.a

protecting the public or any particular members of the public from sexual harm
from the defendant, or

6.136ZG.9.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United
Kingdom.

6.136ZG.10

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 and has not been withdrawn, the court must have
regard to the list in considering—

6.136ZG.10.a

whether any order varying or renewing the relevant Scottish order is necessary
for the purpose of protecting children generally, or any particular children,
from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom, and

6.136ZG.10.b

in particular, whether an order imposing, varying or renewing a prohibition on
foreign travel is necessary for that purpose.

6.136ZG.11

A relevant Scottish order may be renewed or varied under this section so as to
require the defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the defendant’s
compliance with the prohibitions and requirements imposed by the order.

6.136ZG.12

Section 103FA (electronic monitoring requirements) applies in relation to—

6.136ZG.12.a

the variation under this section of a relevant Scottish order to require the
defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the defendant’s compliance
with the prohibitions and requirements imposed by the order, or

6.136ZG.12.b

the renewal of an order to continue such a requirement,

as it applies in relation to the making of a sexual harm prevention order,
subject to subsection (13).

6.136ZG.13

In its application to the variation or renewal of a relevant Scottish order,
section 103FA has effect as if—

6.136ZG.13.a

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to a case where it is proposed to include
in the order a requirement or provision mentioned in sub-paragraph (i) or (ii)
included a case where the order already includes such a requirement or
provision,

6.136ZG.13.b

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to the local justice area in which the
place or area proposed to be specified is situated included the local justice
area in which the place or area already specified is situated, and

6.136ZG.13.c

the reference in subsection (9) to section 103E were to this section.

6.136ZG.14

The court must not discharge a relevant Scottish order, or vary such an order
so as to remove a prohibition or requirement, unless the order or, as the case
may be, the prohibition or requirement is no longer necessary for the purpose
of—

6.136ZG.14.a

protecting the public, or any particular members of the public, from sexual
harm from the defendant, or

6.136ZG.14.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United
Kingdom.

6.136ZG.15

In this section—

“ adult magistrates’ court ” means a magistrates’ court that is not a youth
court; “ the appropriate court ” means— where the defendant is aged 18 or
over, an adult magistrates’ court for the area in which the defendant resides
or, where the application is made by a chief officer of police, any adult
magistrates’ court acting for a local justice area that includes any part of
the chief officer’s police area; where the defendant is under the age of 18, a
youth court for the area in which the defendant resides or, where the
application is made by a chief officer of police, any youth court acting for a
local justice area that includes any part of the chief officer’s police area;
“ child ” means a person under 18; “ prohibition on foreign travel ” includes
a prohibition on foreign travel within the meaning of Chapter 3 of Part 2 of
the Abusive Behaviour and Sexual Harm (Scotland) Act 2016 (see sections 17 and
25 of that Act); “ sexual harm ” and “ vulnerable adult ” have the same
meanings as in Chapter 3 of Part 2 of the Abusive Behaviour and Sexual Harm
(Scotland) Act 2016 (see sections 10 and 25 of that Act).

######### Variation, renewal or discharge of sexual offences prevention order or foreign travel order by court in England and Wales

6.136ZH

6.136ZH.1

This section applies where a relevant order has been made in respect of a
person who now—

6.136ZH.1.a

is residing in England and Wales, or

6.136ZH.1.b

is in or is intending to come to England and Wales.

6.136ZH.2

In this section “ relevant order ” means—

6.136ZH.2.a

a sexual offences prevention order, or

6.136ZH.2.b

a foreign travel order.

6.136ZH.3

A person within subsection (4) may by complaint to the appropriate court apply
for an order varying, renewing or discharging the relevant order.

6.136ZH.4

Those persons are—

6.136ZH.4.a

the defendant;

6.136ZH.4.b

the chief officer of police for the area in which the defendant resides;

6.136ZH.4.c

a chief officer of police who believes that the defendant is in, or is
intending to come to, that officer’s police area.

6.136ZH.5

If—

6.136ZH.5.a

this section applies in relation to a person because that person is subject to
a foreign travel order, and

6.136ZH.5.b

a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime, Sentencing
and Courts Act 2022 (list of countries where children are at high risk of
sexual abuse or sexual exploitation) and has not been withdrawn,

a person mentioned in subsection (4)(b) or (c) must have regard to the list in
considering whether to apply for an order varying or renewing the foreign
travel order.

6.136ZH.6

Subject to subsections (7) to (16), on an application under this section the
court, after hearing the person making the application and (if they wish to be
heard) the other persons mentioned in subsection (4), may make any order
varying, renewing or discharging the relevant order that the court considers
appropriate.

6.136ZH.7

In determining the application the court must have regard to—

6.136ZH.7.a

the time for which the defendant is likely to remain in England and Wales, and

6.136ZH.7.b

whether the defendant is likely to return to, or to visit, Northern Ireland.

6.136ZH.8

A sexual offences prevention order may be renewed, or varied under this
section so as to impose additional prohibitions or requirements on the
defendant, only if it is necessary to do so for the purpose of protecting the
public in England and Wales, or any particular members of the public in
England and Wales, from serious sexual harm from the defendant.

6.136ZH.9

A sexual offences prevention order as renewed or varied under this section may
contain only such prohibitions and requirements as are necessary for the
purpose of protecting the public or any particular members of the public from
serious sexual harm from the defendant.

6.136ZH.10

A sexual offences prevention order may be renewed or varied under this section
so as to require the defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the
defendant’s compliance with the prohibitions and requirements imposed by the
order.

6.136ZH.11

Section 103FA (electronic monitoring requirements) applies in relation to—

6.136ZH.11.a

the variation under this section of a sexual offences prevention order to
require the defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the defendant’s
compliance with the prohibitions and requirements imposed by the order, or

6.136ZH.11.b

the renewal of an order to continue such a requirement,

as it applies in relation to the making of a sexual harm prevention order,
subject to subsection (12).

6.136ZH.12

In its application to the variation or renewal of a sexual offences prevention
order, section 103FA has effect as if—

6.136ZH.12.a

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to a case where it is proposed to include
in the order a requirement or provision mentioned in sub-paragraph (i) or (ii)
included a case where the order already includes such a requirement or
provision,

6.136ZH.12.b

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to the local justice area in which the
place or area proposed to be specified is situated included the local justice
area in which the place or area already specified is situated, and

6.136ZH.12.c

the reference in subsection (9) to section 103E were to this section.

6.136ZH.13

The court must not discharge a sexual offences prevention order before the end
of 5 years beginning with the day on which the order was made without the
consent of the defendant and—

6.136ZH.13.a

where the application under this section is made by a chief officer of police,
that chief officer, or

6.136ZH.13.b

in any other case, the chief officer of police for the area in which the
defendant resides.

6.136ZH.14

A foreign travel order may be renewed, or varied under this section so as to
impose additional prohibitions on the defendant, only if it is necessary to do
so for the purpose of protecting children generally or any child from serious
sexual harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

6.136ZH.15

A foreign travel order as renewed or varied under this section may contain
only such prohibitions as are necessary for the purpose mentioned in
subsection (14).

6.136ZH.16

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 and has not been withdrawn, the court must have
regard to the list in considering whether to renew or vary a foreign travel
order under this section.

6.136ZH.17

In this section—

“ adult magistrates’ court ” means a magistrates’ court that is not a youth
court; “ the appropriate court ” means— where the defendant is aged 18 or
over, an adult magistrates’ court for the area in which the defendant resides
or, where the application is made by a chief officer of police, any adult
magistrates’ court acting for a local justice area that includes any part of
the chief officer’s police area; where the defendant is under the age of 18, a
youth court for the area in which the defendant resides or, where the
application is made by a chief officer of police, any youth court acting for a
local justice area that includes any part of the chief officer’s police area;
“ child ” means a person under 18; “serious sexual harm”— in relation to the
renewal or variation of a sexual offences prevention order, means serious
physical or psychological harm caused by the defendant committing one or more
of the offences listed in Schedule 3; in relation to the renewal or variation
of a foreign travel order, means serious physical or psychological harm caused
by the defendant doing, outside the United Kingdom, anything which would
constitute an offence listed in Schedule 3 if done in any part of the United
Kingdom.

######### Variation, renewal or discharge of sexual risk order made in Scotland by court in England and Wales

6.136ZI

6.136ZI.1

This section applies where a relevant Scottish order has been made in respect
of a person (“ the defendant ”) who now—

6.136ZI.1.a

is residing in England and Wales, or

6.136ZI.1.b

is in or is intending to come to England and Wales.

6.136ZI.2

In this section “ relevant Scottish order ” means a sexual risk order made
under section 27 of the Abusive Behaviour and Sexual Harm (Scotland) Act  2016
(asp 22) .

6.136ZI.3

A person within subsection (4) may by complaint to the appropriate court apply
for an order varying, renewing or discharging the relevant Scottish order.

6.136ZI.4

Those persons are—

6.136ZI.4.a

the defendant;

6.136ZI.4.b

the chief officer of police for the area in which the defendant resides;

6.136ZI.4.c

a chief officer of police who believes that the defendant is in, or is
intending to come to, that officer‘s police area.

6.136ZI.5

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 (list of countries where children are at high
risk of sexual abuse or sexual exploitation) and has not been withdrawn, a
person mentioned in subsection (4)(b) or (c) must have regard to the list in
considering—

6.136ZI.5.a

whether to apply for an order varying or renewing the relevant Scottish order
for the purpose of protecting children generally, or any particular children,
from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom, and

6.136ZI.5.b

in particular, whether to apply for an order imposing, varying or renewing a
prohibition on foreign travel for that purpose.

6.136ZI.6

Subject to subsections (7) to (14), on the application the court, after
hearing the person making the application and (if they wish to be heard) the
other persons mentioned in subsection (4), may make any order varying,
renewing or discharging the relevant Scottish order that the court considers
appropriate.

6.136ZI.7

In determining the application the court must have regard to—

6.136ZI.7.a

the time for which the defendant is likely to remain in England and Wales, and

6.136ZI.7.b

whether the defendant is likely to return to, or to visit, Scotland.

6.136ZI.8

A relevant Scottish order may be renewed, or varied under this section so as
to impose additional prohibitions or requirements on the defendant, only if it
is necessary to do so for the purpose of—

6.136ZI.8.a

protecting the public in England and Wales, or any particular members of the
public in England and Wales, from harm from the defendant, or

6.136ZI.8.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

6.136ZI.9

A relevant Scottish order as renewed or varied under this section may contain
only such prohibitions and requirements as are necessary for the purpose of—

6.136ZI.9.a

protecting the public or any particular members of the public from harm from
the defendant, or

6.136ZI.9.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

6.136ZI.10

If a list has been published under section 172 of the Police, Crime,
Sentencing and Courts Act 2022 and has not been withdrawn, the court must have
regard to the list in considering—

6.136ZI.10.a

whether any order varying or renewing the relevant Scottish order is necessary
for the purpose of protecting children generally, or any particular children,
from sexual harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom, and

6.136ZI.10.b

in particular, whether an order imposing, varying or renewing a prohibition on
foreign travel is necessary for that purpose.

6.136ZI.11

A relevant Scottish order may be renewed or varied under this section so as to
require the defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the defendant’s
compliance with the prohibitions and requirements imposed by the order.

6.136ZI.12

Section 122EA (electronic monitoring requirements) applies in relation to—

6.136ZI.12.a

the variation under this section of a relevant Scottish order to require the
defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the defendant’s compliance
with the prohibitions and requirements imposed by the order, or

6.136ZI.12.b

the renewal of an order to continue such a requirement,

as it applies in relation to the making of a sexual risk order, subject to
subsection (13).

6.136ZI.13

In its application to the variation or renewal of a relevant Scottish order,
section 122EA has effect as if—

6.136ZI.13.a

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to a case where it is proposed to include
in the order a requirement or provision mentioned in sub-paragraph (i) or (ii)
included a case where the order already includes such a requirement or
provision,

6.136ZI.13.b

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to the local justice area in which the
place or area proposed to be specified is situated included the local justice
area in which the place or area already specified is situated, and

6.136ZI.13.c

the reference in subsection (9) to section 122D were to this section.

6.136ZI.14

The court must not discharge a relevant Scottish order, or vary such an order
so as to remove a prohibition or requirement, unless the order or, as the case
may be, the prohibition or requirement is no longer necessary for the purpose
of—

6.136ZI.14.a

protecting the public, or any particular members of the public, from harm from
the defendant, or

6.136ZI.14.b

protecting children or vulnerable adults generally, or any particular children
or vulnerable adults, from harm from the defendant outside the United Kingdom.

6.136ZI.15

In this section—

“ adult magistrates’ court ” means a magistrates’ court that is not a youth
court; “ the appropriate court ” means— where the defendant is aged 18 or
over, an adult magistrates’ court for the area in which the defendant resides
or, where the application is made by a chief officer of police, any adult
magistrates’ court acting for a local justice area that includes any part of
the chief officer’s police area; where the defendant is under the age of 18, a
youth court for the area in which the defendant resides or, where the
application is made by a chief officer of police, any youth court acting for a
local justice area that includes any part of the chief officer’s police area;
“ child ” means a person under 18; “ harm ” and “ vulnerable adult ” have the
same meanings as in Chapter 4 of Part 2 of the Abusive Behaviour and Sexual
Harm (Scotland) Act 2016 (see sections 26 and 36 of that Act); “ prohibition
on foreign travel ” includes a prohibition on foreign travel within the
meaning of Chapter 4 of Part 2 of the Abusive Behaviour and Sexual Harm
(Scotland) Act 2016 (see sections 29 and 36 of that Act).

######### Variation, renewal or discharge of risk of sexual harm order by court in England and Wales

6.136ZJ

6.136ZJ.1

This section applies where a risk of sexual harm order has been made in
respect of a person who now—

6.136ZJ.1.a

is residing in England and Wales, or

6.136ZJ.1.b

is in or is intending to come to England and Wales.

6.136ZJ.2

A person within subsection (3) may by complaint to the appropriate court apply
for an order varying, renewing or discharging the order.

6.136ZJ.3

Those persons are—

6.136ZJ.3.a

the defendant;

6.136ZJ.3.b

the chief officer of police for the area in which the defendant resides;

6.136ZJ.3.c

a chief officer of police who believes that the defendant is in, or is
intending to come to, that officer’s police area.

6.136ZJ.4

Subject to subsections (5) to (10), on the application the court, after
hearing the person making the application and (if they wish to be heard) the
other persons mentioned in subsection (3), may make any order varying,
renewing or discharging the risk of sexual harm order that the court considers
appropriate.

6.136ZJ.5

A risk of sexual harm order may be renewed, or varied under this section so as
to impose—

6.136ZJ.5.a

additional prohibitions on the defendant, or

6.136ZJ.5.b

requirements of the kind mentioned in subsection (7) on the defendant,

only if it is necessary to do so for the purpose of protecting children
generally or any child from physical or psychological harm, caused by the
defendant doing acts within section 123(3).

6.136ZJ.6

A risk of sexual harm order as renewed or varied under this section may
contain only—

6.136ZJ.6.a

such prohibitions as are necessary for the purpose mentioned in subsection
(5), and

6.136ZJ.6.b

such requirements of the kind mentioned in subsection (7) as are necessary for
that purpose.

6.136ZJ.7

A risk of sexual harm order may be renewed or varied under this section so as
to require the defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the defendant’s
compliance with the prohibitions imposed by the order.

6.136ZJ.8

Section 122EA (electronic monitoring requirements) applies in relation to—

6.136ZJ.8.a

the variation under this section of a risk of sexual harm order to require the
defendant to submit to electronic monitoring of the defendant’s compliance
with the prohibitions imposed by the order, or

6.136ZJ.8.b

the renewal of an order to continue such a requirement,

as it applies in relation to the making of a sexual harm prevention order,
subject to subsection (9).

6.136ZJ.9

In its application to the variation or renewal of a risk of sexual harm order,
section 122EA has effect as if—

6.136ZJ.9.a

subsection (4)(b)(i) were omitted,

6.136ZJ.9.b

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to a case where it is proposed to include
in the order a provision mentioned in sub-paragraph (ii) included a case where
the order already includes such a provision,

6.136ZJ.9.c

the reference in subsection (4)(b) to the local justice area in which the
place or area proposed to be specified is situated included the local justice
area in which the place or area already specified is situated, and

6.136ZJ.9.d

the reference in subsection (9) to section 122D were to this section.

6.136ZJ.10

The court must not discharge a risk of sexual harm order before the end of 2
years beginning with the day on which the order was made without the consent
of the defendant and—

6.136ZJ.10.a

where the application under this section is made by a chief officer of police,
that chief officer, or

6.136ZJ.10.b

in any other case, the chief officer of police for the area in which the
defendant resides.

6.136ZJ.11

In this section—

“ adult magistrates’ court ” means a magistrates’ court that is not a youth
court; “ the appropriate court ” means— where the defendant is aged 18 or
over, an adult magistrates’ court for the area in which the defendant resides
or, where the application is made by a chief officer of police, any adult
magistrates’ court acting for a local justice area that includes any part of
the chief officer’s police area; where the defendant is under the age of 18, a
youth court for the area in which the defendant resides or, where the
application is made by a chief officer of police, any youth court acting for a
local justice area that includes any part of the chief officer’s police area;
“ child ” means a person under 16.

Further provision about video and audio links in criminal proceedings

Section 200

##### Criminal Justice Act 2003

1

1.1

The Criminal Justice Act 2003 is amended as follows.

1.2

For section 52 substitute—

########### Further provision about the giving, variation and rescission of live-link directions

1.2.52

1.2.52.1

The power conferred by section  51  includes power to give—

1.2.52.1.a

a direction that is applicable to several, or all, of the persons taking part
in particular eligible criminal proceedings;

1.2.52.1.b

a direction that is applicable to a particular person in respect of only some
aspects of particular eligible criminal proceedings (such as giving evidence
or attending the proceedings when not giving evidence);

1.2.52.1.c

a direction requiring or permitting a person who is outside England and Wales
(whether in the United Kingdom or elsewhere) to take part in eligible criminal
proceedings through a live audio link or a live video link.

1.2.52.2

The court may vary or rescind a direction under section  51  at any time
before or during the eligible criminal proceedings to which it relates (but
this does not affect the court’s power to give a further direction under that
section in relation to the proceedings).

1.2.52.3

A direction under section  51  may not be rescinded unless—

1.2.52.3.a

the court is satisfied that it is in the interests of justice for the
direction to be rescinded,

1.2.52.3.b

the parties to the proceedings have been given the opportunity to make
representations, and

1.2.52.3.c

if so required by subsection  (9) , the relevant youth offending team has been
given the opportunity to make representations.

1.2.52.4

In relation to the variation of a direction given under section  51 —

1.2.52.4.a

so far as the effect of the variation would be to allow a person to take part
in eligible criminal proceedings through a live audio link or a live video
link, or to alter (without removing) a person’s ability to do so, sections  51
(4)  and 53(1) to (3) apply as they apply to the giving of a direction;

1.2.52.4.b

so far as the effect of the variation would be to remove a person’s ability to
take part in eligible criminal proceedings through a live audio link or a live
video link, subsection  (3)  applies as it applies to the rescission of a
direction.

1.2.52.5

Section  51 (5)  and  (6)  applies in relation to the variation or rescission
of a direction given under section  51  as it applies to the giving of a
direction under that section.

1.2.52.6

A direction under section  51  may be given, varied or rescinded—

1.2.52.6.a

on an application by a party to the proceedings, or

1.2.52.6.b

of the court’s own motion.

But a party may not apply for a variation or rescission unless there has been
a material change of circumstances since the direction was given or last
varied.

1.2.52.7

The court must state in open court its reasons for refusing an application for
the giving, variation or rescission of a direction under section  51  and, if
it is a magistrates’ court, must cause them to be entered in the register of
its proceedings.

1.2.52.8

If a hearing takes place in relation to the giving, variation or rescission of
a direction under section  51 , the court may require or permit a person to
take part in that hearing through—

1.2.52.8.a

a live audio link, or

1.2.52.8.b

a live video link.

1.2.52.9

The requirement referred to in section  51 (4)(c)  and subsection  (3)(c)
arises in a case where—

1.2.52.9.a

the defendant is a party to the proceedings, and

1.2.52.9.b

either—

1.2.52.9.b.i

the defendant has not attained the age of 18 years, or

1.2.52.9.b.ii

the defendant has attained the age of 18 years but the court is dealing with
the case as if the defendant had not attained that age.

########### Further provision about the effect of live-link directions

1.2.52A

1.2.52A.1

A person who takes part in eligible criminal proceedings in accordance with a
direction under section  51  is to be treated as complying with any
requirement (however imposed or expressed) for that person to attend or appear
before court, or to surrender to the custody of the court, for the purposes of
that participation in those proceedings.

1.2.52A.2

A person who takes part in eligible criminal proceedings in accordance with a
direction under section  51  is to be treated as present in court for the
purposes of those proceedings.

1.2.52A.3

If eligible criminal proceedings are conducted with one or more persons taking
part in accordance with a direction under section  51 , the proceedings are to
be regarded as taking place—

1.2.52A.3.a

if at least one member of the court is taking part in the proceedings while in
a courtroom, in that courtroom (or, if more than one courtroom falls within
this paragraph, such of them as the court directs),

1.2.52A.3.b

if no member of the court, but at least one other person, is taking part in
the proceedings while in a courtroom, in that courtroom (or, if more than one
courtroom falls within this paragraph, such of them as the court directs), or

1.2.52A.3.c

if no person is taking part in the proceedings while in a courtroom, at such
place as the court directs (being a place where the court could lawfully sit
for the purposes of those proceedings).

1.2.52A.4

In subsection  (3) , “ courtroom ” includes any place where proceedings of the
sort in question might ordinarily be held (if no person were taking part in
the proceedings in accordance with a direction under section  51 ).

1.2.52A.5

A statement made on oath by a witness outside the United Kingdom and given in
evidence through a live audio link or a live video link in accordance with a
direction under section  51  is to be treated for the purposes of section 1 of
the Perjury Act 1911 as having been made in the proceedings in which it is
given in evidence.

1.3

In section 53—

1.3.a

for the heading substitute  “Further provision about live links in
magistrates’ courts” ;

1.3.b

in subsection (1)—

1.3.b.i

in the words before paragraph (a), for “This section applies” substitute
“Subsections (2) and (3) apply” ;

1.3.b.ii

in paragraph (a), for “for evidence to be given through a live link in
proceedings before the court” substitute  “requiring or permitting a person to
take part in proceedings before the court through a live audio link or a live
video link” ;

1.3.b.iii

in paragraph (b), for “receiving such evidence” substitute  “such
participation” ;

1.3.c

after subsection (3) insert—

1.3.c.4

The following functions of a magistrates’ court may be discharged by a single
justice—

1.3.c.4.a

giving a direction under section  51  or varying such a direction under
section  52 (2) ;

1.3.c.4.b

rescinding under section  52 (2)  a direction given under section  51  before
the eligible criminal proceedings concerned begin;

1.3.c.4.c

requiring or permitting, under section  52 (8) , a person to take part by live
audio link or live video link in a hearing about a matter within paragraph
(a)  or (b).

1.4

In section 54(1), for “a live link” substitute  “a live audio link or a live
video link by a witness (including the defendant)” .

1.5

In section 55—

1.5.a

in subsection (2)—

1.5.a.i

in paragraph (a), for “51 or 52” substitute  “ 52 (6) ” ;

1.5.a.ii

in paragraph (b), for “live links” substitute  “live audio links and live
video links” ;

1.5.b

in subsection (3)—

1.5.b.i

in paragraph (a), omit “uncontested”;

1.5.b.ii

in paragraph (b), for “51” substitute  “ 52 (6) ” ;

1.5.b.iii

in paragraph (c), for “51 or 52” substitute  “ 52 (6) ” .

1.6

In section 56—

1.6.a

in subsection (1)—

1.6.a.i

omit the definition of “legal representative”;

1.6.a.ii

before the definition of “local justice area” insert—

“ bail ” includes remand to local authority accommodation in accordance with
Chapter 3 of Part 3 of the Legal Aid, Sentencing and Punishment of Offenders
Act 2012, “ defendant ” includes the person accused or convicted of an offence
and, in the case of an enforcement hearing, the person liable to pay the sum
or financial penalty concerned, “ eligible criminal proceedings ” has the
meaning given in section  51 (3) , “ enforcement hearing ” means a hearing
relating to collection, discharge, satisfaction or enforcement of— a sum that
has been adjudged to be paid on conviction for an offence by a magistrates’
court or the Crown Court, or a financial penalty that is enforceable in
accordance with section 85(6) and (7) of the Criminal Justice and Immigration
Act 2008 as if it were such a sum (including a hearing to determine whether a
financial penalty is so enforceable), “ live audio link ”, in relation to a
person (P) taking part in proceedings, means a live telephone link or other
arrangement which— enables P to hear all other persons taking part in the
proceedings who are not in the same location as P, and enables all other
persons taking part in the proceedings who are not in the same location as P
to hear P, “ live video link ”, in relation to a person (P) taking part in
proceedings, means a live television link or other arrangement which— enables
P to see and hear all other persons taking part in the proceedings who are not
in the same location as P, and enables all other persons taking part in the
proceedings who are not in the same location as P to see and hear P,

;

1.6.a.iii

after the definition of “local justice area” insert—

“ preliminary hearing ” means a hearing in proceedings for an offence held
before the start of the trial (within the meaning of subsection (11A) or (11B)
of section 22 of the Prosecution of Offences Act 1985), including, in the case
of proceedings in the Crown Court, a preparatory hearing held under— section 7
of the Criminal Justice Act 1987 (cases of serious or complex fraud), or
section 29 of the Criminal Procedure and Investigations Act 1996 (other
serious, complex or lengthy cases), “ relevant youth offending team ” means
the youth offending team (established under section 39 of the Crime and
Disorder Act 1998) whose functions are exercisable in relation to the
defendant concerned, “ sentencing hearing ” means any hearing following
conviction for an offence which is held for the purpose of— proceedings (in a
magistrates’ court) relating to committal to the Crown Court for sentencing,
sentencing the offender or determining how the court should deal with the
offender in respect of the offence (including reviewing, amending or revoking
such a sentence or determination), or determining— how the offender has
complied with a sentence given in respect of the offence, or how the offender
should be dealt with in respect of compliance with such a sentence, and here “
sentence ” includes any way in which a court has determined that the offender
should be dealt with in respect of the offence,

;

1.6.b

after subsection (1) insert—

1.6.b.1A

In this Part, reference to taking part in proceedings means taking part in
whatever capacity, including hearing the proceedings as a member of the court.

1.6.b.1B

In the application of this Part in relation to a witness, a reference to
taking part in proceedings includes attending those proceedings for a purpose
preliminary or incidental to the giving of evidence.

;

1.6.c

omit subsections (2) and (3);

1.6.d

for subsection (4) substitute—

1.6.d.4

The following matters are to be disregarded for the purposes of the
definitions of “live audio link” and “live video link” in subsection (1)—

1.6.d.4.a

the extent (if any) to which a person is unable to see or hear by reason of
any impairment of eyesight or hearing;

1.6.d.4.b

the effect of any direction or order which provides for one person taking part
in proceedings to be prevented by means of a screen or other arrangement from
seeing another person taking part in the proceedings.

5.b.A1

This section applies only so far as provided by an order under paragraph 8 of
Schedule 13.

Justice Act 2003).
